(1) ACCEPTED: adjust_stop_loss/adjust_take_profit (paper_control.py:670-679) -> _resolve_open_trade (paper_control.py:110-118, no kernel filter) -> _adjust_protective (paper_control.py:688-726) writes updates={price_key:float(parsed), source_key:'manual', ts_key:...} via _update_open_trade_signal_data(trade_id, updates) at line 725, with NO kernel_managed guard and without setting manual_pause or clearing kernel_managed. The trade stays kernel_managed. This contrasts directly with partial_close_paper_position (paper_control.py:315-334), which DOES raise 409 on `bool(_sd.get('kernel_managed')) and not bool(_sd.get('manual_pause'))` (line 326) — confirming the asymmetry the finding cites. (2) NEVER ENFORCED: the sole enforcer of operator absolute SL/TP, _kernel_handle_manual_exits (scanner.py:5686), explicitly skips kernel positions at scanner.py:5701-5702 `if sd.get('kernel_managed') or sd.get('manual_pause'): continue`; _manual_price_exit_reason (scanner.py:399-421) that actually compares price to stop_loss_price/take_profit_price is only invoked there, so a kernel position's manual stop is never checked — even independent of the overwrite. (3) OVERWRITTEN EVERY SCAN: reconcile emits a refresh for every still-open kernel position matched to an open recorded row each scan (paper_reconcile.py:174-177), dispatched at scanner.py:6146-6147; _kernel_refresh_paper_trade (scanner.py:5617-5626) writes {'stop_loss':pos.get('stop_price'),'stop_loss_price':pos.get('stop_price'),'take_profit':pos.get('target_price'),'take_profit_price':pos.get('target_price')} and skips ONLY late_entry (scanner.py:5615) — no manual/source skip. (4) NONE NOT DROPPED: _update_trade_signal_data does signal_data.update(_clean_signal_data(updates)) (scanner.py:3042) and _clean_signal_data only unwraps numpy scalars via hasattr(v,'item') (scanner.py:3777-3784), so None erases and a kernel stop replaces the manual value. All cited line refs are accurate. No guard or later negating line was overlooked. Net effect: a manual SL/TP on a kernel-managed PAPER position is accepted and displayed but never enforced and reverted within one scan; the position rides to the kernel's stop — exactly the claimed 'accepted but never enforced' failure. Severity: paper-only, no direct real-money loss, but it is a silently-ignored operator risk control and a UI that displays a protective level the system won't honor (and erases within one scan), feeding promotion/live decisions — a 'wrong numbers users act on'/control-integrity issue. High is defensible (borderline medium); left unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified end-to-end on the DEFAULT code path. (1) adjust_stop_loss/adjust_take_profit -> _adjust_protective (paper_control.py:670-726) write {price_key: float(parsed), source_key: "manual"} to signal_data with NO kernel-managed guard — unlike partial_close_paper_position which refuses kernel positions unless manual_pause is set (paper_control.py:326). So the manual SL/TP is accepted and displayed. (2) Kernel management is default-on: _paper_kernel_execution_enabled() = _scanner_bool_setting("paper_kernel_execution", True) (scanner.py:5222), and the scan loop routes vectorized paper strategies through manage_positions_via_kernel, short-circuiting legacy manage_positions (scanner.py:6614). (3) The kernel re-simulates over fetch_candles history each scan (scanner.py:5957-5959); stop_price/target_price are strategy-derived and never read from the trade row, so the manual SL cannot feed back into the kernel. (4) While the kernel holds the position, the reconciler emits a refresh for the matched open row (paper_reconcile.py:175-177), and _kernel_refresh_paper_trade (scanner.py:5607-5627) overwrites stop_loss/stop_loss_price/take_profit/take_profit_price from pos.get("stop_price")/pos.get("target_price"), skipping ONLY late_entry (line 5615) — no manual/stop_loss_source/manual_pause skip. (5) The merge does not drop None: _update_trade_signal_data does signal_data.update(_clean_signal_data(updates)) (scanner.py:3042) and _clean_signal_data only unwraps numpy scalars (scanner.py:3777-3784), so a None kernel stop ERASES the manual SL and a kernel stop REPLACES it. (6) The only operator-SL enforcer, _kernel_handle_manual_exits (scanner.py:5686-5702), explicitly continues on kernel_managed positions (line 5701), so the manual level is never enforced even momentarily. Net: the operator's manual stop is accepted and shown, then reverted within one scan and never enforced — the exact "accepted but never enforced" failure described. Reachability/impact caveats: this is PAPER-scoped (the finding correctly scopes it so) — no REAL money is lost in paper, and the LIVE variant is largely mitigated because _adjust_protective places a real resting reduce-only exchange order (paper_control.py:713-725) that survives the signal_data overwrite. Severity high (unchanged) is appropriate: it is a silent correctness failure of an explicit operator safety control on the default path, with an actively misleading UI, hitting every manual SL/TP on a kernel-managed paper position (not an edge case); it does not rise to critical because no real money is lost in paper.

### `MANUAL-3` — LIVE manual SL/TP can be recorded but left unprotected when the resting trigger order is rejected per-order (no order-id validation)

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** manual  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:712-725, 738-754; forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1637-1657, 1717-1736 vs 1403-1408; forven/scanner.py:6161-6163`
- **Claim:** On a LIVE position, adjust_stop_loss -> _place_live_protective -> place_protective_stop. Unlike market_order, the protective-order placers do NOT call _require_bulk_order_ids, so a per-order rejection (an error nested in response.data.statuses[], with top-level status 'ok') returns a success-shaped payload with no order id. _place_live_protective only inspects the TOP-LEVEL 'error', so it returns None without raising; _adjust_protective then still persists the SL price (pops only the oid). Because the scanner enforces manual SL/TP for paper only, the live position is recorded as protected but has neither a resting exchange order nor any software fallback.
- **Impact:** A live position the operator believes is protected by a stop is in fact naked — no resting exchange order and no software stop — so an adverse move runs to liquidation/kill-switch instead of the operator's stop. Real money lost silently.
- **Suggested fix:** Make place_protective_stop/place_take_profit call _require_bulk_order_ids (or otherwise raise when no oid is returned and there is no explicit error), and have _place_live_protective treat a missing order id as a hard failure (raise 502) so adjust_* does NOT persist an SL/TP that was not actually placed. Surface a clear 'stop not placed' error to the operator.
- **Evidence:** _place_live_protective (paper_control.py:752-754): `if isinstance(result, dict) and result.get("error"): raise ...` then `return result.get("stop_order_id") or result.get("take_profit_order_id") or result.get("order_id")`. place_protective_stop builds its payload via `order_ids = _extract_bulk_order_ids(result, ["stop"])` and returns it with NO _require_bulk_order_ids call (hyperliquid.py:1648-1657); _extract_bulk_order_ids returns {} when a status carries no oid (hyperliquid.py:1229-1247), and a per-order rejection leaves the top-level result without an 'error' key, so no raise. Contrast market_order, which DOES enforce ids: hyperliquid.py:1403-1408 `_require_bulk_order_ids(result, order_labels=order_labels, order_ids=order_ids, ...)` (raises 'Refusing to continue without exchange correlation IDs'). _adjust_protective writes the price regardless of oid (paper_control.py:712 `updates = {price_key: float(parsed), ...}`; 718-722 only pops oid_key when None). Scanner enforces manual exits for paper only (scanner.py:6161-6163 `if not is_live: ... _kernel_handle_manual_exits(...)`), with the comment 'Live manual positions still need a real reduce-only order — deferred'.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: medium): The code-level mechanism is real and verified. place_protective_stop (hyperliquid.py:1648-1657) and place_take_profit (1728-1737) call _extract_bulk_order_ids but, unlike market_order (which enforces via _require_bulk_order_ids at 1402-1408 → raises at 1301-1305), they do NOT validate that an oid came back. A per-order rejection (HL returns top-level status "ok" with a nested {"error": ...} in response.data.statuses[]) makes _extract_bulk_order_ids return {} (1232-1247: an error status carries no oid and no resting/filled container), and _submit (140-179) returns the raw SDK response unchanged, so there is no top-level "error" key. _place_live_protective (paper_control.py:752-754) only inspects result.get("error"), so it returns None without raising. _adjust_protective then still persists stop_loss_price via `updates` (712), only pops the (absent) oid key (721-722), and even stamps exchange_stop_requested=True (724). Scanner enforces manual SL/TP for paper only (scanner.py:6161-6163). So a live position can be recorded with a stop that was never placed on the exchange. All five quoted code claims hold and the path is reachable.

HOWEVER, the finding's central impact claim — "neither a resting exchange order nor any software fallback ... an adverse move runs to liquidation ... Real money lost silently" — is materially overstated, because the auditor overlooked a guard. The daemon runs reconcile_all_books PERIODICALLY in live mode (daemon.py:1481 `if now - last_reconcile[0] > 600`, gated only-skip for paper-without-creds), which calls _repair_position_protection (risk.py:2054 and 2127). For a position that is not fully_protected (no resting reduce-only stop on the exchange — exactly the per-order-rejection case), it re-arms a protective stop via place_protective_stop (risk.py:1354-1366), preferring the operator's persisted stop_loss_price (read by _extract_prior_stop_candidate at risk.py:1227, gated by _is_recovery_stop_sane), else an emergency clamp. Notably the reconcile path DOES validate the oid (risk.py:1370-1373: `not stop_order_id` → placement_error + flagged discrepancy + retried next cycle), so it is the robust path. Net effect: the live position is naked only for a bounded window (≤10 min), then re-protected — not permanently unprotected. The take-profit sub-case is NOT re-armed by the reconcile, but a missing TP is not a liquidation/loss risk (it only fails to lock in profit).

So: confirmed defect (placers lack the oid validation market_order has; adjust persists an SL/TP it did not confirm placing, creating a transient naked window and a misleading "protected" UI state) and the suggested fix is valid. But severity is overstated: the periodic protection reconcile bounds and self-heals the stop-loss exposure, and actual loss requires the conjunction of an uncommon per-order rejection of a reduce-only trigger AND an adverse move within the ≤10-min window. That is an edge-case/degraded-protection gap, i.e. medium, not the silent-liquidation high the finding describes.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: medium): Core code defect is REAL and reachable in live. place_protective_stop (hyperliquid.py:1637-1657) and place_take_profit (1717-1737) do NOT call _require_bulk_order_ids, unlike market_order (1403-1408). On a per-order rejection (nested error in statuses[] with top-level status 'ok'), _extract_bulk_order_ids returns {} (1222-1247), so the placer returns a success-shaped payload with no stop_order_id/order_id and no top-level 'error'. _place_live_protective (paper_control.py:752-754) only checks the top-level 'error', so it returns None without raising. _adjust_protective then persists price_key/source='manual'/exchange_stop_requested=True regardless, only skipping the oid (712, 718-725). The operator therefore receives an immediate FALSE 'protected' confirmation and the position has a genuine unprotected window. This path is reachable for any live position (router paper.py:136-143 dispatches on _trade_is_live with no extra flag gate), and the scanner enforces manual exits for paper only (scanner.py:6161-6163). All of that is confirmed.\n\nHOWEVER, the finding's central impact claim — 'neither a resting exchange order nor any software fallback' -> 'runs to liquidation, money lost silently' — is REFUTED. A software fallback exists that the finding overlooked: the daemon runs reconcile_all_books on startup (daemon.py:819) and periodically every 600s (daemon.py:1481, 1509-1514), behind no feature flag. reconcile_exchange_positions calls _repair_position_protection on every matched live position (risk.py:2054) regardless of adopt_missing_in_sqlite. _summarize_position_protection (risk.py:1441-1476) derives coverage from the ACTUAL exchange open_orders, not the recorded DB price, so a position recorded with stop_loss_price but no resting order is correctly seen as 'missing' and a protective stop is re-placed — at the operator's stop_loss_price if sane (_extract_prior_stop_candidate reads it, risk.py:1227) else an emergency clamp. That repair path DOES validate the oid (not stop_order_id, risk.py:1370-1373) and, if re-placement also fails, raises a missing_protection discrepancy + operator alert (risk.py:2084-2093; daemon.py:1519-1528).\n\nNet: the exposure is a bounded (~600s worst-case) unprotected window plus a misleading instant confirmation, with an automatic repair/alert backstop — not an unbounded silent-loss-to-liquidation scenario. The defect is genuine and the suggested fix (validate order ids in the protective placers; fail closed in _place_live_protective so adjust_* doesn't persist an unplaced SL/TP) is warranted, but the 'high / no fallback / silent loss' severity is overstated. Downgrading to medium.

### `FREEZE-1` — Hung position-managing scanner is invisible to health monitor and is never auto-recovered

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** freeze  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/health_monitor.py:1397-1437 (poll loop / _attempt_recovery); forven/scheduler.py:2407-2415, 1109-1120`
- **Claim:** The component that fires exits/stops for open paper AND live positions is the scheduler job forven-scanner-hourly (kind=scanner_run, scheduler.py:1326-1337). If a run hangs past the 180s timeout the worker thread becomes a zombie and the scheduler KEEPS the lock and refuses to re-run the job, while health_monitor has NO check that watches the scanner's last-completed scan and check_scheduler reports GREEN because the scheduler tick loop is still alive. So a frozen scanner leaves every open position unmanaged with no alert and no auto-recovery.
- **Impact:** During an indefinite scanner hang, strategy/signal exits and time-stops never fire for open paper and live positions, and no Discord/critical-banner alert is raised. Live price-stops are still protected by resting exchange orders, but signal/time exits silently stop — positions ride well past their intended exit with the operator believing the system is healthy (dashboard GREEN).
- **Suggested fix:** Add a health_monitor check that reads scanner_state.last_execution_scan (written by run_scan, scanner.py:7008/7033) and goes RED when it is older than N x the scanner cadence; wire a recovery branch that, when a scanner zombie thread is detected past an absolute ceiling, escalates a CRITICAL operator alert (and ideally flattens or hands off open live positions) rather than silently holding the lock forever.
- **Evidence:** health_monitor._poll_loop runs only these checks (no scanner liveness): `for check_fn in (check_scheduler, check_brain_workers, check_data_collector, check_data_freshness, check_lab_worker, check_pipeline_throughput, check_ai_providers):` (health_monitor.py:1397-1405) plus check_bots. check_scheduler treats a stuck job as merely 'active', not stale: `running_since = _parse_iso(job.get("running_since")); if running_since is not None: active_jobs.append(...); ... continue` (health_monitor.py:381-386), and heartbeat_state is computed from the in-process scheduler tick (`in_process_tick = get_last_tick_at()` ... `scheduler_heartbeat = in_process_tick`, lines 362-369) which stays fresh, so heartbeat_state==GREEN and the AMBER 'draining' branch (`if heartbeat_state == State.RED and active_jobs`, line 409) never fires. The tick loop refuses to re-run the job: `if _job_has_live_zombie_threads(str(job.get("id"))): ... continue` (scheduler.py:2407-2415). Stale-lock recovery also skips it forever (BEFORE the absolute-max force-recover): `if _job_has_live_zombie_threads(job_id): ... continue` (scheduler.py:1109-1120). _attempt_recovery has no 'scanner' branch and no health check ever emits a 'scanner' component, so recovery is impossible even in principle (health_monitor.py:951-994).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every cited line literally does what the claim states, and I independently traced the full chain.

PREMISE: The exit/stop-firing component is the scheduler job forven-scanner-hourly (kind=scanner_run), dispatched at scheduler.py:1326-1337 via `await _run_sync_job(run_scan, ...)`. scheduler.py:166-168 confirms "scanner-hourly manages open paper positions (exits/stops)". daemon.py:1849 sets "scanner_mode":"external_scheduler" and daemon.py:1955 says "scanner runs via scheduler worker" — the daemon does NOT run an independent scan loop (grep of daemon.py for run_scan/scanner_run = no matches), so the scanner runs ONLY via this scheduler job.

HANG -> ZOMBIE -> LOCK HELD: _SCANNER_JOB_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=180 (scheduler.py:90); scanner_run is NOT in _BACKGROUND_SCHEDULER_JOB_KINDS (175-186) so it runs in foreground. On timeout, _run_sync_job registers the still-running worker thread as a zombie (scheduler.py:1205) and the lock is kept via keep_lock=_job_has_live_zombie_threads(...) (861, 964). Tick loop refuses to re-claim: scheduler.py:2407-2415 (`if _job_has_live_zombie_threads(...): ... continue`). Stale-lock recovery skips it (scheduler.py:1109-1120) and — critically — this skip sits BEFORE the _ABSOLUTE_MAX_RUNNING_SECONDS=3900 force-recover (1129-1133), so the deliberate absolute-ceiling safety net is defeated while the thread lives; the lock is held indefinitely.

HEALTH MONITOR BLIND: A job with running_since set goes to active_jobs and continues (health_monitor.py:381-386), never reaching the stale_jobs path. scheduler_heartbeat is the max including in_process_tick=get_last_tick_at() (361-369), which stays fresh because the asyncio tick loop returned after wait_for; heartbeat_state=GREEN, so the AMBER draining branch (line 409, needs RED) never fires, and check_scheduler returns GREEN (446-450). There is NO scanner liveness check anywhere in health_monitor.py (grep: only a comment at line 287); the poll loop runs the 7 checks + check_bots (1397-1425), and check_bots only inspects bot_factory bot heartbeats (514-548). _attempt_recovery (951-994) has no scanner branch and no check emits a 'scanner' component, so recovery is impossible even in principle.

IMPACT: During a scanner hang, signal/time exits for open paper AND live positions stop firing while the dashboard shows GREEN and no alert is raised; live price-stops remain protected by resting exchange orders (as the finding correctly notes). The suggested fix is viable because run_scan writes scanner_state.last_execution_scan (scanner.py:7008/7033/7043).

The only contingency is that fully-unmanaged-forever requires a permanent hang (no-timeout network I/O / deadlock); a transient hang clears via _reap_zombie_job_threads. But the monitoring/recovery gap (false-GREEN, no alert, no re-run, 3900s ceiling bypassed) is real for any hang duration and permanent hangs are realistic. Severity high is appropriate per the rubric (a real, un-recovered failure plus a misleading healthy dashboard affecting open-position exits).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The core mechanism is real and reachable in production (not flag-gated). VERIFIED: (1) The sole position-manager that fires exits/stops is the INLINE scheduler job forven-scanner-hourly (scanner_run, execute_positions=True at scheduler.py:3077); it is NOT in _BACKGROUND_SCHEDULER_JOB_KINDS (175-186) and the daemon delegates all scanning to it (daemon.py:1849 scanner_mode=external_scheduler, 1955). scanner_signal_run is signal-only (1340-1350) so it does not manage positions. (2) On an indefinite hang the worker thread is registered as a zombie (_run_sync_job 1198-1208) and the lock is kept (keep_lock=zombie_held, _execute_claimed_scheduler_job 2162-2169); the tick loop refuses to re-claim (2407-2415) and stale-lock recovery skips it (1109-1120) BEFORE the absolute-max force-recover at 1129 — and that backstop's force-recover branch (1099-1107) only covers background-task jobs, not inline zombie threads, so the inline scanner is never force-recovered while the thread lives. (3) Health stays GREEN: poll loop runs no scanner check (1397-1420); check_scheduler counts the zombie-locked job as active and continues (380-386), never reaching the stale branch (387-394, requires running_since is None), and heartbeat is dominated by the always-fresh in-process tick (361-369; 900s tick watchdog >> 185s scanner). AMBER draining only fires on RED (409). _attempt_recovery has no scanner branch (983-994). So no auto-alert, no auto-recovery, dashboard GREEN — confirmed. CORRECTION: the finding's absolute 'no check exists' is too strong — soak.py:_check_runtime_watchdog DOES flag scanner_execution_stale at 20min off scanner_state.last_execution_scan (soak.py:638-640, line 40), the very KV the fix proposes. But it is only reachable via the on-demand endpoint /api/system/soak-report (routers/status.py:35-43), emits NO push alert, and triggers NO recovery, so the operative impact stands. Severity left at high: it is a real recoverable failure affecting LIVE signal/time exits with no automatic alert. Mitigating factors a human may use to land on medium: it requires a genuine INDEFINITE hang (transient slowness self-heals when the zombie thread exits via _reap_zombie_job_threads), live price-stop downside is bounded by resting exchange orders (finding concedes), paper has no real money, a passive on-demand detection exists, and it recovers on restart.

### `FREEZE-3` — Hung-but-alive daemon is reported 'running'; live liquidation monitor stops with no detection or restart

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** freeze  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/runtime_health.py:128-152; forven/api_domains/analytics.py:344,360-361; forven/daemon.py:2004-2026`
- **Claim:** The daemon runs the live liquidation-distance monitor and the periodic exchange reconcile. The only staleness gate, normalize_daemon_state, declares the daemon stale ONLY when the OS process is dead (process_alive is False). A daemon process that is alive but frozen (event loop wedged, last_tick_ts hours old) keeps running=True, so the dashboard shows it online, no alert is raised, the stale lock is NOT cleared, and the supervisor never restarts it (it only restarts when run_in_loop returns, which a hung loop never does).
- **Impact:** A frozen-but-alive daemon silently stops liquidation-distance monitoring and reconcile for LIVE positions while every UI surface reports the daemon healthy; a developing liquidation goes unwatched with no alert and no automatic restart.
- **Suggested fix:** Treat a large last_tick_ts/last_heartbeat age as a freeze even when process_alive is True (e.g. flip running=False / set a 'daemon_hung' flag and signal the supervisor to recycle the process), and add a health_monitor check on daemon_state heartbeat age so a hung daemon raises a critical alert.
- **Evidence:** `stale_process = bool(running and process_alive is False and (age_seconds is None or age_seconds > max(float(stale_after_seconds), 1.0)))` (runtime_health.py:134-138) — age_seconds is computed (lines 128-131) but only consulted when process_alive is False. The dashboard derives liveness purely from the flag: `daemon_running = bool(daemon.get("running"))` (analytics.py:344) and only surfaces a problem on `if daemon.get("stale_process_detected")` (analytics.py:360). Restart only happens on loop EXIT: the supervisor re-invokes the factory after it returns/raises (api.py:148-154), and `await async_market_loop(state)` in run_in_loop (daemon.py:2022-2023) never returns while the loop is hung. No health_monitor check covers the daemon at all (health_monitor.py:1397-1405).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The code literally exhibits the claimed defect. (1) runtime_health.py:134-138: stale_process = running AND process_alive is False AND (age...). The age_seconds computed at lines 128-131 is only consulted as a sub-clause INSIDE the process_alive-is-False branch; if the OS process is alive but the loop is wedged (last_tick_ts hours old), process_alive=True so stale_process=False, running stays True, stale_process_detected is never set, and remove_stale_daemon_lock is never called. (2) analytics.py:344 reads daemon_running=bool(daemon.get('running')) and analytics.py:360 only surfaces a problem on stale_process_detected; neither consults derived['age_seconds'] (set at runtime_health.py:151), so the dashboard reports a hung-but-alive daemon as online. (3) api.py:142-154: _supervise_background_loop does `result = await factory()` with no timeout/watchdog and only restarts after the factory returns/raises; daemon.py:2022-2026 run_in_loop awaits async_market_loop which runs the while-loop at daemon.py:1724 and never returns while hung, so the supervisor stays blocked and never recycles. (4) The live liquidation monitor (_check_liquidation_distances, daemon.py:1425-1432) and periodic reconcile (reconcile_all_books, daemon.py:1481+) both execute inside _run_tick, which also writes last_tick_ts (daemon.py:1447) — when the tick stops they stop. (5) No health_monitor check references daemon_state/last_tick_ts (grep clean); check_scheduler watches a SEPARATE scheduler subsystem (scheduler:* keys) spawned independently (api.py:454 vs api.py:483), so it cannot detect a frozen daemon thread. (6) selfheal.py has no daemon-freeze watchdog (grep: no matches). The daemon also typically runs on its own thread/event loop (api.py:474-481 runtime_thread_mode via _spawn_supervised_runtime_thread), so a wedge there leaves the API/dashboard serving 'running: true' unaffected, strengthening the impact. Adversarial check: soak.py:551-644 (_check_runtime_watchdog) DOES compute daemon tick-age staleness and flags 'daemon_stale', but it is wired only to the on-demand endpoint GET /api/system/soak-report (routers/status.py:35-40) — not to any scheduler job, the health_monitor poll loop, any alert dispatch, or restart path — so it provides no automatic detection/alert/restart and does not refute the finding (it only mildly tempers the 'every UI surface' phrasing). Severity high is appropriate, not critical: the lost function is a monitoring/alert layer for live positions and the failure requires a daemon freeze as a precondition, so it is a real recoverable-failure/safety gap rather than a path that directly and unconditionally moves money.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All five mechanical claims verified against live code. (1) runtime_health.py:134-138 gates staleness on `process_alive is False`; age_seconds (computed lines 128-131) is only a sub-clause, so an alive-but-frozen process keeps running=True, never sets stale_process_detected, never clears the lock. (2) analytics.py:344 derives liveness purely from `daemon.get("running")` and only surfaces trouble via stale_process_detected (lines 360-361); control_plane/status.py:855 and routers/quant_factory.py:81 use the same flag — a hung daemon shows healthy everywhere. (3) api.py:142-154 supervisor `await factory()` is unbounded with no watchdog/timeout; run_in_loop's `await async_market_loop(state)` (daemon.py:2023) never returns while hung, so the restart branch is unreachable. (4) health_monitor.py:1397-1405 check list contains no daemon-heartbeat check; grep found zero references to daemon_state/last_tick_ts in health_monitor.py, and check_scheduler watches the SEPARATE scheduler loop (scheduler:* KV), not the daemon market loop. selfheal.py has no daemon freeze coverage. heartbeat_gap/exchange_positions_synced_at are written by the daemon but never read for alerting/restart. (5) The frozen loop is the live protection path: _run_tick (daemon.py:1413) runs _check_liquidation_distances (1425-1432) reading REAL Hyperliquid positions via get_positions (1223), plus periodic reconcile_all_books (1481+), and sets last_tick_ts (1447); the daemon runs in-process in the API (api.py:473), always on, for paper and live. Reachability is concrete beyond generic event-loop wedging: the consumer-restart guard at daemon.py:1735 only respawns workers when `consumer is None`, not when the spawned _price_consumer task has crashed/raised, so a dead consumer permanently halts _run_tick (liquidation monitor + reconcile + last_tick_ts) while the OS process and outer loop stay alive and undetected. Severity high is correct: a real recoverable-failure-class gap on the live-money path that disables the last line of liquidation defense behind a green dashboard, with no alert and no auto-restart. Not critical because the loss is conditional (a freeze must coincide with a position drifting toward liquidation), not incurred on every normal run.

### `RESTART-1` — Kernel replay window is capped at ~360–600 bars (cache), not the configured 1500 — a position held longer falls out of the window, loses ALL kernel exit enforcement, and the orphan guard deliberately leaves it OPEN

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** restart  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5958, forven/scanner.py:1692-1722, forven/market_cache.py:160-200, forven/scanner.py:71, forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:209-226, forven/scanner.py:6056-6059`
- **Claim:** The open position's trailing ratchet, bars_held, stop, target and size are NOT persisted; they are reconstructed every scan ONLY by replaying execution_kernel.simulate over the fetched candle history. The kernel requests _paper_kernel_history_bars()=1500 bars (scanner.py:5249), but the candle cache truncates the actual window to ~360–600 bars, so any position whose entry bar scrolls out of that window is no longer reproduced by the kernel and stops being managed entirely (no trailing stop, fixed stop, take-profit, time-stop or signal exit ever fires), while the reconciler's orphan-close guard explicitly leaves it OPEN.
- **Impact:** A paper position held beyond ~(window-200) bars becomes a permanent zombie: its strategy/kernel exits never fire, so its eventual realized PnL is wrong, corrupting the very paper-validation numbers the promotion gate uses to send strategies LIVE. On the live kernel path the same scroll-out suspends trailing/time-stop/signal exits (only the at-open resting SL/TP remain), giving back trailing profit or riding to the fixed stop. The operator-configured 1500-bar safety window is effectively dead.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) fetch the kernel's history bypassing the cache (or with an interval/asset-specific snapshot whose load+publish max_rows >= paper_kernel_history_bars), so the replay window actually equals the configured value; and/or (b) persist a fallback open-position state (entry_bar absolute time, running trailing extreme, bars_held) so a position whose entry predates the window can still be exit-managed instead of being silently abandoned; and (c) when a recorded OPEN's entry predates the kernel's window, surface it as an operator alert rather than silently leaving it unmanaged.
- **Evidence:** manage_positions_via_kernel fetches `fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), interval=timeframe)` (scanner.py:5958). fetch_candles cache-first path returns `cached_df.tail(required_bars)` (scanner.py:1696) where cached_df comes from `load_candle_snapshot`. load_candle_snapshot caps loaded rows: `rows = _normalize_candle_rows(raw.get("rows", []))` with the DEFAULT `max_rows: int = 600` (market_cache.py:106,191,160 `return deduped[-max(int(max_rows),1):]`) — so the kernel can never see more than 600 bars from cache. The regular signal scan publishes only `_CANDLE_CACHE_BARS=360` (scanner.py:71) rows: `publish_candle_snapshot(..., max_rows=max(_CANDLE_CACHE_BARS, required_bars))` with required_bars=300 (scanner.py:1707-1718 + 6194/6303), and run_scan runs the 300-bar `_evaluate_signal_matrix` (line 6920) BEFORE the kernel's `_apply_execution_actions` (line 6949) every cycle, so the kernel almost never gets to do its own 1500-bar direct fetch — it reads the 360-row cache. With KERNEL_WARMUP=200 (scanner.py:6003) and simulate looping `range(warmup+1, len(df))` (execution_kernel.py:183), only ~160 bars are tradeable (1h: ~6.7 days). When the entry scrolls before df.index[KERNEL_WARMUP+1], reconcile() sees no kernel open for that direction and the orphan guard hits `if window_start is not None and entry_time and _ts_lt(entry_time, str(window_start)): continue` (paper_reconcile.py:220-221) — leaving the recorded OPEN untouched and unmanaged.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. The replay window IS effectively capped far below the configured 1500. (1) market_cache.py:191 load_candle_snapshot calls _normalize_candle_rows(raw.get("rows", [])) with NO max_rows, so the default max_rows=600 (market_cache.py:106) and the cap at line 160 (deduped[-max(int(max_rows),1):]) hard-limit EVERY cache LOAD to 600 rows. (2) scanner.py:5958 the kernel calls fetch_candles(bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars()=1500) (default 1500 at scanner.py:5251); the cache-first path at scanner.py:1692-1696 returns cached_df.tail(required_bars) where cached_df has at most 600 rows, so tail(1500) of <=600 = <=600. (3) The signal scan _evaluate_signal_matrix (scanner.py:6920) runs BEFORE _apply_execution_actions->manage_positions_via_kernel (scanner.py:6949), and it fetches fetch_candles(bars=300) (scanner.py:6194/6303) which on a cache miss/stale publishes only max_rows=max(_CANDLE_CACHE_BARS=360,300)=360 (scanner.py:71,1708/1715/1718). So the cache is refreshed to a fresh ~360-row snapshot before the kernel runs, and the kernel reads that fresh <=360-row cache rather than reaching its own direct 1500-bar fetch (the df.tail(1500) at scanner.py:1722 is the only >600 path and is unreachable in steady-state daemon operation). Net: the kernel sees ~360 bars (hard ceiling 600), never 1500. (4) execution_kernel.py:183 loops range(warmup+1, len(df)); with KERNEL_WARMUP=200 (scanner.py:6003) and len(df)~=360 only ~159 bars (idx 201..359) are tradeable and the earliest reproducible entry is df.index[201]. (5) A position whose real entry scrolled before df.index[201] is never recreated by simulate, so it is absent from res.open_positions; the reconciler then hits the orphan guard at paper_reconcile.py:220-221 (if window_start is not None and entry_time and _ts_lt(entry_time, str(window_start)): continue), leaving the recorded OPEN untouched -- no close, no refresh, no kernel exit enforcement. window_start = df.index[min(KERNEL_WARMUP+1, len-1)] (scanner.py:6059) confirms the guard uses df.index[201]. Both paper and live dispatch through this path by default (paper_kernel_execution True scanner.py:5222; live_kernel_execution True scanner.py:5828; dispatch at scanner.py:6616/6621). Live retains exchange resting SL/TP (_kernel_open_live_trade->_execute_direct, scanner.py:5842), matching the finding's stated live impact (loss of trailing/time-stop/signal exits, not a naked position). One nuance the finding under-states: if the strategy re-enters the same direction within the visible window, the recorded OPEN is ADOPTED/refreshed (paper_reconcile.py:184-187) instead of orphaned, so the permanent-zombie state requires both a long hold AND no re-entry in the window -- conditional but genuinely reachable. Core claim holds literally. Severity high is correct: corrupts paper-validation PnL that feeds the promotion gate and suspends dynamic exits on live, but is conditional and live is backstopped by exchange resting orders (not a silent naked loss), so not critical.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): VERIFIED against live code. (1) manage_positions_via_kernel fetches fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars()=1500) at scanner.py:5958/5249-5251. (2) fetch_candles cache-first returns cached_df.tail(required_bars) (scanner.py:1696), but cached_df comes from load_candle_snapshot which calls _normalize_candle_rows(raw.get('rows',[])) WITHOUT max_rows, defaulting to 600 (market_cache.py:191,106,160) — so a fresh-cache read is hard-capped at 600 regardless of stored rows. (3) The daemon (the production cache warmer AND scan-loop runner) publishes only CANDLE_CACHE_BARS=360 rows, interval=1h, every CANDLE_CACHE_REFRESH_INTERVAL=90s (daemon.py:144-145,1592-1606), which is < the 180s stale threshold (scanner.py:70). So for 1h strategies the cache is ALWAYS fresh and the kernel permanently sees 360 bars; the scanner's stale-path 1500-bar direct fetch (scanner.py:1701-1722) never fires. Non-1h is capped at 600 by the load truncation. The configured 1500 window is therefore dead in steady state. (4) KERNEL_WARMUP=200 (scanner.py:6003) + simulate range(warmup+1,len(df)) (execution_kernel.py:183) leaves ~159 tradable bars on a 360-bar frame (~6.6 days at 1h). (5) When a long-held position's entry scrolls before df.index[201] and the re-simulation does not re-enter that direction (realistic for mean-reversion/breakout entries and for trend positions whose entry trigger has passed), reconcile's orphan loop executes the guard `if window_start is not None and entry_time and _ts_lt(entry_time, str(window_start)): continue` (paper_reconcile.py:220-221), leaving the recorded OPEN untouched; the close loop also can't match it because the kernel never reproduced the historical entry (absent from res.closed_trades). (6) No independent stop enforcement exists: _kernel_handle_manual_exits skips kernel_managed trades (scanner.py:5701) and late-entry exits are disabled (scanner.py:6069). So trailing/fixed-stop/take-profit/time-stop/signal exits all stop firing — confirming the unmanaged-zombie mechanism. (7) Reachable on BOTH paper and live by default: _live_kernel_execution_enabled() defaults True (scanner.py:5828) and dispatches execution_type='live' (scanner.py:6619-6622); on live, orphan_close is stripped (scanner.py:6091-6092) and the only residual protection is the at-open resting SL/TP from _execute_direct (scanner.py:5880-5881), so live loses trailing/time-stop/signal exits exactly as claimed. Money/state impact is real: paper validation PnL diverges from backtest (parity break feeding the promotion gate) and live positions held >~window-warmup bars ride past their trailing/time/signal exits. Minor overstatement only: 'permanent' is not strictly accurate — a same-direction re-entry triggers the adopt/refresh branch (paper_reconcile.py:184-187) and a live resting stop can still fire — but this does not change the verdict. Severity 'high' is appropriate: live downside is bounded by the exchange resting stop and the bug requires a multi-day hold without re-entry, so it is below 'critical' but clearly produces wrong numbers users act on and corrupts paper position/validation state.

### `RESTART-2` — Downtime backfill/recovery is bounded by the (small) fetched window, NOT the go-live cutoff — missed trades older than the window are silently dropped, contradicting the documented unbounded-downtime guarantee

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** restart  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5256-5266, forven/scanner.py:5289-5312, forven/scanner.py:6045-6055, forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:151-166`
- **Claim:** The recovery design claims that anchoring recent_cutoff to the paper go-live timestamp means 'ANY downtime backfills every missed trade since go-live no matter how long the scanner was down' (scanner.py:5256-5266, 5297-5301). But the reconciler can only act on trades the kernel actually REPRODUCED, and the kernel only sees the fetched window (~360 bars per RESTART-1). Any trade that opened and/or closed more than ~window bars before the current scan is before df.index[0], never appears in res.closed_trades/open_positions, and is therefore neither backfilled nor closed — it is silently lost.
- **Impact:** After an extended outage (or any operator-stopped daemon longer than the window), the paper book loses entire round-trip trades and can strand a position the strategy already exited during the gap. The promotion-gate metrics computed from this book are then materially wrong (missing trades = inflated/deflated win rate and PnL), and backtest/paper parity — the system's core safety claim — is broken precisely when it is relied upon most.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the backfill/recovery window actually reach back to recent_cutoff (go-live) when reconstructing after downtime: fetch enough bars to cover (now - go_live) for the strategy's timeframe (bounded sanely), or fetch from a non-truncated store. Failing that, detect when go_live < df.index[0] and emit a hard operator warning that pre-window history could not be reconciled, instead of silently proceeding.
- **Evidence:** reconcile() only backfills from `res.closed_trades` (paper_reconcile.py:151) gated by `_recent(entry_time)` (line 159); res.closed_trades is produced solely by simulate over the fetched df. recent_cutoff is the go-live anchor (`_go_live.isoformat()`, scanner.py:6054-6055), which can be months in the past, but window_start is `df.index[KERNEL_WARMUP+1]` (scanner.py:6059) — only ~bars back. There is no separate long-history fetch for backfill; the window is the single `fetch_candles(..., bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars())` capped to ~360–600 (see RESTART-1). So a trade whose entry_time is after go-live but before df.index[0] satisfies `_recent` yet is invisible to the kernel.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code confirms the structural defect. The kernel paper path fetches ONE bounded frame at scanner.py:5957-5959 — fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars()) — and that single df drives both run_strategy_execution (6005-6010) and reconcile (6085-6088). There is no separate long-history fetch for recovery, and selfheal.py/daemon.py recovery covers only live-exchange position reconciliation, not paper-book backfill. The window is bounded: _paper_kernel_history_bars() defaults to 1500/floor 300 (5249-5253), and fetch_candles returns cached_df.tail(required_bars) from a cache bounded by _CANDLE_CACHE_BARS=360 (scanner.py:71), so the effective window can be ~360 in practice. recent_cutoff is the go-live anchor (_go_live.isoformat(), scanner.py:6054-6055; _resolve_paper_go_live 5289-5312 returns stage_changed_at/reset, which can be months old). reconcile backfills ONLY from res.closed_trades (paper_reconcile.py:151), gated by _recent (>= go-live) at 159-160; res.closed_trades/open_positions come solely from simulate over df, so any trade with entry after go-live but before df.index[0] satisfies _recent yet is invisible to the kernel — never backfilled/closed/opened. The stranded-position arm also holds: the orphan-close guard at paper_reconcile.py:220-221 explicitly skips entries earlier than window_start, leaving a held position untouched even though the strategy exited it during the gap. The documented unbounded-downtime guarantee (scanner.py:5297-5301 'no matter how long the scanner was down'; 6048-6051 'ANY downtime ... backfills every missed trade since go-live') is therefore false, and there is no go_live<df.index[0] detection or operator warning anywhere in 6045-6088 — it silently proceeds. Reachable on any outage exceeding the window timespan (short timeframes: days). Severity high is appropriate: the resulting incomplete paper book feeds promotion-gate metrics that gate real-money live promotion (wrong numbers users act on) and can strand positions (state corruption), though it requires extended downtime rather than being a continuous silent loss. Minor imprecision: the finding cites '~360 bars' while the default is 1500 — but the 360-row cache bound corroborates it and the magnitude is not load-bearing for the structural defect.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Traced the full chain against live code; the defect is real and on default-on paths. (1) manage_positions_via_kernel fetches a SINGLE bounded window: fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), interval=timeframe) at scanner.py:5958; _paper_kernel_history_bars defaults to 1500 (scanner.py:5249-5253) and there is NO separate long-history fetch for recovery. (2) For the common 1h timeframe the effective window collapses to ~360 bars: the daemon refreshes the cache with bars=CANDLE_CACHE_BARS=360, max_rows=360, interval="1h" only (daemon.py:145,1592-1606), and fetch_candles returns the fresh cache via cached_df.tail(required_bars) (scanner.py:1696) = 360 rows; non-1h timeframes direct-fetch up to 1500. Either way the window is bounded. (3) recent_cutoff = _go_live.isoformat() (scanner.py:6054-6055) can be months back. (4) reconcile() backfills ONLY by iterating res.closed_trades (paper_reconcile.py:151), gated by _recent (line 159, append at 160); res.closed_trades is produced solely from simulating over df, so a trade with entry_time after go-live but before df.index[0] passes _recent yet is invisible to the kernel and never backfilled — exactly as claimed. (5) The orphan-close guard skips entries older than window_start (paper_reconcile.py:220), so a recorded OPEN the strategy exited during a long gap is stranded open indefinitely. (6) The comments at scanner.py:5297-5301 and 6045-6051 promise unbounded downtime recovery ("ANY downtime ... no matter how long the scanner was down"); no code compares go_live to df.index[0] or warns — the failure is silent. Reachability: default-on for both paper (_paper_kernel_execution_enabled default True, scanner.py:5222) and live (_live_kernel_execution_enabled default True, scanner.py:5828), routed at scanner.py:6614/6619 — NOT behind an off flag. The bug only manifests after downtime exceeding the window time-span (~15 days for 1h, ~5 days for 5m, months for 4h), so it is not a normal-operation loss (hence not critical), but it produces wrong promotion-gate metrics users act on to push strategies to real-money live, can strand positions, and fails silently against a documented guarantee. The finding's "~360-600" window is a fair approximation for the 1h case and understates non-1h (up to 1500 bars), but the structural defect and impact are independent of the exact bar count. High is appropriate.

### `DATA-1` — Live candle fetch supports a narrower timeframe set than the rest of the system — 30m/2h/etc. strategies silently never trade in paper/live

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** data  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/market_data.py:17-24 (INTERVAL_TO_MS); 206-207 and 384-385 (raise on unknown); forven/scanner.py:6298-6330 and 5956-5963 (skip on fetch failure)`
- **Claim:** The live/paper candle fetchers only recognize 1m,5m,15m,1h,4h,1d. Any strategy on another timeframe the rest of the system treats as first-class (notably 30m, plus 2h/6h/8h/12h/3m/45m) raises 'unsupported interval' on every fetch, so the scanner permanently skips it — even though it backtested fine (the backtest reads parquet via load_parquet, which supports all of data.TIMEFRAME_MS).
- **Impact:** A strategy promoted on a non-default timeframe (e.g. operator adds 30m/2h to gate_sweep_timeframes, or a manually-created/MCP strategy uses 30m) passes the full gauntlet on backtest data, then sits permanently dead in paper/live, every scan logging 'failed to fetch'. Backtest/paper parity is silently broken and the operator sees a deployed strategy that never opens a position. Default gate_sweep_timeframes ['15m','1h','4h','1d'] are all fetchable, which is why this is latent rather than universal.
- **Suggested fix:** Make INTERVAL_TO_MS cover the same timeframe set the data layer and strategy creation accept (derive it from data._timeframe_to_ms / data.TIMEFRAME_MS), or validate a strategy's timeframe against the live-fetchable set at promotion time and reject/​warn rather than letting it die silently in paper.
- **Evidence:** market_data.py:17 `INTERVAL_TO_MS = {` lists only `"1m"`,`"5m"`,`"15m"`,`"1h"`,`"4h"`,`"1d"` (no 30m/2h/...). market_data.py:205-207 `interval_ms = INTERVAL_TO_MS.get(normalized_interval)\n    if interval_ms is None:\n        raise ValueError(f"unsupported interval: {interval}")` (same at 383-385 for Binance). scanner.py:6308-6330 catches and emits `f"failed to fetch {strat_timeframe} candles for {asset}: {exc}"` -> blocked row; scanner.py:5961-5963 kernel path catches -> `_skip(f"candle fetch failed: {exc}")`. Contrast: forven/data.py:83-100 TIMEFRAME_MS includes 30m/2h/6h/8h/12h, scanner.py:76-84 _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS includes 30m, execution_selection.py:151 maps 2h=120, lab_matrix_engine.py:91 maps 30m — so these timeframes ARE creatable/backtestable.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: medium): Code genuinely exhibits the defect. market_data.py:17-24 INTERVAL_TO_MS = {1m,5m,15m,1h,4h,1d} only. Both live/paper fetchers raise on anything else: fetch_hyperliquid_candles (205-207) and fetch_binance_candles (383-385) do `interval_ms = INTERVAL_TO_MS.get(normalized_interval); if interval_ms is None: raise ValueError(f"unsupported interval: {interval}")`. scanner.fetch_candles (1665) routes through fetch_market_candles (market_data.py:503-505) to those fetchers with the interval propagated. Both scanner consumers permanently drop the strategy on the raise: legacy path scanner.py:6308-6330 emits _blocked_scan_row("failed to fetch {tf} candles...") then continue; kernel path scanner.py:5961-5963 catches and returns _skip("candle fetch failed: ..."). Parity asymmetry verified: the backtest loads via load_parquet (backtest.py:2384/3067/3254) backed by ccxt submit_ingestion (coverage.py:184) over data.TIMEFRAME_MS (data.py:83-100 includes 30m/2h/6h/8h/12h/3m/45m), so a non-default-tf strategy backtests fine but every live/paper fetch raises. No cache rescue: daemon _refresh_candle_cache publishes only interval="1h" (daemon.py:1593,1605) and the scanner only republishes intervals it actually fetched (scanner.py:1713), so a non-fetchable interval is never cached. Reachability confirmed: gate_sweep_timeframes is operator-editable (default api_core.py:1834 ["15m","1h","4h","1d"] all fetchable -> latent, as the finding states) and coverage backfills + lifecycle.py:140-152 backtests whatever is added; and db.create_strategy_container (db.py:4398-4503) stores the timeframe verbatim with no clamp, so an MCP/manual 30m/2h strategy reaches paper. The only guard, intake.py:31-50 _intended_timeframe, clamps unsupported tf to 1h via INTERVAL_TO_MS but ONLY on the drop-zone file-intake path (callers at intake.py:370,591) — it does not cover the sweep or direct-create paths. Severity lowered to medium: it is not truly silent (each scan logs a specific diagnosable reason via the blocked/skip row), no money is lost and no state is corrupted (pure opportunity cost — a deployed strategy that never opens a position plus a backtest/paper parity break), and it is gated behind non-default timeframe configuration. That maps to edge-case/degraded (medium), not high.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: medium): The defect is real and the mechanism is exactly as claimed, verified against live code. (1) market_data.py:17-24 INTERVAL_TO_MS lists only 1m/5m/15m/1h/4h/1d. (2) Both live/paper fetchers reject anything else: fetch_hyperliquid_candles raises at 206-207 (`interval_ms = INTERVAL_TO_MS.get(normalized_interval); if interval_ms is None: raise ValueError(f"unsupported interval: {interval}")`) and fetch_binance_candles raises identically at 384-385; fetch_market_candles (489-505) dispatches only to these two with no fallback. (3) Scanner converts the raise into a permanent skip/block on BOTH execution paths: kernel manage_positions_via_kernel catches at scanner.py:5961-5963 and returns _skip("candle fetch failed: ..."), and the legacy path catches at 6308-6330 and appends a _blocked_scan_row("failed to fetch {tf} candles..."). (4) The backtest does NOT use this narrow map: load_backtest_candles tries data.load_parquet first (backtest.py:2384), which keys off data.TIMEFRAME_MS (data.py:83-100, which DOES include 30m/2h/6h/8h/12h) — it only falls back to the narrow fetch_candles if parquet load fails. So a 30m strategy backtests fine on parquet but is permanently dead in paper/live — a genuine backtest/paper-live parity break on both paper AND live (live fills via the same fetch_candles chain). Reachability is concrete, not hypothetical: 30m is an explicit UI-selectable option for pipeline.gate_sweep_timeframes (frontend/src/lib/settings/manifest.ts:655); the coverage backfill seeds parquet for gate_sweep_timeframes (coverage.py:238) so the 30m series exists for the gauntlet; run_timeframe_sweep submits backtests across those timeframes (lifecycle.py:88-144); and execution_selection.py:151 / lab_matrix_engine.py:91 treat 30m/2h as first-class — so a 30m (or MCP-created 2h) strategy can pass the gauntlet and be promoted, then never opens a position. I downgrade severity from high to medium for three reasons grounded in the reachability lens: (a) it is LATENT behind non-default config — the default gate_sweep_timeframes ["15m","1h","4h","1d"] (api_core.py:1834) are all fetchable, so it never fires out of the box; (b) it is operator-VISIBLE, not silent — every scan emits a blocked row and a WARNING log naming the strategy and failing timeframe (though the wording "Skip this strategy until the data source recovers" misleadingly implies transience for a permanent condition); (c) it causes neither money loss nor state corruption — the strategy simply never trades. That is a degraded/parity defect (medium), not a wrong-numbers or money-losing failure. The suggested fix (derive INTERVAL_TO_MS from data.TIMEFRAME_MS, or validate timeframe against the live-fetchable set at promotion) is correct.

### `DATA-2` — Kernel execution path (default for paper AND live real fills) has no stale-candle gate; the fail-closed DI-1 staleness gate only guards the legacy path and is ignored for kernel strategies

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** data  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5931-5963 (kernel path, no gate); 6356-6400 (DI-1 staleness gate, legacy only); 6602-6623 (dispatch); 5880 (_execute_direct real fill)`
- **Claim:** manage_positions_via_kernel re-fetches its own candles and runs the kernel to decide opens/closes, but contains NO bar-staleness check. The only stale-feed guard (DI-1) lives in _scan_asset_group and gates the legacy `signal`. _apply_execution_actions dispatches kernel strategies to manage_positions_via_kernel regardless of whether the row was blocked, so the staleness verdict is computed and then ignored for the parity path. With paper_kernel_execution and live_kernel_execution both defaulting ON, the default execution path is unguarded.
- **Impact:** If the candle source serves stale-but-non-erroring bars (the exact 'cache serving old candles / feed outage' scenario the DI-1 comment was written to defend), a live-kernel strategy can decide to OPEN off an hours-old signal bar and fill at the current real market price via _execute_direct, with no guard. Paper-kernel fills are modeled at the bar price so the money loss is live-specific, but the asymmetry (legacy guarded, kernel not) means turning on the 'parity' path actually removes a safety rail. Blast radius is testnet unless FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1, but this audit is the pre-mainnet gate.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the bar-staleness check into a shared helper applied inside manage_positions_via_kernel (right after the trim, before reconcile/open), or have _apply_execution_actions skip the kernel dispatch when the corresponding signal row was staleness-blocked. Fail closed on the live path.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:5957-5960 `df = _enrich_scan_frame(fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), interval=timeframe), asset, timeframe)\n        df = _trim_unclosed_latest_candle(df, timeframe)` — then straight into run_strategy_execution/reconcile with no age check. The DI-1 gate at scanner.py:6356-6400 ('Nothing else between the candle fetch and signal generation checks that the latest CLOSED bar is recent ... a data stall ... would generate live signals and size/stop orders off hours-old prices') exists only inside _scan_asset_group. scanner.py:6614-6623 calls manage_positions_via_kernel for kernel/live strategies with no check of the row's blocked state. scanner.py:5880 `_execute_direct("open", ... ref_price, ...)` places a REAL Hyperliquid order on a kernel 'open'.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code; every load-bearing claim holds.

1) No staleness gate on the kernel path. manage_positions_via_kernel (scanner.py:5931-6179) re-fetches its OWN candles (5957-5959: `df = _enrich_scan_frame(fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), interval=timeframe), ...)`) and only calls _trim_unclosed_latest_candle (5960), which merely drops the still-forming bar (def at 103-130: if current_ts < bar_close_ts return df.iloc[:-1] else return df) — it does NOT check that the last CLOSED bar is recent. Reading the full function (through the open/close applier loop at 6131-6172 and return at 6179) there is no bar-age check before reconcile or before opens/closes are applied.

2) DI-1 is legacy-only. The bar-staleness gate (scanner.py:6356-6400) lives inside _scan_asset_group, computes `_age_since_close = get_now().timestamp() - (_last_ts + _bar_secs)` on strat_df, and on staleness emits results.append(_blocked_scan_row(...)) then `continue`. _blocked_scan_row (5154-5189) just sets entry_signal/exit_signal=False and a block_reason on the legacy `signal`.

3) The blocked verdict is ignored for the kernel dispatch. _evaluate_signal_matrix (6509) appends every scanned item — including blocked rows — into signal_rows with no filtering. _apply_execution_actions (6602-6623) then dispatches kernel strategies to manage_positions_via_kernel based ONLY on _paper_kernel_execution_enabled()/_is_kernel_paper_strategy and _live_kernel_execution_enabled()/_is_live_kernel_stage; it never consults signal.get('block_reason'). block_reason is read only in _build_signal_diagnostics (6783) for UI diagnostics, not for gating. Because the kernel re-fetches its own candles anyway, the DI-1 verdict is structurally moot for the parity path.

4) Defaults ON: _paper_kernel_execution_enabled returns _scanner_bool_setting('paper_kernel_execution', True) (5220-5222) and _live_kernel_execution_enabled returns _scanner_bool_setting('live_kernel_execution', True) (5816-5828), so the unguarded path is the default.

5) Real-money reachability on live. _kernel_open_live_trade calls _execute_direct('open', trade_id, strat_id, asset, direction, units, ref_price, stop_loss=..., take_profit=..., leverage=...) at 5880, placing a REAL Hyperliquid order; ref_price = pos.get('entry_price') is the kernel's modeled entry off the (possibly stale) bar, while the exchange fills at the current market price — exactly the open-off-stale-signal asymmetry the finding describes.

6) fetch_candles (1665-1722) does NOT cover the DI-1 scenario: its freshness check (1695) is on cache *publish* age (_CANDLE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS), not on candle bar-time, and 1697-1699 explicitly returns stale cache rather than failing when direct fetch is disabled. So a feed that serves stale-but-recently-cached bars (the precise scenario DI-1 was written to defend) flows into the kernel unblocked.

Severity: keep high. It is a conditional fail-open (requires a feed stall serving non-erroring stale bars, a fresh entry on the stale bar, a live-kernel strategy, and mainnet), and on paper the fill is modeled at the bar price so no real loss — the real-money exposure is live-specific and currently testnet-bounded unless FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1. But this audit is the pre-mainnet gate, and turning on the default 'parity' path genuinely removes the safety rail the legacy path has, where it must fail closed. Not critical (not a guaranteed/silent loss on every run), not lower (it is a real fail-open on the live execution path). The suggested fix (apply the staleness check inside manage_positions_via_kernel after the trim, before reconcile/open) is sound; note the check should be on bar-time, mirroring DI-1's _age_since_close.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanism fully verified against live code. (1) Both controlling flags default ON: scanner.py:5222 paper_kernel_execution=True; scanner.py:5828 live_kernel_execution=True — so the kernel path is the DEFAULT for paper and live. (2) manage_positions_via_kernel re-fetches its own candles (scanner.py:5957-5960), trims only the still-forming bar, and validates only empty/len<20 (5964-5965); I read the whole function to 6179 and confirm NO bar-age/staleness check before reconcile/open. (3) _trim_unclosed_latest_candle (scanner.py:103-130) is not a staleness gate — it KEEPS a stale last closed bar (returns df when current_ts>=bar_close_ts). (4) The only fail-closed bar-staleness gate (DI-1) is at scanner.py:6356-6400 inside _scan_asset_group (legacy signal path) and merely emits a _blocked_scan_row+continue. (5) Blocked rows are appended to signal_rows (scanner.py:6509) and _apply_execution_actions (scanner.py:6614-6623) dispatches kernel/live strategies keyed on _is_kernel_paper_strategy / _is_live_kernel_stage (stage/type), NOT on block_reason; and because the kernel re-fetches candles, the DI-1 verdict is structurally irrelevant to it. (6) Live opens flow scanner.py:6093 _kernel_open_live_trade -> _execute_direct (scanner.py:5880) = REAL Hyperliquid order with stop/target from the stale kernel geometry. (7) No mitigating global guard: check_signal_freshness (scanner.py:7283) is dead (comment-only ref at 6362); fetch_candles (1665-1722) can serve a stale cache without erroring (cache_age is write-age, not bar-age); health_monitor.check_candle_freshness (1017-1089) only reports a DataCheck status and does not halt the scan. The asymmetry is exactly as described: legacy path guarded, default kernel path not. Severity kept at high: the finding honestly bounds impact — paper fills at the bar price so paper stays internally consistent (no real money loss), and live real-money loss requires FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1 (testnet otherwise). It is not a guaranteed per-scan silent loss (so not critical), but it is a verified fail-OPEN where the legacy path fails-CLOSED on the default live execution path, and this is the explicit pre-mainnet gate — a real recoverable-failure / safety-rail gap that must be closed before mainnet.

### `LIVE-EXCHANGE-RECONCILE-1` — Orphan exchange position appearing after startup is never adopted and never given a protective stop by periodic reconcile (naked until restart)

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** live-exchange-reconcile  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/daemon.py:1509-1514; forven/exchange/risk.py:2095, 2126-2134, 2198-2201`
- **Claim:** A live position present on the exchange but absent from SQLite that appears DURING a daemon run (e.g. an open whose exchange order filled but the DB insert crashed, a partial-fill survivor whose SQLite trade was closed, or a manual position) is neither adopted nor protected by the periodic reconcile, and stays untracked + stop-less indefinitely until the next daemon restart or an operator-triggered reconcile.
- **Impact:** A real, leveraged exchange position can sit with no protective stop for an unbounded period (until restart), exposed to full liquidation. The discrepancy does block NEW entries (daemon.py:1043-1053), so the system is contained, but the orphan position itself is unmanaged and unhedged — a direct path to an uncapped loss the kernel/stop machinery was supposed to prevent.
- **Suggested fix:** In the non-adopt periodic pass, still call `_repair_position_protection` for any exchange position with no matching SQLite trade (place/repair an emergency stop even when not adopting), OR run periodic reconcile with adopt_missing_in_sqlite=True so orphans are both tracked and protected on the normal cadence rather than only at restart.
- **Evidence:** Periodic reconcile is called with NO adopt flag, so adoption is off: daemon.py:1509 `recon = await _to_thread_with_timeout("daemon.reconcile_all_books", RISK_RECONCILE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS, reconcile_all_books, _get_testnet())` and reconcile_all_books defaults `adopt_missing_in_sqlite: bool = False` (risk.py:2345). Only daemon STARTUP passes `adopt_missing_in_sqlite=True` (daemon.py:821). In reconcile_exchange_positions, the protection-repair (`_repair_position_protection`) is reached ONLY in the matched branch (risk.py:2054) and the adopt branch (risk.py:2126-2134). When adopt is False and the asset is on the exchange but not in db_by_asset, control falls straight through to `discrepancies.append({"type": "missing_in_sqlite", ...})` (risk.py:2198-2201) with NO `_repair_position_protection` call. The 60s liquidation check (daemon.py:1425) only ALERTS, it does not place a stop.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified at every cited line. (1) Periodic reconcile is non-adopt: daemon.py:1509-1514 calls reconcile_all_books(_get_testnet()) with no adopt kwarg; reconcile_all_books defaults adopt_missing_in_sqlite=False (risk.py:2345) and propagates that default into reconcile_exchange_positions (risk.py:2378-2383, 2414-2418). (2) Only adopt=True callers are daemon STARTUP (daemon.py:819-824) and the operator-manual reconcile (control_plane/ops.py:589-592, logs "Operator requested exchange reconciliation"); cli.py:1386 is also operator-manual and defaults False. (3) In reconcile_exchange_positions the loop `for asset, position in hl_by_asset.items()` (risk.py:2023) calls _repair_position_protection ONLY in the matched branch (`if asset in db_by_asset:`, repair at risk.py:2054, then continue at 2094) and the adopt branch (`if adopt_missing_in_sqlite:`, repair at risk.py:2127, then continue at 2196). When adopt is False and the asset is absent from db_by_asset, control falls through to discrepancies.append({"type":"missing_in_sqlite",...}) at risk.py:2198-2201 with NO _repair_position_protection — exactly as claimed. (4) db_by_asset is built solely from `SELECT * FROM trades WHERE status='OPEN'` (risk.py:1986,1994-1999), so a closed-trade partial-fill survivor, a DB-insert-crash open, or a manual position genuinely land in the orphan fall-through. (5) The 60s _check_liquidation_distances (daemon.py:1178-1288, invoked at 1425) only emits notifications (emit_notification at 1271-1283); it never places a stop. (6) The discrepancy blocks new entries via recovery_requires_operator/blocked (daemon.py:1043-1057) — system is contained for NEW opens but the orphan itself stays untracked and stop-less. (7) selfheal.py contains no reconcile/recovery/adopt/restart logic (grep returned no matches), and a blocked-recovery state is not a freeze, so nothing auto-re-runs adopt=True; the naked window is unbounded until a daemon restart or operator-triggered reconcile. The impact (a real leveraged exchange position exposed to liquidation with no protective stop until restart/operator action) holds. Severity high is correct, not critical: the exposure is NOT silent (operator is alerted via the blocked-recovery state and the reconciliation warning, and new entries are halted) and it requires an upstream failure to create the orphan, so it falls short of the "silently loses money/corrupts positions" critical bar while clearly exceeding medium (real recoverable failure exposing real money).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) Periodic reconcile at daemon.py:1509-1514 calls reconcile_all_books(_get_testnet()) with no adopt flag; the default is adopt_missing_in_sqlite=False (risk.py:2345), and reconcile_all_books propagates that False to every per-account pass (risk.py:2380, 2414-2418). (2) Only daemon startup (daemon.py:821) and the operator-triggered manual reconcile (control_plane/ops.py:590) pass adopt=True. (3) In reconcile_exchange_positions, _repair_position_protection is reached ONLY in the matched branch (risk.py:2054) and the adopt branch (risk.py:2127). db_by_asset is built from status='OPEN' trades only (risk.py:1986), so a closed-trade residual is unmatched. When adopt is False and the exchange asset is not in db_by_asset, control falls straight to discrepancies.append({type:'missing_in_sqlite'}) at risk.py:2198-2201 with NO protection repair — exactly as claimed. (4) _repair_position_protection (risk.py:1309-1393) works with matched_trade=None, deriving an emergency_risk_clamp stop (risk.py:1341-1347) and placing it, so the protection machinery is intentionally orphan-capable and the suggested fix is feasible; the periodic path simply never calls it. (5) The 60s liquidation check (_check_liquidation_distances, daemon.py:1178-1287) only emits notifications and places no stop, and it skips cross-margin positions lacking per-position liquidationPx (daemon.py:1252-1263), so some orphans get no alert at all. (6) Discrepancies set recovery_requires_operator=True and block NEW entries (daemon.py:1043-1057) but do not protect/adopt the orphan; selfheal.py is strategy-code validation, not daemon restart, so no automatic process re-runs startup adoption for a healthy-but-blocked daemon. Reachability: the reconcile runs against whatever creds point to (mainnet for live operators); a manual live position, a crashed DB insert after a fill, or a partial-fill residual after a SQLite close all reach the unprotected branch and persist until operator restart or operator reconcile. Impact is a genuine uncapped-loss exposure on a leveraged live position. It does not silently lose money by itself (needs an adverse move) and has partial compensating controls (entry block + liquidation alerts), so this is a real recoverable failure = HIGH, not critical. Severity unchanged (high).

### `DIRECTION-BOOKS-ACCOUNTING-2` — Kernel-live OPEN calls _execute_direct unwrapped: a failed/rejected open leaves a phantom recorded-OPEN live trade and leaks the risk slot (legacy path handles this; kernel path does not)

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** direction-books-accounting  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5876-5882 (_kernel_open_live_trade), 6131-6155 (action loop except), 3335-3373 (_execute_direct open raises); contrast forven/scanner.py:4753-4846 + 3963-4032 (_open_via_execution)`
- **Claim:** _kernel_open_live_trade records the trade in SQLite and registers the risk slot, THEN calls _execute_direct('open', ...) with no try/except. _execute_direct raises on a margin rejection, a re-asserted halt, a leverage-set failure, or a missing stop. The exception is swallowed by the generic loop except, leaving a recorded OPEN live trade with no real exchange fill and a held risk slot, unlike the legacy path, which marks pending_open_reconcile and releases the slot.
- **Impact:** On any live open failure (the most likely being a margin rejection, which is MORE likely here precisely because of the mis-sizing in finding 1), the kernel-live path strands a phantom OPEN live row: the operator's live position/P&L view shows a position that does not exist on the exchange, the risk slot stays consumed (blocking same-asset reopen), and on a later kernel close decision _kernel_close_live_trade may book fabricated PnL from the signal prices against a position that never existed. State corruption + misleading live numbers.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the _execute_direct('open', ...) call in _kernel_open_live_trade exactly like _open_via_execution: on failure, stamp pending_open_reconcile + open_execution_failure_reason on the trade and call release(trade_id) so the slot is freed and the reconciler can adopt-or-cancel the row, rather than leaving a phantom OPEN.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:5876-5882: `try: register(...) except Exception: pass` then `_execute_direct("open", trade_id, ...)` (unwrapped) then `return`. _execute_direct raises: `if stop_loss is None and not is_sim_active(): raise ValueError(...)` (3336-3337), halt re-assert `raise RuntimeError(...)` (3344-3345), set_leverage failure `raise RuntimeError(...)` (3353-3356), and order error `if result.get("error"): raise RuntimeError(result.get("error"))` (3372-3373). The only catch is the loop's `except Exception as exc: log.error(...)` at scanner.py:6154; it logs and continues; it does NOT mark the trade pending or release the slot. The legacy path instead uses `_open_via_execution` which wraps _execute_direct in try/except and returns (False, error) (scanner.py:4010-4032); on failure the caller writes `pending_open_reconcile` and calls `release(str(trade_id))` (scanner.py:4816-4832).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Confirmed against live code. In `_kernel_open_live_trade` (forven/scanner.py:5873-5882): `_open_trade_db(...)` records the live trade (5873), `register(...)` consumes the risk slot (5877, wrapped only in try/except:pass), then `_execute_direct("open", ...)` is called UNWRAPPED at 5880-5881 followed by `return`. `_execute_direct` open genuinely raises on real failure modes: missing stop ValueError (3336-3337), re-asserted halt RuntimeError (3344-3345), set_leverage failure RuntimeError (3353-3356), and most importantly a margin/order rejection `if result.get("error"): raise RuntimeError(result.get("error"))` (3372-3373) — reachable in live (non-sim) since market_order hits the real exchange. The ONLY catch is the action-loop `except Exception as exc: log.error(...)` at 6154-6155, which logs and continues; it does NOT stamp pending_open_reconcile nor call release. Result: a recorded OPEN live trade row with no real fill plus a held risk slot. Contrast confirmed: the legacy path wraps _execute_direct in try/except returning (False, error) (4010-4032) and on failure stamps pending_open_reconcile/open_execution_failure_reason and calls release(str(trade_id)) (4815-4846). The slot leak is durable: register inserts into portfolio_positions (risk.py:718-758) which can_open's one-per-asset gate reads, and _rebuild_portfolio_positions skips a failed-open row ONLY when pending_open_reconcile is set without an exchange order id (risk.py:797-809) — since the kernel path never sets that flag, the phantom OPEN row is RE-ADDED on every rebuild (812-822), permanently holding the slot and surfacing as a live position. A later kernel close (_kernel_close_live_trade, 5885-5928) would then book fabricated PnL from signal prices via _close_trade_db (5913-5914). The defect is real and reachable exactly as described. Severity 'high' is appropriate and unchanged: impact is local-state corruption / misleading live numbers / blocked same-asset reopen rather than direct on-exchange money loss (there is no real exchange position behind the phantom row).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): CONFIRMED and reachable on a default-on live path. scanner.py:5872-5882 (_kernel_open_live_trade): _open_trade_db writes the OPEN row (5873), register(...) takes the risk slot (5877), then _execute_direct("open", ...) is called UNWRAPPED (5880-5881) with a bare `return` after. _execute_direct raises on every documented live (non-sim) condition: missing stop -> ValueError (3336-3337), halt re-assert -> RuntimeError (3344-3345), set_leverage failure -> RuntimeError (3353-3356), and order error -> RuntimeError(result.get("error")) (3372-3373, the margin-rejection path). The only handler is the action loop's generic `except Exception as exc: log.error(...)` at scanner.py:6154, which logs and continues — it does NOT release the slot or stamp pending_open_reconcile. Contrast verified: legacy _open_via_execution wraps _execute_direct in try/except returning (False,str(e)) (4010-4032) and the caller stamps pending_open_reconcile + open_execution_failure_reason and calls release(str(trade_id)) (4816-4846). So the kernel path strands a recorded OPEN live row with no real fill and a held risk slot. Slot leak is durable in the interim: register persists to SQLite portfolio_positions (risk.py:747-756) and _rebuild_portfolio_positions only skips re-adding rows flagged pending_open_reconcile without an exchange order id (risk.py:797) — a flag the kernel path never sets — so the slot survives rebuilds and blocks same-asset reopen. Reachability: live kernel wired at scanner.py:6619-6623, live_kernel_execution defaults True (5828), fires for live/live_graduated/deployed strategies; money impact testnet-bounded unless FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1 but state/number corruption happens on testnet too. Severity stays HIGH (not critical): reconcile_exchange_positions (risk.py:1924+) periodically detects the phantom as a ghost, auto-closes it and calls release(str(tid)) (2279), so the corruption is RECOVERABLE with a bounded window rather than permanent/silent loss. That same ghost-close, for a never-filled open, has no fill to recover and force-closes at the exchange mid (price_map.get(asset_key), 2240-2247), booking fabricated PnL against a position that never existed — which corroborates the finding's misleading-live-numbers impact. The suggested fix (wrap _execute_direct in _kernel_open_live_trade like _open_via_execution: on failure stamp pending_open_reconcile and release(trade_id)) is correct and matches the legacy contract.

### `DIRECTION-BOOKS-ACCOUNTING-3` — Reconcile pass scoping uses the settings-swallowing books.book_address(): a transient DB-lock mis-scopes a routed sub-account trade into the master ghost-close pass and auto-closes a real position

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** direction-books-accounting  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:1772-1785 (_trade_routed_address), 1992 (scope filter), 2203-2247 (ghost auto-close), 2342-2404 (reconcile_all_books single books_enabled read, no debounce); forven/exchange/books.py:47-54,109-121; contrast hardened close path forven/scanner.py:3601-3621`
- **Claim:** The reconcile safety scope keys each pass on _trade_routed_address(trade), which resolves the trade's book via books.book_address() -> books._settings() -> kv_get wrapped in a bare try/except that returns {} on a 'database is locked' read, plus its own `except Exception: return None`. A transient settings/DB-lock read during reconcile makes a real short-/long-sub-account trade resolve to address None, so it is excluded from its own book's pass and INCLUDED in the master pass (where its real position is absent) and is auto-closed as a ghost at the master mid price. reconcile_all_books trusts a single books_enabled() read with no debounce.
- **Impact:** During a transient kv/DB lock coinciding with a reconcile sweep (startup recovery or operator reconcile), real sub-account positions can be mis-scoped to the master pass and ghost-closed at the master mid: fabricated PnL booked, the risk slot released, and the REAL sub-account position left open and unmanaged (no longer tracked). Dropping/abandoning a real money position. Lower probability (requires a transient lock) but severe consequence; the codebase already recognized the identical failure mode on the close path.
