- **Suggested fix:** Resolve the routing address for reconcile scoping the same hardened way as _resolve_trade_vault_address: read settings via a kv_get that RE-RAISES on a locked DB, and on any resolution failure treat the trade as UNRESOLVABLE (skip the ghost-close / surface a degraded marker) rather than defaulting to None=master. Add the same books_enabled() debounce reconcile_all_books relies on so a single transient False read can't collapse all passes to master-only.
- **Evidence:** risk.py:1772-1785: `_trade_routed_address` -> `return _norm_addr(books.book_address(book))` inside `try/except Exception: return None`. books.book_address (books.py:109-121) calls _settings(); _settings (books.py:47-54) does `try: raw = kv_get(...) except Exception: raw = {}` (swallowing a locked-DB read to {} -> address None). risk.py:1992: `db_trades = [t for t in db_trades if _trade_routed_address(t) == scope_address]`. Ghost auto-close: risk.py:2203-2247 closes every ghost via close_trade_record at recovered-fill-or-mid and `release(str(tid))` (2279). reconcile_all_books reads `books_on = books.books_enabled()` once (risk.py:2365) and resolves addresses with `books.book_address(label)` per row (2400-2404) with no debounce, whereas daemon._book_aware_account_value DOES debounce a transient books_enabled()=False flip via _BOOKS_OFF_CONFIRM_TICKS (daemon.py:1100-1117). The close path was explicitly hardened against this exact swallow-to-None hazard (scanner.py:3601-3621 BOOKS-1, reading settings via kv_get that re-raises and failing CLOSED), but the reconcile scoping path was NOT.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every link of the described chain is verified in the live code. (1) books._settings() (books.py:50-53) swallows kv_get exceptions to {}; kv_get (db.py:3513-3519) RE-RAISES a 'database is locked' OperationalError (only swallows 'no such table: kv'), so a transient lock degrades settings to {}. (2) book_address('short', {}) -> short_book_address({}) -> _clean_address(None) -> None (books.py:72-74,119). (3) _trade_routed_address (risk.py:1781-1785) returns _norm_addr(None)=None (also caught by its own except->None). (4) Scope filter risk.py:1992 keeps trades where _trade_routed_address(t)==scope_address; the master pass has scope_address=_norm_addr(None)=None (risk.py:1968) and ALWAYS runs (address_labels seeded {None:None} at risk.py:2391, inserted first), so the mis-resolved short trade (None==None) is INCLUDED in the master pass. (5) The master-wallet snapshot lacks the sub-account position -> ghost; is_local_only_paper_trade (trade_state.py:65-68) returns False for live exec_type so a real live short is NOT exempt -> appended to ghost_trades (risk.py:2021) and auto-closed via close_trade_record at recovered-fill-or-mid + release(tid) (risk.py:2230-2279). Once CLOSED, the later short-book pass's SELECT WHERE status='OPEN' cannot see it -> real position left untracked (missing_in_sqlite). (6) reconcile_all_books reads books_enabled() once with no debounce (risk.py:2365) and resolves per-row via books.book_address(label) (risk.py:2404); a sweep-long lock collapses to master-only. By contrast daemon._book_aware_account_value debounces a transient books_enabled()=False flip via _BOOKS_OFF_CONFIRM_TICKS (daemon.py:1100-1117), and the close path was explicitly hardened against this identical swallow-to-None hazard (scanner.py:3601-3621 BOOKS-1, kv_get that re-raises + fail CLOSED) while the reconcile scoping path was not. The sole conditional is the trigger: 'database is locked' on a READ with busy_timeout=60000 in WAL is uncommon within a single process, so probability is low — which the finding itself acknowledges, and the maintainers already deemed this exact failure mode real enough to harden the twin close path. The code literally does what the claim says and is reachable under DB-lock contention during reconcile. Severity high is appropriate: critical-grade consequence (abandoned real-money position + fabricated PnL/state corruption) tempered by an edge-case trigger.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanism fully verified in live code. (1) `_trade_routed_address` (risk.py:1772-1785) resolves a routed trade via `books.book_address(book)` with no settings arg, running through `books._settings(None)`. (2) `books._settings` (books.py:50-53) does `try: raw = kv_get(...) except Exception: raw = {}`. (3) Linchpin confirmed: `kv_get` (db.py:3513-3519) catches `sqlite3.OperationalError` ONLY for "no such table: kv" and otherwise re-raises, so a "database is locked" read propagates -> `_settings` swallows it to `{}` -> `short_book_address({})`/`long_book_address({})` -> None. (4) Scope filter (risk.py:1992) `_trade_routed_address(t) == scope_address`: in the MASTER pass (scope None, always inserted first at risk.py:2391 and run first), a routed trade collapsed to None is INCLUDED; its real position lives in the sub-account so it is absent from the master snapshot -> ghost_trades (it is a live trade, so the line 2006 local-only-paper skip does not apply) -> auto-closed at master mid (risk.py:2239-2247) with slot release(2279). (5) Hardening asymmetry is real: the close path `_resolve_trade_vault_address` (scanner.py:3601-3621, BOOKS-1) reads settings via a re-raising kv_get and fails CLOSED on exactly this swallow-to-None hazard, and daemon._book_aware_account_value debounces transient books_enabled() flips (daemon.py:1106-1117); reconcile_all_books reads books_enabled() once (risk.py:2365) and resolves addresses with the swallowing books.book_address (no debounce, no re-raise). Reachability/impact refinements: gated behind live_books_enabled (default False, books.py:64) plus a precisely-timed transient SQLite lock during the master pass scope resolution -> genuinely low probability. The "real position abandoned/unmanaged" worst case is partly mitigated on the production callers (daemon startup recovery daemon.py:819-821 and operator reconcile ops.py:589-590 pass adopt_missing_in_sqlite=True), so the subsequent same-asset book pass would re-adopt the still-open sub-account position in the same sweep; the CLI caller (cli.py:1386) uses adopt default False and would only flag a missing_in_sqlite discrepancy. The durable, unmitigated harm is the original routed trade being force-closed with FABRICATED PnL at the master mid (master _recover_exit_from_fills finds no closing fills -> falls back to price_map master mid, risk.py:2240), slot released, and original trade/protection lineage lost = corrupted realized-PnL accounting. Defect is real and reachable; severity stays high (severe consequence, but probability capped by non-default flag + transient-lock timing, and worst-case abandonment partially healed by adoption), not critical.

### `PROMOTION-GATE-PARITY-3` — Live-promotion gate counts non-parity legacy paper rows the system itself flags as 'must not be promoted to live on these numbers'

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** promotion-gate-parity  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:6656-6663 (non_vectorizable_legacy flag) and 5642-5651 (converge), 5524-5537 (late close); forven/policy.py:3713-3721`
- **Claim:** When a strategy has no vectorized signals the scanner trades it on the legacy per-bar engine (default paper_legacy_fallback_enabled=True) and records margin-scale rows, explicitly warning they are NOT backtest-parity and 'must not be promoted to live on these numbers'. Late-entry closes and converge/orphan closes likewise produce margin-scale paper rows. Yet the ->live gate query filters only `execution_type LIKE 'paper%'` with no exclusion of these rows, and there is no persisted marker distinguishing them (diagnostics_out is in-memory per-scan only).
- **Impact:** Strategies that never achieved backtest parity (legacy-engine fills) and config-flip/orphan artifacts are counted toward the live-promotion return/drawdown/sample/trade-count decision, directly contradicting the codebase's own stated rule. Cross-asset/converge artifacts (pnl 0) also pad the min_closed_trades sample.
- **Suggested fix:** Persist a parity marker on each closed trade (e.g. signal_data.kernel_managed / execution_decision) and have the ->live gate and readiness checks EXCLUDE non_vectorizable_legacy and converge/cross_asset_orphan rows, or refuse to promote a strategy whose paper book contains any non-parity row.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:6659 `"execution_decision": "non_vectorizable_legacy"`, with scanner.py:6654-6655 comment `... must not be promoted to live on these numbers`; _paper_legacy_fallback_enabled default True (scanner.py:5239). Late close leaves net_pnl_pct unset (margin-scale pnl_pct survives): scanner.py:5524-5537 (the `if late:` branch returns WITHOUT the pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct override that faithful kernel closes do at 5544-5550). Converge close uses close_trade_record only (no net_pnl_pct write): scanner.py:5646-5650. Gate query has no exclusion: policy.py:3714-3721 (only status='CLOSED', pnl_pct NOT NULL, execution_type LIKE 'paper%').
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All load-bearing code claims verified against live code. (1) scanner.py:6659 records execution_decision "non_vectorizable_legacy" with the comment at 6654-6655 "must not be promoted to live on these numbers"; _paper_legacy_fallback_enabled() defaults True (scanner.py:5239), and on fallback the code falls through (no continue) to legacy manage_positions() at scanner.py:6704, which records execution_type="paper_challenger" (scanner.py:4279, matches LIKE 'paper%') and closes via _close_trade_db (scanner.py:4140). (2) Late close branch scanner.py:5524-5537 returns after only stamping closed_at, skipping the faithful net override at 5544-5550, so net_pnl_pct stays NULL and close_trade_record's leveraged pnl_pct (= (exit-entry)/entry*signed*leverage, trade_state.py:268) survives. (3) Converge close scanner.py:5646-5650 calls close_trade_record only (net_pnl_pct NULL); cross-asset orphan scanner.py:5675-5679 closes at entry (pnl_pct~0, still counted, padding min_closed_trades). (4) The paper->live promotion gate query policy.py:3713-3721 selects COALESCE(net_pnl_pct, pnl_pct) filtering ONLY status='CLOSED', pnl_pct IS NOT NULL, execution_type LIKE 'paper%' — no exclusion of non-parity rows, and a grep of policy.py shows no kernel_managed/non_vectorizable/converge/cross_asset marker is ever consulted. The diagnostics_out 'non_vectorizable_legacy' flag is in-memory per-scan only and never persisted on the trade row. Confirmed beyond the finding: compute_live_metrics (policy.py:3892-3900) compounds each pnl as an equity fraction (equity *= 1+pnl), but faithful kernel rows store equity-fraction net (scanner.py:5509) while legacy/late/converge rows store leverage-inclusive position returns (per the code's own comment at scanner.py:5538-5540), so the gate mixes incompatible PnL scales — distorting the total_return_pct and max_drawdown_pct that gate real-money promotion. Defect is real and reachable: legacy fallback is on by default and the converge/cross-asset cleanup paths are ungated. Severity high is appropriate: it corrupts a real-money gating decision via wrong/non-parity numbers (and can spuriously pass OR fail the gate due to the leverage-scale inflation), but does not itself execute a money-losing trade, so not critical.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Core claim verified against live code. The ->live promotion gate (policy.py:3713-3721) selects COALESCE(net_pnl_pct, pnl_pct) from trades filtered ONLY by status='CLOSED', pnl_pct NOT NULL, execution_type LIKE 'paper%', and the stage window — with NO exclusion of non-parity rows and no signal_data parity-marker filter. compute_live_metrics (policy.py:3869+) then compounds every row into total_return/max_dd and counts every row in total_trades.

LEG 1 (non_vectorizable_legacy) CONFIRMED and is the high-severity driver. _paper_legacy_fallback_enabled defaults True (scanner.py:5239) and paper_kernel_execution defaults True (5222). When the kernel returns None for a paper-stage strategy with no vectorized signals, scanner.py:6704 falls through to manage_positions, which records trades with execution_type='paper_challenger' (4279, matches LIKE 'paper%') and closes via _close_trade_db (4140). _close_trade_db writes net_pnl_pct on a LEVERAGE-INCLUSIVE MARGIN scale (explicit comment 3720-3722) — whereas the faithful kernel close writes net_pnl_pct as an EQUITY-FRACTION (5509, 5544). The gate therefore mixes two incompatible PnL scales, and a fully non-vectorizable strategy's entire paper book is the wrong (margin) scale feeding a real-money gate, directly contradicting the in-code rule at 6654-6655 ('must not be promoted to live on these numbers'). The only non-parity marker is diagnostics_out, which is in-memory per-scan (confirmed).

LEG 2 (late-entry close, 5524-5537) is REFUTED as a forward path: late_entry_enabled is HARD-CODED False (scanner.py:6069, 'not operator-gateable') and reconcile is called with late_entry=False (6087), so no new late_entry trades can be produced. The described mechanics (late branch returns without the net_pnl_pct override at 5544-5550, leaving margin-scale pnl_pct via close_trade_record at 5514) are accurate but only affect pre-existing DB rows from when the feature was briefly enabled.

LEG 3 (converge/cross-asset orphan) CONFIRMED reachable: paper_kernel_converge_orphans defaults True (6091), paper-only. Both _kernel_close_orphan (5646-5650) and _kernel_close_cross_asset_orphan (5675-5679) call close_trade_record only, leaving net_pnl_pct NULL so the gate's COALESCE picks the margin-scale pnl_pct (converge: non-zero off last_close) or pnl_pct=0 (cross-asset, padding min_closed_trades). These are documented real events (S04545 data-source switch / config flips), so the gate definitely ingests them.

Reachability: gate path is live-money, default-on, and independently confirmed via the converge/cross-asset legs even setting aside non-vectorizable strategies. The one residual uncertainty is how often a genuinely non-vectorizable strategy reaches the paper stage in this deployment (would require tracing the gauntlet/backtest entry conditions), but the dedicated default-on fallback branch and operator-facing warnings show the developers treat it as a real scenario. Severity stays high (wrong numbers feeding a real-money promotion decision); the dead late-entry sub-claim does not lower the severity of the confirmed core.

### `CONCURRENT-SCAN-RACE-1` — No single-flight guard around run_scan; concurrent execution triggers share one process and bypass the scheduler's per-job lock

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** concurrent-scan-race  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:6811 (run_scan, no guard); forven/api.py:438 (scheduler runs as a thread in the API process); forven/api_domains/paper.py:2315-2353; forven/scheduler.py:893 (_try_mark_job_running), 1326-1337, 3070-3078; forven/control_plane/ops.py:534; forven/cli.py:565`
- **Claim:** run_scan has no cross-thread/cross-process single-flight guard, and at least four independent triggers can invoke it concurrently within the SAME process, so two execution scans can interleave on the same OPEN live trade.
- **Impact:** Enables every downstream race in this report: two scans can each read the same OPEN live trade and both compute open/close/refresh actions for it. The damage is bounded by reduce_only and the unique index (see verified_correct), but residual money/state hazards remain (RACE-2, RACE-3). Operationally it also means redundant exchange order traffic and duplicate post-mortems on every overlap.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap run_scan's execution phase in a real single-flight guard that ALL callers share — e.g. a DB-backed advisory lock (a dedicated kv/`scheduler_jobs`-style row 'scanner_execution_run' acquired via the same atomic compare-and-set as _try_mark_job_running) acquired at run_scan entry when execute_positions=True, with a stale-takeover timeout. The scheduler-job lock alone is insufficient because the API/control-plane/CLI callers bypass it.
- **Evidence:** run_scan begins `init_db(); requested_execution = bool(execute_positions); ...` (scanner.py:6816) with no lock acquisition; a grep for `threading.|Lock(|RLock|filelock|in_progress|acquire(` over scanner.py returns NO matches. The scheduler loop is started as a supervised runtime THREAD inside the API process: `_spawn_supervised_runtime_thread("scheduler-loop", lambda: run_scheduler_loop(interval_seconds=30), ...)` (api.py:438). The scheduler's only mutual-exclusion is `_try_mark_job_running(...)` — `UPDATE scheduler_jobs SET running_since=? WHERE id=? AND (running_since IS NULL OR ... OR running_since < ?)` (scheduler.py:905-913) — which is keyed on the scheduler JOB id and therefore only prevents `forven-scanner-hourly` from overlapping ITSELF. The API path `def _run_scanner_once(...): ... run_scan(execute_positions=execution_positions)` (paper.py:2319) and `start_paper_service(...)` kicking `_run_scanner_once(execute_positions=True)` (paper.py:2353), `control_plane/ops.py:534 run_scan(...)`, and `cli.py:565 run_scan()` never touch scheduler_jobs at all, so they are not serialized against the scheduler scan. A sync FastAPI handler (start paper service) runs on a Starlette worker thread while the scheduler job runs on its own ThreadPoolExecutor thread (scheduler.py:1190 `_run_sync_job`) — two threads, one process, no shared guard.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every code claim is verified against the live source. (1) No single-flight guard exists: a grep for threading./Lock(/RLock/filelock/in_progress/.acquire(/single-flight/advisory over scanner.py returns zero matches; run_scan (scanner.py:6811-6818) acquires nothing, just init_db() + flag reads. The only Lock in the codebase touching the scanner area is data.py:156 _catalog_scan_lock, which guards the data-catalog scan, not run_scan execution. (2) Four independent triggers call run_scan and only the scheduler uses a lock: scheduler.py:1333 (scanner_run kind, run on a ThreadPoolExecutor worker per scheduler.py:1190 _run_sync_job); paper.py:2319 _run_scanner_once→run_scan, kicked with execute_positions=True by start_paper_service at paper.py:2353; control_plane/ops.py:534 (manual operator scan, only gated by is_trading_allowed(), not a concurrency lock); cli.py:565 (separate process). (3) The scheduler loop is spawned as an in-process thread in the API process (api.py:436-440), so a Starlette request thread running start_paper_service/manual scan can run concurrently with the scheduler-job thread in the same process. (4) _try_mark_job_running (scheduler.py:905-913) is an atomic CAS keyed on the scheduler job id only — it serializes forven-scanner-hourly against itself, and the paper/ops/CLI callers never touch scheduler_jobs, so none are serialized against it. (5) The hazard reaches the exchange: execution_fast_path_enabled defaults True (scanner.py:708-709), so in the default path _close_via_execution/_open_via_execution call _execute_direct(...) inline (scanner.py:3935-3952) rather than queuing to a single serialized worker — two overlapping scans can both reach _execute_direct on the same OPEN live trade. The daemon does not call run_scan directly (no match in daemon.py); it drives scans via the scheduler job, so all execution paths are accounted for. The finding honestly bounds its own direct damage (reduce_only + unique index) and defers the deeper money/state corruption to RACE-2/RACE-3; the structural defect (missing cross-thread/cross-process single-flight guard around inline live execution) is real and reachable exactly as described. Severity unchanged at high: a missing guard that permits two execution engines to operate on the same live Hyperliquid position simultaneously, producing redundant real-exchange order traffic and duplicate post-mortems and acting as the enabler for the downstream state-corruption races, is a legitimate high-severity correctness hazard for a system about to handle real money — even with the bounding guards in place.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: medium): The structural claim is verified against live code. (1) run_scan (scanner.py:6811-6818) does `init_db(); requested_execution = bool(execute_positions); ...` with NO lock; a grep over scanner.py for threading./Lock(/RLock/filelock/in_progress/.acquire(/single_flight returns no matches. (2) The scheduler loop runs as a supervised THREAD inside the API process (api.py:436-440; FORVEN_API_RUNTIME_THREAD_MODE defaults True at api.py:431) on a dedicated ThreadPoolExecutor (scheduler.py:1190-1198). (3) The only mutual-exclusion is _try_mark_job_running's `UPDATE scheduler_jobs SET running_since=? WHERE id=? AND (...)` (scheduler.py:905-913), which is keyed on the JOB id and so only stops forven-scanner-hourly overlapping itself. (4) Three callers bypass scheduler_jobs entirely: paper.py:2319 (_run_scanner_once->run_scan), reached by start_paper_service which is a SYNC FastAPI handler (routers/paper.py:32-34) running on a Starlette worker thread in the same process; ops.py:534 (manual operator scan, sync route); and cli.py:565 (separate process, shared DB). So two run_scan(execute_positions=True) can interleave in one process with no shared guard — confirmed.\n\nReachability/impact corrections that lower severity from high to medium: (a) The daemon does NOT call run_scan (no matches in daemon.py), and run_signal_scan = run_scan(execute_positions=False) (scanner.py:7054-7056), so the concurrently-scheduled forven-scanner-signal job applies NO position actions. During normal autonomous operation only forven-scanner-hourly runs execution scans, and it is serialized against itself. Two EXECUTION scans interleaving therefore requires an OPERATOR-initiated trigger (start-paper kick — itself gated by `not already_running` at paper.py:2352 — or a manual ops scan, or a CLI run) coinciding with the scheduled run; it is not a constant background condition. (b) The finding itself concedes the direct money/state damage is bounded by reduce_only and the unique index, and defers the real hazards to separate findings (RACE-2, RACE-3). As a standalone defect this is a latent/defense-in-depth concurrency gap (missing single-flight guard) that is real and reachable but does not by itself silently lose money or corrupt positions, so medium is the defensible severity; the suggested DB-backed advisory lock shared by all callers is the correct fix.

## CONFIRMED — MEDIUM (37)

### `PNL-2` — pnl_usd is stored GROSS (no fees/slippage) on legacy/manual/converge/live closes but NET on kernel closes; paper sandbox equity (SUM(pnl_usd)) and next-trade sizing overstate on non-kernel closes

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** pnl  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/trade_state.py:274,301-303 (pnl_usd gross); forven/scanner.py:3742-3746 (fees only -> net_pnl_pct, pnl_usd untouched); forven/scanner.py:5511 (kernel pnl_usd NET); forven/scanner.py:604-615 (paper equity = SUM(pnl_usd))`
- **Claim:** close_trade_record computes pnl_usd = (exit-entry)*size*signed with NO cost deduction and writes it to both pnl and pnl_usd. _close_trade_db then deducts fees only into net_pnl_pct/fees_pct, leaving pnl_usd GROSS. The kernel path instead writes pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net, which IS net of fees+slippage+funding. There is no net_pnl_usd column, so the two paths disagree on what pnl_usd means.
- **Impact:** Same worked example: a legacy/manual paper close stores pnl_usd = $900 (gross), but the true net is ~$891.90 (fee/slippage ~$8/trade at lev 3). The kernel path stores $888.30 (net). On a legacy or mixed paper book, the displayed paper-card equity and the SUM(pnl_usd) that drives next-trade sizing accumulate the un-deducted costs, overstating equity and slightly over-sizing subsequent trades. Live trades close the same gross way, but live equity is read from real HL balance so only paper is affected. Per-trade magnitude is small (one round-trip fee) but it compounds over a long paper book.
- **Suggested fix:** Deduct the round-trip fee+slippage from pnl_usd on the legacy/manual close paths (mirror the kernel: net dollars), or add a net_pnl_usd column and have _get_paper_strategy_equity sum the NET dollars so paper equity matches realized net carry on every path.
- **Evidence:** trade_state.py:274 `pnl_usd = (resolved_exit_price - entry_price) * size * signed`; trade_state.py:301-303 writes pnl=pnl_usd (gross). scanner.py:3744-3745 `UPDATE trades SET fees_pct = ?, net_pnl_pct = ? WHERE id = ?` — pnl_usd/pnl are NOT updated. Kernel: scanner.py:5511 `pnl_usd = round(float(equity_at_entry) * pnl_pct_net, 4)` where pnl_pct_net is net-of-drag-and-funding. Paper equity: scanner.py:604 `SELECT COALESCE(SUM(pnl_usd), 0.0) AS realized` feeds _get_paper_strategy_equity (scanner.py:615 `_PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL + realized`), which is then used as sizing_equity for the next position (scanner.py:5454-5457, 4555-4561).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited code verified literally. trade_state.py:274 computes pnl_usd = (resolved_exit_price - entry_price) * size * signed (GROSS, no fee/slippage deduction); lines 291/293/301/303 write that same gross value to BOTH pnl and pnl_usd. _close_trade_db (scanner.py:3743-3746) then issues `UPDATE trades SET fees_pct = ?, net_pnl_pct = ?` only — it never touches pnl_usd, so the legacy/manual/converge/live close paths leave pnl_usd GROSS. By contrast the kernel faithful-close path computes pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net (scanner.py:5511, NET-of-drag/funding) and overrides the row at 5544-5545 (`SET ... pnl=?, pnl_usd=?` = NET). This is the ONLY path that normalizes pnl_usd to net. Confirmed there is no net_pnl_usd column (the only match, bot_factory/runner.py:528, is an unrelated local var), so the two paths genuinely disagree on pnl_usd semantics. _get_paper_strategy_equity (scanner.py:604 `SUM(pnl_usd)`, 615 initial + realized) sums this inconsistent column and is wired into sizing_equity at 4296/5588/6044, which feeds _sizing.position_units at 5454-5457 and 4555-4561. Reachable non-kernel paper closes that store gross: _close_paper_manual_price_exits (5699-5718, explicitly paper, manual SL/TP), the manual-owned/legacy exit loop (4104-4140), and late hop-in kernel closes (5524-5537, which deliberately skip the 5544 net override). No later reconcile/sweep re-normalizes pnl_usd for the scanner path (db.py:7595-7629 is the separate bot_factory bot_runner subsystem). Impact direction is correct: gross > net (fees omitted) overstates SUM(pnl_usd) -> overstated paper-card equity -> slight over-sizing of subsequent paper trades; live is unaffected because live sizing uses _get_real_account_equity (6041), matching the finding's caveat. The promotion gate uses net_pnl_pct (net on both paths), so harm is scoped to displayed paper equity + next-trade sizing exactly as claimed. Per-trade magnitude is one round-trip fee (fees_pct = 2*(fee_bps/10000)*leverage), small but compounding over a mixed paper book. Medium severity is appropriate: genuine money-math/parity inconsistency feeding sizing, but paper-scoped, minority-path, and small per trade.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. The two close paths genuinely disagree on the meaning of pnl_usd. GROSS path: trade_state.py:274 computes pnl_usd = (exit-entry)*size*signed with NO cost deduction, and :301-303 writes this same gross value to BOTH pnl and pnl_usd. scanner.py:3742-3746 (_close_trade_db) then only does UPDATE trades SET fees_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=? — pnl/pnl_usd are never updated, so they remain gross. NET path: the kernel close (scanner.py:5511 pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net, then the override at 5544-5550) writes pnl_usd net of fees+funding. There is no net_pnl_usd column, so the inconsistency is real. Paper equity (scanner.py:604-615) = _PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL + SUM(pnl_usd), and that value is the sizing_equity for the next kernel paper open (scanner.py:6044 -> 5588 -> position_units at 5454-5457), so a gross-stored close over-sizes subsequent trades. Reachability: with paper_kernel_execution default True (5222), the DOMINANT vectorizable-strategy path closes via _kernel_close_recorded and stores NET correctly, so the bug does NOT affect a pure-kernel book. But three non-kernel PAPER close paths are reachable and store GROSS: _kernel_handle_manual_exits (5715-5717 -> _close_trade_db; operator-set SL/TP on manually-opened paper positions, a shipped feature; paper-only via the not-is_live guard at 6161), _kernel_close_orphan (5646 -> close_trade_record directly, gross and no net_pnl_pct at all; paper-only, orphan_close dropped on live at 6091), and the legacy fallback (4140, non-vectorizable strategies). So the defect is a real, reachable edge-case on mixed paper books. Live is correctly unaffected: scanner.py:6041 sizes live off _get_real_account_equity(), not SUM(pnl_usd) — matching the finding's own caveat. Impact is paper-only (no real money lost), small per-trade (one un-deducted round-trip fee; slippage is already in the fill), always biased toward overstating equity (gross gain > net; gross loss less negative than net), and it inflates the paper track record/sizing that feeds promotion-to-live decisions. Medium is appropriate: edge-path, degraded-accuracy, parity break — not cosmetic (it changes sizing and displayed equity), but no real-money loss and the primary path is correct.

### `SIZE-2` — Kelly evidence window differs between the validated profile-selection backtest and the live/paper kernel → kelly-sized strategies size differently than their approved backtest

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** size  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5249-5253,5956-5958,6005-6010; forven/strategies/execution_selection.py:142-154; forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:165,177-181,272`
- **Claim:** Kelly sizing depends on the running `closed_gross` evidence list, which is rebuilt from scratch over whatever bar window the kernel is fed. The execution-profile selection (which validates the chosen profile and its metrics) runs over the confirmation duration, while the live/paper scanner runs the kernel over a different fixed bar window (default 1500). For kelly profiles this yields a different f* → different size_fraction than the validated run.
- **Impact:** A strategy whose execution profile was chosen/validated as kelly will be sized larger or smaller in paper/live than the backtest the promotion gate approved, breaking the 'achievable backtest returns' invariant for real money. Direction of the error is data-dependent (window is shorter than confirmation at 1h/5m, longer at 4h/1d).
- **Suggested fix:** Drive the live/paper kernel kelly evidence over the SAME window the profile was selected on (e.g. tie paper_kernel_history_bars to stage_backtest_duration_days('confirmation') in bar units for the strategy's timeframe), or persist/replay the selection-time closed_gross so kelly f* is computed over an identical evidence base in both engines.
- **Evidence:** Paper/live kernel history window: `return max(int(_scanner_float_setting("paper_kernel_history_bars", 1500)), 300)` (scanner.py:5251), consumed in `manage_positions_via_kernel` via `fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), ...)` (scanner.py:5957-5958). Selection/confirmation window is duration-derived: `duration_days = stage_backtest_duration_days("confirmation")` → bars = days*24*60//tf_minutes (execution_selection.py:146-154); at 1h confirmation=180d ≈ 4320 bars. Kelly reads the cumulative replay evidence: `closed_gross: list[float] = []` reset per `simulate` call (execution_kernel.py:165) and `size_fraction = _sizing.size_fraction(..., closed_gross=closed_gross)` (execution_kernel.py:177-181,272); `kelly_fraction` uses `closed_gross[-lookback:]` (sizing.py:83). When fewer than `kelly_lookback` (default 100) trades fall inside the 1500-bar window, the win-rate/payoff — hence f* — differ from the 4320-bar validation.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited code verified literally. Paper/live kernel is fed a 1500-bar (default) window: scanner.py:5249-5253 (`_paper_kernel_history_bars` = max(1500,300)) consumed at scanner.py:5957-5958 (`fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars())`) and run via run_strategy_execution at 6005-6010. The execution-profile selection runs over the duration-derived confirmation window: execution_selection.py:142-154 (`_resolve_bars` uses `stage_backtest_duration_days('confirmation')` when bars is None) and the gate caller gauntlet/tasks.py:1303-1311 does NOT pass `bars`, so selection uses the duration window. Kelly sizing is evidence-window dependent: execution_kernel.py:165 resets `closed_gross` to [] every simulate() (no persistence), feeds it to _sizing.size_fraction at 177-181/272, and sizing.py:234-235 + 74-95 compute f* from `closed_gross[-kelly_lookback:]` (default lookback 100, sizing.py:160). Kelly is a genuine candidate profile (execution_selection.py:98-101). Because `[-100:]` is window-start-independent once >=100 trades sit behind an entry, the two engines agree for high-frequency strategies; the divergence manifests exactly when fewer than kelly_lookback trades fall inside the ~1300 post-warmup replay bars of the 1500-bar paper window, as the finding states. Then the paper f* is computed from a thinner evidence base than the selection backtest's window, producing a different size_fraction than the validated/approved run (and in the degenerate only-wins/only-losses case, kelly_fraction=0 -> zero size -> a skipped trade). No guard ties the paper window to the selection window. The mechanism is a deterministic code property and reachable. One factual nit in the finding: the confirmation window default is not 180d/4320 bars but 730d (confirmation_duration_days=0 -> inherits backtest_duration_days=730, api_core.py:1580,1716; the 180 is only the bare except-fallback in _resolve_bars). This widens the mismatch versus 1500 bars rather than narrowing it, so it strengthens the finding. Severity medium is apt: real sizing/parity break on real money, but scoped to kelly mode under a data-dependent low-frequency condition, bounded by kelly_multiplier/clamp01, and does not corrupt state.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The defect is real and reachable on the PRIMARY paper AND live execution path (not behind a default-off flag, and not paper-only). Verified chain: (1) kelly f* depends on the per-replay `closed_gross` evidence list, which is reset every `simulate()` call (execution_kernel.py:165) and consumed via `_size_fraction`→`_sizing.size_fraction(...closed_gross=...)` (execution_kernel.py:177-181,272), with `kelly_fraction` reading `closed_gross[-lookback:]` (sizing.py:83). (2) Paper/live feeds a fixed 1500-bar window (scanner.py:5251 default, consumed scanner.py:5958), with no per-strategy/timeframe tie to the selection window. (3) Profile selection runs over the confirmation window resolved from `stage_backtest_duration_days('confirmation')` (execution_selection.py:146-154). (4) The kernel's `size_fraction` flows UNCHANGED into both paper open (scanner.py:5453-5457) and live open (scanner.py:5858-5859) order sizing via `position_units`. Because exits are price-based and `closed_gross` stores pre-size gross returns, the trade set is deterministic regardless of window start, so f* differs ONLY when fewer than `kelly_lookback` (100) closed trades fall inside the 1500-bar window before the recent entry — a normal condition for any strategy trading less often than ~1 trade/15 bars. Selection is default-on (tasks.py:1254) and kelly is in the lean candidate grid the gate uses (execution_selection.py:99-101), so a kelly-chosen strategy will size differently in paper/live than the validated backtest, breaking the achievable-returns parity invariant.

One factual correction to the finding's evidence (does not refute it): the finding states confirmation=180d≈4320 bars at 1h. The actual default `confirmation_duration_days`=0 (api_core.py:1716) inherits `DEFAULT_BACKTEST_DURATION_DAYS`=730 (api_core.py:1580), giving ~17,520 bars at 1h — so the selection window is far larger than claimed and the divergence is bigger, not smaller. The finding's direction-of-error table (shorter at 1h/5m, longer at 4h/1d) is roughly right qualitatively under the true 730d default (paper shorter at 1h/4h, longer at 1d) — the discrepancy still exists across timeframes.

Severity medium is appropriate (unchanged): impact is confined to kelly-mode profiles (a subset), the f* delta is bounded and data-dependent (can over- or under-size), and it does not directly lose money or corrupt state — it is a sizing/parity break. It does touch live real money, but the bounded magnitude and kelly-only scope keep it at medium rather than high. Mitigating but not eliminating: if an asset's data history is short (limited coverage), the selection window can be close to 1500 bars and the divergence small; for well-covered majors with years of data the windows genuinely diverge.

### `KERNEL-4` — Kelly sizing is not replay-stable under the scanner's sliding window → paper kelly trades diverge from the validated backtest

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** kernel  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:177-181, :272; forven/strategies/sizing.py:81-95; forven/scanner.py:5958, :6003-6010`
- **Claim:** The kernel's replay-safety property is proven only for a GROWING prefix (docstring lines 24-27), but the scanner re-runs `simulate` each scan over a fixed-size SLIDING window (most-recent 1500 bars) with a fixed warmup of 200. Kelly `size_fraction` reads `closed_gross` (the trades closed earlier in THIS run); as the window front slides, the kelly evidence available to a given entry changes, so the same calendar trade can be sized differently across scans and differently from the backtest (which uses its own window/warmup).
- **Impact:** For kelly-mode strategies, a recorded paper trade's open-time size can differ from the size used to compute its close PnL on a later scan (`pnl_pct` comes from a fresh re-simulation in scanner.py:6005), and from the backtest the promotion gate approved — i.e. paper does not mirror the backtest for kelly. Opt-in mode and bounded (kelly uses last-`lookback` trades), but it is a real parity gap that produces wrong numbers users act on.
- **Suggested fix:** For kelly, anchor the kelly evidence to a stable origin (e.g. persist the go-live closed_gross or run the scanner kernel over a fixed start anchored at go-live rather than a sliding bar count), or exclude kelly from the kernel-paper parity claim until evidence is made replay-stable.
- **Evidence:** size_fraction for kelly depends on the in-run closed_gross list: kernel line 272 `"size_fraction": _size_fraction(stop_dist_pct)` → line 178-181 passes `closed_gross=closed_gross`; sizing.py line 83 `window = closed_gross[-max(int(lookback),1):]`. The scanner fetches a sliding window `fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), ...)` (scanner.py:5958, default 1500) and runs the kernel at `KERNEL_WARMUP = 200` (scanner.py:6003) via `run_strategy_execution(..., warmup=KERNEL_WARMUP, ...)` (scanner.py:6006). Non-kelly modes (full/fixed/fraction/atr) do NOT read closed_gross (sizing.py:228-240), so they are unaffected; the ATR EWM seed influence decays to ~1e-7 by bar 200 so atr-mode is effectively stable.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the defect. (1) execution_kernel.py:165 builds a FRESH `closed_gross=[]` per simulate() call, accumulated from the window start (bar warmup+1); :178-181/:272 feed it into kelly sizing at entry. (2) sizing.py:83 and :234-235 show kelly is the only mode reading closed_gross[-lookback:]; sizing.py:228-240 confirms full/fixed/fraction/atr never read it, so the "non-kelly unaffected" scoping is correct. (3) scanner.py:5251 default 1500, :5958 fetch_candles(bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars()) is a fixed-size SLIDING window, :6003 warmup 200, :6005-6010 re-runs each scan. (4) DECISIVE: the replay-safety proof (execution_kernel.py:24-27) is verified only for a GROWING prefix with a fixed start — tests/test_execution_parity.py:108-109 uses `sub = df.iloc[:i]`, never a sliding window. With a fixed start, kelly's evidence prefix to a calendar entry is invariant (why the kelly case passes); the scanner's window START moves as old bars drop, so the kelly evidence is NOT invariant. (5) Impact reachable: open records size from the open scan (scanner.py:5453-5457 units, :5470 kernel_size_fraction); close overwrites pnl_pct/pnl_usd with the CLOSE scan's fresh re-sim pnl (scanner.py:5509 then :5541-5551), so a drifted kelly fraction makes recorded units and realized PnL use different sizes, plus a structural gap vs the differently-anchored backtest. (6) Kelly is reachable: execution_selection.py:98-101 includes kelly candidates by default; nothing anchors the kernel's kelly evidence (the legacy _recent_strategy_returns at scanner.py:4548-4553 is a separate non-kernel path). The drift is amplified because kelly_lookback=100 < ~1300 tradable bars, so low/medium-frequency strategies use all in-window trades as evidence and the sliding front changes the set. Bounded, opt-in, parity/reporting divergence (not a silent unbounded drain) -> medium is correct.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): VERIFIED against live code. Mechanism: execution_kernel.py:165 starts closed_gross fresh per simulate run; the kelly _size_fraction closure (:177-181) and entry site (:272) feed the in-run closed_gross to sizing; sizing.py:83 uses closed_gross[-lookback:]; only the kelly branch (sizing.py:234-235) reads it (full/fixed/fraction/atr at :228-240 do not), so the divergence is kelly-specific exactly as claimed. Sliding window: scanner.py:5958 fetches bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars() (default 1500, :5249-5253) — a most-recent-N window whose left edge/origin advances each scan; scanner.py:6003 sets KERNEL_WARMUP=200 and :6005 re-runs the kernel each scan with NO persisted closed_gross and NO fixed origin, so kelly evidence is purely the in-run sliding prefix. The backtest that selected/validated kelly uses a different window/warmup (execution_selection._resolve_bars ~4320 bars for 1h confirmation; run_strategy_execution backtest.py:7212 passes the backtest's own warmup ~210), so the same calendar entry's kelly evidence differs → parity break confirmed. The cited parity proof does NOT cover this: tests/test_execution_parity.py::_incremental (:99-119) replays df.iloc[:i] (fixed-origin GROWING prefix, left edge never moves), so kelly is trivially stable in the test while the real advancing left edge is untested. Open-size vs close-PnL inconsistency confirmed: _kernel_open_paper_trade records size_fraction/units from the open-scan run (scanner.py:5453-5457,:5470); _kernel_refresh_paper_trade updates only stop/target not size (:5618-5621); _kernel_close_recorded reads pnl_pct from the close-scan re-sim (:5509), so a held kelly trade's recorded size can diverge from the size embedded in its realized pnl_usd. Reachability: kernel paper path default ON (_paper_kernel_execution_enabled True, :5222) and kernel live path default ON (_live_kernel_execution_enabled True, :5828); kelly is a default-included selectable candidate (execution_selection.py:54,:98-101) that can win the sweep and freeze into execution_profile — so it affects both paper and real-money live sizing. For the common infrequently-trading case (<100 trades per ~1300-bar window), the whole window holds fewer than lookback trades, so the sliding left edge changes the evidence on essentially every scan, making the divergence routine rather than a rare edge case. Severity stays medium: genuine parity break and internally inconsistent numbers (plus bounded live order-size divergence from the validated backtest), but confined to opt-in kelly mode (default atr engine is replay-stable, consistent with the ~1e-7 ATR-seed decay the finding cites), bounded by kelly fraction x kelly_multiplier (0.25-0.5), and it does not corrupt position state or double-close. All cited file:line references are accurate.

### `KCOPY-2` — Purity guard cannot detect now()/clock or external/stable-global reads, so a time- or data-dependent per-bar strategy is certified pure and runs on the kernel with non-reproducible signals

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** kcopy  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:6833-6845 (docstring + design), 6867-6878 (back-to-back determinism check)`
- **Claim:** The determinism probe evaluates the same window twice back-to-back and only requires equality, so any impurity that is STABLE within those two microsecond-apart calls passes: wall-clock/time-of-day gates (datetime.now()), network/file/DB reads, and reads of mutable module globals.
- **Impact:** Such a strategy is certified pure and runs on the kernel/backtest where now() equals the backtest-run wall time (not the historical bar time), producing signals that differ from live execution at the real bar time — a silent backtest↔paper↔live parity break. Results used for promotion would be untrustworthy.
- **Suggested fix:** Add the promised AST/source scan rejecting datetime.now/time.time/random/open/requests/global-mutation in generate_signal, or inject a frozen clock during the probe and require equality across two different injected times. Until then, document that clock/external-dependent strategies must not be promoted.
- **Evidence:** `a = _per_bar_sig_key(chk(w)); b = _per_bar_sig_key(chk(w)); ... if a != b: return False` (6870-6878) — two immediate calls on the same window. The docstring openly admits: 'this does NOT reliably catch wall-clock / external reads that are STABLE across two back-to-back calls (e.g. a now() time-of-day gate read in the same microsecond) — those need an AST/source check (a follow-up)' (6842-6845). The cross-bar check (6886-6902) clones and walks but is best-effort and swallows exceptions (`except Exception: pass`, 6901-6902); a constant external read during the probe passes it too.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every load-bearing claim matches the live code. The determinism probe at forven/strategies/backtest.py:6870-6871 calls the checker twice on the identical window (`a = _per_bar_sig_key(chk(w)); b = _per_bar_sig_key(chk(w))`) and rejects only on inequality at 6877-6878 (`if a != b: return False`). Any impurity that is stable across those two back-to-back calls (a datetime.now()/time-of-day gate, a constant file/DB/network read, or an unmutated module-global read) returns a==b and is certified deterministic. The docstring at 6841-6844 openly admits exactly this gap and that an AST/source check is an unimplemented follow-up. The cross-bar probe (6886-6902) cannot catch it either: a value that is constant across the sub-second probe makes cold==walk, and the whole block is wrapped in `except Exception: pass` (6901-6902) so it never adds a negative verdict. _per_bar_checker (6794-6797) confirms chk() really invokes check_signal/generate_signal, so the probe path is reachable. I verified no mitigating source scan exists: the only AST walk in the strategies tree (intake.py _file_uses_banned_imports, 53-83) bans only the `ta` import (_BANNED_IMPORT_ROOTS = frozenset({"ta"}), line 22) and is an intake-time import filter unrelated to the purity verdict — datetime/time/random/requests/os are not banned. Thus a clock- or external-state-dependent per-bar strategy is certified pure and runs on the kernel/backtest, where now() reads the run wall-time rather than the historical bar time, producing a silent backtest/paper/live parity break and untrustworthy promotion numbers. Severity stays medium: the defect is real and reachable but conditional on such an impure strategy being created and promoted, and the legacy path is equally exposed (the guard fails to add protection rather than regressing existing behavior).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Defect is real and reachable. forven/strategies/backtest.py:6870-6878 implements the determinism probe as two immediate back-to-back calls on the SAME window with equality-only acceptance (a = _per_bar_sig_key(chk(w)); b = _per_bar_sig_key(chk(w)); if a != b: return False). Any impurity that is STABLE across two microsecond-apart calls passes. The docstring (6841-6844) explicitly admits this gap for wall-clock/external reads, and the cross-bar check (6886-6902) both swallows exceptions (except Exception: pass, 6901-6902) and, run within the same probe interval, also treats a constant now() as stable — so neither stage catches it.\n\nReachability is established: the per-bar→kernel adapter defaults ON (_per_bar_kernel_adapter_enabled -> _scanner_bool_setting("per_bar_kernel_adapter", True), backtest.py:6772), and _signals_from_per_bar gates only on _certify_per_bar_pure (6972). Crucially, a clock-dependent strategy can actually be REGISTERED: the AST guard's ALLOWED_IMPORTS allowlists datetime (forven/sandbox/ast_guard.py:59), so datetime.datetime.now()/.today() passes static validation. (random is also allowlisted but is caught by the back-to-back equality check since two calls differ; open/requests/time/forven.db are blocked by the allowlist — so the dominant uncaught vector is precisely a now() time-of-day gate, exactly as the finding states.)\n\nImpact is genuine: a certified-"pure" per-bar strategy reading now() runs on the shared kernel where the backtest evaluates all historical bars at backtest-run wall time, while the scanner (paper/live) evaluates each bar at real time, producing a silent backtest↔paper↔live parity break that feeds the promotion gate. This matches the finding's stated impact.\n\nSeverity unchanged (medium): the impact is conditional on a strategy actually misusing now()/today() (a latent strategy bug rather than a kernel-computation error), it affects only per-bar-only strategies (most builtins are vectorized and bypass this guard), and the legacy slow path is equally exposed — so the kernel does not uniquely introduce the divergence, it merely fails to certify against it. That is consistent with medium, not a money-losing critical/high.

### `KCOPY-3` — Purity refusal does not gate trading: an impure strategy falls open to the legacy engine and still trades real money (paper AND live)

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** kcopy  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:6972-6989 (refusal → None) → forven/scanner.py:6630-6710 (None → legacy manage_positions)`
- **Claim:** When _certify_per_bar_pure returns False, _signals_from_per_bar returns None and run_strategy_execution returns None. The scanner conflates this with 'genuinely non-vectorizable' and (with paper_legacy_fallback_enabled defaulting True) routes the strategy to the legacy per-bar engine, which runs the SAME impure generate_signal. The purity guard therefore only logs/flags; it does not stop the strategy from trading.
- **Impact:** A strategy the kernel deems 'untrustworthy on ANY engine' (non-deterministic / stateful) still opens and manages positions on the legacy engine — real money on non-reproducible signals — with only a log/diagnostic flag as protection. Contradicts the guard's stated purpose and the project's fail-closed stance.
- **Suggested fix:** Distinguish 'impure/refused' (fail-closed: skip, never trade on any engine) from 'no vectorized signals' (the legacy-fallback case). Have _signals_from_per_bar/run_strategy_execution surface the impurity verdict to the scanner (e.g. a distinct sentinel) so impure strategies are skipped/quarantined rather than silently downgraded to legacy.
- **Evidence:** Refusal path: `if not _certify_per_bar_pure(...): ... log.warning('...its results are untrustworthy on ANY engine, fix or archive it') ... return None` (backtest.py:6972-6989). Scanner: `if actions is None: ... if not _paper_legacy_fallback_enabled(): ... continue` else falls through to `actions = manage_positions(strat_id, strat, signal, ...)` (scanner.py:6630-6710); the live branch (6677-6710) likewise drops to the legacy live engine. Default fallback is ON: `_scanner_bool_setting("paper_legacy_fallback_enabled", True)` (scanner.py:5239).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Traced and confirmed against live code. (1) backtest.py:6972-6989: when _certify_per_bar_pure returns False, _signals_from_per_bar only logs a warning + log_activity and `return None`. (2) backtest.py:7172-7173: run_strategy_execution then `return None` (same as the genuinely-non-vectorizable case). (3) scanner.py:6014-6015: manage_positions_via_kernel returns a PLAIN None (NOT KERNEL_SKIP_SCAN) — the comment literally labels it "genuinely non-vectorizable," confirming the conflation. (4) The kernel gates _is_kernel_paper_strategy (scanner.py:5315-5319) and _is_live_kernel_stage (scanner.py:5831-5833) check ONLY stage, so an impure per-bar-only strategy still enters the kernel path; the adapter is default-ON (backtest.py:6772). (5) scanner.py:6630-6710: actions is None → with _paper_legacy_fallback_enabled() default True (scanner.py:5239) the paper branch falls through to legacy manage_positions; the live branch (6677-6703) drops to the legacy live engine (real Hyperliquid orders, _live_kernel_execution_enabled default ON at scanner.py:5816). (6) The legacy `signal` is produced by strategy_instance.generate_signal(df) (scanner.py:2680) — the exact impure method the guard refused; legacy manage_positions (scanner.py:3840) opens/closes on it. So the purity guard does NOT gate trading; the impure strategy still trades on the legacy engine on non-reproducible signals, with only a log/flag as protection. There is no distinct impure-vs-non-vectorizable sentinel; only KERNEL_SKIP_SCAN is special-cased, and impurity does not use it. All cited line references are accurate. Severity medium retained: real fail-open contradicting the guard's purpose and the project's fail-closed stance, but it requires a truly impure strategy to have reached paper/live and the legacy engine still applies normal sizing/risk; the claim's phrase "real money (paper AND live)" is slightly imprecise (paper is simulated) but the live branch is genuinely real money and paper corrupts promotion-feeding results, so the substance holds.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The defect is real and reachable on default config. Traced the full chain against live code:

1) backtest.py:6972-6989 — when `_certify_per_bar_pure(...)` is False, `_signals_from_per_bar` logs "...its results are untrustworthy on ANY engine, fix or archive it" and `return None`. This is the IDENTICAL `return None` used when the strategy has no per-bar checker (line 6964-6965), so the impurity verdict is indistinguishable from "genuinely non-vectorizable."

2) backtest.py:7171-7173 — `vectorized = _signals_from_per_bar(...); if vectorized is None: return None`. The impurity signal is erased into a plain None.

3) scanner.py:6014-6015 — `if res is None: return None  # genuinely non-vectorizable → caller decides`. The comment confirms the author treated None as ONLY "non-vectorizable", not "impure refusal". Returns None (not KERNEL_SKIP_SCAN).

4) scanner.py:6630-6710 — the `if actions is None:` block conflates kernel-disabled / non-kernel-stage / non-vectorizable, with NO awareness of impurity. PAPER (kernel_mode=="paper") falls through to legacy `manage_positions(...)` at line 6704 when `_paper_legacy_fallback_enabled()` (default True, scanner.py:5239). LIVE (kernel_mode=="live", lines 6677-6703) logs but UNCONDITIONALLY drops to the same `manage_positions` at 6704 — no fallback-flag gate at all. The legacy engine then runs the SAME impure generate_signal.

All controlling flags default ON: paper_kernel_execution=True (5222), per_bar_kernel_adapter=True (6772), paper_legacy_fallback_enabled=True (5239), live_kernel_execution=True (5828). So the purity guard is purely advisory — it logs/flags but never blocks trading, directly contradicting its stated text and the project's fail-closed stance.

Severity stays medium: the affected population is narrow (custom per-bar-only strategies that the probe deems non-deterministic/stateful — built-ins are vectorized/pure), live mainnet additionally requires FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1 (testnet-bounded otherwise), and the legacy engine still functions (applies stops/exits) so the trades are non-reproducible/untrustworthy rather than state-corrupting. Not critical/high, but a genuine fail-open safety gap (real paper money always, real live money when mainnet-enabled, on signals the kernel explicitly refused). The suggested fix (distinct impurity sentinel surfaced to the scanner so impure strategies are quarantined/skipped on every engine) is the correct remedy.

### `SCANAPPLY-1` — Drifted/legacy open + kernel close-in-gap double-books a closed trade (backfill + converge-close)

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** scanapply  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:158-160, 215-226`
- **Claim:** When a recorded OPEN's match key (direction, entry_time) no longer lines up with the kernel's re-derived entry_time — the exact data-source drift the code elsewhere acknowledges ('the HL->Binance switch', and legacy/manual orphans) — AND the kernel CLOSES that position during a missed-scan gap, the reconciler emits BOTH a `backfill` (a brand-new closed record at the kernel's drifted entry_time) AND an `orphan_close` (closing the stale recorded OPEN). The same logical position is booked twice, double-counting PnL into paper equity, and the converge-close finalizes at the CURRENT bar price (`last_close`) rather than the real exit.
- **Impact:** Silent double-count of a closed trade -> corrupted paper equity / track record (and a wrong converge-close price), on the very operational event (data-source/candle drift) the system is built to tolerate. Default-on for paper (`paper_kernel_converge_orphans` defaults True, scanner.py:6091).
- **Suggested fix:** Before emitting `orphan_close` for a recorded OPEN, suppress it if that (direction) already produced a `backfill` or `close` in this plan (i.e. the kernel just booked the same logical position under a drifted key). Equivalently, give the close-loop an adopt-by-direction fallback symmetric to the open-loop so a drifted close MATCHES the stale recorded OPEN instead of backfilling a duplicate.
- **Evidence:** Close-loop, no exact key match -> backfill (paper_reconcile.py:158-160): `r = recorded_by_key.get(k)\n if r is None:\n   if _recent(entry_time):  # ... backfill\n     backfills.append(ReconcileAction("backfill", direction, entry_time, trade=kc))`. Orphan-close fires for the still-unmatched recorded OPEN when the kernel holds no position that direction (paper_reconcile.py:216-222): `for direction, r in recorded_open_by_dir.items():\n   if id(r) in matched or direction in kernel_open_dirs:\n     continue\n   ... orphan_closes.append(ReconcileAction("orphan_close", ...))`. Both are returned in ONE plan (paper_reconcile.py:226): `return closes + backfills + opens + refreshes + orphan_closes`. The adopt-by-direction de-dup that WOULD have prevented this only runs in the OPEN loop (paper_reconcile.py:184-187), i.e. only when the kernel still HOLDS the position — it does not cover the close-in-gap case. The backfill's own idempotency guard `_kernel_trade_exists(strat_id, action.direction, action.entry_time)` (scanner.py:5585) keys on the DRIFTED entry_time T', which no recorded row carries, so it does not block this.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited line references and code behaviors verified exactly against live code. TRACE for the scenario (recorded OPEN at key (dir,T); kernel re-derives the SAME logical position at a drifted entry_time T'!=T after canonicalization, e.g. the HL->Binance switch the code itself names at paper_reconcile.py:180-183, AND closes it during a missed-scan gap so it sits in res.closed_trades, not res.open_positions):\n\n1) Close-loop (paper_reconcile.py:157-160): k=_key(dir,T'); r=recorded_by_key.get((dir,T')) is None (recorded row keys on T); _recent(T') true -> backfills.append(ReconcileAction(\"backfill\", dir, T', trade=kc)). The recorded OPEN is NOT added to `matched` and `recorded_open_by_dir[dir]` is untouched.\n2) Open-loop adopt-by-direction (184-187) is INSIDE `for direction,pos in res.open_positions.items()`; the kernel is flat on this direction (closed in gap), so the loop body never runs for it -> no adoption. Confirmed the de-dup does not cover the close-in-gap case.\n3) Orphan-loop (216-222): the recorded OPEN at T is still in recorded_open_by_dir, id(r) not in matched, dir not in kernel_open_dirs -> orphan_close emitted (window_start guard at 220 passes because T is in-window).\n4) Return (226): closes+backfills+opens+refreshes+orphan_closes — both returned, no cross-suppression.\n5) Scanner backfill guard (scanner.py:5585 -> _kernel_trade_exists 5396-5410) queries json_extract(signal_data,'$.kernel_entry_time') = T'; the stale OPEN carries kernel_entry_time=T, so guard returns False -> a brand-new closed record is booked at T' (open+close round-trip).\n6) orphan_close -> _kernel_close_orphan (5630-5651) closes at signal_exit_price=last_close/exit_price=last_close (current bar), reason reconcile_flat — wrong exit price, as claimed.\n7) Default-on for paper: scanner.py:6091 _scanner_bool_setting(\"paper_kernel_converge_orphans\", True); orphan_closes only dropped on live (is_live) or when disabled. Apply loop (6131-6149) dispatches backfill and orphan_close independently with no de-dup.\n\nNet effect (paper): one logical position recorded as TWO closed trades -> double-counted PnL into paper equity, plus a wrong converge-close price. Reachable on an operational event (data-source/candle drift) the system explicitly tolerates elsewhere, combined with a designed-for missed-scan gap — the defect is the uncovered seam between the two mechanisms.\n\nSeverity unchanged (medium): it is paper-only (live drops orphan_close at 6091), so it corrupts the track record / paper equity rather than losing real money. It can second-order influence promotion-to-live decisions, but requires the specific drift+close-in-gap conjunction, so medium is appropriate. The auditor's suggested fix (suppress orphan_close when the same direction already produced a backfill/close in this plan, or give the close-loop a symmetric adopt-by-direction fallback) is sound.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The defect is real and reachable as described, on the paper path. Traced end-to-end against live code: (1) When a recorded OPEN's match key (kernel_entry_time=T) drifts from the kernel's re-derived close entry_time (T'), the close loop finds no match and appends a backfill without adding to `matched` (paper_reconcile.py:158-160). Because the kernel is now FLAT in that direction, res.open_positions has no entry, so the open loop and its adopt-by-direction fallback (paper_reconcile.py:184-187) never iterate it; the orphan loop then appends orphan_close (paper_reconcile.py:216-222). Both are returned in one plan (line 226). (2) The backfill idempotency guard `_kernel_trade_exists(strat_id, direction, action.entry_time)` (scanner.py:5585) queries json_extract kernel_entry_time = T' (scanner.py:5407); the stale recorded OPEN carries T, not T', so the guard misses and the backfill writes a NEW closed row. (3) The orphan converge-close finalizes at the current bar price: close_trade_record(signal_exit_price=last_close, exit_price=last_close, close_reason="reconcile_flat") (scanner.py:5646-5650), not the real exit. (4) Paper equity = $10k + SUM(pnl_usd) over ALL CLOSED paper trades (scanner.py:604-615), so both closed rows for the one logical position are summed → silent double-count plus a wrong converge price.

Reachability/impact checks support keeping MEDIUM. It is paper-only (orphan_close is dropped on the live path, scanner.py:6091-6092) and default-on for paper (`paper_kernel_converge_orphans` defaults True), so no direct real-money loss. It is one-time per occurrence (self-heals on the next scan — backfilled T' matches as closed, orphan row is now closed — non-compounding). Two preconditions narrow the window: (a) the entry timestamps must GENUINELY differ — `_canonical_ts` (paper_reconcile.py:74-90) heals pure space/tz/format drift, so it requires a real data-source switch (HL→Binance, explicitly named in scanner.py:6070-6074 / paper_reconcile.py:180-183) or a signal firing on a different bar from differing OHLC; and (b) the scan gap must span the kernel's close, because if any scan runs while the kernel still HOLDS the drifted position the open-loop adopt-by-direction re-stamps kernel_entry_time=T' (scanner.py:5624-5625) and heals the drift before any close. Both are real operational events the system is explicitly built to tolerate, so their coincidence is genuine but not common. The silent corruption of the paper track record — which gates promotion to live — keeps it above low; the paper-only, non-compounding, coincidence-gated nature keeps it below high. Severity unchanged (medium).

### `SCANAPPLY-2` — Non-atomic close: net-pnl override is a separate transaction from close_trade_record; a crash leaves wrong-scale pnl_pct permanently

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** scanapply  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5513-5552`
- **Claim:** `_kernel_close_recorded` first calls `close_trade_record` (which, in its own `with get_db()` transaction, sets status=CLOSED and writes a POSITION-RETURN pnl_pct and a drag-free pnl_usd), then in a SEPARATE `with get_db()` transaction OVERRIDES pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd with the kernel's net EQUITY-FRACTION values. If the process dies between the two writes, the trade is permanently CLOSED carrying the wrong-scale pnl_pct (position-return, larger than the equity-fraction by ~1/size_fraction) and a drag-free pnl_usd. The next scan sees it already-closed and never re-applies the override.
- **Impact:** A torn write silently corrupts a recorded paper trade's PnL (wrong scale + missing fee/slippage/funding drag), which feeds equity and promotion-gate metrics, and is never self-healed.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute the kernel net pnl up front and write status=CLOSED together with the final pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd/closed_at in a SINGLE transaction (e.g. pass the kernel net values into close_trade_record, or fold close+override into one UPDATE) so the close and its authoritative PnL are atomic.
- **Evidence:** Two distinct transactions in _kernel_close_recorded: `close_trade_record(trade_id, signal_exit_price=exit_price, exit_price=exit_price, ...)` (scanner.py:5514) then `with get_db() as conn:\n   conn.execute("UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=?, pnl=?, pnl_usd=?, closed_at=? WHERE id=?", (round(pnl_pct_net,8), ...))` (scanner.py:5541-5546). close_trade_record computes the DIFFERENT-semantics value it temporarily leaves behind: `pnl_pct = ((resolved_exit_price - entry_price)/entry_price)*signed*leverage` ... `pnl_usd = (resolved_exit_price-entry_price)*size*signed` (trade_state.py:268-274). The kernel value is equity-fraction: `pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction` (execution_kernel.py:114). Re-processing is suppressed because reconcile treats an already-closed match as a no-op: `else: matched.add(id(r))  # already recorded closed -> nothing to do` (paper_reconcile.py:164-165).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The defect is real and reachable exactly as described. (1) Two separate transactions: `get_db()` (forven/db.py:429-453) is a @contextmanager that opens a fresh connection and calls conn.commit() on clean block exit (db.py:448-449). `_kernel_close_recorded` calls `close_trade_record(...)` at scanner.py:5514, which opens its OWN `with get_db()` (trade_state.py:166) and commits status='CLOSED' + pnl_pct/pnl_usd at block exit; control then returns to scanner.py, runs pure-Python lines 5519-5540, then opens a NEW `with get_db()` at scanner.py:5541 for the override UPDATE. These are two independently-committed transactions with a real (if tiny) gap. (2) Wrong-scale residue: close_trade_record writes pnl_pct = ((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage (trade_state.py:268, position-return, no size_fraction, no drag) and pnl_usd = (exit-entry)*size*signed (trade_state.py:274, drag-free). The override installs the kernel net value pnl_pct = gross*size_fraction where gross already subtracts round_trip_drag (execution_kernel.py:111-114). So a torn write leaves pnl_pct larger than intended by ~1/size_fraction and drag-free — confirmed. Notably close_trade_record's UPDATE (trade_state.py:284-307) does NOT write net_pnl_pct at all, so net_pnl_pct also stays stale after a torn write (corruption is slightly worse than claimed). (3) No self-heal: paper_reconcile.py:164-165 makes an already-closed recorded row matching a kernel closed trade a no-op (`matched.add(id(r))`), and close_trade_record defaults only_if_open=True (trade_state.py:159), so the override is never re-applied. Severity unchanged at medium: the crash window is vanishingly small (two consecutive commits separated only by string-formatting, no I/O/network/blocking), and the impact is paper-only (uses _PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL, scanner.py:5510), corrupting one trade's recorded PnL that indirectly feeds equity/promotion-gate metrics rather than directly losing real money — a degraded edge case that fits medium.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified all load-bearing claims against live code. (1) Two separate committed transactions: close_trade_record runs in its own `with get_db()` (trade_state.py:166) and its UPDATE (trade_state.py:284-307) commits status='CLOSED' + a position-return pnl_pct=((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage (trade_state.py:268) and a drag-free pnl_usd=(exit-entry)*size*signed (trade_state.py:274); it does NOT write net_pnl_pct. The override is a distinct `with get_db()` block (scanner.py:5541) committing kernel net values pnl_pct=net_pnl_pct=pnl_pct_net (scanner.py:5544-5545). get_db() commits per-with-block (db.py:448-449), so the two writes are non-atomic with only a trivial string op between them. (2) Scale mismatch is real: kernel pnl_pct = gross*size_fraction where gross=((exit-entry)/entry)*sign*leverage-drag (execution_kernel.py:111-114), so close_trade_record's leftover value is larger by ~1/size_fraction plus the missing drag; a torn write also leaves net_pnl_pct NULL/stale. (3) Never self-healed: paper_reconcile.py:164-165 treats an already-CLOSED kernel match as a no-op (`matched.add(id(r))  # nothing to do`), so the override is never re-applied. (4) Reachability confirmed default-ON for BOTH paper (paper_kernel_execution default True, scanner.py:5222) and live (live_kernel_execution default True, scanner.py:5828), selected at scanner.py:6614-6620; the override fires for the common non-late faithful close (the `late` branch returns early at scanner.py:5537). Severity unchanged at medium: the failure window is microscopic (two adjacent SQLite commits, no I/O between) and corrupts at most one trade per crash, but it is permanent, never self-healed, feeds equity/promotion-gate metrics, and sits on a default path — matching the audit's edge-case/degraded definition of medium. The reachability lens provides no downgrade since the path is not flag-gated off and not dead.

### `RECON-1` — Reconciler match key is asset-blind; scanner guard only filters cross-asset OPEN rows, leaving cross-asset CLOSED rows in the key map

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** recon  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:93-94 (_key); forven/scanner.py:6079-6084 (partition); paper_reconcile.py:158-160, 188`
- **Claim:** Asset is NOT in the reconciler match key for ANY action type. The reconciler keys purely on (direction, canonical_entry_time). The only cross-asset protection lives in the scanner and only excludes recorded rows whose status == 'open'; cross-asset CLOSED records still flow into reconcile and pollute recorded_by_key, where a (direction, timestamp) collision with the current asset can suppress a legitimate open/backfill or, via last-writer-wins, shadow a same-asset OPEN so a kernel exit never closes it.
- **Impact:** After a symbol/asset flip (the exact scenario that motivated the guard — S04545), the strategy retains CLOSED records on the old asset. Because both assets share the candle grid (same timeframe, aligned bar timestamps), an old-asset closed trade can carry the SAME (direction, bar-timestamp) as the new asset's current kernel open. Worst cases: (1) the current asset's open is silently suppressed (missed paper/live entry), (2) a missed backfill (lost paper round-trip), (3) the same-asset OPEN is shadowed in recorded_by_key so the kernel's exit no-ops against the cross-asset closed row — and because orphan_close is stripped on the live path (scanner.py:6091-6092), a LIVE position the strategy already exited would be held open = a missed live exit (money risk). The headline refresh/adopt splice IS prevented (cross-asset OPENs are removed), but the reconciler remains structurally asset-blind, so a single removed/changed guard line, a new call site, or a blank/representation-drifted asset value re-opens the splice.
- **Suggested fix:** Put asset in the reconciler key itself (carry asset on KernelResult positions/trades and on recorded rows, include it in _key) instead of relying on an external partial pre-filter. At minimum, also exclude cross-asset CLOSED rows from same_asset_recorded (drop the `status == 'open'` condition at scanner.py:6081 so ANY asset-mismatched record is held out of reconcile).
- **Evidence:** _key: `def _key(direction, entry_time): return (str(direction or "long").strip().lower(), _canonical_ts(entry_time))` (paper_reconcile.py:93-94) — no asset. Docstring confirms: `Matching is by ``(direction, entry_time)``` (paper_reconcile.py:15). Scanner partition only removes OPEN cross-asset rows: `if _rec.get("status") == "open" and _rec_asset and _strat_asset_u and _rec_asset != _strat_asset_u: cross_asset_open_rows.append(...) else: same_asset_recorded.append(_rec)` (scanner.py:6081-6084) — a CLOSED cross-asset record falls into the `else` and is passed to reconcile. In the open loop a colliding key suppresses the open: `elif r is not None:` ... `continue` (paper_reconcile.py:188,196); in the close loop it suppresses a backfill: `if r is None:` ... `backfills.append(...)` (paper_reconcile.py:158-160). recorded_by_key is last-writer-wins: `recorded_by_key[_key(...)] = r` (paper_reconcile.py:142).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The structural defect is verified literally in code. (1) The reconciler key is asset-blind: forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:93-94 `_key` returns `(direction.lower(), _canonical_ts(entry_time))` with no asset. (2) The only cross-asset protection is the scanner pre-filter at forven/scanner.py:6079-6084, and its condition `if _rec.get("status") == "open" and _rec_asset and _strat_asset_u and _rec_asset != _strat_asset_u:` (line 6081) routes ONLY open cross-asset rows to `cross_asset_open_rows`; a CLOSED cross-asset row (status "closed") hits the `else` (line 6084) and is appended to `same_asset_recorded`, which is then passed to `reconcile` (line 6085). (3) Those closed cross-asset rows are genuinely returned by `_kernel_recorded_trades` (scanner.py:5364-5375) — any row with a `kernel_entry_time` is emitted open or closed, carrying `_row.asset`. (4) `recorded_by_key` is last-writer-wins (paper_reconcile.py:142). (5) A colliding closed key suppresses a legitimate open via `elif r is not None: ... continue` (paper_reconcile.py:188,196) and suppresses a backfill via the `if r is None:` gate (paper_reconcile.py:158-160). (6) orphan_close is stripped on the live path (scanner.py:6091-6092). So the code does exactly what the claim says: cross-asset CLOSED rows flow into reconcile and pollute the asset-blind key map. Reachability: because both assets share an aligned candle grid, the kernel's replay of the NEW asset over the same calendar bars can produce a same-direction entry at a bar where the OLD asset also traded, so the paper open/backfill suppression (impacts 1 and 2) is genuinely reachable in narrow conditions, and the defensive fragility (one removed guard line or blank/drifted asset re-opens the splice) is real. One caveat that does NOT change the verdict: the most severe sub-scenario — a LIVE missed exit (impact 3) — is essentially unreachable because a real live position stores its post-flip real-time `kernel_entry_time`, which cannot collide with a pre-flip cross-asset CLOSED row's entry_time; this specific money-risk path is overstated. Net: the defect is real and reachable as a medium-severity edge case / structural fragility, matching the assigned severity.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every code claim verified against live code. (1) The reconciler key is asset-blind: paper_reconcile.py:93-94 `_key` returns only (direction, canonical_ts); docstring line 15 confirms. (2) _kernel_recorded_trades (scanner.py:5360-5363) selects by COALESCE(strategy_id, strategy) with NO asset filter and status IN ('OPEN','CLOSED'), so after an asset flip old-asset CLOSED rows for the strategy_id are returned. (3) The scanner cross-asset guard (scanner.py:6081-6084) only diverts rows where status=='open'; a cross-asset CLOSED row fails that test and falls into the else -> same_asset_recorded -> reconcile(). Confirmed: cross-asset closed rows DO enter reconcile. (4) recorded_by_key is unconditional last-writer-wins (paper_reconcile.py:142); rows arrive ORDER BY opened_at DESC (5361), so the older pre-flip cross-asset closed row is iterated last and WINS the key over a newer post-flip same-asset OPEN at the same (direction, bar-ts) -> it shadows it.

All three stated impacts are mechanically reachable given a key collision: suppressed open via `elif r is not None: ... continue` (paper_reconcile.py:188,196); suppressed backfill via `if r is None` being False (158-160); and a shadowed same-asset OPEN whose kernel exit no-ops in the close loop (recorded_by_key returns the closed row -> matched.add at 164-165, no close action). On the live path that orphaned open is NOT rescued: orphan_close is stripped (scanner.py:6091-6092) and _kernel_close_live_trade (5885) only runs for close/backfill actions, with no separate live converge handler -> a persistent missed LIVE exit on a real position = money risk. Live is reachable by default: live_kernel_execution defaults True (scanner.py:5828; test asserts at test_kernel_live_parity.py:28), and the audit is explicitly pre-mainnet.

Reachability is real but gated on one coincidental precondition shared by all impacts: an exact (direction, bar-timestamp) collision between an old-asset trade and the current new-asset position on a shared candle grid. Asset flips with retained strategy_id are a documented production scenario (S04545; the entire cross_asset guard exists for it), and correlated assets entering on the same bar make a collision plausible but not guaranteed. The headline OPEN-refresh splice IS prevented by the OPEN-only guard, and the residual exposure is exactly the edge-case set the finding describes. The structural asset-blindness is a genuine latent footgun (the lone guard line at scanner.py:6081 is all that stands between this and the worse splice).
