Verdict: confirmed; severity medium is appropriate (edge-case trigger, but real money/state impact on a default-on live path), so unchanged.

### `LATE-2` — Downtime/long-hold blind spot: trades whose entry ages past the kernel's reproducible window are never backfilled (missed closes) or stranded open forever

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** late  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5251, 6003, 6059; forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:183; forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:220-221`
- **Claim:** The documented guarantee ('every trade since go-live is recorded/backfilled no matter how long the scanner was down') is false beyond the kernel's reproducible window. The kernel re-simulates only _paper_kernel_history_bars (default 1500) bars and its loop starts at warmup+1 (KERNEL_WARMUP=200), so it can only reproduce entries in roughly the last 1299 bars. An entry older than that is never produced in res.closed_trades or res.open_positions, so (a) a missed round-trip there is never backfilled, and (b) a still-held position there is never refreshed AND the orphan-close guard (window_start) deliberately leaves it alone, so it is held open forever and its eventual exit is never recorded. This also hits positions held longer than ~1299 bars even with zero downtime.
- **Impact:** Bounded by timeframe: ~1299 bars is ~54 days at 1h / ~216 days at 4h (edge), but only ~4.5 days at 5m and ~13.5 days at 15m (realistic). In the blind spot, missed trades silently vanish and held positions become un-exitable phantoms accruing fake unrealized PnL, corrupting the paper track record used for promotion/sizing.
- **Suggested fix:** Either size the history window from the strategy's max-hold/expected-downtime per timeframe, or add a fallback that records the close of a recorded-open whose entry has aged out of the kernel window (e.g. close at the strategy's last reproducible exit, or surface for operator review) instead of stranding it.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:5251 `return max(int(_scanner_float_setting('paper_kernel_history_bars', 1500)), 300)`; 6003 `KERNEL_WARMUP = 200`; 6059 `window_start = str(df.index[min(KERNEL_WARMUP + 1, len(df) - 1)]) ...`. execution_kernel.py:183 `for idx in range(max(int(warmup), 0) + 1, len(df)):` (entries before warmup+1 are never taken). paper_reconcile.py:220-221 `if window_start is not None and entry_time and _ts_lt(entry_time, str(window_start)): continue  # entry predates the kernel's evaluated window -> leave it alone`.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified the full chain against live code. (1) scanner.py:5958 fetches the kernel df via fetch_candles(bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars()), default 1500 (scanner.py:5251); fetch_candles (1665) loads exactly `bars` candles, so the kernel re-simulates from scratch over only the last ~1500 bars each scan with no memory of older entries. (2) scanner.py:6003 KERNEL_WARMUP=200 is passed as warmup to run_strategy_execution (6006), which calls _kernel.simulate(d, signals, warmup, ...) (backtest.py:7212-7213); execution_kernel.py:183 loops `for idx in range(max(int(warmup),0)+1, len(df))` = bars 201..end, so entries before bar 201 are never produced in res.open_positions/res.closed_trades — reproducible entries ≈ last 1299 bars, exactly as claimed. (3) scanner.py:6059 window_start = df.index[201]; paper_reconcile.py:220-221 skips (`continue`) any recorded OPEN whose entry_time < window_start → aged-out opens are deliberately never orphan-closed. (4) paper_reconcile.py:159-160 only backfills trades present in res.closed_trades, so an aged-out missed round-trip is never backfilled. (5) The guarantee is overclaimed at scanner.py:6048-6050 ("ANY downtime ... backfills every missed trade since go-live") with no window qualifier. No mitigation: sweep_pending_close_reconcile (scanner.py:7064) only remediates trades already flagged pending_close_reconcile against exchange truth, not normal-status aged paper OPENs; late_entry hop-in is hard-disabled (scanner.py:6069) and could not help anyway because it still requires the kernel to surface the open. Both halves hold: (a) missed round-trips with aged entries vanish, and (b) long-held opens beyond the window are stranded open forever (never refreshed, never closed), accruing fake unrealized PnL and never recording their real exit. The zero-downtime variant is real on short timeframes (5m ~4.5d, 15m ~13.5d). Severity medium is appropriate: it corrupts the paper track record feeding promotion/sizing but requires long holds or long outages, the window is large on 1h/4h, and the guard is a conscious tradeoff against the worse failure of wrongly closing a still-valid open.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The defect is real and reachable on the default-on production path (paper_kernel_execution and live_kernel_execution both default True at scanner.py:5222 and 5828). The kernel df is hard-bounded to ~1500 bars (scanner.py:5958 fetches bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars()=1500, scanner.py:5251; _enrich_scan_frame only adds columns, _trim drops one bar). The kernel loop starts at warmup+1 (execution_kernel.py:183 with KERNEL_WARMUP=200 at scanner.py:6003), so every entry has entry_bar>=201 and the earliest reproducible entry_time is df.index[201] (~1298 bars before now). Therefore res.open_positions can NEVER contain a position whose entry_time < window_start, where window_start=df.index[201] (scanner.py:6059). In reconcile, such a recorded OPEN cannot be matched by a refresh (kernel doesn't hold it) and the orphan-close guard at paper_reconcile.py:220-221 deliberately `continue`s past it — so it is stranded open forever, accruing fake unrealized PnL and never recording its real exit; and a fully-missed round-trip beyond the window is never in res.closed_trades so never backfilled (closes/backfills loop at paper_reconcile.py:151-160). No mitigating cleanup exists: time_stop_bars defaults to None (sizing.py:260) so there is no max-hold; phantom_recovery.py only handles gauntlet/backtesting lifecycle stages, not open positions; selfheal.py is strategy-code validation; and manage_positions_via_kernel short-circuits the legacy per-bar manager for kernel strategies. The documented guarantee in the comment at scanner.py:6045-6051 ("ANY downtime ... backfills every missed trade since go-live") is genuinely overstated. The stranded-open sub-case is reachable even with ZERO downtime for any continuously-held position exceeding ~1299 bars (>4.5 days at 5m, >13.5 days at 15m — realistic for a trend strategy with no time stop); the missed-round-trip sub-case is narrower (needs sustained downtime spanning the whole window). Severity medium is correct: it does not affect the common case (positions that exit within the window while the scanner is up) and requires the aging-out precondition, but when it triggers it corrupts the paper track record used for promotion/sizing (phantom position with fake unrealized PnL, lost real exit) and leaves live positions unmanaged by the kernel (orphan_close is dropped on the live path at scanner.py:6091-6092; only exchange-side protection orders would still fire). Not critical (no silent loss in the common path), not low (real state corruption when reached).

### `LIVE-2` — Failed live kernel CLOSE (exit) is silently logged with no operator notification

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5900 (caller 6144-6145, 6154-6155); compare legacy forven/scanner.py:3953-3961`
- **Claim:** _kernel_close_live_trade calls _execute_direct('close', ...) without a try/except. If the real reduce-only close order raises (close_position error / network), the exception propagates to the action loop which only log.error()s it. The trade correctly stays OPEN for retry, but unlike the legacy _close_via_execution — which calls _report_execution_failure(action='close') to fire the trade_failed notification — the kernel live path emits NO operator alert that a REAL position's exit is repeatedly failing.
- **Impact:** An operator gets no visibility when a live position cannot be exited (exchange degraded, reduce-only rejected). The scanner retries each scan so it is self-healing once the exchange recovers, but during an outage a real position rides on its resting stop only, with no surfaced alarm.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the close in try/except and call _report_execution_failure(action='close', ...) (which deliberately keeps the trade OPEN for retry) so the operator is notified, matching the legacy path.
- **Evidence:** `result = _execute_direct("close", trade_id, strat_id, asset, direction, size, ref_price, close_reason=reason)` (5900) is unguarded; the only failure path is the loop's `log.error(...)` (6154-6155). Legacy: `except Exception as e: log.error("Direct close failed ..."); _report_execution_failure(strategy_id=strat_id, action="close", trade_id=trade.get("id"), reason=str(e))` (3953-3960).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) forven/scanner.py:5900 calls _execute_direct("close", ...) with NO try/except; the only try/excepts in _kernel_close_live_trade (5915-5923 retire, 5924-5927 release) and the _close_trade_db finalize (5914) all run AFTER and only if the close returned, so a raised exception propagates. (2) _execute_direct's close branch genuinely raises: close_position(...) at 3436 can raise on network failure, and 3448-3450 does `if result.get("error"): raise RuntimeError(result.get("error"))` on a reduce-only rejection. (3) The exception unwinds to the action loop, where 6144-6145 invokes close_applier and the sole handler at 6154-6155 is `log.error(...)` — no _report_execution_failure, hence no notification. (4) The legacy _close_via_execution at 3953-3961 DOES call _report_execution_failure(action="close"), and that function (3218-3228) emits the trade_failed Discord+in-app notification while deliberately NOT fail-unfilling close actions (3203 fires only for open-prefixed), leaving the trade OPEN for retry. (5) Reachability confirmed and default-on: close_applier=_kernel_close_live_trade when is_live (6094), is_live from execution_type=="live" (6027), routed at 6619-6622 under _live_kernel_execution_enabled() (default True, 5828) for live/live_graduated/deployed stages (5831-5833). The trade correctly stays open (exception precedes _close_trade_db at 5914) and retries next scan, and the position retains its resting exchange SL/TP placed at open (3361/3367-3368). So no money is silently lost or state corrupted — the genuine gap is purely the missing operator alert that a real live exit is repeatedly failing, a parity/observability divergence from the legacy path. Medium is appropriate: self-healing retry + resting-stop backstop mitigate impact; it manifests only during persistent exchange degradation/reduce-only rejection.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) _kernel_close_live_trade calls _execute_direct("close", ...) UNGUARDED at scanner.py:5900. (2) A real close failure does raise: _execute_direct's close branch raises RuntimeError on an exchange error at scanner.py:3449-3450 ("if result.get(\"error\"): raise RuntimeError(...)"), and close_position network errors propagate too — so the exception premise holds. (3) For live, close_applier = _kernel_close_live_trade (scanner.py:6094), invoked at 6145; the only failure handler is the action loop's "except Exception as exc: log.error(...)" at 6154-6155 — it does NOT call _report_execution_failure, so no trade_failed notification fires. (4) The legacy _close_via_execution path catches the same exception and calls _report_execution_failure(strategy_id, action="close", trade_id, reason) at scanner.py:3955-3960, which emits the wired trade_failed operator notification (Discord + in-app) at scanner.py:3218-3228; because the action is "close" (not "open"), the 3203 guard skips _fail_unfilled_open_trade, leaving the trade OPEN. The parity gap (legacy alerts, kernel-live does not) is real. (5) The trade-stays-OPEN claim is correct: _close_trade_db (5914) runs only after _execute_direct returns, so a raise leaves the row OPEN for automatic retry next scan, and the position remains protected by its resting reduce-only stop placed at open. REACHABILITY: this is the DEFAULT production live route — live_kernel_execution defaults True (scanner.py:5828) and _is_live_kernel_stage matches live/live_graduated/deployed stages (5831-5833), dispatched at 6619-6623; it is exactly the path active when the system goes live with real money. SEVERITY: medium is fair — no direct money loss or state corruption (trade stays open, auto-retries, resting stop still protects), but on the REAL live path an exchange-degraded failure to execute the intended signal exit produces no operator alarm, a genuine recoverable-failure observability gap. Not raised to high because the resting stop and per-scan retry bound the exposure.

### `LIVE-5` — Kernel execution path is not bar-staleness gated — live can trade off hours-old candles during a feed stall

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5956-5965 (kernel fetch, no recency check); DI-1 gate lives only in _scan_asset_group at 6356-6380`
- **Claim:** manage_positions_via_kernel independently fetches its own candles (fetch_candles + _trim_unclosed_latest_candle) and re-runs the full kernel to DECIDE opens/closes, but performs no recency check on the latest closed bar. The DI-1 fail-closed staleness gate (block when the last closed bar is older than N bar-durations) is implemented only in _scan_asset_group (the signal-matrix builder) and does not cover the kernel execution path, which runs regardless of whether the matrix signal was blocked.
- **Impact:** On a data-feed stall (cache serving old candles), the live kernel can generate spurious entry/exit decisions and stop/target levels off stale prices and place a REAL order (the market fill itself is at the current mid, but the decision and geometry are stale). Affects paper too, but only live costs money. Likelihood depends on cache behavior under outage.
- **Suggested fix:** Apply the same DI-1 last-closed-bar staleness check inside manage_positions_via_kernel after the fetch (using scanner_max_candle_staleness_bars and _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS) and _skip the scan when stale, so the parity execution path fails closed exactly like the signal path.
- **Evidence:** Kernel fetch: `df = _enrich_scan_frame(fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), interval=timeframe), ...); df = _trim_unclosed_latest_candle(df, timeframe)` (5957-5960) followed only by `if df is None or df.empty or len(df) < 20: return _skip(...)` (5964) — no age check. DI-1 (only in _scan_asset_group): comment 'Nothing else between the candle fetch and signal generation checks that the latest CLOSED bar is recent ... this is the real gate' and `if _max_bars > 0 and _age_since_close > _max_bars * _bar_secs: ... BLOCKED` (6356-6380).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified. manage_positions_via_kernel (forven/scanner.py:5931) independently fetches candles at 5957-5960 (fetch_candles + _trim_unclosed_latest_candle) and the ONLY post-fetch guard is the length check at 5964 (`df is None or df.empty or len(df) < 20`). I read the full function body 5931-6179: there is NO last-closed-bar recency/staleness check anywhere. The one staleness-aware branch (late-entry hop-in vs _PRICE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS at 6104-6111) is unreachable because late_entry_enabled=False (6069). The DI-1 fail-closed staleness gate is confirmed to exist ONLY in _scan_asset_group at 6356-6400 (the `_age_since_close > _max_bars * _bar_secs` block with the comment 'this is the real gate'). Crucially, the kernel execution path runs independently of the matrix block: _evaluate_signal_matrix appends EVERY scanned item — including _blocked_scan_row rows — to signal_rows (6509), and _apply_execution_actions (called at 6949) dispatches manage_positions_via_kernel at 6614-6623 based on stage/flag (_is_kernel_paper_strategy / _is_live_kernel_stage), not on the matrix signal, which the kernel ignores entirely (it re-fetches and re-simulates). So a DI-1 block on the signal does not stop the kernel from opening/closing off stale candles. Reachability of stale data is real: fetch_candles (1692-1699) returns a non-empty stale cache outright when scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch is off (1698-1699), and an upstream source that succeeds while lagging (exactly the 'cache serving old candles' threat DI-1 names) flows in ungated under default config too. On live, a faithful kernel open routes to _kernel_open_live_trade (6093/6142) and places a REAL order; the fill is at current mid via _execute_direct but the entry/exit decision and stop/target geometry are derived from the stale bar — matching the claimed impact. Line refs (5956-5965, 6356-6380) are accurate. Severity medium retained: default execution path touching live money, but bounded (fill at current mid, not stale price) and the most direct stale-serve path needs non-default config or upstream lag — a defense-in-depth parity gap rather than an open hole.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) manage_positions_via_kernel (forven/scanner.py:5956-5965) independently fetches candles (fetch_candles + _enrich_scan_frame + _trim_unclosed_latest_candle) and the only guard before run_strategy_execution (6005) and reconcile (6085) is `len(df) < 20` (5964). Reading the whole body 5956-6157, there is NO last-closed-bar recency/age check; the only staleness-aware code (live-price cache at 6108) is in the late-entry branch, which is dead because late_entry_enabled=False is hard-coded (6069). (2) The DI-1 fail-closed staleness gate exists ONLY in _scan_asset_group at 6356-6400 (scanner_max_candle_staleness_bars default 2, _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS), with its own comment 'this is the real gate'. (3) The paths are genuinely independent: when DI-1 fires it appends a _blocked_scan_row and continues (6390-6400), but _evaluate_signal_matrix still appends EVERY row including blocked ones to signal_rows (6509), and _apply_execution_actions (6602-6623) invokes manage_positions_via_kernel based solely on the feature flags + stage, never inspecting the signal's block_reason. The kernel re-fetches its own candles and re-derives opens/closes, so a DI-1 block does not stop it. DI-1 thus protects only the legacy path, not the default kernel path. Reachability: paper_kernel_execution defaults True (5222) and live_kernel_execution defaults True (5828); _is_live_kernel_stage covers live/live_graduated/deployed (5831-5833); live places a REAL order via _kernel_open_live_trade/_execute_direct (5836+). The impact description is accurate — fill is at current mid but the open/close decision and stop/target geometry are off the stale bar. Real-money loss is double-gated (feed stall + FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1, testnet otherwise per 5824-5826), and the codebase itself confirms the precondition (DI-1 comment: cache can serve old candles during a stall). Severity stays medium: requires a data-stall edge condition, and money loss additionally requires mainnet; paper (default on) is also affected but only corrupts the track record. Note for reviewers: because the kernel is the DEFAULT execution path for all vectorized strategies, DI-1 staleness protection is effectively bypassed for the primary order-placing path — a case could be made for high, but the conjunction of conditions required for real loss keeps it at medium.

### `LIVE-6` — Fill recording falls back to the aggressive limit price when the exchange response omits avgPx, recording a non-real entry/full-fill

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1410-1417; forven/scanner.py:3370-3402`
- **Claim:** market_order returns entry_price = actual_fill if avgPx present else `price` (the 2%-aggressive IOC limit: mid*1.02 buy / mid*0.98 sell) and filled_size = actual_size if present else the requested `size`. _execute_direct then records that fallback via _update_trade_fill as the real fill_entry_price (and a full filled_size). So when the HL response lacks fill data (e.g. an IOC that did not fill but returned a resting/oid, or a response without `filled.avgPx`), the trade is booked as fully filled at a price ~2% off the mark, not the real avgPx — or a phantom fill for an order that never filled.
- **Impact:** Live entry price (and thus every downstream PnL/stop-distance calc for that trade) can be recorded ~2% wrong on a long/short when avgPx is missing, and an unfilled IOC can be booked as a full position at the limit price. Shared with the legacy path (both use market_order + _execute_direct), so not kernel-specific, but it is on the live fill path in scope. Frequency depends on how often HL omits avgPx on a filled market IOC (normally present).
- **Suggested fix:** Treat a missing avgPx as 'fill unknown' on the OPEN path (mirror the close path's fill-is-None handling): mark pending_open_reconcile / verify against the exchange position+real avgPx before recording fill_entry_price=limit, rather than silently substituting the aggressive limit price and claiming a full fill.
- **Evidence:** `"entry_price": actual_fill if actual_fill is not None else price` and `"filled_size": actual_size if actual_size is not None else size` (hyperliquid.py:1415,1417); actual_fill is None when `filled.avgPx` is absent (_extract_fill_price returns None, 1187-1199). _execute_direct: `fill, exchange_order_id, order_meta = _extract_order_meta(result)` then `if fill is not None: _update_trade_fill(trade_id, fill, "entry", ...)` (3374-3402) — fill is never None on open because of the limit fallback.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The code literally does what the claim states. In forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py, market_order's payload sets "entry_price": actual_fill if actual_fill is not None else price (line 1415) and "filled_size": actual_size if actual_size is not None else size (line 1417), where actual_fill=_extract_fill_price (line 1410) returns None when filled.avgPx is absent (line 1195 falsy-checks filled.get("avgPx")), and price is the 2%-aggressive IOC limit (mid*1.02 buy / mid*0.98 sell, lines 1343-1344). So a missing avgPx books the entry at the aggressive limit, and a missing totalSz books a full fill.

In forven/scanner.py::_execute_direct open path, _extract_order_meta computes fill = payload.get("entry_price") or ... or payload.get("mid") (lines 3283-3289); entry_price is always populated by market_order, so fill is never None on open, and lines 3394-3402 always call _update_trade_fill(trade_id, fill, "entry", ..., filled_size=filled_size_f). With filled_size falling back to the full size, the partial-fill check at line 3386 (filled<size) is False, so it is recorded as a full fill at the limit price. _open_via_execution (lines 3963-4032) returns opened_ok=True whenever _execute_direct does not raise, so the pending_open_reconcile path (lines 4816-4825) does NOT cover this — it only fires on raised open failures.

The asymmetry strongly corroborates the gap: close_position (line 1893) returns "exit_price": fill_price with NO limit fallback (None when avgPx absent), and the close path forces fill=None then mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile (scanner.py lines 3453-3454, 3499-3512). The open path lacks this fail-to-reconcile handling, exactly as the suggested fix notes.

Two caveats on reachability (which the finding itself acknowledges, and which keep this at medium not higher): (1) a fully-filled HL market IOC essentially always returns avgPx alongside totalSz, so the wrong-by-2% entry rarely fires; (2) the headline "phantom fill for an unfilled IOC" is partly mitigated — _require_bulk_order_ids (lines 1280-1305) raises when the entry status carries no oid (the top-level "error" is empty for an "ok" response), turning a true zero-fill into a raised failure -> pending_open_reconcile rather than a phantom fill, UNLESS HL returns an oid for a zero-fill IOC (not verifiable from code). The core defect — fail-open substitution of a non-real price/size on the live OPEN path, asymmetric with the close path's fail-closed reconcile — is genuinely present and would corrupt the recorded entry, stop distance, and PnL when it fires. Severity medium (edge-case/degraded, real money impact when triggered, low frequency) is appropriate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-verified and reachable on the LIVE fill path. forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1415 sets entry_price = actual_fill if actual_fill is not None else price, and 1417 sets filled_size = actual_size if actual_size is not None else size; price is the 2%-aggressive IOC limit (mid*1.02 buy / mid*0.98 sell, lines 1343-1344), and _extract_fill_price (1187-1199) returns None when filled.avgPx is absent. In scanner._execute_direct, _extract_order_meta (3283-3289) reads entry_price FIRST, so on the open path fill is the limit fallback and is never None; line 3394-3402 then records it via _update_trade_fill(trade_id, fill, "entry", ...) as the real fill_entry_price with the (full) filled_size. The asymmetry the finding cites is real: the CLOSE path keeps the real fill (exit_price=fill_price, None when avgPx absent; the limit is stored separately as close_price — hyperliquid.py:1892-1893) and explicitly forces fill=None when the real fill is missing (scanner.py:3452-3454), routing to mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile (3505-3511). The OPEN path has no equivalent reconcile/verify guard, so a missing avgPx silently books the aggressive limit as the true entry, corrupting downstream PnL/stop-distance. This is the live path (paper is handled separately via paper_test_local_execution at scanner.py:3971-3983; the legacy/queued live paths at 1188/3936/4011 share market_order + _execute_direct). Severity stays medium, not higher: the most alarming sub-claim (a never-filled IOC booked as a full position) is largely mitigated because a fully-canceled IOC has no oid and _require_bulk_order_ids (1280-1305) raises on a missing entry oid, failing the open. The remaining trigger — a filled IOC whose HL response omits avgPx, or an oid-bearing-but-unfilled status (improbable under IOC semantics) — is an exchange anomaly that I cannot quantify from code, and the finding itself flags it as 'normally present'. So the defect (fail-open substitution of the limit price as the real fill, no reconcile guard) is confirmed and live, but its real-world frequency is low; medium (edge-case/degraded on the money path) is the right level.

### `HL-3` — place_protective_stop / place_take_profit silently swallow a per-status order rejection (no error, no oid); manual adjust then reports a false 'success' on an unarmed stop

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** hl  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1637-1657 (place_protective_stop), 1717-1737 (place_take_profit); caller forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:738-754 and 718-725`
- **Claim:** Unlike market_order/limit_order, these single-order placers do NOT call _require_bulk_order_ids and never synthesize a top-level error. On a per-status rejection (`statuses:[{"error":...}]`) or a top-level `{"status":"err"}`, they return a payload with neither 'error' nor 'stop_order_id'/'take_profit_order_id'. A caller that only checks result.get('error') will believe the protective order was armed.
- **Impact:** Operator sets a manual stop, gets a success response, but the stop was rejected and is not on the book. The position is unprotected until the periodic reconcile's _repair_position_protection re-arms it (risk.py correctly checks `not stop_order_id` at 1371, so the automated path is safe — but the manual UX/state is wrong and there is an interim unprotected window with a false confirmation).
- **Suggested fix:** In place_protective_stop/place_take_profit, when _extract_bulk_order_ids returns no id, detect the per-status/top-level rejection and return {"error": <status error or 'protective order rejected'>} (or raise), so every caller fails closed and surfaces the rejection instead of silently returning None.
- **Evidence:** place_protective_stop: `order_ids = _extract_bulk_order_ids(result, ['stop']); payload = {**result, 'stop_loss': stop_px, 'order_ids': order_ids}; if 'stop' in order_ids: payload['stop_order_id'] = ...` (1648-1656) — no error path when order_ids is empty. paper_control._place_live_protective: `if isinstance(result, dict) and result.get('error'): raise...; return result.get('stop_order_id') or result.get('take_profit_order_id') or result.get('order_id')` (752-754) returns None on rejection; _adjust_protective then `new_oid = ...; if new_oid is not None: updates[oid_key]=...; else: updates.pop(oid_key,None); ... updates['exchange_stop_requested']=True; ... return _refresh(session_id)` (718-726) — reports success to the operator with NO stop armed.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified at every cited line. place_protective_stop (forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1648-1657) and place_take_profit (1728-1737) call only _extract_bulk_order_ids and build payload = {**result, ..., 'order_ids': order_ids}, setting stop_order_id/take_profit_order_id/order_id ONLY when the label is in order_ids. Neither calls _require_bulk_order_ids and neither synthesizes an 'error'. This is the exact contrast with market_order (calls _require_bulk_order_ids at 1403) and limit_order (1541); _require_bulk_order_ids (1280-1305) is the fail-closed guard that raises RuntimeError when IDs are missing and no top-level error is present. The maintainers clearly know placements can return a dict with no oid and no 'error' (that is the whole purpose of _require_bulk_order_ids), so the rejection scenario is real and reachable.

On a per-status rejection the status is {'error': ...} with no oid/resting/filled, so _extract_bulk_order_ids (1232-1247) skips it and returns {}; on a top-level {'status':'err','response':<str>} the response is not a dict so it again returns {}. _submit (140-179) returns the raw SDK dict and never injects 'error'. Hence the returned payload has neither 'error' nor any order-id key.

Downstream confirmed: _place_live_protective (forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:752-754) sees result.get('error') == None so does NOT raise, and the order-id or-chain is all None → returns None. _adjust_protective (718-726) then takes the else branch (updates.pop(oid_key, None)), still sets exchange_stop_requested=True, writes the new manual stop price, and returns _refresh(session_id) — a success response to the operator with no stop actually on the book.

Impact/mitigation accurate: the automated recovery path risk.py:1370-1373 computes stop_order_id and fails closed on `not stop_order_id` (sets placement_error, does not claim success), and exchange_stop_requested is only ever written, never read as a skip-gate (verified via grep — all matches are assignments), so the periodic reconcile re-arms. Therefore the defect is a fail-OPEN/false-confirmation with an interim unprotected window rather than a permanent naked position. This matches the medium rating: a real asymmetry where the entry placers fail closed but the manual protective-adjust path fails open. Severity unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): VERIFIED against live code. (1) place_protective_stop (forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1648-1657) and place_take_profit (1728-1737) extract IDs via _extract_bulk_order_ids but, unlike market_order (1403-1408) and limit_order (1541-1546), do NOT call _require_bulk_order_ids and never synthesize a top-level error. The payload is {**result, 'stop_loss': stop_px, 'order_ids': order_ids} with stop_order_id added only when the label is present (1654-1656). (2) Both rejection shapes yield empty order_ids: a per-status {'statuses':[{'error':...}]} (no oid/resting/filled, so _extract_bulk_order_ids 1232-1247 extracts nothing) and a top-level {'status':'err','response':'<string>'} (response is a string, so data/statuses are None → {} at 1226-1230). (3) _submit (140-179) returns the SDK dict verbatim and injects no 'error' key on a business-level rejection (it only re-raises on network/breaker failures), so the placer payload has neither 'error' nor an order-id field. (4) Caller _place_live_protective (forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:748-754) raises only on result.get('error'); with no error key it returns result.get('stop_order_id') or take_profit_order_id or order_id → None. (5) _adjust_protective (718-726): new_oid is None → updates.pop(oid_key, None) (a no-op since oid_key was never added in the rejection branch), sets exchange_stop_requested=True, persists the new stop_loss_price, and returns _refresh() = a success response with NO stop armed. So the false-success-on-unarmed-stop chain is exactly as claimed. Additional state corruption I confirmed: the replace branch passes no `removals` (contrast the clear branch at 703 which uses removals=(price_key, oid_key)), so the now-cancelled OLD exchange_stop_order_id (cancelled at 716-717) is retained in signal_data alongside the phantom new stop price. REACHABILITY: live-only (guarded by `if live:` at 713); manual position controls and live execution are enabled in production per memory, so this is a real real-money path. Because the prior stop is cancelled before the rejected replacement, the position is genuinely naked during the interim window under a false confirmation. IMPACT BOUND (mitigation confirmed): _repair_position_protection (forven/exchange/risk.py:1319-1393) computes coverage from the live order book via _summarize_position_protection (1322/1326 fully_protected), not from the DB oid, and re-places a prior/emergency stop when the book shows no resting reduce-only stop (1371 `not stop_order_id`). So the automated reconcile re-arms protection regardless of the stale DB oid, bounding money loss to the reconcile-cadence window. Per-status rejections of a valid reduce-only trigger are edge cases (sub-min-notional position, near-mid trigger; wrong-side stops are already blocked client-side by _validate_protective_level at 710), not the common path. Net: a genuine fail-open / false-confirmation defect on a safety-critical live control, with a real but bounded naked window and an additional stale-oid state inconsistency — medium is the correct severity (not critical/high given the automated reconcile safety net and edge-case trigger conditions).

### `HL-2` — get_all_mids serves cached mids with NO staleness/TTL bound when the price breaker is open; these feed order pricing and defeat limit_order's stale-price guard

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** hl  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:2072-2076 (get_all_mids breaker-open fallback), 1463-1474 (limit_order stale-price reject), 1339-1344 (market_order slippage limit), 1865-1876 (close_position slippage limit)`
- **Claim:** When hl_price_breaker is open, get_all_mids returns kv_get('daemon_state').last_prices with no timestamp/age check. limit_order computes both its reference mid AND its stale-order rejection threshold from this same (possibly stale) value, so price_deviation_pct = abs(price-mid)/mid is measured against a stale anchor — the _LIMIT_ORDER_STALE_REJECT_PCT guard becomes meaningless. market_order/close_position also size their aggressive IOC limit off this stale mid.
- **Impact:** For an emergency reduce-only IOC close, mispricing off a stale mid is partially self-limiting (reduce-only, IOC just fails to fill if too far) — the documented tradeoff. But for limit_order the staleness guard intended to block off-market orders is silently disabled, and any non-reduce-only order priced off a stale mid can fill far from the true market. No fix is needed if limit_order is never used on the live hot path, but the guard is advertised as a safety check and is not reliable when the breaker is open.
- **Suggested fix:** Stamp last_prices with a timestamp in daemon_state and have get_all_mids drop / age-flag cached mids older than a small bound; have limit_order refuse (fail closed) rather than trust a flagged-stale mid for its deviation check.
- **Evidence:** `if not hl_price_breaker.can_execute(): cached = kv_get('daemon_state', {}).get('last_prices'); if isinstance(cached, dict): return {str(k): float(v) for k,v in cached.items() if _is_valid_price(v)}` (2072-2076) — _is_valid_price only checks >0, never age. limit_order: `mid = float(get_all_mids(testnet).get(asset,0) or 0); ... price_deviation_pct = abs(price-mid)/mid; if price_deviation_pct > _LIMIT_ORDER_STALE_REJECT_PCT: return {error...}` (1463-1474).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): Code-truth confirmed at every cited line. get_all_mids (forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:2072-2076) returns kv_get("daemon_state").get("last_prices") filtered only by _is_valid_price, which is literally `float(value) > 0` (2097-2101) — no timestamp/age check. last_prices is persisted at daemon.py:1458 as a bare symbol→price dict (`dict(snapshot.get("prices") or prices)`) with no per-key timestamp; the daemon does stamp state["last_tick_ts"] (1447) in the same daemon_state but get_all_mids never reads it, so there is genuinely no TTL/staleness bound on the served mids. limit_order (1463-1474) derives BOTH its reference `mid` and the stale-reject threshold (`price_deviation_pct = abs(price-mid)/mid` vs _LIMIT_ORDER_STALE_REJECT_PCT=0.05) from that same value, so when hl_price_breaker is open the guard measures the order price against a stale anchor and is unreliable — exactly as claimed. market_order (1339-1344) and close_position (1865-1876) likewise price their aggressive IOC limit off the same mid. The breaker opens after 5 price-API failures and stays open 20s (circuit_breaker.py:78-83), so the path is reachable.

Severity downgraded medium→low on impact: (1) limit_order — the function whose guard the finding centers on — is NOT on the live/paper hot path; only an agent tool (forven/agents/tools_exchange.py:415) and a verify script call it. The scanner hot path uses market_order (scanner.py:3369) and close_position (3436, 7229), both IOC. (2) IOC and limit orders fill at limit-or-better, so a stale mid changes fill PROBABILITY, not fill quality beyond the stated limit — a buy never pays above stale_mid*1.02, a sell never sells below stale_mid*0.98 — which the finding itself acknowledges as self-limiting. (3) last_prices may well stay fresh from an independent WS feed even when the HTTP price breaker trips, so true staleness often does not materialize. The one genuinely money-relevant residual is a missed/stranded emergency close during a simultaneous extended price-outage AND sharp adverse move, partly mitigated by the kill-switch slippage_bps escalation to 10% (1871-1874). The defect is real and the suggested fix (timestamp last_prices, age-flag in get_all_mids, fail-closed in limit_order) is sound, but the practical loss exposure is low rather than medium.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): Code facts verified exactly. get_all_mids breaker-open fallback (hyperliquid.py:2072-2076) returns kv_get('daemon_state').last_prices filtered only by _is_valid_price (2097-2101: float(value) > 0), with NO timestamp/age bound. limit_order (1463-1474) derives both its reference mid and its price_deviation_pct stale-reject threshold from the same get_all_mids value, so the guard anchors on the possibly-stale cache and cannot detect that its anchor is stale. market_order (1339-1344) and close_position (1865-1876) likewise price their IOC limit off the cached mid. All four line citations are accurate. So the defect (cached mids feed order pricing with no staleness bound, and limit_order's guard is self-anchored) is real and present.\n\nReachability lowers it from medium to low: (1) The headline guard-defeat is non-production — limit_order's ONLY caller is the agent tool at forven/agents/tools_exchange.py:415, which hardcodes testnet=True (line 422); there is no real-money caller, so the 'advertised safety check is unreliable' impact does not touch live funds. (2) The live hot path (_execute_direct -> market_order/close_position) submits IOC limit orders where limit_px is a price CAP: fills happen at true market within the cap or the order doesn't fill, so over-pay is bounded by the 2% (open) cap and closes are self-limiting (the finding itself concedes this 'documented tradeoff'). (3) last_prices is primarily sourced from an independent Binance WS feed (daemon.py:1693 BinancePriceFeed; HL HTTP all_mids is only a fallback poll at daemon.py:1758), so during a typical hl_price_breaker-open (HL HTTP flaky, WS alive) the cache is actually fresh; the genuinely-stale case needs BOTH feeds down, where no fresh price exists anywhere. (4) The worst live scenario (a stranded emergency close priced off a stale mid) is mitigated by kill-switch slippage_bps escalation (close_position:1869-1875). Net: a real but bounded, edge-case degradation of a defensive price source, with the strongest claim confined to a testnet-only path.

### `RISK-1` — Kernel paper open path (now the DEFAULT) bypasses every risk gate, including the operator STOP / kill-switch / daily-halt / cooldown

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** risk  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5415-5501 (_kernel_open_paper_trade), dispatched at 6093 + 6142-6143 (manage_positions_via_kernel), 6614-6618 (default-on dispatch); gate-bearing alternatives at 5855 (live) / 4407 (legacy) / 971 (guard)`
- **Claim:** For vectorizable paper strategies (the default path, paper_kernel_execution=True at scanner.py:5222), opens are applied by _kernel_open_paper_trade, which calls _open_trade_db + register() WITHOUT ever calling can_open() or is_trading_allowed(). The legacy paper path and ALL live paths gate; this one does not.
- **Impact:** When an operator presses STOP (system pause), or while the live kill-switch / daily-loss halt is tripped, or during a strategy's post-loss cooldown, the now-default paper engine keeps opening NEW paper positions. No real money is lost directly, but (a) the operator's STOP no longer halts paper trading (a control-integrity regression vs the legacy path), and (b) paper track records are the data the promotion gate uses to send strategies LIVE — opening trades during halts/pauses distorts that record and can promote a strategy on invalid numbers.
- **Suggested fix:** Call is_trading_allowed() (and, for the per-asset/concurrency/cooldown checks, can_open with enforce_risk_caps=False) at the top of _kernel_open_paper_trade, or gate the open branch in manage_positions_via_kernel/_apply_execution_actions, so the kernel paper path honors the same STOP/kill-switch/daily-halt/cooldown gates the legacy paper path and the live kernel path already enforce.
- **Evidence:** _kernel_open_paper_trade opens directly: scanner.py:5491 `trade_id = _open_trade_db(... execution_type="paper" ...)` then 5497 `register(trade_id, ...)` — no can_open/is_trading_allowed anywhere in 5415-5501. The applier is selected at 6093 `open_applier = _kernel_open_live_trade if is_live else _kernel_open_paper_trade` and invoked at 6142 `msg = open_applier(...)`. By contrast the LIVE applier gates: scanner.py:5855 `allowed, alloc_risk, why = can_open(asset, direction, strat_id, execution_type="live", enforce_risk_caps=False)`. run_scan/_apply_execution_actions never checks the pause: _apply_execution_actions (6597) runs whenever `execution_allowed` (6948), and execution_allowed = requested_execution and _scanner_execution_enabled() (scanner.py:6818, setting default True), independent of is_system_paused. The scheduler only skips the scan in MANUAL mode: scheduler.py:2289 `if autonomy_paused:` where is_autonomy_paused()=='manual' (system_pause.py:135-137), which system_pause.py:140-186 documents as ORTHOGONAL to the operator STOP flag (is_system_paused). is_trading_allowed (the gate the legacy path used) blocks on is_system_paused (risk.py:3293-3294), kill_switch_active (3307), and daily_loss_halt (3310) — none of which are consulted on the kernel paper path.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the defect. (1) _kernel_open_paper_trade (scanner.py:5415-5501) opens directly via _open_trade_db at 5491 (execution_type="paper") + register at 5497 + _update_trade_fill at 5500, with NO can_open/is_trading_allowed; a grep for those calls across scanner.py confirms none appear between 5501 and the live opener at 5855. (2) It is the default: _paper_kernel_execution_enabled() = _scanner_bool_setting("paper_kernel_execution", True) (5220-5222); applier selected at 6093 (open_applier = _kernel_open_live_trade if is_live else _kernel_open_paper_trade) and invoked at 6142-6143. (3) By contrast the LEGACY paper path gates: manage_positions calls can_open(..., execution_type=execution_type, enforce_risk_caps=False) at 4407, and can_open calls is_trading_allowed() at risk.py:535 (Rule 0, BEFORE the paper/live scope split at 623) plus the post-loss cooldown at risk.py:661-664 — both apply to paper scope. (4) The LIVE kernel path gates too: can_open(..., execution_type="live") at 5855. (5) is_trading_allowed (risk.py:3287-3313) blocks on is_system_paused() 3293, kill_switch_active 3307, daily_loss_halt 3310 — exactly as claimed. (6) The autonomous scan path has no pause gate: the scheduled scanner_run job calls run_scan(execute_positions=True) directly (scheduler.py:1326-1337); run_scan gates only on execution_allowed = requested_execution and _scanner_execution_enabled() (6818), and _scanner_execution_enabled() = _scanner_bool_setting("scanner_execution_enabled", True) (704-705), no is_system_paused. The scheduler skips jobs only when autonomy_paused (scheduler.py:2289) = get_system_mode()==MODE_MANUAL (system_pause.py:135-137), which is orthogonal to the operator STOP flag is_system_paused() (system_pause.py:123-124; docstring 143 states the halt flag is orthogonal to autonomy mode). Net: when the operator presses STOP (or kill-switch / daily-halt trips, or a strategy is in post-loss cooldown), the default kernel paper engine keeps opening NEW paper positions, whereas the legacy paper path and live kernel path would block. Reachability and impact are as described. One nuance: the MANUAL operator-triggered scan (control_plane/ops.py:520) DOES call is_trading_allowed() before run_scan, so manually-triggered execution scans are blocked during a pause — but the autonomous scheduled scanner_run is the live, default trigger and is ungated. Severity medium is correct: no direct money loss (paper), but a real control-integrity regression vs the legacy path and a distortion vector for the live-promotion record. Kept unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every link verified against live code. (1) _kernel_open_paper_trade (scanner.py:5415-5501) opens via _open_trade_db (5491) + register (5497) with NO can_open/is_trading_allowed in the function. (2) The live kernel applier DOES gate: _kernel_open_live_trade calls can_open(..., execution_type="live", enforce_risk_caps=False) at 5855 and returns BLOCKED. (3) The legacy paper applier DOES gate: manage_positions calls can_open at 4407 and emits BLOCKED at 4416. (4) can_open (risk.py:490) unconditionally calls is_trading_allowed at 535; is_trading_allowed (3287) returns False on is_system_paused (3293), kill_switch_active (3307), daily_loss_halt (3310). (5) The default paper dispatch selects the ungated applier: scanner.py:6093 picks _kernel_open_paper_trade for non-live; paper_kernel_execution defaults True (5222) and _apply_execution_actions dispatches to it (6614-6618). Reachability confirmed: run_scan computes execution_allowed = requested_execution and _scanner_execution_enabled() (6818), neither consulting is_system_paused; _scanner_execution_enabled defaults True (705). The scheduler scanner_run job (scheduler.py:1326-1337) calls run_scan(execute_positions=True) with no pause check, and only skips on autonomy_paused (2289), which is manual-mode-only (system_pause.py:135-137). Operator STOP is orthogonal to mode: stop_system (ops.py:63) and post_emergency_halt (ops.py:987) call set_system_paused(True) only, and set_system_paused deliberately preserves the mode (system_pause.py:143-149), so the scheduler keeps scanning while paused. The emergency-halt KS-2 comment (ops.py:982-986) explicitly relies on system pause to block new opens — exactly what the default kernel paper path defeats for paper. Impact correctly sized: paper-only (live is protected at 5855), so no direct real-money loss, which caps severity below high/critical; it is a genuine, reachable control-integrity regression on the now-default path. The secondary promotion-distortion claim is plausible but weaker (parity intentionally makes paper mirror the backtest, which never pauses for STOP). Medium is appropriate; unchanged.

### `RISK-3` — Manual LIVE open can place a naked real position (no protective stop) and skips the execution-time halt re-assert the automated path enforces

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** risk  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:536-643 (_live_open), reached from open_manual_position 482-488; contrast scanner.py:3336-3345 (_execute_direct)`
- **Claim:** _live_open places a real Hyperliquid market_order with stop_loss_price that may be None, and calls market_order directly rather than _execute_direct, so it neither requires a protective stop nor re-asserts is_trading_allowed at execution time.
- **Impact:** An operator opening a live position by hand without a stop creates an unbounded-loss real position; a gap/violent move can run it far past any intended risk before manual intervention. The automated engine treats a missing stop as a hard refusal, so this is an inconsistent, money-exposing hole on the manual live path. (Note: router comment paper.py:110-111 claims manual controls are paper-only, but the _session_is_live -> _live_open branch is live-capable, so the comment is stale.)
- **Suggested fix:** In _live_open, refuse to open when stop_loss_price is missing/invalid (mirror scanner.py:3336), or route the manual live open through _execute_direct so it inherits the stop requirement and the H8 execution-time is_trading_allowed re-assert.
- **Evidence:** open_manual_position passes the (optional) stop through: paper_control.py:475-476 `sl = _coerce_optional_float(stop_loss_price)` (validated only `if sl is not None and sl > 0`), then 482-487 `if _session_is_live(session): _live_open(... stop_loss_price=sl ...)`. In _live_open the order is sent with the possibly-None stop: paper_control.py:586-590 `result = market_order(asset, side, float(resolved_size), stop_loss_price=stop_loss_price, take_profit_price=take_profit_price, testnet=testnet, vault_address=vault)`. There is no `if stop_loss_price is None: raise` guard. The automated path refuses exactly this: scanner.py:3336-3337 `if stop_loss is None and not is_sim_active(): raise ValueError(f"refusing to open {trade_id} without a protective stop")` and re-checks the halt at 3341-3345 (H8). The can_open gate at paper_control.py:556 runs earlier but does not require a stop and is not re-asserted before the order at 586.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): CODE-TRUTH confirms the primary defect. open_manual_position (forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:450) defaults stop_loss_price=None; line 475 `sl = _coerce_optional_float(stop_loss_price)` yields None and the validation at 477 (`if sl is not None and sl > 0`) is skipped, then 482-487 calls _live_open with stop_loss_price=sl=None. _live_open (536-643) has NO None-stop guard. When an explicit size>0 is supplied, the risk-sizing branch (565-580) is bypassed and control reaches market_order at 586-590 with stop_loss_price=None. forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1308 market_order only attaches the protective stop leg under `if stop_loss_price:` (line 1356), so a None stop places a bare IOC entry = a naked real position with no protective stop. This is reachable in production: routers/paper.py:123-133 (/api/paper/sessions/{id}/open-position) calls open_manual_position, which branches to _live_open for deployed/live sessions via _session_is_live -> _session_is_deployed (paper_control.py:85-86); the router comment at paper.py:111 ("paper-only; deployed/live sessions are rejected") is genuinely stale. The contrast is exact: the automated engine hard-refuses a stopless open at scanner.py:3336-3337 `if stop_loss is None and not is_sim_active(): raise ValueError(...)`. The secondary claim is also accurate but minor: can_open (forven/exchange/risk.py:490) does run is_trading_allowed() internally at line 535, but it executes at paper_control.py:556 and is NOT re-asserted immediately before the order at 586, whereas the automated path adds the H8 re-assert at scanner.py:3341-3345. Because the manual path is synchronous, the halt-window is tiny, so the missing-stop hole is the real money-exposing issue, not the halt gap. Severity medium is appropriate: it is operator-initiated and still passes the can_open risk gates (kill-switch/daily-loss/margin), but it inconsistently permits an unbounded-loss real position that the automated engine forbids. Suggested fix (mirror scanner.py:3336 in _live_open, or route through _execute_direct) is sound.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified end-to-end against live code. (1) The endpoint body makes the stop optional: api_core.py:3335 `stop_loss_price: float | None = Field(default=None, gt=0)`. (2) open_manual_position only validates the stop if present: paper_control.py:475 `sl = _coerce_optional_float(stop_loss_price)` and :477 `if sl is not None and sl > 0: _validate_protective_level(...)` — no existence requirement. (3) For live (deployed) sessions it routes to _live_open with the possibly-None stop: paper_control.py:482-487; _session_is_live (:85-86) = compat_kind=='deployed', set when stage_status=='live_graduated' (paper.py:741, :886) — a real, shipped live state. (4) _live_open (read fully 536-643) passes the None stop straight through with no guard: paper_control.py:586-590 `market_order(asset, side, float(resolved_size), stop_loss_price=stop_loss_price, ...)`. (5) market_order places a NAKED entry-only order when the stop is falsy: hyperliquid.py:1356 `if stop_loss_price:` gates the whole protective-stop leg, so None => no stop submitted (and the SIZE-1 inverted-stop guard is also skipped). On a configured live/mainnet deploy (_assert_execution_allowed only blocks unintended mainnet) this is a real, unprotected position. (6) The automated path enforces exactly what the manual path skips: scanner.py:3336-3337 hard-refuses opening without a protective stop, and :3341-3345 re-asserts is_trading_allowed() at execution time. _live_open only calls risk_mod.can_open (paper_control.py:556); can_open does check the halt (risk.py:535) but takes no stop param and is not re-asserted before the order at :586. (7) The router comment routers/paper.py:111 ('paper-only; deployed/live sessions are rejected') is stale — the domain explicitly routes deployed sessions to _live_open. The defect is real and reachable on the live path; it is gated only by the operator running live mode and deliberately omitting the stop (not a default-off flag, not a dead path). Because it requires explicit manual misuse rather than causing a silent automatic loss or surfacing wrong numbers, medium is the correct severity: an operator-facing safety-invariant gap that can expose real money to unbounded loss. Severity unchanged.

### `BOOT-1` — Unsynchronized boot race: scanner can run a live execution scan before the daemon writes the startup recovery gate, reading a stale recovery_active from the prior run

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** boot  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/api.py:436-481; forven/scheduler.py:2563-2576; forven/daemon.py:1883-1890; forven/exchange/risk.py:3296-3301`
- **Claim:** The startup recovery gate (daemon_state.recovery_active) that is supposed to keep NEW live entries blocked until the boot reconcile confirms the exchange is aligned is written ONLY by the daemon thread, while the scanner that opens positions runs in a SEPARATE scheduler thread that starts with the same delay and a head start, with no synchronization. On the first scan the scanner can read the PRIOR run's recovery state.
- **Impact:** If the prior run persisted recovery_active=False (last session reconciled cleanly) and the process crashed/restarted, a live new entry can pass can_open->is_trading_allowed during the boot window BEFORE the daemon re-verifies the exchange — defeating the startup recovery gate exactly when an orphaned/divergent position may exist. (can_open Rule 0c margin check and the resting stop still apply, which bounds but does not eliminate the harm.)
- **Suggested fix:** Make the scanner's execution path fail-closed until the in-process/external daemon has stamped a fresh recovery check for THIS boot: e.g. block live opens unless daemon_state.recovery_last_checked_at is newer than process start (or unless recovery_status is a terminal 'ok'/'resolved'), or have the lifespan write recovery_active=True/'checking' to daemon_state synchronously BEFORE spawning the scheduler thread.
- **Evidence:** api.py spawns both as supervised runtime threads with the SAME initial delay: scheduler-loop `_spawn_supervised_runtime_thread("scheduler-loop", lambda: run_scheduler_loop(interval_seconds=30), initial_delay_seconds=runtime_start_delay)` (api.py:436-440) and, AFTER it, daemon-loop `_spawn_supervised_runtime_thread("daemon-loop", run_daemon_in_loop, initial_delay_seconds=runtime_start_delay)` (api.py:475-481). The scheduler thread is created first, so its delay timer expires first. run_scheduler_loop then calls `apply_startup_catchup()` (scheduler.py:2563) which fast-forwards every stale job (incl. the execution scanner forven-scanner-hourly) to `now - 1s`, and the first `await asyncio.wait_for(tick(), ...)` runs immediately with no pre-sleep (scheduler.py:2571-2576). The daemon writes the gate only after acquiring the lock + the psutil orphan sweep + init_db: `_set_recovery_state(state, recovery_active=True, recovery_status="checking", ...)` then `_persist_daemon_state(state)` (daemon.py:1883-1890). The scanner's live open gate reads the PERSISTED state: is_trading_allowed() does `recovery_state = _get_recovery_state(); if recovery_state.get("recovery_active"): return False, ...` (risk.py:3296-3301), and _get_recovery_state reads kv_get("daemon_state") (risk.py:833).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every cited code fact is accurate and the architectural gap is real. (1) api.py:436-440 spawns scheduler-loop FIRST, then api.py:475-481 appends daemon-loop, both with initial_delay_seconds=runtime_start_delay (default 5.0s); _spawn_supervised_runtime_thread (api.py:175-185) just does threading.Event().wait(delay) then asyncio.run — no cross-thread sync on the recovery gate. (2) run_scheduler_loop (scheduler.py:2554-2576) calls apply_startup_catchup() then enters `while True:` and immediately awaits tick() with NO pre-sleep; apply_startup_catchup (747-766) fast-forwards every enabled job stale by >1min to now-1s, including the execution scanner. (3) The daemon stamps the gate (_set_recovery_state recovery_active=True / _persist_daemon_state, daemon.py:1883-1890) only AFTER _acquire_daemon_lock (1797), the psutil _sweep_orphan_multiprocessing_workers (1805), init_db (1813) and compute_runtime_code_fingerprint (1852) — so it is NOT instantaneous on wake; the CR-1 carry-forward (1856-1882) only re-blocks if the prior state was already a block and does nothing when the prior run cleanly persisted recovery_active=False. (4) is_trading_allowed (risk.py:3296-3301) reads _get_recovery_state, which reads kv_get("daemon_state") and DEFAULTS recovery_active to False (risk.py:836) — fail-OPEN. (5) The scanner's live-open path is gated only by is_trading_allowed (scanner.py:971) and can_open (scanner.py:1035; can_open re-checks is_trading_allowed at risk.py:535). A grep for any recovery/daemon-heartbeat precondition in scanner.py and scheduler.py found none (scanner only reads daemon_state for equity at 532-536). Thus a valid interleaving exists in which the scanner reads a stale recovery_active=False before the daemon stamps the boot gate, defeating the startup recovery block — a fail-open on the exact safety gate meant to fail-closed at boot. Severity unchanged (medium): the race is genuinely reachable but narrow — the daemon's stamp path is short and all-local while the scanner's path to the live-open gate is long (catch-up planner + tick + strategy/candle load + signal compute + network margin check), so the daemon wins on the overwhelming majority of boots, and the harm requires a conjunction (crash restart + a real divergence arising while down + a fresh live signal on the first tick + scanner winning the race + passing can_open Rule 0c margin and the resting stop). This places it at the lower edge of medium but it is a real defect.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): The structural defect is verified exactly as described. (1) api.py:434-481 spawns scheduler-loop and daemon-loop as independent supervised threads with the SAME initial_delay (default 5.0s, api.py:432; delay is a bare threading.Event().wait at api.py:177-178), scheduler first, with no cross-thread synchronization. (2) scheduler.py:2563 apply_startup_catchup() fast-forwards any job late by >1min to now-1s (line 760), and the first tick() at line 2576 runs with no pre-sleep. (3) daemon.py:1883-1890 writes the fail-closed gate (recovery_active=True/"checking") only AFTER _acquire_daemon_lock + _sweep_orphan_multiprocessing_workers + init_db (daemon.py:1797-1813), leaving an unprotected pre-write boot window. The CR-1 comment at daemon.py:1857-1862 shows the authors knew the scanner reads this KV cross-thread and fail-closed on prior blocks, but did NOT close the pre-write window itself — the exact residual gap. (4) risk.py:3287-3301 is_trading_allowed reads _get_recovery_state (risk.py:832-847) which kv_get("daemon_state") and DEFAULTS recovery_active to False, so a stale False from a clean prior reconcile (preflight success sets recovery_active=False, daemon.py:889/1067) passes the gate. The scanner re-checks the gate at scanner.py:971, can_open at :1035, and the H8 re-assert at :3343 — all read the same KV, so a single stale False passes every check. So the un-synchronized fail-open boot window is genuinely reachable in principle on the LIVE path. However, I downgrade severity to low because practical reachability is very low and harm is bounded: the scanner's path to a live-order gate-read (heavy tick() preamble of ~8 DB recovery sweeps, then run_scan loading candle data, per-strategy kernel advance, reconcile compute, passing the :971/:1035 guards, reaching :3343) is dramatically heavier than the daemon's local-only path to the gate write (lock+psutil+init_db+one KV write, all before the slow preflight at daemon.py:1905), so the daemon almost certainly stamps the gate first; and any money/state harm additionally requires a LIVE strategy emitting a fresh first-bar entry, a prior clean reconcile, AND an actual exchange divergence, while can_open Rule 0c's real exchange margin check plus the mandatory resting stop bound the downside. This is a real boot-time fail-open hardening gap, not a likely money-losing path; the suggested fix (write checking synchronously in lifespan before spawning the scheduler thread, or gate on recovery_last_checked_at being newer than process start) is appropriate.

### `FREEZE-2` — DI-1 stale-candle gate does not protect the kernel execution path it claims to guard

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** freeze  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:6356-6400 (DI-1 gate), 6509, 6602-6623 (_apply_execution_actions), 5956-5960 (kernel re-fetch)`
- **Claim:** The DI-1 gate's comment states it is 'the real gate' that stops the system generating live signals and 'size/stop orders off hours-old prices' during a data stall. But the gate lives only in the signal-evaluation loop and emits a _blocked_scan_row; that blocked row is still appended to signal_rows and _apply_execution_actions runs manage_positions_via_kernel for it WITHOUT consulting block_reason. The kernel re-fetches its own candles (which can return stale-but-valid data) with no staleness check, so paper/live kernel decisions — including real Hyperliquid opens sized and stopped off the stale bar's price — are still taken on stale data.
- **Impact:** On a feed/exchange stall that returns old-but-valid candles, the live kernel can still place a real market order (sized off the stale entry_price with resting SL/TP at stale levels via _kernel_open_live_trade, scanner.py:5850-5869) on a stale bar's signal — exactly the hours-old-price trade DI-1 is documented to prevent. The protection is illusory for the actual execution path.
- **Suggested fix:** Apply the same last-closed-bar staleness check inside manage_positions_via_kernel (after the candle fetch/trim) and skip OPEN actions when the data is stale, or have _apply_execution_actions short-circuit kernel execution for rows whose signal carries block_reason.
- **Evidence:** Gate just skips the SIGNAL path: `if _max_bars > 0 and _age_since_close > _max_bars * _bar_secs: ... results.append(_blocked_scan_row(...)); continue` (scanner.py:6377-6400). Blocked rows still enter the execution matrix: `all_signals[strat_id] = signal; signal_rows.append(item)` (scanner.py:6508-6509). Execution ignores block_reason and runs the kernel: `if _paper_kernel_execution_enabled() and _is_kernel_paper_strategy(strat): ... actions = manage_positions_via_kernel(...)` / `elif _live_kernel_execution_enabled() ...: actions = manage_positions_via_kernel(... execution_type="live" ...)` (scanner.py:6614-6623) — no staleness check anywhere in that block. The kernel path has no staleness gate, only `df = _trim_unclosed_latest_candle(df, timeframe)` (scanner.py:5960), and its source can serve old data: `# Prefer stale cache over hard failure ... return cached_df.tail(required_bars)` (scanner.py:1697-1699).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally confirms the defect. The DI-1 staleness gate (scanner.py:6377) only short-circuits the signal-evaluation loop: on stale data it appends _blocked_scan_row(...) and `continue`s (6390-6400). That blocked row (entry_signal=False, exit_signal=False, block_reason set — see _blocked_scan_row 5163-5189) is still collected into signal_rows unconditionally at 6508-6509. _apply_execution_actions (6602-6623) then routes to manage_positions_via_kernel based ONLY on _paper/_live kernel-enabled + kernel-stage checks; it never reads signal.get("block_reason"). The only other block_reason reads are telemetry (6546) and the display-only _build_signal_diagnostics (6783-6802), neither of which gates execution. manage_positions_via_kernel (5931-6179) re-fetches its own candles via fetch_candles(...) and applies only _trim_unclosed_latest_candle (5956-5960); I read the entire body and confirmed there is no staleness/_age_since_close check — a grep shows the DI-1 block is the ONLY bar-staleness gate in the file. The kernel's candle source can serve stale data (1694-1702: returns stale cache when scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch is off, and a stalled feed returning old-but-valid candles passes through; both paths use the same fetch_candles, so when DI-1 fires the kernel sees the same stale data). On the live path, _kernel_open_live_trade (5836-5871) sizes off pos.get("entry_price") and sets resting SL/TP from the kernel's stop_price/target_price — all derived from the stale df — so a reconciled "open" places a REAL Hyperliquid order anchored to stale levels. The documented protection is therefore illusory for the actual execution path. Severity unchanged (medium): the defect is real and reachable, but the money impact is conditional — it needs a feed stall returning stale-but-valid candles plus a new un-recorded open surfacing in the backfill/recovery window; an already-recorded position triggers no new order, and the live fill itself lands at the real current price (only sizing and SL/TP levels are stale). The auditor's own framing ("on a feed/exchange stall") matches this conditional reachability. Suggested fix (staleness check inside manage_positions_via_kernel skipping OPEN actions, or short-circuiting kernel execution for rows carrying block_reason) is sound.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. The DI-1 staleness gate exists only in the signal-evaluation loop (scanner.py:6356-6400) and merely emits a _blocked_scan_row + continue. _blocked_scan_row (5154-5189) returns {strategy_id, strategy, signal} with entry/exit=False and block_reason set; those rows are still appended to signal_rows (6509). In _apply_execution_actions (6614-6623), kernel-eligible strategies are run via manage_positions_via_kernel(strat_id, strat, ...) which never receives or consults the signal/block_reason — block_reason is read only in _build_signal_diagnostics (6783) for telemetry, not as a gate. (Asymmetry: the legacy fallback at 6704 DOES receive signal so entry_signal=False blocks legacy opens, but the kernel path bypasses this.) manage_positions_via_kernel (5956-5965) re-fetches via the same fetch_candles used by the signal path (5958 vs 6303) — which can serve stale cache (1694-1699) — and its only data guards are _trim_unclosed_latest_candle and len<20. _trim_unclosed_latest_candle (103-130) only drops a still-forming latest bar; a stale CLOSED bar is returned unchanged, so the kernel decides off the hours-old bar with no staleness check. Both kernel paths default ON (paper_kernel_execution=True 5222, live_kernel_execution=True 5828) and run_scan gates execution only on policy (6818), not data freshness — no upstream halt mooting the gap. The live open _kernel_open_live_trade (5850-5881) sizes units off the stale kernel entry_price and places SL/TP at the stale kernel levels, so risk is mis-sized and stops can be on the wrong side of the live price. One framing correction: the live FILL itself is a real market order at the current HL price (not the stale price), but sizing and stop/target are off the stale bar, so the money/risk impact is real. Severity kept at medium: the defect is unambiguously real and on the default-on primary path with live-money exposure, but a NEW spurious open specifically on a stale bar generally requires a scan gap (restart/freeze recovery/fresh promotion) or re-entry coinciding with a feed stall — steady-cadence opens occur while the bar is fresh and are already in the DB — which bounds everyday probability below the 'high' bar.

### `FREEZE-4` — Late exit on thaw fills a live position at current price with no delayed-exit alert

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** freeze  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5836-5928 (_kernel_open/close_live_trade), 6144-6145 (close applier dispatch)`
- **Claim:** After a freeze, when the kernel re-simulates and determines a signal/time exit fired on a bar inside the frozen interval, the live close is executed now at the real current Hyperliquid price via _execute_direct, not at the gap-bar price the kernel exited on, and nothing flags that the exit is severely delayed. A multi-hour freeze can convert a small intended in-bar exit into a large adverse-price fill.
- **Impact:** A long scanner/daemon freeze (per FREEZE-1/3) makes live exits fill at thaw-time prices that can be far from the bar the strategy intended to exit on, harming realized PnL, with no operator warning that the exit was delayed.
- **Suggested fix:** When a kernel exit-bar timestamp is older than a small multiple of the timeframe at execution time, emit a delayed-exit warning (and consider operator review) before placing the late market close; record the realized fill price/slippage distinctly from the kernel's intended exit price.
- **Evidence:** Live closes route to the exchange at market: `result = _execute_direct("close", trade_id, strat_id, asset, direction, size, ref_price, close_reason=reason)` (scanner.py:5900); the close applier for kernel actions is `close_applier = _kernel_close_live_trade if is_live else _kernel_close_paper_trade` and is invoked for both 'close' and 'backfill' actions (scanner.py:6094, 6144-6145). The kernel exit timestamp is the historical bar (trade.get('exit_time')) but the fill happens at scan/thaw time, and there is no guard comparing the kernel exit-bar time to wall-clock to warn on a stale exit.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-true on all substantive claims. (1) The live close path _kernel_close_live_trade (scanner.py:5885-5928) takes ref_price = trade.get('exit_price') — the kernel's HISTORICAL exit-bar price (5897) — and calls _execute_direct('close', ..., ref_price) (5900). In _execute_direct (located at scanner.py:3253, not api_domains/trading.py as the prose says — harmless location error) the close branch calls close_position(asset, size, close_side) (3436), a real reduce-only MARKET order; ref_price is recorded only as signal_price (3494) while the realized fill is the exchange's result['exit_price']/['fill_price'] (3452, 3489-3496). So the exit fills at the CURRENT thaw-time Hyperliquid price, not the gap-bar price the kernel intended. (2) Dispatch is correct: close_applier = _kernel_close_live_trade if is_live (6094), invoked for a.kind in ('close','backfill') (6144-6145). (3) Reachability is genuine: the reconciler (paper_reconcile.py:151-165) is explicitly built to backfill/close trades the kernel finalized during missed scan cycles, so a signal/time exit firing inside a freeze gap WILL produce a live market close at thaw. Stop/target exits are covered by resting exchange orders placed at open (3357-3369), but signal/time exits have no resting order, so the position stays open through the freeze — exactly the finding's scope. (4) No staleness guard exists: _kernel_close_live_trade does not compare trade.get('exit_time') to wall-clock, neither does the dispatch loop (6131-6155) nor the reconciler; health_monitor staleness logic (602-709) is about data-stream/scheduler freshness, not a late exit fill. Severity unchanged at medium: the recorded PnL is accurate (reflects the real fill via fill_exit_price, so no wrong number is shown to users — not 'high'), the adverse fill is inherent to any delayed exit and requires a multi-hour outage, and the true defect is the missing delayed-exit alert / distinct slippage recording. Not critical (no silent state corruption or unconditional loss).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) Live closes fill at the CURRENT market price, not the kernel's intended bar price: scanner.py:5900 _kernel_close_live_trade calls _execute_direct("close", ... ref_price ...) where ref_price=trade.get("exit_price") is the kernel's historical exit (5897); _execute_direct (3436) calls hyperliquid.close_position, a reduce-only IOC MARKET order priced off the current mid (hyperliquid.py:1865-1876, fill=exit_price at 1893). ref_price is used only as signal_price for record-keeping (scanner.py:3494). (2) Dispatch matches: close_applier=_kernel_close_live_trade if is_live (scanner.py:6094) invoked for close+backfill (6144-6145); live backfill is a no-op (row is None, 5889-5891) so the money action is "close". (3) No delayed-exit guard exists: neither paper_reconcile.reconcile (emits a close for any recorded-OPEN the kernel finalized, regardless of staleness — paper_reconcile.py:161-163) nor _kernel_close_live_trade compares kernel exit_time to wall-clock; grep found no delayed/stale-exit/wall-clock logic in the live close path. (4) Reachability confirmed: live path gated by live_kernel_execution (default True, scanner.py:5828) + live stage; real money on mainnet via FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET. Scenario correctly scoped to signal/time exits — stop/target are placed as RESTING exchange orders at open (3361,3367; open requires a protective stop, 3336-3337), so they fire on-exchange during a freeze and are immune; only signal/time exits (no resting order) get delayed to a thaw-time market fill. Severity stays medium: the late fill itself is the only physically possible behavior for a market close, the realized-vs-intended slippage IS already recorded (signal_price vs fill), and the downside is bounded by the mandatory resting stop; the genuine defect is the absence of an operator delayed-exit alert/review, contingent on a separate recoverable freeze. That is degraded/edge-case on a recoverable failure with bounded money impact and an observability gap — medium, not critical/high.

### `RESTART-4` — After restart the refreshed DB/UI stop is the kernel's FIXED entry stop, never the live trailing level — the displayed stop is wrong for trailing strategies

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** restart  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5607-5627, forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:267-277, forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:218-249`
- **Claim:** _kernel_refresh_paper_trade writes stop_loss_price = pos.get("stop_price") on every scan, but open_positions[direction]["stop_price"] is the STATIC entry stop (or None for trail-only) — the kernel never stores the ratcheted trailing level there. So after a restart (and every scan), the DB/UI shows the fixed/None stop, not the actual trailing stop the kernel will enforce.
- **Impact:** Operators (and any UI risk display) see a stop that does not match where the position will actually exit; for a trail-only strategy stop_loss_price is shown as None entirely. Enforcement for PAPER is still correct (done via kernel replay), so this is primarily a misleading-display/risk-visibility issue rather than direct money loss — but it can drive wrong manual decisions during/after a restart.
- **Suggested fix:** Have simulate expose the current effective trailing level in open_positions (e.g. add a computed `effective_stop_price` alongside the static stop), and refresh that into stop_loss_price so the DB/UI reflects the real protective level.
- **Evidence:** Refresh: `updates = {"stop_loss": pos.get("stop_price"), "stop_loss_price": pos.get("stop_price"), ...}` (scanner.py:5618-5619). In simulate the position's `stop_price` is assigned once at entry (execution_kernel.py:273) and never mutated; only `extreme` is ratcheted (line 249) and the effective trailing level is recomputed transiently in the exit check (lines 219-231) — it is not propagated into open_positions["stop_price"].
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the defect. (1) scanner.py:5618-5619 writes `stop_loss`/`stop_loss_price = pos.get("stop_price")` on every refresh; the refresh action is dispatched for both paper and live (scanner.py:6146-6147, ungated). The `position` is res.open_positions[direction] (paper_reconcile.py:176/186). (2) execution_kernel.py:261-273: `stop_price` is the FIXED entry stop, and is None for a trail-only strategy (the assignment at 262-263 is gated on stop_loss_pct/atr sizing); it is set once into active_trades[direction]["stop_price"] (273) and never mutated.
