(3) execution_kernel.py:218-249: the live trailing level (`eff_stop = at["extreme"] * (1 - sign*trail_pct)`) is computed transiently in the exit check (220-224) and never written back; only `at["extreme"]` ratchets (249). open_positions is built directly from active_trades (279), so pos["stop_price"] stays static. Therefore the DB/UI stop_loss_price shows the fixed entry stop (or None for trail-only), never the ratcheted trailing level — on every scan and after restart. Impact statement also verified: for kernel-managed paper trades the stored stop is display-only — `_kernel_handle_manual_exits` skips kernel_managed trades (scanner.py:5701), the legacy `_manual_price_exit_reason`/`_risk_exit_reason` enforcement path is short-circuited for kernel strategies, and `_kernel_handle_late_entry_exits` (5755) only enforces late_entry trades, which refresh skips (5615-5616). Enforcement is via kernel replay (reconciler `close`), so this is a misleading-risk-display issue, not direct paper money loss. Reachable for any trailing-stop strategy in paper/live. Medium severity is appropriate. (Note: on live, the real resting exchange stop placed at open via _execute_direct is also the static stop_price — scanner.py:5862/5880 — but the kernel-replay close still enforces the trailing exit; that resting-stop behavior is a separate concern outside this display-scoped finding.)
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) _kernel_refresh_paper_trade writes stop_loss_price=pos.get("stop_price") and reads nothing else trailing-related (scanner.py:5618-5619), ignoring pos["trail_pct"]/pos["extreme"] that the kernel carries (execution_kernel.py:275-276). (2) at["stop_price"] is the static entry stop set once at entry (execution_kernel.py:273; None for pure-trail strategies via the gate at 262) and never mutated; the trailing level is only a transient eff_stop in the exit check (lines 218-231) and only at["extreme"] ratchets (line 249) — neither is written back. (3) reconcile emits a refresh every scan for any kernel-open position matching a recorded open (paper_reconcile.py:176, comment line 129), dispatched each scan at scanner.py:6146-6147, so after restart (and continuously) the persisted/displayed stop is the fixed stop or None, not the ratcheted trailing level. Reachable for any strategy with trailing_stop_pct set (a supported config across execution_kernel/sizing/params/optimizer). The refresh is NOT gated by is_live, so it affects live display too, but it only calls _update_trade_signal_data (a DB write, no exchange order), confirming the finding's claim that this is display/risk-visibility only — paper enforcement remains correct via kernel replay and the live resting stop is untouched. Impact correctly characterized: misleading risk display that can drive wrong manual decisions (especially trail-only, where stop shows None), no direct money loss or state corruption. Medium is appropriate.

### `RESTART-5` — Kelly-sized strategies: size_fraction is re-derived from closed_gross accumulated WITHIN the replay window, so a restart with a slid/shorter window changes the kelly fraction and the recorded close PnL

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** restart  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:177-181, forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:111-114, forven/scanner.py:5509-5552`
- **Claim:** For kelly sizing, the per-entry size_fraction depends on the evidence list closed_gross built from trades that closed earlier in the SAME replay. After a restart the fetched window is shorter/slid (RESTART-1), so fewer prior trades feed closed_gross, the re-derived kelly size_fraction differs from the value used at the original open, and _kernel_close_recorded overwrites the recorded trade's pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct with the kernel's freshly recomputed (now different) value.
- **Impact:** For kelly-mode strategies, recorded paper PnL is non-deterministic across restarts/window changes, breaking strict backtest/paper parity and feeding inconsistent numbers to the promotion gate. Narrow (kelly only) and bounded, but it is a real parity break.
- **Suggested fix:** Persist the size_fraction chosen at open (already stored as kernel_size_fraction in signal_data, scanner.py:5470) and use it for the recorded close PnL instead of the kernel's re-derived value, OR seed the kelly evidence series from persisted closed-trade history so the fraction is reconstructed independent of the fetched window.
- **Evidence:** simulate sizes via `_size_fraction` → `_sizing.size_fraction(ec, stop_dist_pct, leverage, initial_capital, closed_gross=closed_gross)` (execution_kernel.py:177-181), where closed_gross is appended only as trades close within this run (finalize, line 112). On close, _kernel_close_recorded sets `pnl_pct_net = float(trade.get("pnl_pct"))` and writes it back: `UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=?, pnl=?, pnl_usd=? ...` (scanner.py:5509-5511,5541-5552). pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction (execution_kernel.py:113-114), so a window-dependent size_fraction yields a window-dependent recorded PnL. (fraction/atr/full sizing are window-independent and unaffected.)
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every cited code fact checks out literally, and the kelly-only window-dependence is real and reachable.

1. Kelly size_fraction IS window-dependent. sizing.py:234-235 `if mode == "kelly": return clamp01(ec["kelly_multiplier"] * kelly_fraction(closed_gross or [], ec["kelly_lookback"]))`, and kelly_fraction (sizing.py:74-95) computes W and R from `window = closed_gross[-lookback:]`. full(=1.0), fixed(=fixed_size/capital), and fraction/atr(=risk/(stop*lev)) never touch closed_gross — so the claim's "fraction/atr/full unaffected" is correct (fixed is also unaffected; harmless omission).

2. closed_gross is a fresh per-run accumulator. execution_kernel.py:165 `closed_gross: list[float] = []` (init empty inside simulate), appended only as trades close (line 112 `closed_gross.append(gross)` inside finalize). _size_fraction passes it through (lines 177-181). So at an entry, the kelly fraction reflects only trades that closed earlier WITHIN that same replay window.

3. pnl is size_fraction-scaled. execution_kernel.py:113-114 `size_fraction = float(at.get("size_fraction", 1.0)); pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction`. The entry stored `size_fraction` = `_size_fraction(stop_dist_pct)` (line 272), re-derived from the current window's closed_gross.

4. The recorded close PnL is OVERWRITTEN with the kernel's re-derived value, not the value stored at open. scanner.py:5509 `pnl_pct_net = float(trade.get("pnl_pct") or 0.0)` then 5541-5552 `UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=?, pnl=?, pnl_usd=? ...`. pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net (5511). This overwrite runs for faithful kernel trades; late hop-ins are correctly excluded (5524 `if late:`). The size_fraction chosen at open is persisted as kernel_size_fraction (5470) and used to compute recorded UNITS, but is NOT used for the recorded close PnL — confirming the divergence the finding describes.

5. Reachability. The paper kernel re-runs simulate over a sliding window each scan: scanner.py:5958 `fetch_candles(asset, bars=_paper_kernel_history_bars(), ...)` (default 1500, min 300; 5249-5253) and 6005 run_strategy_execution → simulate, rebuilding closed_gross from scratch every time. The window's front edge advances over time and can be shorter after a restart with reduced coverage, so the count of closed trades preceding a still-open entry can fall below kelly_lookback (default 100), changing the re-derived fraction and thus the overwritten PnL. Kelly is a genuinely selectable, frozen profile (execution_selection.py:98-101, kelly_lookback=100).

The mechanism is genuine and the recorded kelly-mode PnL is window/restart-dependent, breaking the shared-kernel parity invariant and feeding non-deterministic numbers to the promotion gate. It is correctly scoped as narrow (kelly only) and bounded — it does not directly lose money and only manifests when the window slides/shrinks across the lookback boundary. Note (not a refutation): even without a restart, the sliding-window-vs-full-history difference means paper kelly PnL can already diverge from the backtest, so the restart framing is one trigger of a slightly broader window-dependence. Severity medium is appropriate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanism verified against live code. execution_kernel.py:165 initializes closed_gross fresh per simulate() run and appends only as trades close within that run (finalize, line 112); _size_fraction (177-181) feeds this local list to sizing.size_fraction, and for kelly (sizing.py:234-235) the fraction = clamp01(kelly_multiplier * kelly_fraction(closed_gross, lookback)), so it depends on which prior trades fall inside the replay window. pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction (113-114). On close, _kernel_close_recorded reads the kernel's freshly recomputed pnl_pct (scanner.py:5509) and OVERWRITES the recorded trade's pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd (5541-5552) for faithful (non-late) paper closes. run_strategy_execution -> simulate rebuilds closed_gross from scratch each scan with no DB seeding, so a restart/downtime that shifts which scan first observes the close, and slides the rolling 1500-bar window (scanner.py:5251/5958), changes the kelly fraction and thus the recorded close PnL. Reachable: kelly is a default-included selection candidate (execution_selection.py:54,98-101). Scope is correctly narrow and I confirmed it is PAPER-ONLY: the live close path (_kernel_close_live_trade, scanner.py:5912-5913) derives PnL from the real fill, not the kernel kelly value; late hop-ins are exempt (5524); fraction/atr/full/fixed are window-independent (sizing.py:227-240). One nuance the finding understates: kelly_fraction only uses closed_gross[-lookback:] (sizing.py:83, default 100), so when >=100 prior trades sit inside the window before the entry the fraction is stable and there is NO effect; the non-determinism manifests only for sparse/low-frequency kelly strategies (or early book, or when a win/loss needed for a nonzero kelly drops off the window edge). That is still a realistic regime under a 1500-bar window. Net: a genuine paper-only PnL determinism/parity break that feeds the promotion gate (which gates go-live), bounded to kelly mode. No direct real-money loss. Medium is appropriate.

### `DB-1` — Trade close finalizes across THREE separate transactions — a crash/lock-failure mid-way permanently corrupts the recorded PnL (no self-heal)

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** db  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5513-5552 (_kernel_close_recorded); forven/scanner.py:3690-3746 (_close_trade_db); forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:161-165`
- **Claim:** A single logical 'close' mutates the trades row across multiple independent get_db() transactions. If the process dies or the final write hits a busy_timeout AFTER close_trade_record has committed status=CLOSED but BEFORE the kernel-net override commits, the trade is permanently left CLOSED with the WRONG pnl_pct and a NULL net_pnl_pct, and the reconciler never re-touches a CLOSED trade so it is never repaired.
- **Impact:** On a daemon restart/kill or a lock-timeout in the inter-transaction gap (made more likely by the documented single-worker WS-starvation contention), a closed paper trade keeps the GROSS leverage-inclusive position return (e.g. ~0.06) instead of the kernel net equity-fraction (e.g. ~0.012) and a NULL net_pnl_pct. That value is read by _recent_strategy_returns (scanner.py:631-644) for kelly sizing and by promotion-gate per-trade return stats, and the un-deducted drag/funding overstates paper equity which sums pnl_usd (scanner.py:604). The corruption is silent and permanent.
- **Suggested fix:** Finalize the close in ONE transaction: compute the final exit_price, pnl_pct, net_pnl_pct, fees_pct, pnl_usd and closed_at up front and write them in a single close_trade_record call (extend its signature to accept caller-supplied net pnl), or wrap fill+close+override in one get_db_immediate() BEGIN IMMEDIATE block so a tear rolls the whole close back to OPEN (where the reconciler will retry it).
- **Evidence:** _kernel_close_recorded does three commits in sequence: `_update_trade_fill(...fill_kind="exit"...)` (scanner.py:5513), then `close_trade_record(...)` which commits status='CLOSED' with a GROSS position-return pnl_pct = `((resolved_exit_price - entry_price)/entry_price)*signed*leverage` (trade_state.py:268, committed at trade_state.py:284-307), then a SEPARATE `with get_db() as conn: conn.execute("UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=?, pnl=?, pnl_usd=?, closed_at=? WHERE id=?", (round(pnl_pct_net,8), round(pnl_pct_net,8), pnl_usd, ...))` (scanner.py:5541-5546) that REPLACES the gross value with the kernel net equity-fraction. close_trade_record never writes net_pnl_pct, so on a tear net_pnl_pct stays NULL. The reconciler skips already-closed trades: `elif str(r.get('status') or 'open').strip().lower() == 'closed': matched.add(id(r))  # nothing to do` (paper_reconcile.py:164-165), so the override action is never re-emitted. A grep for net_pnl_pct/pnl_pct recompute found no repair job that revisits CLOSED trades. _close_trade_db has the same shape: close_trade_record (scanner.py:3690) then a separate `UPDATE trades SET fees_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=?` (scanner.py:3744).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the non-atomic multi-transaction close. get_db() (db.py:430-454) commits on each with-block exit (line 449), so each block is an independent commit. (1) close_trade_record opens its own transaction (trade_state.py:166) and commits status='CLOSED' with a GROSS leverage-inclusive pnl_pct = ((resolved_exit_price - entry_price)/entry_price)*signed*leverage (trade_state.py:268), persisted at 284-307; that UPDATE never writes net_pnl_pct, so on a tear net_pnl_pct stays NULL. (2) _kernel_close_recorded then opens a SEPARATE with get_db() block (scanner.py:5541) that overrides pnl_pct and sets net_pnl_pct (5544/5549). A process kill or busy_timeout exhaustion in the gap between commit-1 (CLOSED+gross) and commit-2 (override) leaves the trade permanently CLOSED with the gross pnl_pct (overstated by the size_fraction factor) and NULL net_pnl_pct. (3) The reconciler never repairs it: paper_reconcile.py:164-165 adds an already-CLOSED row to matched and emits no action; a grep of all net_pnl_pct writes (scanner.py:3744/5544/5549, risk.py:2274) finds only close-time writers, no periodic repair job. (4) Downstream impact confirmed: _recent_strategy_returns reads pnl_pct directly (scanner.py:631) feeding kelly sizing, and paper equity sums pnl_usd (scanner.py:604) which would retain the drag-un-deducted gross value. (5) _close_trade_db (scanner.py:3690 then 3742-3746) and the recovery path (risk.py:2241 then 2272-2276) share the identical non-atomic shape. get_db_immediate() (db.py:492, BEGIN IMMEDIATE) — the exact atomic fix suggested — exists but is not used on this path. Trigger window is narrow (crash or 60s lock contention between two commits) and impact is bounded to a single trade's recorded metrics, consistent with medium severity; keeping unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The non-atomicity defect is real and verified against live code. _kernel_close_recorded (scanner.py:5504-5552) finalizes a close across THREE independent get_db() transactions with no outer atomicity: (1) _update_trade_fill exit (line 5513, own txn at scanner.py:3059), (2) close_trade_record (line 5514) which commits status='CLOSED' with a GROSS leverage-inclusive pnl_pct = ((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage (trade_state.py:268, UPDATE at 284-307) and writes NO net_pnl_pct, (3) a separate `with get_db() as conn` UPDATE (lines 5541-5551) that replaces pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd with the kernel net equity-fraction and sets net_pnl_pct. A tear between txn 2 and txn 3 (process kill or lock failure) leaves the trade permanently CLOSED with the wrong-SCALE gross pnl_pct and NULL net_pnl_pct. The scale mismatch is genuine (line 5509 comments pnl_pct_net as 'kernel net, equity-fraction', a different scale than the position return), so the corruption is more than a missing fee deduction. No self-heal exists: the reconciler explicitly skips CLOSED trades (paper_reconcile.py:164-165), and the only other net_pnl_pct writes are at close-time and gated (risk.py:2272 fires only on closed.get('updated')==True, i.e. OPEN→CLOSED, never on an already-CLOSED row; _close_trade_db's override at scanner.py:3744 is wrapped in a try/except at 3755 that silently swallows a lock failure on the LIVE path). Consumers are confirmed to read the corrupted fields: equity sums pnl_usd (scanner.py:604), kelly reads pnl_pct (scanner.py:631-643), the promotion gate uses COALESCE(net_pnl_pct, pnl_pct) (policy.py:1244/1275/3714) so a NULL net silently falls back to the gross/wrong-scale value, and DSR does the same (deflated_sharpe.py:193-195). _close_trade_db (scanner.py:3690 then 3744) has the identical multi-txn shape, so the live path is affected too. Reachability is on the core paper+live close paths, but the TRIGGER is low-probability: get_db() sets PRAGMA busy_timeout=60000 (db.py:444), so the lock-timeout vector the finding leans on requires ~60s of sustained write-lock contention (extreme; this part is overstated), and the process-kill window is microseconds wide. The defect, its non-recoverability, and its money-relevant downstream impact (gate decisions, kelly sizing) all hold as described, but it manifests only on a rare crash/timeout rather than routinely. Medium is appropriate: edge-case trigger yet permanent silent corruption of numbers that feed promotion-to-live decisions, with no repair path. The suggested fix is feasible — get_db_immediate() (db.py:492) already exists to wrap the close in one BEGIN IMMEDIATE block, or close_trade_record could be extended to accept caller-supplied net values for a single-statement finalize.

### `DB-2` — The append_strategy_event approval-gate tripwire guards only the audit log, not the strategies.stage column; raw stage writes + raw strategy_events inserts bypass it entirely

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** db  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/db.py:5331-5355 (tripwire); forven/db.py:3864-3874 (restore_migration_snapshot); forven/brain.py:3644-3654 (run_gauntlet_backtest_migration); forven/db.py:2691-2697 (legacy migration)`
- **Claim:** The 'out-of-band stage-change' tripwire lives INSIDE append_strategy_event and only blocks callers that use that function to log a from!=to event without _lifecycle_authorized. It does not constrain the actual lifecycle state: strategies.stage is mutated by raw SQL in several places, and strategy_events rows are inserted by raw SQL, both of which never invoke the tripwire. There is no DB-level trigger/constraint on strategies.stage. So the 'approval gate' is enforced by convention (everyone-should-call-transition_stage) plus a narrow Python log guard.
- **Impact:** Any code path (or a future agent-exposed tool) that issues a raw `UPDATE strategies SET stage=...` changes lifecycle state — including promoting to live or demoting a live strategy — without the approval gate, the canonical-flag carve-out, the pending-approval task, or an authorized audit event. The currently-reachable raw writers are operator CLI (restore) and one-time/system migrations (demotions), so practical exploitability today is low, but the gate is structurally incomplete and a single new direct-write caller silently defeats it.
- **Suggested fix:** Enforce at the data layer: a BEFORE UPDATE trigger on strategies that rejects a stage change unless an authorized-transition marker is set in the same transaction (mirroring how transition_stage operates), or funnel EVERY stage write + event through one authorized function and make restore_migration_snapshot / the migrations call transition_stage(..., force=True, _lifecycle_authorized) instead of raw SQL.
- **Evidence:** Tripwire: `if normalized_from and normalized_to and normalized_from != normalized_to and not _lifecycle_authorized: ... return None` (db.py:5331-5355) — but append_strategy_event only writes the strategy_events table, never strategies.stage. restore_migration_snapshot bypasses it on BOTH layers: `conn.execute("UPDATE strategies SET stage = ?, status = ?, updated_at = ? WHERE id = ?", (snap.get('stage','quick_screen'), ...))` (db.py:3864-3867) and a raw `INSERT INTO strategy_events (strategy_id, from_state, to_state, ...) VALUES (?, 'restored', ?, 'operator', ...)` (db.py:3868-3874). run_gauntlet_backtest_migration does the same raw UPDATE + raw INSERT (brain.py:3644-3654). A legacy migration promotes rows straight to live_graduated: `UPDATE strategies SET stage = 'live_graduated', status = 'live_graduated', owner = 'execution-trader' ...` (db.py:2691-2697). The canonical transition_stage path is correctly atomic and authorized (brain.py:1690-1740), confirming the gate is meant to be the sole writer — but nothing enforces that at the data layer.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited code verified literally. (1) The tripwire at db.py:5331-5355 is inside append_strategy_event (def at db.py:5298), which only INSERTs into strategy_events (db.py:5373-5376) and never writes strategies.stage; on trip it just returns None. So it guards the audit log, not the lifecycle column. (2) restore_migration_snapshot (db.py:3864-3874) does a raw `UPDATE strategies SET stage = ?, status = ?, updated_at = ? WHERE id = ?` plus a raw `INSERT INTO strategy_events (...) VALUES (...)` (from_state='restored') — both bypass append_strategy_event, so the tripwire never fires. (3) run_gauntlet_backtest_migration (brain.py:3644-3654) does the same raw UPDATE + raw INSERT with from='gauntlet', to='quick_screen' (from!=to) yet is never checked — concretely proving the tripwire is not enforced on raw inserts. (4) The legacy migration (db.py:2691-2697) raw-promotes straight to live: `UPDATE strategies SET stage = 'live_graduated', status = 'live_graduated', owner = 'execution-trader' ...` with no gate. (5) The canonical transition_stage (brain.py:1690-1740) is atomic and is the intended sole writer, and even it writes its event via raw INSERT (brain.py:1718-1721) rather than append_strategy_event, confirming the tripwire is a narrow log-side check. (6) No DB-level enforcement exists: the only triggers on `strategies` (db.py:2063-2078) validate hypothesis_id FK; there is no BEFORE UPDATE OF stage trigger/constraint. policy.py:2828-2844 documents that one prior raw `UPDATE strategies SET stage='archived'` was migrated to route through transition_stage, confirming the team relies on convention-based routing with no data-layer backstop. The impact is correctly scoped and not overstated (concedes the currently-reachable raw writers are operator restore + one-time/system migrations, so live exploitability is low). Medium is appropriate: it is a defense-in-depth gap on a money-critical control (stage gates live deployment), structurally incomplete rather than an active money-losing bug — a single new direct-write caller silently defeats the gate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): VERIFIED IN CODE. (1) The tripwire (db.py:5331-5355) is inside append_strategy_event, whose only DB write is INSERT INTO strategy_events (db.py:5373-5389) — it never mutates strategies.stage, so it guards the audit log, not lifecycle state. (2) Raw strategies.stage writes that bypass it confirmed at db.py:3865 (restore_migration_snapshot), brain.py:3645 (run_gauntlet_backtest_migration), db.py:2693 (legacy CEO->live_graduated migration), plus db.py:2205/2236 init migrations. (3) Raw strategy_events inserts bypassing append_strategy_event confirmed at db.py:3868-3874 and brain.py:3649-3654. (4) The canonical writer (brain.py:1690-1740) does its own atomic raw UPDATE+INSERT, showing it is MEANT to be the sole gate, but nothing enforces that. (5) No DB-level trigger on strategies.stage: the only strategies triggers (db.py:2063-2078) guard hypothesis_id; the rest (db.py:3057+) are audit-log triggers on other tables. The team's own post-mortem note independently corroborates this: 'a reconciliation tripwire for a silent strategies.stage column flip with no canonical event ... (not yet done).' So the approval gate is enforced by convention plus a narrow Python log guard, exactly as claimed.\n\nREACHABILITY (lens): The only currently-reachable raw-stage writers are operator-initiated or one-time/system migrations, exactly as the finding states. restore_migration_snapshot is called solely from the operator CLI (cli.py:121) and restores to the strategy's own snapshotted prior stage; run_gauntlet_backtest_migration is called once from a flag-gated startup migration (api_core.py:160) and only DEMOTES to quick_screen; the legacy migration runs once in init_db. The original adversarial path — an in-process agent reaching forven.db directly (the S01601 incident this tripwire was shipped to fix) — was closed by a SEPARATE control (the AST import allowlist), not by this tripwire. Thus there is no live money-losing or state-corrupting path reachable today; this is a defense-in-depth/structural gap.\n\nSEVERITY: Downgraded medium->low. The rubric maps 'cosmetic/defensive' to low, and 'edge-case/degraded' to medium. No currently-reachable caller produces wrong money/state in normal or adversarial operation, and the finding itself states 'practical exploitability today is low.' The architectural concern (a single future direct-write caller silently defeats the gate; stage->live is money-critical) is legitimate and worth the suggested DB-trigger/funnel fix, but it does not rise to medium given today's reachability.

### `DB-4` — Kernel live/paper reconcile path lacks the pending_close_reconcile guard the legacy engine has, and _execute_direct close has no idempotency key — a pending live close is re-issued every scan

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** db  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:3410-3436,3436 (_execute_direct close, no idempotency_key); forven/scanner.py:5900-5903 (_kernel_close_live_trade returns early on pending); forven/scanner.py:5347-5393 (_kernel_recorded_trades does not exclude pending); contrast forven/scanner.py:4045 (legacy guard)`
- **Claim:** When a live close returns _close_reconcile_state='pending' (close_position returned no avgPx), the trade stays OPEN and is NOT marked done. The kernel reconcile path never filters trades flagged pending_close_reconcile out of `recorded`, so the next scan's reconciler re-emits a close and _kernel_close_live_trade calls _execute_direct again — and the close leg passes no idempotency_key, so a fresh reduce-only order is sent each scan until the sweep or a fill resolves it.
- **Impact:** On the live path (operator-enabled mainnet; testnet by default) a stuck pending close fires a new reduce-only order on every scan cycle. Reduce-only semantics cap total reduction at the open size so it cannot flip the position, but it generates repeated orders/fees and log noise until reconciliation, and a still-open position keeps re-attempting rather than being held for the sweep grace window.
- **Suggested fix:** Skip trades flagged pending_close_reconcile in the kernel reconcile (mirror scanner.py:4045) and pass an idempotency_key (e.g. f"{trade_id}:close") to the close_position call in _execute_direct so a re-emitted close is deduped at the exchange.
- **Evidence:** _execute_direct open passes `idempotency_key: f"{trade_id}:open"` (scanner.py:3362) but the close leg calls `close_position(asset, size, close_side, **close_kwargs)` where close_kwargs = {testnet[, vault_address]} only (scanner.py:3412-3414,3436) — no idempotency key. _kernel_close_live_trade returns `f"LIVE-KERNEL-CLOSE {asset} {state}"` without finalizing when state in ('pending','partial') (scanner.py:5901-5903), leaving the trade OPEN. _kernel_recorded_trades selects all OPEN trades with no pending_close filter (scanner.py:5359-5375). The legacy engine explicitly guarded this: `if _trade_pending_close_reconcile(trade): ... continue` (scanner.py:4045); the kernel path has no equivalent.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All structural claims verified against live code. (1) Open passes idempotency_key=f"{trade_id}:open" (scanner.py:3362); the close leg at scanner.py:3412-3414,3436 builds close_kwargs={"testnet":testnet}(+vault) and calls close_position(asset,size,close_side,**close_kwargs) with NO idempotency key. Stronger than stated: close_position (hyperliquid.py:1830-1833) does not even accept one and submits via exchange.order(...) with no cloid (hyperliquid.py:1878-1883) — zero exchange dedup on the close. (2) On a no-fill close (fill is None, scanner.py:3499) it sets pending via mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile and _close_reconcile_state="pending" (scanner.py:3505-3512); _kernel_close_live_trade returns early at scanner.py:5901-5903 for state in ("pending","partial") WITHOUT calling _close_trade_db/release, so the row stays status='OPEN'. (3) _kernel_recorded_trades (scanner.py:5358-5392) selects status IN ('OPEN','CLOSED') and emits every OPEN row with a kernel_entry_time — no pending_close_reconcile filter. (4) The pure reconciler matches the still-OPEN recorded trade against the kernel's deterministically re-simulated closed trade by (direction,entry_time) and emits a close action (paper_reconcile.py:161-163); for live, close_applier=_kernel_close_live_trade (scanner.py:6094) is invoked for kind in ("close","backfill") (scanner.py:6144-6145), re-calling _execute_direct("close",...) every scan. (5) The legacy engine guards exactly this with if _trade_pending_close_reconcile(trade): ...continue (scanner.py:4045-4048); the kernel path has no equivalent (I read _kernel_close_live_trade 5885-5928 and manage_positions_via_kernel 5939-6157 in full — neither checks pending). The designed remediation is sweep_pending_close_reconcile (scanner.py:7064, 30-min grace _RECONCILE_MAX_AGE_MINUTES=30). Aggravator: _execute_direct's re-mark passes no requested_at and mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile overwrites pending_close_reconcile_at=get_now() each call (trade_state.py:85,108), so re-firing every scan can reset the grace clock and starve the sweep. Impact bounded by reduce_only=True (hyperliquid.py:1882) — no position flip; cost is repeated reduce-only orders/fees, log noise, and a potentially stuck-OPEN ghost trade. Severity medium is correct; the ghost-open/sweep-starvation sub-case could be high but is conditional on the exchange's response for a reduce-only order on an already-flat position, which is not verifiable from code alone.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every link verified in live code. (1) Open leg sets idempotency_key (scanner.py:3362); close leg calls close_position(asset,size,close_side,**close_kwargs) with close_kwargs={testnet[,vault_address]} only (scanner.py:3412-3414,3436) — no idempotency key (and close_position at hyperliquid.py:1830-1833 doesn't accept one). (2) On no-fill, scanner.py:3499-3512 marks pending_close_reconcile and leaves the trade OPEN. (3) _kernel_close_live_trade calls _execute_direct('close',...) FIRST then returns early on pending/partial without finalizing (scanner.py:5900-5903), so the order is re-issued each scan. (4) _kernel_recorded_trades (5347-5393) surfaces OPEN trades to the reconciler with NO pending filter; the legacy path guards at 4045. (5) paper_reconcile.py:157-163 re-emits a 'close' action for a still-OPEN recorded trade whose kernel exit recurs in res.closed_trades every scan. (6) Reachable on the live path: live_kernel_execution defaults True (5828), kernel is the live close applier (6094); testnet-bounded by default but identical logic on mainnet. ADDED aggravator: each re-mark resets pending_close_reconcile_at to now (trade_state.py:85,108; _execute_direct passes no requested_at), and the sweep skips trades whose timer hasn't aged past cutoff (scanner.py:7162-7168) — so the kernel's per-scan retries can perpetually reset the grace timer and defeat the safety-net sweep, leaving a flat-but-mis-parsed-pending trade stuck OPEN and holding its risk slot. Severity stays medium, not higher: the order is reduce-only IOC (hyperliquid.py:1882) so it cannot flip or over-close the position and incurs no extra fees beyond a legitimate close (no silent money loss / position corruption), and the trigger (close returning no fill on an aggressive 300bps IOC) is an uncommon edge. Not lower than medium: it is a genuine live-path state defect with order/fee spam, log noise, a stuck-OPEN trade, a held risk slot, and a defeated reconcile sweep.

### `DATA-3` — _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS is incomplete and silently defaults to 1h; currently masked by DATA-1 but a coupled trap that re-introduces partial-bar trading if INTERVAL_TO_MS is widened

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** data  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:76-84 (_TIMEFRAME_SECONDS); 118 (_trim_unclosed_latest_candle); 6371 (staleness gate)`
- **Claim:** _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS omits 2h/6h/8h/12h/3m/45m/3d/1w (and is itself inconsistent: it lists 30m which INTERVAL_TO_MS rejects). Both _trim_unclosed_latest_candle and the DI-1 staleness gate do `_TIMEFRAME_SECONDS.get(tf, 3600)`, silently using a 1h bar width for any unlisted timeframe. For a >1h timeframe this makes the trim compute bar_close_ts = open+3600 and KEEP a still-forming bar (lookahead/partial-bar entry), and makes the staleness gate false-block a healthy strategy (e.g. a 2h strategy is flagged 'stale' for ~half of every 2h period; 6h/12h almost always). Today no such timeframe reaches this code because DATA-1's INTERVAL_TO_MS rejects the fetch first — so the two incomplete maps mask each other.
- **Impact:** Latent. The obvious fix for DATA-1 — adding 2h/6h to INTERVAL_TO_MS — would immediately activate partial-bar trading and bogus stale-feed false-blocks for those timeframes unless _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS is widened in lockstep. The 30m disagreement already exists today (30m is 'supported' here but unfetchable), so the maps are not in sync.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS lookups with the single shared data._timeframe_to_ms (//1000) so trim/staleness always use the true bar width and can never silently fall back to 1h; keep one canonical timeframe table across data.py, market_data.py and scanner.py.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:118 `bar_duration = _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS.get(str(timeframe or "1h").strip().lower(), 3600)`; scanner.py:128-129 `if current_ts < bar_close_ts:\n        return df.iloc[:-1]`; scanner.py:6371 `_bar_secs = _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS.get(str(strat_timeframe or "1h").strip().lower(), 3600)` then 6376-6377 `_age_since_close = get_now().timestamp() - (_last_ts + _bar_secs)\n  if _max_bars > 0 and _age_since_close > _max_bars * _bar_secs:`. _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS (76-84) has 1m/5m/15m/30m/1h/4h/1d only.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): The code literally matches every factual claim. scanner.py:76-84 _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS = {1m,5m,15m,30m,1h,4h,1d} — it omits 2h/6h/8h/12h/3m/45m/3d/1w and DOES list 30m. market_data.py:17-24 INTERVAL_TO_MS = {1m,5m,15m,1h,4h,1d} has NO 30m, so the two tables are genuinely inconsistent. Both consumers default to 1h: scanner.py:118 `bar_duration = _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS.get(...,3600)` and scanner.py:6371 `_bar_secs = _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS.get(...,3600)`. I verified the impact direction: for a true 2h bar with bar_duration=3600, _trim_unclosed_latest_candle (118-130) computes bar_close_ts=open+3600 so once now>=open+3600 it returns df unchanged and KEEPS the forming bar (partial-bar/lookahead); the staleness gate (6376-6377) computes _age_since_close=now-(open+3600), over-stating age by 3600s, which false-blocks a healthy 2h strat for ~half of each 2h cycle and a 6h/12h strat essentially always (age>2*3600 immediately). The masking claim is also TRUE and is the reason this is latent, not active: fetch_binance_candles (market_data.py:383-385) and fetch_hyperliquid_candles (205-207) both raise ValueError for any interval not in INTERVAL_TO_MS, the scanner catches that at 6308 and `continue`s, so an unlisted >1h timeframe never reaches lines 6337/6371; the snapshot cache (fetch_candles:1692) can only be populated via those validating fetches; and intake.py:44-50 coerces stored timeframes to INTERVAL_TO_MS. Crucially, EVERY timeframe currently in INTERVAL_TO_MS is also in _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS with the correct value, so the 3600 fallback is unreachable today and there is zero current money/state impact. The defect is real and accurately described, but because it is fully masked and only activates if a future DATA-1 fix widens INTERVAL_TO_MS without updating _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS, it is a defensive/latent coupling trap rather than a currently-degraded behavior — so I downgrade severity from medium to low. The 30m inconsistency the finding cites is real but presently harmless (30m can't be stored or fetched, and _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS' 30m value 1800 is correct anyway).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): All cited code is accurate. _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS (scanner.py:76-84) = {1m,5m,15m,30m,1h,4h,1d}; INTERVAL_TO_MS (market_data.py:17-24) = {1m,5m,15m,1h,4h,1d}. Both _trim_unclosed_latest_candle (scanner.py:118) and the DI-1 staleness gate (scanner.py:6371) do _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS.get(tf, 3600). The maps are genuinely inconsistent (30m present in one, absent in the other), and the silent 3600 fallback is real. The latent coupling trap is also real: widening INTERVAL_TO_MS to add 2h/6h without updating _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS would make trim compute bar_close_ts=open+3600 and KEEP a still-forming >1h bar (partial-bar entry/lookahead at scanner.py:124-129), and make the staleness gate at 6376-6377 false-block healthy >1h strategies. HOWEVER, on the REACHABILITY/IMPACT lens this has zero current production impact: (1) fetch_hyperliquid_candles raises ValueError for any interval not in INTERVAL_TO_MS (market_data.py:206-207), and intake._intended_timeframe coerces any unsupported declared _timeframe to '1h' against INTERVAL_TO_MS (intake.py:44-50), so no strategy with a timeframe outside INTERVAL_TO_MS can be stored or fetched; (2) crucially, every key in INTERVAL_TO_MS IS present in _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS with the correct value (INTERVAL_TO_MS keys are a strict subset), so any timeframe that survives the fetch and reaches lines 118/6371 always resolves correctly and never hits the 3600 fallback. The 30m mismatch is harmless in both directions (30m unfetchable; and _TIMEFRAME_SECONDS['30m']=1800 is correct anyway). So the defect is a verified latent maintainability/coupling hazard, not an active money/state bug — exactly as the finding admits ('Latent', 'masked by DATA-1'). Confirmed as real, but severity downgraded medium->low because nothing reachable today loses money or corrupts state; it only manifests on a specific future edit. The suggested fix (single shared data._timeframe_to_ms table) is sound and would eliminate the silent-fallback coupling.

### `DATA-6` — Daemon shared candle cache is hardcoded to 1h; non-1h strategies break entirely when direct market fetch is disabled

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** data  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/daemon.py:1582-1607 (interval="1h" hardcoded); forven/scanner.py:1692-1702 (cache miss + direct-fetch gate)`
- **Claim:** _refresh_candle_cache only ever fetches and publishes interval="1h". The cache is keyed by interval, so every non-1h strategy (15m/4h/1d — all live-fetchable) gets a permanent cache miss and depends entirely on a synchronous per-scan direct fetch. If the operator sets scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch=False (a supported strict-parity / no-silent-fallback knob), fetch_candles raises 'Candle cache unavailable/stale' for all non-1h strategies and they stop trading, while 1h strategies keep running off the cache.
- **Impact:** With direct fetch on (default) it is a throughput/rate-limit cost (every non-1h strategy hits Binance synchronously each scan). With direct fetch off, non-1h strategies silently go dark — an availability/parity gap tied to a documented setting.
- **Suggested fix:** Have the daemon refresh the cache for the union of timeframes actually used by active strategies (it already enumerates active coins), not just 1h.
- **Evidence:** daemon.py:1590-1593 `fetch_market_candles, coin, bars=CANDLE_CACHE_BARS, interval="1h",` and 1601-1606 publish_candle_snapshot(..., interval="1h"). scanner.py:1698-1702 `if not _scanner_bool_setting("scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch", True): return cached_df.tail(...)` / `raise RuntimeError(f"Candle cache unavailable/stale for {normalized_coin}")`.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited mechanics verified against live code. (1) Daemon's only cache refresh is `_refresh_candle_cache` (daemon.py:1582-1607, called at daemon.py:1772); it hardcodes interval="1h" at the fetch (daemon.py:1593) and publish (daemon.py:1605) — no other per-timeframe refresh exists in the daemon. (2) The cache is interval-keyed: `candle_cache_key` = `{prefix}:{symbol}:{interval}` (market_cache.py:24-27) and `load_candle_snapshot` reads that exact key (market_cache.py:186), so a non-1h lookup cannot hit the 1h-only cache. (3) Both scanner fetch sites forward the strategy's own timeframe: `fetch_candles(asset, ..., interval=timeframe)` at scanner.py:5958 and `interval=strat_timeframe` at scanner.py:6303, with timeframe = strat.get("timeframe") (scanner.py:5954, 6297); the `if strat_timeframe != "1h"` branch (scanner.py:6298) confirms non-1h is a real supported path. (4) On a non-1h cache miss, `cached_df` is empty so fetch_candles reaches scanner.py:1701-1702 and raises `RuntimeError("Candle cache unavailable/stale...")` when scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch is False; otherwise it does a synchronous direct fetch (scanner.py:1706). (5) scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch is a real operator-facing setting, default True (api_core.py:1643, mutable at api_core.py:2751; surfaced in frontend manifest.ts:1789 and help content). When the raise fires, the kernel path returns _skip (scanner.py:5961-5963) and the scan path emits a blocked row and continues (scanner.py:6308-6325), so the reconciler never runs and open non-1h positions go unmanaged — slightly worse than the finding's "no trades" wording, but consistent with "go dark." Severity medium is correct: under the default config it is only a throughput/rate-limit cost; the money/state impact (unmanaged open positions) requires the operator to disable a non-default knob.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) forven/daemon.py:1582-1619 `_refresh_candle_cache` publishes only `interval="1h"` (fetch line 1593, publish line 1605) while iterating only over active COINS, never active-strategy timeframes. (2) The cache is interval-keyed: forven/market_cache.py:184 `load_candle_snapshot(asset, *, interval="1h")`, so non-1h is a permanent miss. (3) forven/scanner.py:1692-1702 on a cache miss with `scanner_allow_direct_market_fetch=False` raises `RuntimeError("Candle cache unavailable/stale for ...")`. (4) Default flag is True (forven/api_core.py:1643), so default = synchronous per-scan direct fetch for non-1h, flag-off = non-1h dark. (5) Both scan paths fetch on the strategy's own timeframe and SKIP the strategy on fetch failure: kernel paper/live path scanner.py:5958 (`interval=timeframe`, _skip at 5961-5963) and legacy path scanner.py:6303 (`interval=strat_timeframe`, "SKIPPED" at 6313-6319) — so this is NOT paper-only; it hits live signal generation too. (6) Non-1h timeframes (5m/15m/4h/1d) are first-class and used across the codebase/tests. (7) The only two production publish_candle_snapshot call sites are the daemon (1h hardcoded) and the scanner self-fallback (scanner.py:1713), and the latter only runs after passing the direct-fetch gate — so with the flag off nothing ever populates the non-1h cache. (8) The flag is a documented operator-facing toggle (frontend manifest.ts:1788-1800 default true; help/content.ts:1717-1727 "Disable for strict data/exec separation and deterministic cache-only operation") aligned with the project's fail-closed/no-silent-fallback stance — an operator enabling it for strict parity would unknowingly take all non-1h strategies dark. Severity stays medium: in the default config it is an always-on throughput/synchronous-fetch + rate-limit-cascade cost (not silent money loss/state corruption), and the dark-strategy money/availability impact (missed entries plus unmanaged open positions) requires the non-default-but-supported flag. Confirmed and correctly sized at medium.

### `LIVE-EXCHANGE-RECONCILE-2` — Ghost-recovered close records net PnL with only the exit-leg fee and zero funding, overstating realized net vs the normal close path

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live-exchange-reconcile  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:2254-2278; contrast forven/scanner.py:3722-3739`
- **Claim:** When a ghost SQLite trade is closed from the recovered exchange fill, net_pnl_pct is computed as gross minus ONLY the closing-leg fee, with no entry-leg fee and no funding — whereas every normal live close subtracts round-trip (2-leg) fees plus realized funding. Ghost-recovered live closes therefore systematically overstate net PnL. (The mid-fallback ghost close, risk.py:2239-2247, records no net_pnl_pct at all → NULL.)
- **Impact:** Realized net PnL of ghost-recovered live closes is biased optimistic by ~one fee leg plus all accrued funding; for a perp held across many funding intervals the funding omission can be material. This net feeds reported live PnL and the promotion gate (policy.py SELECT COALESCE(net_pnl_pct, pnl_pct); deflated_sharpe.py reads net_pnl_pct), so it can flatter a strategy's live track record.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the normal close net-cost computation in the ghost-recovery branch: subtract a round-trip fee (or the actual entry fee from the fill ledger) AND fold realized funding, rather than only the exit-leg fee; also populate net_pnl_pct on the mid-fallback ghost close instead of leaving it NULL.
- **Evidence:** Ghost path: `_fees_pct = float(recovered_exit["fee_usd"]) / _margin; _net_pct = float(closed["pnl_pct"]) - _fees_pct` (risk.py:2270-2271) where fee_usd is the sum of CLOSING fills only (risk.py:1882 `fee_usd += float(f.get("fee") or 0)` inside the closing-dir filter). No entry fee, no funding term. Normal close path: `fees_pct = 2.0 * (fee_bps / 10000.0) * leverage; net_pnl_pct = float(gross_pnl_pct) - fees_pct` then `net_pnl_pct -= funding_pct` (scanner.py:3722-3739) — explicitly both legs plus funding.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) risk.py:_recover_exit_from_fills (1810-1851) matches ONLY closing-direction fills — expected_dir = "Close Long"/"Close Short", and the 1843-1850 filter skips non-close and opposite-direction-close fills; entry "Open" fills are excluded. fee_usd (line 1882) thus sums exit-leg fees only. (2) Ghost-recovery branch risk.py:2270-2271 computes _fees_pct = fee_usd/_margin (one leg: fee_usd/margin ≈ fee_rate*leverage) and _net_pct = pnl_pct - _fees_pct, with NO entry-leg fee and NO funding term anywhere in 2254-2278. (3) Normal close path _close_trade_db (scanner.py) subtracts a round-trip fee fees_pct = 2.0*(fee_bps/10000)*leverage (3722) AND folds realized funding net_pnl_pct -= funding_pct (3739); its docstring (3686-3688) confirms funding is folded for live trades. So relative to the normal path the ghost path is systematically optimistic by ~one fee leg plus all accrued funding. (4) The mid-fallback ghost close (2239-2247) leaves net_pnl_pct NULL: the net-recompute block is gated on recovered_exit being truthy with a non-None fee_usd (2254-2258), and close_trade_record itself does not write net_pnl_pct (trade_state.py:149 — no internal net write), so the fallback close yields gross-only. (5) Downstream policy.py:1244/1275/3714 use COALESCE(net_pnl_pct, pnl_pct), so the optimistic ghost net (and the gross-only mid fallback) feed the promotion gate. The claim, evidence, and impact all hold. Severity medium is appropriate: this is a recovery/edge path (live position closed on-exchange but still open in SQLite), it does not directly lose money or corrupt position state, but it flatters recorded net PnL and the promotion-gate input.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Confirmed against live code. Ghost-recovery net (forven/exchange/risk.py:2270-2271) computes `_fees_pct = recovered_exit["fee_usd"] / _margin; _net_pct = closed["pnl_pct"] - _fees_pct` with no funding term. `fee_usd` is exit-leg-only: _recover_exit_from_fills filters fills to the closing direction (risk.py:1843-1851 skips non-close / opposite-side closes) and sums only those (`fee_usd += float(f.get("fee") or 0)`, line 1882), so the opening fill's fee is excluded. The normal close path (scanner.py:3722-3739) subtracts round-trip fees `2.0 * (fee_bps/10000) * leverage` (fee_bps default 4.5/leg, _resolve_trade_assumptions line 724) AND folds funding via `net_pnl_pct -= funding_pct` (line 3739). So the ghost path systematically understates costs by ~one fee leg + all accrued funding → net overstated (optimistic). The mid-fallback ghost close (risk.py:2239-2247) leaves net_pnl_pct NULL because the net-write guard (risk.py:2254-2258) requires recovered_exit.fee_usd. This net feeds the promotion gate (policy.py:1244,1275,3714 `COALESCE(net_pnl_pct, pnl_pct)`) and deflated_sharpe.py:193, so it flatters the live track record. Reachability confirmed: wired into the daemon at startup (daemon.py:819) and periodic reconcile (daemon.py:1508-1514) via reconcile_all_books→reconcile_exchange_positions; ghost auto-close runs unconditionally with no feature flag whenever a SQLite OPEN trade has no matching exchange position — a genuine live desync scenario (exchange-side stop/TP fill, liquidation, manual close). Live-only path (operates on Hyperliquid fills); paper never reaches it. Medium severity is correct: not silently money-losing, but biases real numbers users and the gate act upon, confined to an edge-case recovery path.

### `LIVE-EXCHANGE-RECONCILE-3` — True-exit recovery matches fills by coin+direction+time only (never by oid/hash); a size mismatch can blend later unrelated closes into the exit price

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live-exchange-reconcile  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:1837-1901`
- **Claim:** The fill-to-trade attribution ignores the oid/hash that uniquely identify a fill (and that the docstring itself lists as available). It matches purely on coin, closing-direction, a lower-only time bound, chronological order, and a size cap. If the SQLite trade's recorded size exceeds the size actually closed on-exchange (rounding, a prior scale-down, or a wrong DB size), the `total_sz >= target_sz*0.99` cap never trips and the loop keeps consuming EVERY subsequent same-direction close on that coin, blending multiple positions' fills into one size-weighted exit price.
- **Impact:** A ghost-recovered close can record a wrong exit price (and thus wrong realized PnL) by averaging in an unrelated later position's fills on the same coin/direction. closedPnl is summed but only stored as informational signal_data (risk.py:2227), so there is no sign/scale PnL bug there — but the price used for PnL can be corrupted.
- **Suggested fix:** Match closing fills to the trade by oid/hash when the open order's fill oid is known, or at minimum cap the consumed fills to a single contiguous close cluster (stop at the first time-gap after target coverage) and refuse to aggregate beyond the trade's size by more than tolerance.
- **Evidence:** Matching is by coin (`str(f.get("coin")).upper() != asset_u: continue`, risk.py:1841) and closing direction (risk.py:1843-1851); oid/hash are never read. Stop condition: `if target_sz > 0: if total_sz >= target_sz * 0.99: break` (risk.py:1897-1899). If target_sz (trade size) is larger than the real closed size, the break never fires and all matched later closes are aggregated into `notional/total_sz` (risk.py:1906). The fill dicts DO carry oid/hash per get_user_fills docstring (hyperliquid.py:2029-2030) but they are unused.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every load-bearing code claim checks out against forven/exchange/risk.py.

(1) Matching ignores oid/hash. The loop filters fills ONLY by coin (risk.py:1841 `str(f.get("coin")...).upper() != asset_u: continue`) and closing direction (risk.py:1843-1851). oid/hash are never read anywhere in `_recover_exit_from_fills`, yet hyperliquid.py:2028-2030 docstring explicitly lists `oid` and `hash` as present on every fill. Confirmed.

(2) The size cap is the ONLY stop condition. risk.py:1897-1899: `if target_sz > 0: if total_sz >= target_sz * 0.99: break`. There is no oid clustering, no time-gap detection, and no upper time bound on the query (start_ms is a lower bound only, risk.py:1813-1831). So if `target_sz` (the DB `trade.size`, risk.py:1862) is not reached by this position's own closing fills, the loop iterates the entire chronologically-sorted `matched` list (risk.py:1861, 1870) and aggregates every subsequent same-coin/same-direction close into `notional`/`total_sz`, yielding a blended `exit_price = notional / total_sz` (risk.py:1906). No post-loop sanity check compares total_sz to target_sz (risk.py:1903 only rejects total_sz<=0). Confirmed exactly as claimed.

(3) Impact path verified. The caller uses the blended price as both signal_exit_price and exit_price (risk.py:2222-2238) and never inspects `recovered_size`, so over-consumption is undetected. That exit_price flows into close_trade_record, where realized PnL is recomputed: trade_state.py:274 `pnl_usd = (resolved_exit_price - entry_price) * size * signed` (resolved from provided exit_price, trade_state.py:217-219). So a corrupted recovered exit price corrupts booked realized PnL. The exchange `closedPnl` is, as the finding states, stored only as informational signal_data (risk.py:2227 `exit_closed_pnl_exchange`), so there is no sign/scale PnL bug there — the corruption is purely via the price. Confirmed.

(4) Reachability. The code provides NO invariant that `trade.size` equals the sum of this position's true closing fills, and three realistic conditions defeat the size cap: a wrong/oversized DB size, fills skipped by the px<=0/sz<=0 guard (risk.py:1876-1877) leaving total below target, or a prior scale-down. I independently found a concrete reachable scale-down path: partial_close_paper_position places a real reduce-only close fill on the exchange for a live trade (paper_control.py:339-340) and shrinks the parent to the residual (paper_control.py:419-420). That earlier partial-close "Close Long/Short" fill is within [start_ms, now) and matches coin+direction, so when the residual later closes (e.g. resting reduce-only stop) and the parent ghost-reconciles, the loop consumes the earlier partial fill first, spends the size budget across two distinct close events, and blends both prices into one exit. Same impact (corrupted exit price -> wrong PnL). Note: rounding alone is the weakest of the cited causes — the 1% tolerance (target_sz*0.99) absorbs typical lot-size rounding — but the other causes hold.

Net: the defect is real and code-accurate; the no-oid matching plus size-cap-only isolation genuinely blends multiple distinct close events into one weighted exit price, corrupting the booked realized PnL. It is confined to the H4 ghost-recovery edge path and affects one trade's recorded exit at a time, so medium is the correct severity (unchanged).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All technical claims verified against live code. (1) oid/hash unused: the matching loop reads only coin (risk.py:1841) and dir (1843-1851); get_user_fills docstring lists oid/hash/startPosition as available (hyperliquid.py:2028-2030) but none are referenced. (2) Match keys are exactly coin + closing-direction + lower-only time bound + chronological order + size cap. The time bound is structurally lower-only: start_ms comes from opened_at (risk.py:1815-1827) and get_user_fills uses info.user_fills_by_time(address, start_time_ms) with no upper bound (hyperliquid.py:2048-2055). Fills are sorted chronologically (1861). (3) The only stop condition is total_sz >= target_sz*0.99 (1897-1899); target_sz = abs(trade size) (1862). If the DB size exceeds the size actually closed for this position, the break never fires after this trade's own close fills and the loop continues into later matched fills (a same-coin/same-direction re-close within the unbounded-above window), folding them into exit_price = notional/total_sz (1906). (4) Impact correctly sized: recovered exit_price drives close_trade_record(signal_exit_price=exit_price, exit_price=exit_price) at risk.py:2222-2238, so the trade's recorded realized PnL can be corrupted; the exchange closedPnl is only stored informationally as exit_closed_pnl_exchange (2227), so there is no separate sign/scale bug — matching the finding's own honest impact note. Reachability: LIVE-only (reconcile_exchange_positions reconciles real Hyperliquid positions; recovery runs only on the ghost-close branch at risk.py:2203-2221, invoked from startup recovery/operator reconcile via reconcile_all_books). The defect requires a conjunction — a live ghost trade, an inflated/wrong DB size vs the actual closed size, and a later unrelated same-direction close on the same coin within the window. This is a real residual hole the existing mitigations (mandatory lower bound, chronological isolation, tolerance break) do not cover. Minor imprecision: it stops at target_sz*0.99 rather than literally consuming EVERY later close, but it still blends at least one unrelated close into the exit price. Net: confirmed, live-reachable but narrow; medium is appropriate (corrupts a recorded PnL/exit-price number on an exceptional recovery path, not a direct live mis-action, double-close, or lost position).

### `LIVE-EXCHANGE-RECONCILE-4` — Adopted real positions are stamped paper_challenger in non-live mode and carry no entry exchange id, so is_local_only_paper_trade later shields them from ghost-close → perpetual stale OPEN on exchange close

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live-exchange-reconcile  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:1649-1661, 1700-1732; forven/trade_state.py:45-68; forven/exchange/risk.py:2006-2020`
- **Claim:** An unmatched adoption (a real exchange position with no matching SQLite trade) in any non-live execution mode is inserted with execution_type='paper_challenger' and WITHOUT entry_exchange_order_id/entry_exchange_client_order_id. On a later reconcile, once that real position closes on-exchange, is_local_only_paper_trade() returns True for the adopted row, so the ghost branch treats it as a local paper trade and SKIPS the close — the SQLite trade never closes, never realizes PnL, and keeps occupying the asset slot.
- **Impact:** In testnet/paper mode (no real money) this corrupts the paper-validation book with a phantom perpetually-open trade and ties up the one-net-position-per-asset slot. Real mainnet ('live'/'mainnet') is unaffected because execution_type='live' makes is_local_only_paper_trade return False immediately.
- **Suggested fix:** Stamp adopted REAL positions with a marker that makes them reconcilable regardless of execution_type (e.g. set signal_data['entry_exchange_order_id'] or a dedicated reached_exchange flag at adoption), so a recovered real position is never later mistaken for a local-only paper ghost.
- **Evidence:** `_recovered_default_exec = "live" if _recovery_mode in {"live", "mainnet"} else "paper_challenger"` (risk.py:1651). For an unmatched adoption matched_trade is None, so signal_data starts empty and only `exchange_stop_order_id` is set (risk.py:1660-1661) — never entry_exchange_order_id. trade_reached_exchange checks only entry_exchange_order_id/entry_exchange_client_order_id (trade_state.py:49-52) → False; is_local_only_paper_trade returns True for exec_type in {paper, paper_challenger} (trade_state.py:65-68). The ghost branch then routes it to `informational` and `continue` (risk.py:2006-2020) instead of closing it.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every link in the chain holds against the live code. (1) Unmatched adoption: at risk.py:1601 signal_data = dict(matched_signal_data); with matched_trade=None the dict is empty. At risk.py:1650-1655 _recovery_mode = get_execution_mode(), which defaults to "paper" (config.py:199; always "paper" in beta builds), so _recovered_default_exec = "paper_challenger" and execution_type resolves to "paper_challenger". (2) No entry exchange id: grep confirms entry_exchange_order_id / entry_exchange_client_order_id are only READ in risk.py (lines 798, 1545), never written on the adoption path; only exchange_stop_order_id is set (risk.py:1661), which trade_reached_exchange does NOT check (trade_state.py:49-52) so it returns False. Hence is_local_only_paper_trade returns True (trade_state.py:65-68: exec_type 'paper_challenger' in set AND not reached_exchange). (3) Ghost branch: risk.py:2003-2021 — for an asset in db_by_asset but absent from hl_by_asset, is_local_only_paper_trade(trade)==True routes the trade to `informational` and `continue`, so it is never appended to ghost_trades and close_trade_record (risk.py:2203+) never runs → the SQLite trade stays OPEN forever, realizes no PnL, and keeps the one-net-position-per-asset slot. Reachability is real: adoption runs with adopt_missing_in_sqlite=True from daemon startup recovery (daemon.py:818-824) and operator manual reconcile (ops.py:589-592); neither gates adoption on live mode — the only skip is no-credentials+paper (daemon.py:787). So in paper mode with credentials, an unmatched REAL exchange position (e.g. leftover from an out-of-band live override, a manual testnet position, or a post-DB-reset position) is adopted as paper_challenger with no entry marker and is later shielded from ghost-close. Live/mainnet is correctly exempt because _recovered_default_exec='live' makes is_local_only_paper_trade return False (trade_state.py:66). Severity medium is appropriate: paper mode only (no real money), but it permanently corrupts the paper-validation book and ties up the asset slot, and the trigger requires the edge-case precondition of an unmatched real position existing while running paper.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Logic verified end-to-end against live code. (1) forven/exchange/risk.py:1651 sets `_recovered_default_exec = "live" if _recovery_mode in {"live","mainnet"} else "paper_challenger"`; for an unmatched adoption matched_trade is None so execution_type resolves to "paper_challenger" (1652-1655). (2) For unmatched adoption, signal_data starts from parse_trade_signal_data(None)={} (risk.py:1600) and across the whole insert block (1600-1759) only exchange_stop_order_id (1661), stop_loss, recovery_*, data_source, execution_venue, execution_mode are written into signal_data — entry_exchange_order_id / entry_exchange_client_order_id are never set; confirmed by reading the INSERT at 1700-1732. (3) trade_state.py:45-53 trade_reached_exchange checks ONLY entry_exchange_order_id / entry_exchange_client_order_id, so it returns False; trade_state.py:56-68 is_local_only_paper_trade returns True because exec_type=='paper_challenger' and reached_exchange is False. (4) The ghost branch at risk.py:2003-2021 does `if is_local_only_paper_trade(trade): informational.append(...); continue`, so the row is never added to ghost_trades and never reaches close_trade_record (risk.py:2203+) — the SQLite trade stays OPEN forever, never realizing PnL. Reachability holds: production execution mode is paper (config.py:193-199; set_execution_mode refuses non-paper), so the paper_challenger branch is the DEFAULT live path, not a dead/flag-off path; daemon.py:819-824 runs reconcile_all_books(adopt_missing_in_sqlite=True) in paper mode whenever creds exist (only skipped when creds absent AND mode==paper, daemon.py:786-798). An unmatched real exchange position is plausible via (a) paper_stage_local_execution_only=False routing paper trades to real testnet orders (scanner.py:1418-1419, flippable; test_live_session_real_balance.py:317 exercises it) with a crash-before-persist of the entry id, or (b) any external/leftover testnet wallet position. Mainnet is correctly unaffected (execution_type=='live' makes is_local_only_paper_trade short-circuit False), exactly as the finding states. I found no other code path that closes adopted exchange_recovered/paper_challenger rows, so the phantom-open is genuine. Severity medium is right: real state corruption of the paper-validation book + asset-slot occupation that can poison promotion-gate metrics, but no real money at stake and it requires the unmatched-real-position edge trigger.

### `LIVE-EXCHANGE-RECONCILE-6` — Ghost-close fails OPEN on a successful-but-empty exchange read (no sanity guard for zero positions while DB holds open live trades)

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** live-exchange-reconcile  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1911-1915; forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:658-661; forven/exchange/risk.py:2001-2021`
- **Claim:** Transient connectivity is correctly fail-closed (the breaker raises → reconcile returns error_kind=fetch_unavailable and closes nothing). But a user_state call that SUCCEEDS at the HTTP level yet returns an empty or partial assetPositions (valid JSON, no exception) records a breaker success and makes every tracked live position look absent — reconcile then ghost-closes ALL of them at the mid and cancels their reduce-only stops, while the real positions remain open and now naked. There is no sanity guard for the contradiction 'DB has N open live trades (with resting reduce-only stops) but the exchange snapshot shows 0 positions'.
- **Impact:** Low probability (requires the SDK to return a valid-but-empty/partial state while positions exist) but catastrophic if it fires: fabricated closes, stripped protective stops, and the daemon ceasing to manage still-open real positions.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a defensive guard before mass ghost-close: if the snapshot reports zero positions while SQLite has open live trades AND/OR resting reduce-only orders for those assets are still visible, treat the read as suspicious (skip ghost-close, surface fetch_unavailable, retry) rather than force-closing everything on a single empty read.
- **Evidence:** `get_positions` returns `{"positions": state.get("assetPositions", []), ...}` — `[]` when the key is missing/empty (hyperliquid.py:1912-1913). `_with_breaker` calls `breaker.record_success(); return result` on ANY non-exception return (hyperliquid.py:660-661), so an empty payload is treated as a clean read. reconcile then builds `hl_by_asset = {}` and every db trade hits the `if asset not in hl_by_asset` ghost branch (risk.py:2003-2021) with no guard comparing exchange_open against the open-live-trade count or the presence of resting reduce-only orders.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All code-truth claims verified against live code. (1) get_positions returns state.get("assetPositions", []) → [] on missing/empty key, and an empty-dict user_state response passes cleanly (hyperliquid.py:1912-1913). (2) _with_breaker records success on ANY non-exception return, so an empty-but-valid payload is a clean read, not a fault (hyperliquid.py:659-661). (3) _normalize_exchange_positions([]) → [] with no guard (risk.py:979-991), so hl_by_asset = {} (risk.py:2001). (4) Every live DB trade hits `if asset not in hl_by_asset` (risk.py:2004); is_local_only_paper_trade returns False for live trades (trade_state.py:65-68), so each is appended to ghost_trades (risk.py:2021). (5) The ghost-close is unconditional — pending_close_reconcile only changes the close_reason string (risk.py:2207-2212), not gating; the trade is closed via close_trade_record either way (risk.py:2230-2247) and its resting reduce-only stops are cancelled at risk.py:2280-2285. With the position still open there is no real close fill, so the exit falls back to the current mid via price_map.get (risk.py:2240), fabricating PnL exactly as claimed. (6) NO sanity guard exists anywhere in reconcile_exchange_positions (risk.py:1955-2339) or reconcile_all_books (risk.py:2342-2470) comparing exchange_open=0 against the open-live-trade count or the still-visible resting reduce-only orders. (7) The daemon's fail-closed path only triggers on recon.get("error") (_is_reconcile_fetch_unavailable, daemon.py:877-911,957); the empty-success path returns a non-error result AFTER the ghost-close already executed inside the pass, so the daemon protection is bypassed. The transient-exception path IS correctly fail-closed, confirming the finding's distinction. The only non-code element is the external trigger (HL returning valid-but-empty assetPositions while positions exist), which the finding itself rates low-probability; the defensive-guard gap (the actual defect) is fully present and reachable given such a degraded-API response. Severity medium is correct: low-probability trigger, catastrophic impact (fabricated closes, stripped stops, abandoned naked live positions on the real-money path).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-traced and confirmed end to end. (1) hyperliquid.py:1912-1913 `get_positions` returns `state.get("assetPositions", [])` -> `[]` for an empty/missing key. (2) hyperliquid.py:658-661 `_with_breaker` does `result = fn(...); breaker.record_success(); return result`, so a valid-but-empty payload is recorded as a clean read (no exception, no breaker failure). (3) risk.py:1018-1019/1039 `_snapshot_exchange_state` consumes that payload and does NOT raise on empty positions (`_normalize_exchange_positions([])` -> `[]`, risk.py:979-1007), so the exception->`fetch_unavailable` fail-closed branch (risk.py:1959-1966) is bypassed. (4) risk.py:2001 builds `hl_by_asset` from the empty list, and risk.py:2003-2021 classifies every DB OPEN trade whose asset is absent as a ghost; the ONLY exemption is `is_local_only_paper_trade` (trade_state.py:56-68 — paper trades that never reached the exchange), so LIVE trades and exchange-backed trades are NOT exempt. (5) risk.py:2230-2295 then force-closes each ghost (`close_trade_record` at mid via `price_map.get(asset_key)`, risk.py:2240), releases the lock (2279), and cancels the resting reduce-only stop via `_cancel_reduce_only_orders_for_asset` -> `cancel_order` (risk.py:2280-2285, 1103-1107). (6) There is NO guard anywhere comparing `exchange_open==0` against the open-live-trade count or resting reduce-only orders, and no two-pass confirmation gate — a single empty-but-successful read closes everything. The daemon periodic reconcile (daemon.py:1481-1517) invokes `reconcile_all_books` with no upstream sanity gate. The fail-open asymmetry is genuine: connectivity exceptions fail closed, but an empty-200 read fails open. The path is live (not paper-only) and the impact (fabricated closes + stripped protective stops leaving real positions naked) is correctly described. Reachability hinges on the SDK/API returning a successful-but-empty/partial state while positions exist — which is the one element not provable from code and which the finding itself rates low-probability — but the code-level defensive gap is fully verified. Medium is well-calibrated (catastrophic blast radius x low trigger probability), so severity unchanged.

### `DIRECTION-BOOKS-ACCOUNTING-4` — No per-book aggregate notional cap: each strategy sizes off FULL book equity (enforce_risk_caps=False drops the portfolio gate); only the lagging 80% margin read backstops, so concurrent same-scan opens can over-commit one book and strand the rejected side

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** direction-books-accounting  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:4336-4338,4551-4561 (legacy per-book sizing off full _book_eq), 5858-5859 (kernel sizing off aggregate), forven/exchange/risk.py:541-542,692,576-579 (caps skipped; only 80% margin gate)`
- **Claim:** When N strategies route to the same book, each sizes its position off the FULL book sub-account equity as if it were the sole user, and the portfolio-budget/per-trade caps are intentionally skipped (enforce_risk_caps=False) for parity sizing. There is no aggregate-notional cap per book. The only live backstop is can_open Rule 0c's 80% margin-ratio read, which reflects only ALREADY-FILLED positions, so two opens firing in the same scan (or before the exchange margin propagates) can both pass and push the book past available margin.
- **Impact:** On a books-enabled deployment running multiple live strategies per book, aggregate intended notional can exceed the book's margin capacity. The 80% gate is reactive (it blocks the (k+1)th open only after the kth fill propagates), so concurrent opens on the same book can over-commit; the exchange then rejects an order. Combined with finding 2 (kernel path) or the legacy pending_open_reconcile flow, the rejected side can be left stranded/unprotected. Degraded/edge-case rather than a silent loss, hence medium.
- **Suggested fix:** Track per-book committed notional/risk within can_open (book-scoped exposure already exists for one-per-asset) and enforce an operator-set aggregate per-book budget even when enforce_risk_caps is False, or divide book equity by the number of strategies routed to that book when sizing. At minimum, make the min-notional/over-commit preflight book-aware on BOTH the legacy and kernel paths.
- **Evidence:** Legacy: `_book_eq = _book_account_equity(_book_addr); if _book_eq and _book_eq > 0: sizing_equity = _book_eq` (scanner.py:4336-4338) then `size = round(_sizing.position_units(equity=float(sizing_equity), size_fraction=_size_fraction, leverage=_leverage, entry_price=float(price)), 6)` (4555-4561), full book equity, no division across strategies. Kernel: `units = ... position_units(equity=float(sizing_equity), ...)` with sizing_equity=aggregate equity (scanner.py:5858-5859, 6041). can_open skips the per-trade cap (`if enforce_risk_caps and risk_pct > max_risk_per_trade`, risk.py:541-542) and the portfolio-budget clamp (`if enforce_risk_caps and abs(new_net) > portfolio_budget`, risk.py:692). The only book-margin check is `margin_ratio = margin_used / acct_val; if margin_ratio >= 0.80: return False` (risk.py:576-579), reading live (already-filled) margin.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All code-level claims verified against the live source. (1) enforce_risk_caps=False is passed on both the legacy open path (scanner.py:4414) and the kernel live path (scanner.py:5855). (2) With that flag, risk.py:541-542 skips the per-trade cap (Rule 0b) and risk.py:692-703 skips the portfolio-budget clamp/block (Rule 3) — confirmed; the portfolio budget is also a risk-pct gate, not a notional cap. (3) Sizing is off FULL equity with no division across strategies: legacy sets sizing_equity = _book_eq (scanner.py:4337-4338) and calls position_units(equity=float(sizing_equity), ...) (scanner.py:4555-4561); the kernel does the same at scanner.py:5859. (4) The only exchange-margin backstop is the 80% gate (risk.py:576-579), which reads margin_used/acct_val from a live get_account_value — i.e. already-filled positions — and is evaluated BEFORE the order WITHOUT adding the pending order's own margin; there is no in-process committed-notional accumulator. (5) No aggregate per-book notional cap exists: max_concurrent_positions is a COUNT cap defaulting to unlimited (risk.py:159-172), the _MIN_LIVE_ORDER_NOTIONAL_USD preflight (scanner.py:4587-4604) is a floor not a ceiling, and per_book_passes (risk.py:2474) is reconciliation. The missing control the finding describes is genuinely absent.

One framing correction (does not change the verdict): execution is sequential, not parallel — _apply_execution_actions iterates strategies single-threaded (scanner.py:6602); only signal EVALUATION uses the ThreadPoolExecutor (scanner.py:6482). So the literal 'two opens firing in the same scan' via concurrent threads is inaccurate. But the finding explicitly hedges with '(or before the exchange margin propagates),' and the substantive over-commit mechanism holds sequentially: the 80% gate is a pre-order snapshot that does not reserve/pre-account for the order being placed (one large or full-mode open can jump 79%->129%), and back-to-back opens re-read margin that may not yet reflect the prior fill. Reachability is correctly scoped to a books-enabled multi-strategy-per-book live deployment (and applies broadly to multiple live strategies sharing the master wallet). Medium is appropriate: the exchange rejects truly over-margin orders so it is not a silent loss, but the gap can over-commit a book and — combined with a rejected-order stranding path — leave the rejected side unprotected.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited code claims verify exactly against the live source. Legacy path sizes off full book equity with no division (scanner.py:4336-4338 sets sizing_equity=_book_eq; 4555-4561 position_units(equity=float(sizing_equity))). Kernel live path sizes off the daemon aggregate (scanner.py:6041 sizing_equity=_get_real_account_equity(), reads daemon_state.account_equity which is the book-aggregate snapshot; 5858-5859 position_units off it). Both live paths call can_open(..., enforce_risk_caps=False) (legacy 4414, kernel 5855), which in risk.py skips both the per-trade cap (541-542) and the portfolio-budget clamp/block (692). The only remaining aggregate backstop is Rule 0c's 80% margin gate (risk.py:576-579), which reads totalMarginUsed from a live get_account_value call (already-filled positions). Defaults confirm there is no other aggregate cap: live max_concurrent_positions defaults unlimited (risk.py:170-172), portfolio_budget (0.01-0.02) is disabled by the flag. Reachability: live-only money impact, kernel live default ON (live_kernel_execution=True at 5828); the gap is NOT books-gated — with books disabled (default live_books_enabled=False) all live orders route to the master wallet, each full-sized, Rule 3 disabled, unlimited concurrent positions, so per-pool aggregate is uncapped except by the reactive 80% gate. One framing inaccuracy: position actions are dispatched SEQUENTIALLY, not concurrently (_apply_execution_actions iterates `for item in signal_rows` at scanner.py:6602), so opens are not literally simultaneous; but the finding explicitly also names the true mechanism (margin not yet propagated between sequential opens — Rule 0c reads the exchange, not the local register() pool that disabled Rule 3 would read), so the TOCTOU/propagation race holds. Medium is correct: the 80% gate is a genuine fail-closed backstop with a 20% buffer, an actual over-commit-to-rejection requires already being near capacity, and the money-losing 'stranded side' outcome is explicitly conditional on other findings. The standalone verified defect (no aggregate per-pool notional cap; reactive-only lagging margin backstop; full-equity per-strategy sizing) is a real, live-reachable architectural gap.
