### `PROMOTION-GATE-PARITY-4` — Regime-sensitivity detector (compute_dual_score / regime_sensitive) that would catch the gated-vs-ungated divergence is dead code, wired into no gate

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** promotion-gate-parity  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/fitness.py:166-211`
- **Claim:** compute_dual_score computes a degradation_delta between gated and ungated scores and sets regime_sensitive when an edge collapses under gating — exactly the signal needed to detect PARITY-1. But this function and the regime_sensitive flag are referenced nowhere outside fitness.py, so nothing computes the ungated score or blocks/flags regime-dependent strategies before live.
- **Impact:** There is no automated guardrail detecting that a strategy's edge depends on the regime gate before it reaches live capital; the only mechanism designed for it is inert.
- **Suggested fix:** Either wire compute_dual_score into the gauntlet/live gate (compute the ungated score, reject or position-reduce when regime_sensitive) or remove the dead code. Given PARITY-1, wiring it (or simply matching the gates' regime_gate to the execution path) is the real fix.
- **Evidence:** fitness.py:203 `regime_sensitive = degradation_delta > _REGIME_SENSITIVITY_THRESHOLD` and :210 `"deployment_fitness": primary_score,  # Always use gated score for deployment`. A whole-tree grep for `compute_dual_score|regime_sensitive|deployment_fitness|degradation_delta|ungated_metrics` returns matches ONLY in forven/strategies/fitness.py — no caller in policy.py, scanner.py, brain.py, gauntlet/, or routers/.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified. compute_dual_score (forven/strategies/fitness.py:166-211) computes degradation_delta (line 199: `1.0 - (primary_score / ungated_score)`), sets regime_sensitive (line 203: `degradation_delta > _REGIME_SENSITIVITY_THRESHOLD`), and always returns the gated score for deployment (line 210: `"deployment_fitness": primary_score`). Whole-tree greps confirm compute_dual_score, regime_sensitive, and deployment_fitness each match in ONLY one file — fitness.py — i.e., no caller in policy.py, optimizer.py, evolution.py, scanner.py, gauntlet, or routers. The 4 extra hits for the substring "ungated" are unrelated: paper.py:2009 (chart trigger markers), runner.py:1160 and runtime_worker.py:973 (agent tool-gating/security). Meanwhile score_strategy (the inner function compute_dual_score wraps) IS wired into the live scoring path (policy.py, optimizer.py, evolution.py, db.py, tools_backtesting.py), so gates score via score_strategy directly and never compute an ungated score or evaluate regime_sensitive. Thus the regime-sensitivity detector designed to catch a gated-vs-ungated edge collapse is genuinely inert dead code, wired into no gate, exactly as claimed. Severity left unchanged: as a standalone defect this is a missing/defensive guardrail (dead code), not a direct money-loss or state-corruption bug; its monetary impact is contingent on the separate PARITY-1 finding which is outside this single-finding verification. medium is reasonable for a designed-but-inert pre-live safety mechanism.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: low): The literal claim is verified. compute_dual_score (forven/strategies/fitness.py:166) computes degradation_delta=1.0-(primary/ungated) at :199, sets regime_sensitive = degradation_delta > _REGIME_SENSITIVITY_THRESHOLD (0.60) at :203, and emits deployment_fitness=primary_score (gated) at :210. Whole-tree greps for the exact identifiers compute_dual_score, regime_sensitive, and deployment_fitness return matches ONLY in fitness.py — no caller in policy.py, scanner.py, brain.py, gauntlet/, routers/, or tests/. The function is genuinely dead and the regime_sensitive flag is consumed by no gate. So "dead code, wired into no gate" is factually correct → confirmed.

However, on the REACHABILITY & IMPACT lens I downgrade medium→low: (1) the code never executes, so it has zero direct money/state impact — the only "harm" alleged is a missing guardrail; (2) the guardrail's premise is undercut by the live pipeline, where the gate's execution-profile selection (forven/gauntlet/tasks.py:1309, regime_gate=False, comment "match the paper scanner's kernel call (the parity reference)") and the paper/live kernel call (forven/scanner.py:6007, regime_gate=False) BOTH run ungated — there is no gated-vs-ungated divergence between gate and execution for this detector to catch; (3) compute_dual_score's own design treats regime_gate=True as the "deploy-realistic" primary (docstring :172, :177), the OPPOSITE of the actual ungated deployment path, so even if wired in unchanged it would measure the wrong baseline and could not function as a PARITY-1 detector without rework. This is a defensive/cleanup-class issue (inert, stale-by-design dead code) whose protective value is contingent on a separate unverified PARITY-1, not an edge-case that degrades real money/state. Hence severity low rather than medium.

### `PROMOTION-GATE-PARITY-5` — Same kernel decisions record different pnl_pct units for paper vs live, so paper 'proof' metrics do not predict the live numbers the operator will see

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** promotion-gate-parity  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5504-5552 (paper kernel close) vs 5885-5914 (live kernel close)`
- **Claim:** The paper kernel close records pnl_pct as an equity-fraction, but the LIVE kernel close records pnl_pct as a leverage-inclusive margin-return via _close_trade_db. The promotion gate validates a strategy on the paper (equity-fraction) numbers, yet once live the same strategy's recorded per-trade pnl_pct is on a ~1/size_fraction-larger scale — so live dashboard returns/Sharpe/DD are not comparable to the paper proof they were promoted on.
- **Impact:** Post-promotion, the live metrics the operator monitors are on a different scale than the paper metrics that justified going live, undermining drift/regression comparison (e.g. P4-4 graduation baseline snapshot at policy.py:3856) and any paper-vs-live parity check.
- **Suggested fix:** Record one canonical per-trade return convention across paper and live closes (compute the equity-fraction net for live closes too, or store both gross-margin and equity-fraction explicitly). Coordinate with the live-PnL/metrics auditor — this overlaps the live dashboard math.
- **Evidence:** Paper: scanner.py:5544-5550 writes `pnl_pct=net_pnl_pct=pnl_pct_net` (equity-fraction, per 5509 comment). Live: scanner.py:5912 `pnl_pct = ((ref_price - entry_price) / entry_price) * signed * leverage` then 5914 `_close_trade_db(trade_id, ref_price, pnl_pct, pnl_usd, ...)` → net_pnl_pct = margin-return - fees (scanner.py:3722-3723).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): CORE CLAIM CONFIRMED against live code. Paper kernel close (_kernel_close_recorded) writes pnl_pct AND net_pnl_pct = pnl_pct_net (scanner.py:5544-5551), where pnl_pct_net = trade.get("pnl_pct") (scanner.py:5509, explicitly "kernel net, equity-fraction"). The kernel computes this as pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction (execution_kernel.py:114; header comment line 14: "(price_return*sign*leverage - drag) * size_fraction") — an equity-fraction. Live kernel close (_kernel_close_live_trade) computes pnl_pct = ((ref_price-entry_price)/entry_price)*signed*leverage (scanner.py:5912) — a leverage-inclusive margin-return with NO size_fraction term — so recorded live returns are ~1/size_fraction larger than paper for the same kernel decision. So the two paths genuinely record per-trade returns on different scales.

ONE MECHANICAL IMPRECISION (does not change verdict): the finding says line 5912's value is passed to _close_trade_db and becomes net_pnl_pct. Actually _close_trade_db ignores the passed pnl_pct for the DB write — close_trade_record recomputes it (trade_state.py:268) with the IDENTICAL formula ((exit-entry)/entry*signed*leverage), then net_pnl_pct = gross(margin) - fees - funding (scanner.py:3722-3723). Same value, same scale, so the conclusion holds.

Both paths reachable: live_kernel_execution defaults True (scanner.py:5828); close applier = _kernel_close_live_trade if is_live else _kernel_close_paper_trade (scanner.py:6094), routed at scanner.py:6619.

IMPACT mostly holds, with one overstatement. Paper gate reads COALESCE(net_pnl_pct,pnl_pct) for paper% (policy.py:3714 = equity-fraction); baseline backtest_sharpe/max_dd are kernel-derived equity-fraction (policy.py:3639-3641); drift reads live% pnl_pct (monitoring.py:794 = margin-return). The dd_inflation drift check (monitoring.py:822, threshold 2.0 at line 761) compares margin-scale live DD against equity-fraction baseline DD — a real scale mismatch that can spuriously flag drift and freeze the P4-7 allocation ramp (policy.py:1376-1382). Total/avg-return comparisons are likewise non-comparable. HOWEVER the finding overstates by lumping in Sharpe: Sharpe = mean/std is scale-invariant, so sharpe_degradation (monitoring.py:821) is NOT affected by the unit difference.

Severity unchanged (medium): no direct money loss or position corruption; the defect yields non-comparable recorded returns/DD between paper proof and live, plus a corrupted DD-drift gate that fails in the conservative direction (caps allocation at 25%).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): CONFIRMED and reachable on the default-on live path. Paper kernel close `_kernel_close_recorded` overrides the row with the kernel's net pnl at scanner.py:5544-5545 (`pnl_pct = net_pnl_pct = pnl_pct_net`); that kernel value is an EQUITY-FRACTION per execution_kernel.py:114 (`pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction`, gross = price_return*sign*leverage - drag). The live kernel close `_kernel_close_live_trade` (scanner.py:5885-5928) persists pnl_pct via close_trade_record (trade_state.py:268: `((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage`) = MARGIN-RETURN, NOT scaled by size_fraction, and net_pnl_pct = that minus fees (scanner.py:3722-3723). So paper/backtest and live record pnl_pct on scales differing by ~1/size_fraction; sizing.py:239 gives size_fraction ~0.1-0.5 for the default atr profile, so live numbers run ~2-10x larger for identical performance. Minor evidence nit: the live recorded net does not literally consume the pnl_pct computed at scanner.py:5912 (close_trade_record/_close_trade_db recompute it), but the formula is the same margin-return, so the conclusion holds. Impact is real and arguably understated: the paper gate validates equity-fraction (policy.py:3714), the graduation baseline stores backtest-scale DD (policy.py:3639-3640), and compute_paper_live_drift (monitoring.py:793-822) compares LIVE margin-return DD against the equity-fraction baseline with a 2.0x dd_inflation threshold (monitoring.py:761) — the units gap alone can false-flag drift, and a flag freezes allocation at 25% (policy.py:1376-1382). This drift job is scheduled in production (scheduler.py:1505-1506). Severity stays MEDIUM (not high): dollar accounting (pnl_usd/equity) is correct in both paths, the promotion gate uses one consistent paper-only scale, and the drift false-flag is conservative (caps allocation downward), so it produces wrong comparative metrics and can mis-fire a safety control rather than silently losing money or corrupting positions.

### `DAEMON-EQUITY-FEED-RISK-STATE-2` — books_aggregate -> exchange transition (books disabled mid-session) keeps the stale higher aggregate HWM, computing a phantom ~100% drawdown that FALSE-fires the kill-switch and flattens live positions

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** daemon-equity-feed-risk-state  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/daemon.py:1100-1120; forven/exchange/risk.py:2826,2862-2866,2913-2924; forven/exchange/risk.py:2755`
- **Claim:** The re-baseline at risk.py:2826 only re-bases on paper->non-paper. A books_aggregate->exchange transition (live source to live source) does NOT re-baseline, so when capital legitimately lives in sub-accounts and books get disabled, equity collapses to master-only against an aggregate-level HWM and the kill-switch fires on a phantom drawdown.
- **Impact:** Disabling books (operator action, or 3+ consecutive glitchy settings reads of live_books_enabled) while sub-accounts hold capital force-flattens live positions on a non-existent loss and latches a kill-switch that requires manual reset — a real-money loss from premature closes plus an outage of all live trading until the operator intervenes.
- **Suggested fix:** Re-baseline (or proportionally adjust) the HWM on ANY equity-source change whose denominator basis changes (books_aggregate<->exchange), not only paper->non-paper; or compute drawdown only across a stable account-set. At minimum, when the aggregate basis shrinks because books were disabled, recompute the HWM against the new basis before evaluating the kill-switch, and require confirm-ticks symmetric to the books-on path.
- **Evidence:** When books_enabled() reads False for >= _BOOKS_OFF_CONFIRM_TICKS (=3) consecutive ticks, _book_aware_account_value commits to master-only equity: `_LAST_BOOKS_ENABLED = False; return get_account_value(testnet=testnet)` with source="exchange" (daemon.py:1106-1117). The re-baseline guard requires `prev_source == "paper"` (risk.py:2826), so a books_aggregate->exchange change leaves high_water_mark at the aggregate (sum of master+subs) level (risk.py:2818). With master-only equity << aggregate HWM, `drawdown_pct = (hwm - account_equity) / hwm` (risk.py:2866) is huge, and `if drawdown_pct >= max_drawdown and kill_switch_enabled:` latches the kill-switch (risk.py:2913-2918), which the daemon then re-flattens on a throttled loop off the persisted flag (daemon.py:1328-1335). _validate_equity_sample does not protect against this: its relative-jump check only rejects UPWARD jumps (`eq > last * _EQUITY_JUMP_REJECT_MULT`, risk.py:2755), never a drop.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every link in the chain is verified against live code. (1) The re-baseline guard at risk.py:2826 is literally `if prev_source == "paper" and source != "paper" and hwm > 0:` — a books_aggregate->exchange change is non-paper->non-paper and is NOT re-baselined; equity_source is otherwise only read at 2816 / written at 2817, so there is no other source-transition handling. (2) daemon.py:1106-1117: once books_enabled() reads False for >= _BOOKS_OFF_CONFIRM_TICKS (=3, daemon.py:166) it commits `_LAST_BOOKS_ENABLED=False; return get_account_value(testnet=testnet)` (master-only). (3) hyperliquid.py:1997-2004 returns `"source": "exchange"`, and daemon.py:1309 reads `acct.get("source","exchange")`, so master-only equity arrives tagged exchange while the HWM is still at the aggregate (master+subs, which the kernel tracked up via risk.py:2862). (4) drawdown_pct=(hwm-equity)/hwm at risk.py:2866 is therefore large. (5) Kill switch latches at risk.py:2914 since default max_drawdown is 0.05/0.10 capped 0.30 (risk.py:46/53/105). (6) _validate_equity_sample only rejects UPWARD jumps (risk.py:2755 `eq > last*_EQUITY_JUMP_REJECT_MULT`); the downward drop is not rejected. (7) The daemon re-flattens off the persisted kill_switch flag (daemon.py:1328-1335) and reset_kill_switch (risk.py:3229) is manual, confirming the real-money flatten + latched outage. The only mitigations are the 3-tick confirm gate (defeated by a sustained 3+ tick glitch, e.g. kv_get failing -> books.py:50-54 defaults to {} -> False) and the equity<=0 early return (daemon.py:1306, which only helps if the master is fully drained). The canonical books layout (long book = master at address None, short book = dedicated sub; books.py:156-159) leaves master-only positive, so disabling books produces a genuine phantom drawdown — reachable. Severity stays medium: correct and reachable, but gated entirely on the opt-in books feature (live_books_enabled default False) and on the master holding a positive-but-small balance, so it is not a default-config money loss. No overlooked guard or negating line found.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All code-level claims verified against live code. The re-baseline guard at risk.py:2826 is `if prev_source == "paper" and source != "paper" and hwm > 0:` — a books_aggregate->exchange transition (both non-paper) does NOT re-baseline. When books_enabled() reads False for >=_BOOKS_OFF_CONFIRM_TICKS (=3) consecutive ticks, _book_aware_account_value commits to master-only via `return get_account_value(testnet=testnet)` (daemon.py:1116-1117). That live path returns `"source": "exchange"` (hyperliquid.py:2003), and the daemon reads `equity_source = acct.get("source", "exchange")` (daemon.py:1309), so the transition is genuinely books_aggregate->exchange. The drawdown is then `(hwm - account_equity)/hwm` (risk.py:2866) using the stale aggregate HWM (sum of master+subs) against master-only equity = a phantom collapse. Nothing else catches it: _validate_equity_sample only rejects UPWARD jumps (`eq > last * _EQUITY_JUMP_REJECT_MULT`, risk.py:2755) so the downward drop passes; the corrupted-HWM self-heal only fires when `hwm > _MAX_PLAUSIBLE_EQUITY` (risk.py:2850), which a normal aggregate HWM won't trip. The kill-switch then latches (risk.py:2913-2918, default kill_switch_enabled=True) and the daemon re-flattens off the persisted flag (daemon.py:1328-1335), force-closing live positions and requiring manual reset. Reachability: gated behind live_books_enabled which DEFAULTS TO FALSE (books.py:64), but it is a real, used feature (the PNL-1 comment at risk.py:2820-2825 references a real soak with ~$675 live books equity). The trigger is plausible via operator disable with funded sub-accounts, or a sustained >=3-tick forven:settings KV glitch where _settings() returns {} on exception (books.py:52-53) while the exchange master-read still succeeds. Severity kept at medium: the impact (premature live flatten on a non-existent loss + latched kill-switch outage) is real money loss, but it is gated behind a default-off opt-in flag and requires a specific mid-session on->off transition with capital actually held in sub-accounts. The author's medium rating already reflects this gating, so unchanged.

### `CONCURRENT-SCAN-RACE-2` — _execute_direct('close') has no idempotency key and pending_close_reconcile trades stay OPEN, so a real reduce-only close is re-issued every scan and by concurrent scans

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** concurrent-scan-race  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:3410-3436 (close path, no cloid/idempotency key); forven/scanner.py:5885-5900 (_kernel_close_live_trade calls _execute_direct('close')); forven/scanner.py:5347-5393 (_kernel_recorded_trades); forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:161-163; forven/trade_state.py:107-136 (mark keeps status OPEN)`
- **Claim:** A live trade whose close left no confirmed fill is marked pending_close_reconcile but stays status='OPEN'; the reconciler re-classifies it as a still-open recorded trade and emits a fresh 'close' action on the very next scan (and on a concurrent scan), causing _execute_direct to place ANOTHER reduce-only close order with no idempotency key.
- **Impact:** Mostly bounded by reduce_only (a redundant close on an already-flat position is rejected/no-op), but: (a) it generates repeated real exchange order attempts every scan until a reconcile sweep finally finalizes the row; (b) it opens an over-close window — if a NEW same-direction position is opened (after the prior trade is marked CLOSED in the DB, freeing the unique index) before a stale/concurrent scan issues its reduce-only close for the OLD row's size, that reduce-only order will partially/fully flatten the NEW, wanted position (real money: an unintended close the strategy did not request). The reconcile loop later repairs the DB/exchange divergence, so it is recoverable but with a real unwanted fill.
- **Suggested fix:** Exclude pending_close_reconcile rows from the reconciler's close generation (skip them in _kernel_recorded_trades or short-circuit in _kernel_close_live_trade when `_trade_pending_close_reconcile(row)` is true and the prior request is recent), and pass a deterministic client order id (e.g. derived from trade_id + close epoch) to close_position so a duplicate close is dedupable at the exchange. Combined with RACE-1's single-flight guard this closes the over-close-on-reopen window.
- **Evidence:** `mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile` only writes signal_data + signal_exit_price (`UPDATE trades SET signal_exit_price=?, signal_data=? WHERE id=?`, trade_state.py:124-136) — it never changes `status`. `_kernel_recorded_trades` selects `status IN ('OPEN','CLOSED')` and emits any OPEN row with a kernel_entry_time as `"status":"open"` (scanner.py:5360-5375) with NO pending_close_reconcile exclusion. The reconciler then does: `elif str(r.get('status') or 'open').strip().lower() != 'closed': closes.append(ReconcileAction("close", ...))` (paper_reconcile.py:161-163). The close itself, `result = close_position(asset, size, close_side, **close_kwargs)` (scanner.py:3436), passes no client-order-id; `close_position` issues a fresh reduce-only IOC each call (hyperliquid.py:1878-1883). `_trade_pending_close_reconcile` exists (scanner.py:3535) but is only consulted on the legacy manage_positions path (scanner.py:4045), NOT in the kernel close path.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every literal code assertion verifies against the live code. (1) mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile (trade_state.py:124-136) writes only signal_exit_price + signal_data and never changes status, so the row stays OPEN. (2) _kernel_recorded_trades (scanner.py:5359-5375) selects status IN ('OPEN','CLOSED') and re-emits any OPEN row with a kernel_entry_time as status:"open" with NO pending_close_reconcile exclusion. (3) The reconciler (paper_reconcile.py:161-163) appends a "close" action for every kernel-closed trade matching a recorded row whose status != 'closed'. Because manage_positions_via_kernel re-runs run_strategy_execution(df,...) fresh each scan (scanner.py:6005), the deterministic kernel re-emits the same closed trade every scan while its exit bar is in the replay window — so the close action recurs on the very next scan. (4) Dispatch (scanner.py:6144-6145, close_applier set at 6094) has no pending-reconcile guard; _kernel_close_live_trade re-calls _execute_direct("close") (scanner.py:5900); the close handler calls close_position(asset,size,close_side,**close_kwargs) at scanner.py:3436 where close_kwargs holds only testnet/vault_address — no cloid; hyperliquid.py:1878-1883 submits a reduce-only IOC with no client order id. The OPEN path by contrast passes idempotency_key=f"{trade_id}:open" (scanner.py:3362), confirming the asymmetry. (5) _trade_pending_close_reconcile (scanner.py:3535) is consulted only on the legacy path (scanner.py:4045), never in the kernel close path. The reconcile sweep (scanner.py:7143-7229) applies a ~30-min grace and checks exchange truth (_exchange_open_size, has_position False→local close) before retrying — a safety the kernel path bypasses, so during the grace window the kernel blindly re-fires the close every scan. The repeated-reissue defect is real and reachable single-threaded. The over-close-on-reopen impact (b) is concurrency-dependent: single-threaded, _kernel_close_live_trade returns early on "pending" without marking the row CLOSED, so a same-direction reopen hits the unique-index IntegrityError (scanner.py:5874) within the same scan; the dangerous unwanted fill needs concurrent scans (RACE-1's premise). Net effect is mostly bounded by reduce_only (no-op when flat, beneficial retry when genuinely open), so medium severity is correct.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every link of the chain verifies against live code, and the path is reachable in PRODUCTION (live default-on). (1) mark_trade_pending_close_reconcile writes only signal_exit_price + signal_data (trade_state.py:124-136) and sets signal_data['pending_close_reconcile']=True (line 107) — status stays 'OPEN'. (2) _execute_direct close path marks pending and returns state='pending' when fill is None (scanner.py:3499-3512). (3) _kernel_close_live_trade returns early on pending WITHOUT marking the row CLOSED and WITHOUT any _trade_pending_close_reconcile short-circuit (scanner.py:5900-5903). (4) _kernel_recorded_trades selects status IN ('OPEN','CLOSED') and emits any OPEN row with a kernel_entry_time as status='open' with NO pending exclusion (scanner.py:5360-5375). (5) The reconciler re-emits a 'close' for any matched recorded row whose status!='closed' (paper_reconcile.py:161-163). (6) close_position issues a fresh reduce-only IOC with no cloid (hyperliquid.py:1878-1883). (7) The legacy manage_positions path guards this exact case (if _trade_pending_close_reconcile(trade): continue, scanner.py:4045-4048) but the kernel close-application loop (scanner.py:6094/6131-6155) has no equivalent guard — a genuine parity gap. (8) REACHABILITY: _live_kernel_execution_enabled() = _scanner_bool_setting('live_kernel_execution', True) — default ON (scanner.py:5828; test_kernel_live_parity.py:24-28 asserts True; matches MEMORY note), so this is the live production path, not a dead/default-off branch. (9) The sweep only finalizes rows older than _RECONCILE_MAX_AGE_MINUTES=30 (scanner.py:7061, 7167-7168), so the close re-fires on every scan for up to ~30 min. Impact (a) — repeated real reduce-only close orders every scan — is solidly real but mostly benign no-ops (reduce_only on a flat position is rejected). Impact (b) — the over-close-on-reopen unwanted real fill — is genuine but concurrency-dependent: while the OLD row is status='OPEN' the unique-index duplicate-open guard (sqlite3.IntegrityError, scanner.py:5874-5875) blocks a new same-direction open, so the unwanted fill needs the OLD row CLOSED + a NEW open + a stale/concurrent close interleaving (the race the finding attributes to sibling RACE-1; reconcile_sweep and scanner_run are distinct scheduler jobs with separate locks at scheduler.py:1326-1337/1726-1732, making cross-job concurrency plausible). Medium is the right level: common case benign, real-money path rare and self-healed by the reconcile loop, but a real defect on the default-on live path and a clear regression vs. the legacy guard. Confirmed; severity unchanged.

### `CONCURRENT-SCAN-RACE-3` — Concurrent partial-fill double-close strands a DB ghost: both closers shrink size to a residual and leave the trade OPEN while the exchange position is fully flat

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** concurrent-scan-race  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:3459-3488 (partial-close residual branch); forven/scanner.py:5900-5903 (_kernel_close_live_trade returns early on partial)`
- **Claim:** When two concurrent reduce-only close orders each PARTIAL-fill the same position, each one independently computes residual = requested - its_own_fill, writes `UPDATE trades SET size=?` to that residual, marks partial_close, and returns early — so the DB keeps the trade OPEN at a residual size even though the two fills together fully closed the exchange position.
- **Impact:** The DB shows an OPEN live position (and holds a risk slot) for size that is already flat on the exchange — a ghost. PnL for the position is deferred to the next scan's reduce-only retry (rejected, no fill -> pending) and ultimately to the daemon reconcile/ghost-close, which finalizes at a recovered fill-ledger price. State is eventually consistent but, in the interim, exposure and available-risk accounting are wrong and the position can block legitimate re-entries via the unique index.
- **Suggested fix:** Have the partial-close branch re-read the live exchange position size (or trust the reconciler) before persisting a residual, and/or gate the residual write behind the RACE-1 single-flight guard so two closers cannot each subtract their own partial from the original full size. At minimum, when _close_reconcile_state is 'partial', confirm residual>0 against the exchange before keeping the trade OPEN.
- **Evidence:** `_closed_filled_f = float(result.get('filled_size')); ... if _closed_filled_f is not None and _requested > 0 and _closed_filled_f + 1e-9 < _requested: residual = round(max(_requested - _closed_filled_f, 0.0), 8) ... conn.execute("UPDATE trades SET size = ? WHERE id = ?", (residual, str(trade_id))) ... result['_close_reconcile_state'] = 'partial'; ... return result` (scanner.py:3459-3488). `_kernel_close_live_trade` then `state = ...; if state in ('pending','partial'): return f"LIVE-KERNEL-CLOSE {asset} {state}"` (scanner.py:5901-5903) WITHOUT calling _close_trade_db. Both racing closers read the same pre-close `size` and each compute the residual from its own partial fill, so the last writer leaves size = a non-zero residual that no longer exists on the exchange.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanical claims verified literally. scanner.py:3464-3488: residual is computed as `_requested - _closed_filled_f` where `_requested = float(size or 0)` is the size passed INTO this call (the recorded row size), and the branch does a blind `conn.execute("UPDATE trades SET size = ? WHERE id = ?", (residual, str(trade_id)))` (3473) with NO `WHERE size>?` guard, NO re-read of the live exchange remaining position, and NO single-flight lock, then sets `_close_reconcile_state='partial'` and returns. scanner.py:5901-5903: `_kernel_close_live_trade` returns on state in ('pending','partial') BEFORE `_close_trade_db` (5914) and BEFORE `release(trade_id)` (5925), so the trade stays OPEN and keeps its risk slot — confirmed.\n\nReachability of two concurrent closers: within one run_scan the close path is serial (_apply_execution_actions, scanner.py:6602 for-loop) and the reconciler emits one close per trade, so no intra-scan double-close. The scheduler blocks its own duplicate scanner_run via the atomic CAS lock _try_mark_job_running (scheduler.py:893-923) on a single job_id. BUT manual triggers bypass it: _run_manual_scanner_cycle (control_plane/ops.py:534) and _run_scanner_once (api_domains/paper.py:2319, also via start_paper_service) call run_scan directly with no check against the in-flight scheduled scan, in a separate process sharing the same SQLite DB. So a manual/paper-service scan can overlap the scheduled execution scan; each loads the open live trade independently and both reach _execute_direct('close', size=full). No per-trade lock exists (Grep of scanner.py and paper_reconcile.py found none).\n\nGhost mechanism is interleaving-robust: with both reduce-only orders requesting the original X, whichever fills the remainder reports filled<X and writes residual = X-filled>0, leaving DB size non-zero while the exchange is flat. The only runtime precondition not provable from code is that the book is thin enough that neither order fully fills X alone (on a deep book the first fills fully and the second is rejected/pending → no ghost) — an edge case consistent with medium. Impact (transient DB ghost, held risk slot, blocked re-entry via unique index, eventually consistent via daemon reconcile) is accurate. Defect is real and reachable; severity medium unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code mechanism verified exactly as described. scanner.py:3464 sets _requested = float(size or 0) from the DB-row size argument (passed in at _kernel_close_live_trade, scanner.py:5896) and is never re-read from the exchange. scanner.py:3465-3466 computes residual = _requested - _closed_filled_f (each closer subtracts its OWN partial fill from the same stale base), writes UPDATE trades SET size=? (3473), marks partial_close, sets result["_close_reconcile_state"]="partial", and returns early (3486-3488). _kernel_close_live_trade (scanner.py:5901-5903) returns on state in ("pending","partial") WITHOUT calling _close_trade_db, so the trade stays OPEN. close_position genuinely returns filled_size (hyperliquid.py:1888,1895), so the partial branch is live code.

Reachability confirmed on a default-ON live path: _live_kernel_execution_enabled() = _scanner_bool_setting("live_kernel_execution", True) (scanner.py:5828; test_live_kernel_execution_is_on_by_default asserts True), wired at scanner.py:6094/6619-6623. There is NO global lock in run_scan (scanner.py:6811) and NO per-trade close lock or DB-status recheck before sending the close (_row is a scan-start snapshot, scanner.py:5889). The scheduler serializes the scheduled scanner_run via a per-job CAS lock (_try_mark_job_running, scheduler.py:893), but other entry points (api_domains/paper.py:2319, control_plane/ops.py:534, scripts/trigger_paper_scan.py, CLI) do NOT share that lock and run run_scan in separate threads of the same process; stale-lock takeover is a second (B-30-mitigated) window. So two overlapping scans can both send a reduce-only close for the same live trade.

Impact correctly sized: a ghost-open trade holds a risk slot and the unique-open index (evidenced by the IntegrityError duplicate-open guard at scanner.py:5874) blocks re-entry until daemon reconcile/ghost-close; eventually consistent with no direct money loss = medium.

Caveat (not refuting): the exact "both partial, leaves OPEN" outcome requires the exchange to split the reduce-only close into two partial fills each < requested (plausible via IOC band exhaustion in a thin/fast market). The common one-full + one-zero ordering would have the full-fill closer call _close_trade_db and close the trade, while the sibling only re-stamps size (does not flip status back to open). That double-partial behavior plus the overlapping-scan requirement gives a low joint likelihood, which is exactly what medium severity reflects. Severity unchanged.

### `FUNDING-LIFECYCLE-FLIP-2` — Partial close folds full-position funding (sinceOpen) onto the residual's smaller margin, overstating funding_pct

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** funding-lifecycle-flip  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:3455-3488, 3735-3739`
- **Claim:** On a partial fill the trade's recorded size is shrunk to the residual (3473) and the close returns before _close_trade_db. On the next scan the residual closes and _close_trade_db reads cumFunding.sinceOpen — which HL accumulates over the WHOLE position life since open (it does NOT reset on a partial reduce) — but divides it by the RESIDUAL margin (size_abs = residual). So funding for the original full notional is expressed as a fraction of the smaller residual margin.
- **Impact:** funding_pct on partially-closed live trades is inflated by roughly original_size/residual_size, distorting the recorded net for those trades. Bounded to partial-fill cases (uncommon on liquid majors) and compounds with the sign bug in FLIP-1.
- **Suggested fix:** Scale folded funding to the residual notional (or capture and fold the funding attributable to each closed slice), or fold funding using the ORIGINAL size captured before the partial-close size mutation. At minimum, persist the original size alongside partial_close_residual and use it for the margin denominator when folding funding.
- **Evidence:** Partial branch shrinks size: scanner.py:3473 `conn.execute("UPDATE trades SET size = ? WHERE id = ?", (residual, str(trade_id)))` and returns at 3488 (no _close_trade_db). On residual close, margin uses the (now residual) size: scanner.py:3735-3736 `size_abs = abs(_coerce_positive_float(trade_row.get("size")) or 0.0); margin = (entry_p * size_abs / leverage)` while funding_usd = full-position sinceOpen.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally does what the claim describes. (1) Partial-fill branch at scanner.py:3465-3473 shrinks the trade row to the residual (`UPDATE trades SET size = ? WHERE id = ?`, residual) and returns at 3486-3488 with `_close_reconcile_state="partial"`; the caller at scanner.py:1222-1244 returns early on this state, so _close_trade_db is NOT invoked at the partial close. (2) Funding is read from HL's `cumFunding.sinceOpen` before every close (scanner.py:3419-3435, line 3430 picks `sinceOpen`). HL exposes both `sinceOpen` and `sinceChange`; `sinceOpen` accumulates over the whole position life and does NOT reset on a partial reduce (only `sinceChange` does) — the code deliberately chose `sinceOpen`, so the HL-behavior premise is well-founded and is the H6 feature's basis. (3) On the residual (final) close, full-life funding flows into _close_trade_db both via the queued path (funding_usd=result['funding_since_open_usd'] at scanner.py:1288) and the fast path (re-read close_funding_usd at scanner.py:3715). _close_trade_db at scanner.py:3735-3739 reads `size_abs = trade_row['size']` — now the shrunken residual — computes `margin = entry_p*size_abs/leverage`, and `funding_pct = funding_usd / margin`, then subtracts it from net_pnl_pct. Thus full-position funding is divided by the smaller residual margin, inflating |funding_pct| by ~original_size/residual_size. No compensating logic exists: partial_close_residual/partial_close_filled (scanner.py:3477-3479) are only written, never read to reconstruct the original notional for the funding denominator. Reachable only for LIVE trades with a partial fill on close (paper has no funding read). Cited lines and evidence quotes are accurate. Severity medium is appropriate: it distorts recorded net_pnl_pct/funding_pct that users and the promotion gate act on, but is bounded to an uncommon edge case (partial fills, rare on liquid majors) and funding magnitudes are typically small basis points, so absolute distortion is modest. I cannot independently confirm HL's runtime sinceOpen behavior from this repo alone, but the documented HL field semantics and the explicit sinceOpen-vs-sinceChange distinction strongly support it; the code-level defect (full-life funding / residual margin) holds regardless of the exact accrual timing.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. On a partial close, scanner.py:3473 shrinks the recorded trade size to the residual and scanner.py:3486-3488 returns "partial"; the main close loop continues at scanner.py:4126-4131 without finalizing. On the next scan the residual fully closes and _close_trade_db is invoked: fast path scanner.py:4140 passes no funding_usd so it falls back to close_funding_usd from signal_data (scanner.py:3713-3717); queued path scanner.py:1282-1289 passes funding_usd=result.funding_since_open_usd. In both cases the funding value is HL cumFunding.sinceOpen, captured and persisted on every close call at scanner.py:3419-3446 — i.e. funding over the WHOLE position life. _close_trade_db then computes margin from the now-shrunk residual size (scanner.py:3735-3736: size_abs=trade_row size; margin=entry_p*size_abs/leverage) and funding_pct=funding_usd/margin (3738), subtracting it from net (3739). So full-position-life funding is divided by the residual margin, overstating funding_pct (and thus net_pnl_pct) by roughly the original/residual notional ratio. Reachability: LIVE ONLY — paper closes short-circuit at scanner.py:3893 and never reach the funding capture, and the fold only fires when close_funding_usd/funding_usd is present, which only the live HL path sets; there is no off-by-default flag suppressing the fold. Both live close sub-paths (fast-path and queued) hit the bug. Trigger is bounded to partial fills on a close (uncommon on liquid majors but real for reduce-only/IOC in thin/fast books). The impact is a corrupted recorded statistic (funding_pct/net_pnl_pct), which feeds promotion scoring and user-visible net, not a direct realized-cash loss — consistent with medium. The only unprovable element is HL's sinceOpen reset semantics, but sinceOpen by definition spans the pre-reduce larger-notional period (only sinceChange resets on a size change per HL docs), so the overstatement is structurally certain. Confirmed, severity unchanged (medium).

## CONFIRMED — LOW (27)

### `PNL-3` — Kelly sizing evidence (_recent_strategy_returns) reads pnl_pct mixing post-size (kernel) and margin (legacy) scales — diverges from the backtest's pre-size gross kelly series

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** pnl  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:631-643 (_recent_strategy_returns); forven/scanner.py:4548-4554 (legacy kelly sizing); forven/strategies/sizing.py:234-235 (kelly uses closed_gross)`
- **Claim:** The legacy open path feeds _recent_strategy_returns (raw closed pnl_pct) as the kelly evidence series, but the backtest/kernel kelly uses PRE-SIZE gross returns (closed_gross appended in execution_kernel.finalize before size-scaling). The recorded pnl_pct is post-size equity-fraction for kernel-closed history and margin-return for legacy history, so neither matches the kernel's pre-size gross — kelly f* computed live can diverge from the validated backtest's, especially on a mixed-path history.
- **Impact:** Kelly-mode strategies on the legacy path (or with mixed history) size off a kelly fraction that does not reproduce the backtest's, breaking the size-parity invariant. Limited to kelly sizing_mode and the legacy path (the kernel paper path rebuilds pre-size closed_gross internally each scan, so it is correct there).
- **Suggested fix:** Persist the kernel's pre-size gross return (already computed as KernelResult.closed_gross) per trade and have _recent_strategy_returns read THAT for kelly evidence, rather than the post-size/margin pnl_pct.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:631 `SELECT pnl_pct FROM trades ...` returned as closed_gross proxy (docstring scanner.py:619-623 'best-effort proxy for the backtest's pre-size gross returns'); execution_kernel.py:112 `closed_gross.append(gross)  # pre-size, for kelly evidence` (gross, BEFORE `pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction`); sizing.py:235 `clamp01(ec["kelly_multiplier"] * kelly_fraction(closed_gross or [], ec["kelly_lookback"]))`. Kernel-closed pnl_pct is post-size (scanner.py:5544), legacy-closed pnl_pct is margin-return (trade_state.py:268).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the described behavior. Legacy kelly open path at scanner.py:4548-4549 feeds `_recent_strategy_returns(strat_id)` as the `closed_gross` kelly evidence into `_sizing.size_fraction` (4551-4553). `_recent_strategy_returns` (scanner.py:631-637) does `SELECT pnl_pct FROM trades WHERE status='CLOSED'` with NO execution_type or close-path filter, so it returns the stored pnl_pct as-is. That stored value is NOT the kernel's pre-size gross: kernel-closed rows store `pnl_pct_net` ("net-of-drag, size-scaled equity impact", scanner.py:5538-5545) = POST-size; legacy-closed rows store `((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage` (trade_state.py:268) = pre-size margin-return but GROSS of drag. The genuine kelly evidence used by both backtest and kernel is `closed_gross.append(gross)` where `gross = ((exit-entry)/entry)*sign*leverage - round_trip_drag`, appended BEFORE `pnl_pct = gross*size_fraction` (execution_kernel.py:111-114; identical backtest.py:6587-6590) = pre-size, NET of drag. So neither stored value reproduces the validated series, and the live kelly fraction can diverge — large divergence on kernel-closed (mixed) history (off by size_fraction, which is <<1 for kelly), smaller divergence on pure-legacy history (off by drag). Impact-scoping confirmed: `_recent_strategy_returns` is called ONLY at scanner.py:4549 (grep-verified); the kernel path's `_size_fraction` closure (execution_kernel.py:177-181) reads the in-loop-rebuilt `closed_gross` (entry at 272) and the backtest rebuilds its own (backtest.py:6563/6575-6579/6588) — both never touch the DB, so both are correct. The legacy path is reached only for non-vectorizable strategies (dispatch scanner.py:6614-6710), a path already flagged "NOT backtest parity," and the kelly output is clamped to [0,1] (sizing.py:235). Real and reachable, but it mis-scales position size on an already-non-parity, kelly-only, non-vectorizable path rather than corrupting fills/PnL — low is correct.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All technical claims verified against live code. (1) The legacy open path feeds kelly evidence from raw DB pnl_pct: scanner.py:4548-4549 sets _closed_gross = _recent_strategy_returns(strat_id) only when sizing_mode=='kelly', and _recent_strategy_returns (scanner.py:631) does `SELECT pnl_pct FROM trades ... status='CLOSED'`. (2) The kernel/backtest kelly uses PRE-SIZE gross: execution_kernel.py:111-112 appends gross = (price_return*sign*leverage - round_trip_drag) BEFORE line 114 pnl_pct = gross*size_fraction, and the kernel feeds its own internally rebuilt closed_gross to sizing (execution_kernel.py:177-180), so the kernel path is self-consistent and correct. (3) Recorded pnl_pct semantics differ from pre-size gross on BOTH stored sources: kernel-closed rows store the post-size net equity fraction (scanner.py:5509 `pnl_pct_net ... # kernel net, equity-fraction`, written at 5544), legacy-closed rows store a leveraged margin return with no drag and no size scaling (trade_state.py:268 `((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage`). Neither equals the kernel's pre-size gross (leveraged return minus drag). The mixing is real because scanner.py:631 reads all closed rows regardless of close path. (4) sizing.py:235 consumes closed_gross via kelly_fraction. REACHABILITY: kelly is a genuine selectable profile (execution_selection.py:98-101, include_kelly default True). The kernel flags default ON (paper_kernel_execution True scanner.py:5222; live_kernel_execution True scanner.py:5828), so vectorizable strategies take the correct kernel path. But the legacy path at scanner.py:4548 is still reachable with DEFAULT flags for non-vectorizable strategies (run_strategy_execution returns None -> legacy fallback, _paper_legacy_fallback_enabled default True at scanner.py:5239), and whenever an operator disables the kernel flags. So the defect is real and production-reachable but doubly-conditioned: kelly mode AND legacy path. IMPACT: bounded — kelly_fraction is clamp01(...), so it shifts the f* estimate rather than causing unbounded oversize; affects only kelly-mode legacy-path strategies, which (being non-vectorizable) already cannot perfectly reproduce a kernel backtest. The finding's own scope statement (kernel path is correct, limited to kelly+legacy) is accurate. Severity low is defensible and conservative (borderline low/medium); keeping unchanged.

### `SIZE-3` — Backfill open path resolves leverage from `params['leverage']` directly instead of `resolve_leverage`, so recorded units use 1x when operator default_leverage != 1

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** size  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5589`
- **Claim:** In `_kernel_close_paper_trade`'s backfill branch (a trade the kernel opened AND closed between scans), leverage is read as a bare param with a 1.0 default, bypassing the shared `resolve_leverage` used everywhere else, so the recorded `units`/`size` diverge when the strategy declares no leverage and the operator set a non-1 default_leverage.
- **Impact:** Cosmetic/state only: backfilled trades are immediately closed and their PnL is taken from the kernel's `pnl_pct_net` (which used the correct replay leverage), and equity is summed from `pnl_usd`, not units — so only the stored `size` field is wrong. No PnL/equity corruption. Could mislead a units-based reconciliation/exposure readout for those rows.
- **Suggested fix:** Use `_bt.resolve_leverage(strat.get('params') or {})` in the backfill branch (scanner.py:5589) so every path resolves leverage identically.
- **Evidence:** `leverage = float((strat.get("params") or {}).get("leverage", 1.0) or 1.0)` (scanner.py:5589), whereas the live scan path uses `leverage = _bt.resolve_leverage(p)` (scanner.py:5985) which falls back to `resolve_default_leverage` (backtest.py:7615-7628 / 7598-7613). For a profile-less strategy with operator default_leverage=3, this backfill computes units at 1x.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified. scanner.py:5589 in the backfill branch of _kernel_close_paper_trade reads leverage as `float((strat.get("params") or {}).get("leverage", 1.0) or 1.0)` — a bare param read defaulting to 1.0, bypassing the shared resolver. The normal scan path at scanner.py:5985 uses `_bt.resolve_leverage(p)`, which (backtest.py:7615-7628) falls back to resolve_default_leverage (7598-7612) reading the operator default_leverage. Units scale linearly with leverage: sizing.py:290 `units = (eq * lev * sf) / px`, so a profile-less strategy with default_leverage=3 records 1x units in backfill vs 3x everywhere else. Reachability is genuine: the main dispatcher passes the resolved leverage to the OPEN path (scanner.py:6142) but calls close_applier WITHOUT leverage (6144-6145), forcing _kernel_close_paper_trade to re-derive it locally with the wrong fallback (5589) before calling _kernel_open_paper_trade(... leverage=leverage) (5596). The leverage flows into position_units (5454-5457) and the stored units/leverage column/sizing dict (5491-5493). Impact analysis holds: _kernel_close_recorded (5504-5552) overwrites pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd with the kernel's pnl_pct_net (5509) and equity_at_entry*pnl_pct_net (5511), values produced by run_strategy_execution at 6005-6010 driven by the CORRECT leverage from 5985; paper equity sums pnl_usd, not units. So only the stored size/units/leverage of these immediately-closed paper-only (execution_type="paper") backfill rows diverge — no PnL or equity corruption. Severity low is accurate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-verified. scanner.py:5589 in `_kernel_close_paper_trade`'s backfill branch reads `leverage = float((strat.get("params") or {}).get("leverage", 1.0) or 1.0)`, bypassing the shared resolver, while the main scan path (scanner.py:5985) uses `_bt.resolve_leverage(p)`, which falls back to the operator `default_leverage` (backtest.py:7615-7628 -> 7598-7613). So when a strategy declares no `params['leverage']` and the operator set `default_leverage != 1` (default is 1.0 at api_core.py:1699, but operator-configurable to e.g. 3.0/2.5 per api_core.py:2890-2892 and test_default_leverage_parity.py), the backfill passes leverage=1.0 to `_kernel_open_paper_trade`. That value feeds `units = position_units(equity, size_fraction, leverage, entry_price)` (scanner.py:5454-5457) and the stored `leverage` DB column / signal_data (scanner.py:5488, 5491-5493), so the recorded `size`/`units`/`leverage` are wrong (1x) on these backfilled rows.

Impact is correctly characterized as low/state-only. The backfilled trade's PnL is taken from the kernel's net `pnl_pct` (scanner.py:5509-5511, 5542-5551), which the replay computed with the correctly-resolved leverage at scanner.py:6005-6006, so PnL is right. Paper equity sums `pnl_usd`, not units (`_get_paper_strategy_equity`, scanner.py:604), so equity is right. The open and close happen synchronously within the same function call (no scan boundary), so the mis-sized `units` is never seen as a live open position for exposure. Only the stored `size`/`leverage` fields on already-closed rows diverge — no money/equity corruption.

Reachability: backfill (open+close within one scan interval) is genuinely reachable, but the divergence is gated on the operator explicitly setting default_leverage != 1 for an undeclared-leverage strategy. Real, reachable, cosmetic — confirmed at low. Suggested fix (use `_bt.resolve_leverage(p)` at scanner.py:5589) is correct.

### `KERNEL-1` — Trailing-stop peak (`extreme`) excludes the entry bar's own high/low → trailing stop under-ratchets by one bar

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kernel  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:276 (init), :247-249 (update)`
- **Claim:** The trailing-stop ratchet never folds the ENTRY bar's high (long) / low (short) into the running peak, so the trailing level is computed from a peak that is one bar stale at the start of every trade, making the trailing stop slightly looser than a true trailing stop.
- **Impact:** A trailing stop triggers slightly later/looser than intended, giving back marginally more profit. Identical in backtest and scanner (parity holds), so it is a modeling looseness, not a parity break.
- **Suggested fix:** On entry, seed extreme to the entry bar's high (long) / low (short) — i.e., fold the entry bar's range into the peak — or document that entry-bar excursion is intentionally excluded.
- **Evidence:** At entry the peak is seeded to the fill price only: line 276 `"extreme": fill_price,`. The position dict is created in step (2) which runs AFTER step (1) for the same bar, so the entry bar's own range is never seen by the extreme-update, which only runs on LATER bars and only when the trade survives: lines 247-249 `elif at.get("trail_pct"):  at["extreme"] = max(at["extreme"], bar_high) if direction == "long" else min(at["extreme"], bar_low)`. The trailing level at line 220 `trail_level = at["extreme"] * (1.0 - sign * at["trail_pct"])` therefore ignores any favourable excursion during the entry bar — contradicting the code's own comment ('the trailing level uses the peak through the PRIOR bar').
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the defect. In forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py the per-bar loop (line 183) executes step (1) intrabar exit checks (lines 193-249) BEFORE step (2) entries (lines 252-277) for the same idx. On the entry bar, step (1) hits line 194-196 `if at is None: continue` (no position yet), so no trailing logic runs; step (2) then creates the position with `"extreme": fill_price` (line 276) — seeded to the entry bar's OPEN, never its high/low. The only ratchet of `extreme` is the `elif at.get("trail_pct")` branch at lines 247-249, which by loop structure runs only on bars where the position already existed at the top of step (1), i.e. strictly after the entry bar (the docstring lines 154-156 confirm: "a position entered on bar i is first stop-checked on bar i+1"). Therefore the entry bar's own high/low is never folded into the peak, and on bar entry_bar+1 the trail level at line 220 `at["extreme"] * (1.0 - sign * at["trail_pct"])` is computed from entry-open instead of max(entry-open, entry-bar-high), producing a looser stop for a long (lower trail_level) / short. This contradicts the code's own comment at lines 215-217 stating the trail level uses "the peak through the PRIOR bar." Net: every bar's range is folded into the peak EXCEPT the entry bar's — a genuine under-ratchet asymmetry. Impact is correctly characterized as minor: eff_stop = max(stop_price, trail_level) (line 224) means the fixed stop usually dominates early, so the exclusion only bites in an entry-bar-spike-then-decline scenario; give-back is marginal. Identical in backtest and scanner (shared kernel), so parity holds — modeling looseness, not a parity break. Low severity is correct. Minor nit: the finding's "one bar stale" wording understates it slightly (the entry bar is excluded permanently from the peak, not merely lagged by one bar), but this does not change the verdict or severity.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanics verified against live code. execution_kernel.py:276 seeds "extreme": fill_price (= opens[idx], the entry-bar OPEN, per line 186). Entry creation is loop step (2) (lines 251-277) which runs AFTER the exit/ratchet step (1) on the same bar idx, so the entry bar's own high/low is never folded into extreme on the entry bar. On bar idx+1 the trail level at line 220 (at["extreme"] * (1 - sign*trail_pct)) is computed from the seeded entry-open, and only AFTER the breach check does line 249 ratchet with highs[idx+1]/lows[idx+1]. The entry bar's high highs[idx] is therefore permanently excluded from the running peak; the trailing level is one favorable-excursion looser at trade start, and stays looser for the whole trade in the case where highs[idx] is the trade's global peak. Parity holds: the legacy backtest path is identical (backtest.py:6709 seeds "extreme": fill_price; :6682 ratchets the same way), so backtest == paper == live — a uniform modeling looseness, not a parity break, exactly as the finding states. Reachability: trailing_stop_pct is NOT produced by the auto execution-profile sweep (candidate_profiles in execution_selection.py:50-105 never emits it), so it is never auto-selected; but it IS reachable in production via strategy params (mapped at backtest.py:616), the lab execution-settings editor, the manual-backtest API, and the operator paper-control adjust path. paper_control.py:943-944 applies a trailing stop and :905 shows that path covers BOTH paper and live trades, so the defect is real on paper and live whenever a trailing stop is configured. Impact is bounded to the single entry-bar excursion and is symmetric across all engines, costing only marginal given-back profit — not silent money loss or state corruption. Low severity is appropriate.

### `KERNEL-2` — Stop/TP placed at entry cannot fire on the entry bar — intrabar exits are deferred a full bar and may fill at a gapped price

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kernel  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:192-249 (step 1) vs :251-277 (step 2)`
- **Claim:** Because exits (step 1) are evaluated before entries (step 2) within a bar, a position opened at bar i is first exit-checked at bar i+1. A stop or take-profit that price reaches intrabar DURING the entry bar is never honored; the check is deferred to the next bar, where a gap can fill it materially worse (or the level may be skipped entirely if price recovers).
- **Impact:** For a long entered at 100 with a 95 stop, if bar i dips to 90 intrabar the kernel does not exit at ~95; on bar i+1 a gap-down open (e.g. 91) fills the deferred stop at 91 via `min(fill_price, eff_stop)` (line 227) — a larger loss than the intended stop. The effect is symmetric (a recovery can avoid the stop entirely) and identical across backtest/scanner, so it is an intentional 'unknown intrabar path' modeling choice, but on high timeframes one bar is a large move.
- **Suggested fix:** Keep as-is but document the entry-bar-exit exclusion explicitly as a known limitation; optionally offer a conservative entry-bar stop check (stop only, pessimistic) for tight-stop strategies.
- **Evidence:** Step 1 (`for direction in allowed_modes: at = active_trades.get(direction); if at is None: continue`, lines 193-195) runs before the entry that creates the trade in step 2 (`active_trades[direction] = {...}`, lines 267-277). So on the entry bar `at is None` and no stop/TP check occurs against `highs[idx]`/`lows[idx]` for the just-opened position.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The code literally does what the finding claims. In execution_kernel.py the per-bar loop (line 183) runs Step 1 exit checks (lines 192-249) on positions already in active_trades, then Step 2 entries (lines 251-277) which set active_trades[direction] = {"entry_bar": idx, ...} (lines 267-277). Because Step 2 runs after Step 1 in the same iteration, a position opened at bar idx is first visible to Step 1 at iteration idx+1 and checked against highs[idx+1]/lows[idx+1]; the entry bar's own high/low (highs[idx]/lows[idx], lines 189-190) are never tested against the just-opened position's stop/TP. On the entry bar, at = active_trades.get(direction) is None for that direction so line 195-196 continues past it. The deferred-fill impact is accurate: a gap-through fills the long stop at min(fill_price, eff_stop) (line 227; line 230 symmetric for shorts), so an idx+1 gap-down open of 91 against a 95 stop fills at 91, worse than intended; the recovery-avoids-stop case is also real. Cited line ranges (193-195, 267-277, 227) all match. The docstring (lines 154-156) explicitly documents this as intentional ("a position entered on bar i is first stop-checked on bar i+1"). Severity low is correct and unchanged: the behavior is produced by the SAME shared kernel for backtest and scanner/paper/live, so it does not create a parity break, does not differentially lose money, and does not corrupt state — it is a standard, symmetric, documented intrabar-path modeling limitation. No other per-bar path (force_close at line 283+ is end-of-data only) checks the entry bar.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The kernel behavior is exactly as described. In execution_kernel.py:simulate the per-bar loop runs step 1 (exit checks) at lines 192-249 BEFORE step 2 (entries) at lines 251-277. Step 1 begins with `at = active_trades.get(direction); if at is None: continue` (193-195) and tests `bar_high = highs[idx]` / `bar_low = lows[idx]` (189-190) against the stop/TP. Step 2 then creates the position with `entry_bar: idx, entry_price: fill_price` (267-277). Because the trade does not exist yet when step 1 runs on bar idx, the just-opened position is never exit-checked against bar idx's own high/low; its first exit check is at idx+1. The gap-fill example is accurate: line 227 `exit_price = min(fill_price, eff_stop)` fills a deferred long stop at the (worse) next-bar open when it gaps below the stop. Reachable on every trade. It is identical across backtest (backtest.py:7212 simulate) and the paper scanner (run_strategy_execution → simulate, scanner.py:5196), confirming there is NO backtest↔paper parity break — the backtest metrics users act on already embody this same modeling, so it does not mislead. The effect is genuinely symmetric (an intrabar whipsaw to the stop that recovers by the next bar is also ignored, sparing the user a stop-out), which is the standard 'unknown intrabar path' approximation. Real-money (live) impact is further bounded BELOW the finding's framing: the live path places a REAL reduce-only protective stop on the exchange at entry (scanner.py:3336-3337 'refusing to open ... without a protective stop'; 3357-3369 market_order with stop_loss_price/take_profit_price), so a live stop fires intrabar at the venue on the entry bar — the deferred worse-gap-fill loss the finding warns about is a paper/backtest modeling artifact, not a live loss. Defect is real and reachable, correctly self-classified as a low-severity intentional modeling limitation rather than a money-losing parity bug; LOW is appropriate.

### `KERNEL-3` — No finite/NaN guard on OHLC: a NaN `open` evades the `fill_price <= 0` skip and produces a NaN-PnL trade

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kernel  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:186-188, :107-114`
- **Claim:** The only bad-bar guard is `if fill_price <= 0: continue`. A NaN open satisfies neither `<= 0` nor the `entry_price <= 0` guard in finalize (NaN comparisons are False), so a NaN bar is processed and, with a signal/time-stop exit, finalize records a trade with `pnl_pct = NaN`, and an entry stores a NaN `entry_price`.
- **Impact:** A single NaN bar would corrupt the recorded trade's PnL and (in the scanner) the closed trade's equity impact. Reachability is LOW on the normal path because the data loaders drop NaN OHLC (forven/data.py:358 and forven/market_data.py:112,324 `dropna(subset=[...open/high/low/close...])`), but the shared kernel relies on every caller pre-cleaning, which is fragile.
- **Suggested fix:** Guard with finiteness: `if not math.isfinite(fill_price) or fill_price <= 0: continue`, and add `if not math.isfinite(entry_price) or entry_price <= 0: return` in finalize; optionally skip bars where high/low are non-finite.
- **Evidence:** Line 186-188: `fill_price = float(opens[idx]); if fill_price <= 0: continue` — `float('nan') <= 0` is `False`, so the bar is NOT skipped. finalize line 107-109: `entry_price = float(at["entry_price"]); if entry_price <= 0: return` — again `nan <= 0` is `False`, so a NaN entry price flows into `gross = ((exit_price - entry_price) / entry_price) * sign * leverage - round_trip_drag` (line 111) → NaN `pnl_pct` (line 114).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The code literally exhibits the defect as described. execution_kernel.py:186-188 has only `fill_price = float(opens[idx]); if fill_price <= 0: continue`; I confirmed empirically that `float('nan') <= 0` is False, so a NaN open bar is NOT skipped. The entry at line 269 stores `"entry_price": fill_price`, persisting a NaN. In finalize, lines 107-109 (`entry_price = float(at["entry_price"]); if entry_price <= 0: return`) also fail to catch NaN, and line 111 (`gross = ((exit_price - entry_price)/entry_price)*sign*leverage - round_trip_drag`) plus line 114 (`pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction`) produce NaN, recorded at line 122. There is NO finiteness guard anywhere in the module — grep for isfinite/isnan/math./np.isnan returned zero matches and the file never imports math, so no later line negates the issue and the cited line numbers are exact. Reachability is correctly characterized as LOW: I verified the loaders drop NaN OHLC at data.py:358, market_data.py:112, and market_data.py:324, so a NaN bar is removed on the normal path; the kernel itself is simply non-defensive and relies on every caller pre-cleaning. The defect is real, line references are exact, and the severity (low) is self-consistent with the acknowledged low reachability — this is a legitimate defensive-coding/robustness gap, not an actively-firing money bug under normal operation.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code mechanism verified exactly. execution_kernel.py:186-188 is `fill_price = float(opens[idx]); if fill_price <= 0: continue` — `float('nan') <= 0` is False (IEEE/Python semantics), so a NaN open is NOT skipped; the bar then stores `entry_price=fill_price` (NaN) at line 269 and, on a signal/time-stop exit (lines 203/212 set exit_price=fill_price), reaches finalize. finalize at :107-109 `entry_price = float(at["entry_price"]); if entry_price <= 0: return` likewise does not catch NaN, so line 111 gross = ((exit_price-entry_price)/entry_price)*sign*lev - drag → NaN and line 114 pnl_pct → NaN, and a trade is appended. Grep confirms the kernel has zero isfinite/isnan/notna guards (only an ATR fillna at :56). The finding's quotes/line numbers are accurate. Reachability is correctly rated LOW: run_strategy_execution does NOT dropna OHLC (backtest.py:7199 `d = df.copy()`; the backtest fast-path entry at :10743 passes raw df, with the OHLC dropna at :10837 only on the unused slow-path), so the kernel relies on upstream cleaning — but every production caller strips NaN OHLC: scanner fetch_candles uses clean=True and the cache path ohlcv_rows_to_dataframe (market_data.py:324) + the clean path (market_data.py:112) both dropna OHLC; backtest loads via load_parquet → _normalize_ohlcv_frame dropna (data.py:358); the vectorized path dropna's at backtest.py:7354. Enrichment adds only supplementary columns and never nulls OHLC. So a NaN open does not reach the kernel on any current path. This is a real latent/defensive gap accurately described (including its honest low-reachability caveat); it cannot currently lose money or corrupt state, so severity low is correct.

### `KERNEL-5` — Same-bar close-and-reopen feeds the just-closed trade's gross into the new trade's kelly evidence (1-trade lookahead)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kernel  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:243-246 (step 1 append) vs :251-272 (step 2 read)`
- **Claim:** Within one bar, a trade that closes (step 1) appends its gross to `closed_gross` BEFORE a new same-direction entry on the same bar (step 2) reads `closed_gross` for kelly sizing. If the closing trade exited via an INTRABAR stop/target (not at the open), its result was not yet known at the bar's open when the new trade fills, so the new trade's kelly size uses one bar of lookahead.
- **Impact:** Kelly-only, bounded to one trade of evidence, and identical across backtest/scanner (parity holds). Slightly biases kelly sizing on same-bar flips.
- **Suggested fix:** If strict no-lookahead for kelly is desired, snapshot `closed_gross` length at the start of each bar and size step-2 entries off the pre-bar evidence; otherwise document as accepted.
- **Evidence:** finalize appends in step 1: line 112 `closed_gross.append(gross)` (called at line 244). Step 2 entry then reads the same list via `_size_fraction(stop_dist_pct)` (line 272) → `closed_gross=closed_gross` (line 180). With a single direction, step 1 can null the active trade (line 246) and step 2 reopens on the same bar if `entry_series.iloc[signal_idx]` is set.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the described mechanism. In execution_kernel.py, step 1 (lines 192-249) closes an already-open position; when exit_price is set it calls finalize at line 244, which appends the trade's gross to closed_gross at line 112, then nulls the slot at line 246. Step 2 (lines 251-277) is a fully-subsequent loop whose guard at line 254 (active_trades.get(direction) is not None) now passes, so a pending entry signal from signal_idx=idx-1 reopens at fill_price=opens[idx] with size_fraction=_size_fraction(stop_dist_pct) (line 272), which forwards closed_gross=closed_gross (line 180). Only kelly reads closed_gross (sizing.py:234-235 kelly_fraction(closed_gross...)); full/fixed/fraction/atr ignore it, so the kelly-only scope is correct. The lookahead is genuine: stop_loss/trailing_stop (lines 226-231) and take_profit (lines 238-241) are INTRABAR exits (triggered on the bar's high/low, exit_price=min/max(fill_price,eff_stop) or tp), realized after the open, yet their gross is already in closed_gross when the same-bar reopen — which fills at the open (the first tick) — computes its kelly size. So the new trade's evidence includes a result that, in time order, occurred after its own entry: a 1-trade ordering inversion. time_stop (line 203) and signal (line 212) exit at the open and would not constitute lookahead, consistent with the claim's qualifier. Reachable: needs a position open into bar idx that exits intrabar on bar idx, a stale entry signal at idx-1, and sizing_mode==kelly; no guard prevents same-bar reopen (step 1 fully precedes step 2, so closed_gross is updated before any step-2 sizing read). Parity holds because both backtest and scanner run the identical simulate. All cited lines (112, 180, 244, 246, 272) are exact. Severity low is appropriate: bounded to one trade of evidence, kelly-only, parity-preserving — a subtle sizing bias, not a silent money-loser or state corruptor.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The mechanism is fully verifiable in the live code. Step 1: at execution_kernel.py:243-246, an exit calls finalize() which appends the trade's gross to closed_gross (line 112) and then nulls active_trades[direction] (line 246). The stop_loss/trailing_stop (lines 226-231) and take_profit (lines 238-241) exits are intrabar (fill at the stop/target level), so their result is NOT known at the bar's open. Step 2: lines 252-272 reopen a position when active_trades.get(direction) is None and entry_series.iloc[signal_idx] is True, sizing via _size_fraction(stop_dist_pct) (line 272) -> _sizing.size_fraction(..., closed_gross=closed_gross) (line 180), and for kelly mode sizing.py:235 reads closed_gross via kelly_fraction(). The new trade nominally fills at opens[idx] (line 269), which precedes the intrabar exit, so its kelly evidence includes a trade whose outcome was not yet known at fill -> one-trade lookahead. Confirmed.\n\nReachability: kelly IS a production-selectable profile. execution_selection.py:98-101 emits kelly candidates by default (include_kelly=True), and select_execution_profile can pick a kelly profile (only zero-evidence degenerate kelly is excluded, line 276). Once chosen it is frozen into params and used in paper AND live.\n\nParity: backtest.py:6743 and 7212 both call _kernel.simulate, the same function the scanner advances; closed_gross is rebuilt within each simulate() call (line 165), so the append-then-read sequence is reproduced identically in backtest and live. Therefore this does NOT cause a backtest-vs-live divergence.\n\nImpact is correctly sized as low: kelly-only, bounded to one trade of evidence within kelly_lookback (default 100, ~1% perturbation), requires the edge case of a same-bar intrabar close coinciding with a persistent entry signal, and does not directly lose money or break parity. A defensible counter-view also exists (in single-side mode the new position cannot physically exist until the old one closes, making the old result legitimately knowable), which further limits the harm. Severity low stands.

### `KCOPY-4` — Per-bar signals cache key omits the asset/symbol and any content hash (latent cross-asset / data-revision collision)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kcopy  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:6993`
- **Claim:** The adapter signal cache is keyed only by (strategy_id, truncated params signature, mode, n, warmup, first_ts, last_ts). Two different price series sharing the same strategy_id and an identical index shape (same n and endpoints — e.g. two assets on the same 1h grid, or a mid-window data revision that preserves endpoints) would collide and return the wrong/stale signals.
- **Impact:** Currently not reachable in production: in the long-lived daemon strategy_id is unique per asset, and backtests run in per-strategy child processes (fresh module-global cache), so no same-process same-sid multi-asset run occurs. It is a defense-in-depth gap that would silently corrupt signals if a future flow backtests one strategy_id across multiple assets in one process, or if data is revised in place.
- **Suggested fix:** Fold the asset/symbol and a cheap content fingerprint (e.g. hash of close[::k] or len+first/last close) into the cache key.
- **Evidence:** `cache_key = (sid, _per_bar_params_signature(strategy_obj), mode, n, int(warmup), str(idx[0]), str(idx[-1]))` (6993) — no asset/symbol and no hash of the OHLCV values. The docstring asserts prefix-stability but the key cannot detect differing bar CONTENT under matching endpoints.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified. At forven/strategies/backtest.py:6993 the key is literally `cache_key = (sid, _per_bar_params_signature(strategy_obj), mode, n, int(warmup), str(idx[0]), str(idx[-1]))` — it contains no asset/symbol and no fingerprint of the OHLCV values, exactly as claimed. The cache is a process-global OrderedDict (backtest.py:6779, `_PER_BAR_SIGNALS_CACHE = _OrderedDict()`), so two lookups with identical (sid, params-sig, mode, n, warmup, first_ts, last_ts) return the same cached DirectionalSignals regardless of differing bar CONTENT under matching endpoints. `_per_bar_params_signature` (6783-6791) is `repr(sorted(...))[:300]` — truncated params, no content hash — so it cannot detect differing values either. The docstring (6938-6942) asserts prefix/trailing-window stability but says nothing that would prevent a content/asset collision.\n\nThe finding correctly self-scopes this as low severity / not currently reachable, and my trace supports that: (1) daemon in-process path (scanner.py:6005) keys on the per-strategy strat_id, and each strategy row binds a single asset, so the same strategy_id is not run against two assets in one process → sid discriminates; (2) the isolated path constructs `cls(\"isolated\", ...)` in a one-shot subprocess per request (sandbox/strategy_worker.py:137) with a fresh module-global cache, so no same-process multi-asset run. The collision is only reachable via a future flow that backtests one strategy_id across multiple assets in a single long-lived process, or an in-place data revision that preserves both n and the first/last timestamps — a real but currently-unexercised defense-in-depth gap. Confirmed as a latent correctness gap at the stated low severity; suggested fix (fold asset/symbol + a cheap close-fingerprint into the key) is appropriate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code claim verified verbatim at backtest.py:6993 — `cache_key = (sid, _per_bar_params_signature(strategy_obj), mode, n, int(warmup), str(idx[0]), str(idx[-1]))`, with no asset/symbol and no OHLCV content hash. `_per_bar_params_signature` (6783-6791) fingerprints only `strategy_obj.params`, never the price data, and `_PER_BAR_SIGNALS_CACHE` (6779) is a process-lifetime module-global LRU. So two series sharing the same sid + identical params + identical (mode, n, warmup, first_ts, last_ts) but different bar CONTENT would collide and return stale signals — the mechanism is real.

Reachability matches the finding's own LOW / 'not reachable in default production' assessment: the default path is in-process at 7171 (the worker is gated by `_isolated_strategy_exec_enabled()`, which defaults OFF at 7088), and there `sid` is the real strategy_id (6967). In the daemon, manage_positions_via_kernel binds each strat_id to a single `asset` (scanner.py:5951) and fetches that asset's candles, so sid is unique per asset and cross-asset collision cannot occur; the trailing window also shifts endpoints as bars close, so the data-revision case needs an in-place rewrite of a CLOSED bar preserving endpoints — not realistic.

One correction to the finding's rationale (does not change the verdict): its claim that 'backtests run in per-strategy child processes (fresh module-global cache)' is imprecise. The isolated worker is a reused module-global singleton (strategy_worker.py:348-368) and inside it sid is hardcoded 'isolated' (137), so the same cache at 6993 runs there shared across all isolated strategies — a genuine shared-process/shared-sid/multi-asset path where two same-type, same-params custom per-bar strategies on same-grid assets WOULD collide and produce wrong trades. But that path is behind the same default-OFF `isolated_strategy_exec` flag and only fires for custom strategies, so the real-world severity stays LOW. Confirmed as a real low-severity latent defense-in-depth gap; suggested fix (fold asset + a cheap close-fingerprint into the key) is appropriate.

### `KCOPY-5` — Params signature truncated to 300 chars in both the signal cache and purity cache keys (stale-signal collision for many-param strategies)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kcopy  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:6789 (truncation), used at 6919 (purity cache) and 6993 (signals cache)`
- **Claim:** `repr(sorted((str(k),str(v)) for k,v in params.items()))[:300]` truncates the signature at 300 chars. Two distinct param sets that share the same first 300 chars (e.g. a strategy with >~15 params where the swept key sorts after the cutoff) map to the same signature and would reuse another param set's cached signals / purity verdict.
- **Impact:** Neutralized today: the optimizer assigns a UNIQUE strategy_id per trial (`strategy_id=f"{strategy_id}-opt-{i}"`, optimizer.py:507) so sid differs even when the truncated params match, and backtests are per-process. Residual risk only if a long-lived process re-instantiates the same strategy_id with edited (>300-char) params. Latent.
- **Suggested fix:** Hash the full sorted params (e.g. blake2b of the repr) instead of truncating, so distinct param sets never collide.
- **Evidence:** `return repr(sorted((str(k), str(v)) for k, v in params.items()))[:300]` (6789).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited code verified verbatim. backtest.py:6789 truncates the params signature: `return repr(sorted((str(k), str(v)) for k, v in params.items()))[:300]`.
