It is used in the purity cache key at 6919 (`key = (sid, _per_bar_params_signature(strategy_obj))`) and the signals cache key at 6993 (`(sid, _per_bar_params_signature(...), mode, n, int(warmup), str(idx[0]), str(idx[-1]))`). Two distinct param sets sharing the same first 300 chars produce identical signatures, so the truncation-collision mechanism is real. It is genuinely latent (not impossible): params carries a nested `execution_profile` dict (sizing.py:98-118), whose `str(v)` repr alone is long, so a many-param strategy's signature readily exceeds 300 chars. The claim's mitigation is accurate and verified — optimizer.py:507 assigns a unique `strategy_id=f"{strategy_id}-opt-{i}"` per trial, so the composite `sid` differs and the truncated-sig collision cannot reuse another trial's cache entry. Residual risk is correctly characterized as latent: a long-lived process re-instantiating the SAME strategy_id with edited >300-char same-prefix params. Realistic impact is at or below the stated low severity — the signals cache additionally keys on frame identity (n, idx[-1]) which changes every scanner bar, preventing bar-to-bar stale-signal collisions, and the purity cache reuse is benign because purity is a property of the generate_signal function rather than param values. The auditor's honest low/latent assessment holds; severity unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanism verified in live code. backtest.py:6789 truncates the params signature at 300 chars: `return repr(sorted((str(k), str(v)) for k, v in params.items()))[:300]`. It is used as a cache-key component at both cited sites: purity cache key `(sid, _per_bar_params_signature(strategy_obj))` (6919) and signals cache key `(sid, _per_bar_params_signature(...), mode, n, int(warmup), str(idx[0]), str(idx[-1]))` (6993). So two param sets sharing the first 300 sorted-repr chars under the same strategy_id genuinely collide. The truncation precondition is in fact easier to hit than the finding claims: params carry a nested `params['execution_profile']` dict (backtest.py:6381-6394) whose `str(v)` serializes the entire sub-dict into one long value, so even a modest-param strategy that carries an execution_profile can exceed 300 chars.\n\nNeutralization confirmed and correctly sized as LOW: optimizer.py:507 sets `strategy_id=f\"{strategy_id}-opt-{i}\"`, giving every trial a unique sid; since sid is the leading element of both cache keys, distinct trial params never collide despite truncation. (Note the optimizer actually runs backtest_strategy in-process at 506, so the module-level _PER_BAR_*_CACHE persist across trials — the finding's incidental \"backtests are per-process\" wording is imprecise — but the unique-sid guard makes that immaterial.)\n\nResidual risk is narrow but real, matching the finding's \"latent\" framing: a collision needs the SAME sid re-instantiated with different params whose changed key sorts past char 300, and for the signals cache an identical frame (mode,n,warmup,idx endpoints). In the live scanner/daemon the frame advances every bar so n/idx change, making the signals-cache collision effectively unreachable there; only the purity cache (keyed solely sid+signature, no frame) can go stale, and a param edit rarely flips determinism — minimal impact. The one money-relevant reachable case is a manual re-run of the same built-in strategy_id with an edited beyond-cutoff param on the exact same backtest frame inside the long-lived single-worker backend, which would return another param set's cached signals and thus wrong metrics. Real but rare. Defect confirmed; LOW severity is appropriate and the cheap full-hash fix (blake2b of the repr) is the right remedy.

### `KCOPY-6` — EC-resolution drift between the two kernel entry points: _run_directional_signal_series ignores the persisted execution_profile, run_strategy_execution honors it

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** kcopy  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:6444-6452 vs 7204-7210`
- **Claim:** When no explicit execution_controls are passed, run_strategy_execution falls back to the strategy's persisted execution_profile (execution_controls_from_params(params)) before defaulting; _run_directional_signal_series falls straight to default_controls() and never reads the profile.
- **Impact:** If a profiled strategy ever reaches the _run_signal_backtest→_run_directional_signal_series path with execution_controls=None, its stops/sizing would silently drop to the 1% atr default instead of its profile. Largely unreachable because run_strategy_execution is tried first and builtins expose generate_signals (so they don't fall through), and the scanner passes the profile explicitly. Inconsistent fallback nonetheless.
- **Suggested fix:** Make _run_directional_signal_series resolve execution_controls_from_params(params) in its None branch too, or route it through run_strategy_execution's resolution, so both entry points pick the same ec for profiled strategies.
- **Evidence:** run_strategy_execution: `ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls); if ec is None: ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls_from_params(params)) or _sizing.default_controls()` (7204-7210). _run_directional_signal_series: `ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls); if ec is None: ec = _sizing.default_controls()` (6444-6452) — no profile read.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified at both cited locations. _run_directional_signal_series (backtest.py:6444-6452) resolves `ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls); if ec is None: ec = _sizing.default_controls()` with NO read of the persisted profile (and its signature, 6414-6426, doesn't even receive `params`). run_strategy_execution (backtest.py:7204-7210) instead does `if ec is None: ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls_from_params(params)) or _sizing.default_controls()`, honoring the profile. The divergence is literal and exactly as claimed. Reachability confirmed in a narrow corner: backtest_strategy threads its raw execution_controls param (default None) down through _isolated_backtest_worker -> _run_signal_walk (8367/8434) WITHOUT resolving execution_controls_from_params first, so None is the normal value reaching the fallback. _run_signal_walk tries run_strategy_execution first (10743) and only falls to _run_vectorized_backtest -> _run_signal_backtest -> _run_directional_signal_series (10770/7294) when run_strategy_execution returns None. That happens for a vectorizable builtin whose _resolve_worker_strategy_class returns None (strategy_obj stays None; docstring 271-272 notes some 'pure checker/vectorized types' have no class, and worker guard 318 allows continuing since family in _VECTORIZABLE_TYPES) and which exposes no per-bar checker (_signals_from_per_bar returns None at 6963-6965). In that case a profiled strategy with execution_controls=None silently drops to the atr default (sizing.py:255-256 confirms default_controls() is sizing_mode='atr' at 1% risk, matching the impact's '1% atr default'), while the scanner honors the profile — a genuine but narrow parity break. Matches the LOW 'largely unreachable but inconsistent' framing. Minor caveat: the suggested fix can't be applied literally to _run_directional_signal_series/_run_signal_backtest (neither receives params); it must go in _run_vectorized_backtest, which does carry params. Severity low is appropriate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code claim verified exactly. _run_directional_signal_series (backtest.py:6444-6452) does `ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls); if ec is None: ec = _sizing.default_controls()` with NO profile read, while run_strategy_execution (backtest.py:7204-7210) does `ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls); if ec is None: ec = _normalize_execution_controls(execution_controls_from_params(params)) or _sizing.default_controls()`. The divergent None-branch is real and as described. Reachability is correctly characterized as largely unreachable: _run_directional_signal_series has a single caller chain (_run_signal_backtest@7294 <- _run_vectorized_backtest@7407 <- _run_signal_walk@10770), and that fallback only fires AFTER run_strategy_execution returns None AND strategy_type in _VECTORIZABLE_TYPES (10743-10770). With _per_bar_kernel_adapter_enabled() default ON (6759-6774), run_strategy_execution returns None only when a strategy exposes neither vectorized nor per-bar signals; a built-in _VECTORIZABLE_TYPES strategy resolves vectorized signals and never returns None, so reaching the buggy fallback requires the self-contradictory case of a vectorizable type that cannot vectorize. Critically, this is a BACKTEST-ONLY path: the paper/live scanner calls run_strategy_execution directly (scanner.py:6005-6008, execution_controls=ec) and on res is None returns None (6014-6015) instead of falling through, so no live/paper money or position state is affected. At worst it yields wrong backtest metrics (default 1% sizing instead of the profile) for a profiled strategy that hits this contradictory fallback with execution_controls=None. Genuine but minor consistency gap; LOW severity is correct.

### `SCANAPPLY-3` — Backfill temp-open uses raw params leverage (default 1.0) instead of resolve_leverage, mis-stamping leverage/size

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** scanapply  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5589`
- **Claim:** The backfill path derives leverage as `float((strat.get('params') or {}).get('leverage', 1.0) or 1.0)`, whereas the main kernel path uses `_bt.resolve_leverage(p)` which applies the operator `default_leverage` when the strategy declares none. A backfilled (opened+closed-in-gap) trade for a strategy relying on the operator default therefore stores leverage=1.0 and a mis-scaled `units`/`size`.
- **Impact:** Stored leverage and position size on backfilled trades are wrong (cosmetic for PnL because _kernel_close_recorded overrides PnL with the kernel net, but misleading and inconsistent with faithfully-recorded trades; any downstream consumer recomputing from size/leverage would diverge).
- **Suggested fix:** Use `_bt.resolve_leverage(strat.get('params') or {})` in the backfill path so it matches the main kernel run.
- **Evidence:** Backfill: `leverage = float((strat.get("params") or {}).get("leverage", 1.0) or 1.0)` (scanner.py:5589). Main path: `leverage = _bt.resolve_leverage(p)` with comment 'so the kernel paper run matches the confirmation backtest's leverage (operator default_leverage when undeclared)' (scanner.py:5985).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the divergence. Backfill path (scanner.py:5589) computes `leverage = float((strat.get("params") or {}).get("leverage", 1.0) or 1.0)` — reads only the declared params leverage, hardcoded 1.0 fallback. Main kernel path (scanner.py:5985) uses `_bt.resolve_leverage(p)`, which (backtest.py:7615-7628) falls back to `resolve_default_leverage(settings)` = operator `default_leverage` (backtest.py:7598-7612) when the strategy declares none. Both feed `leverage` into `_kernel_open_paper_trade`, where `units = position_units(...)` scales linearly with leverage (sizing.py:290: `(eq*lev*sf)/px`) and both `units` and `leverage` are persisted to the DB row (scanner.py:5491-5493) and signal_data.sizing (5485-5489). So a backfilled (opened+closed-in-gap) trade for a leverage-undeclared strategy run while operator default_leverage != 1.0 stores leverage=1.0 and 1x-scaled units, inconsistent with faithfully-recorded trades. Impact is correctly characterized as cosmetic/metadata-only: the backfill immediately calls _kernel_close_recorded (scanner.py:5604), whose non-late branch overrides pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd with the kernel net (5544-5551); pnl_pct_net comes from run_strategy_execution which used the correct resolve_leverage, and pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net is leverage-independent. PnL/equity stay correct; only stored leverage/units/size diverge. Real and reachable, but money-neutral — low severity is appropriate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code discrepancy verified exactly as claimed. forven/scanner.py:5589 (backfill path in _kernel_close_paper_trade) uses `leverage = float((strat.get("params") or {}).get("leverage", 1.0) or 1.0)`, a hardcoded 1.0 fallback. The main kernel run at scanner.py:5985 uses `leverage = _bt.resolve_leverage(p)`. resolve_leverage (backtest.py:7615-7628) falls back to resolve_default_leverage (7598-7612), which returns the operator `settings["default_leverage"]` when the strategy declares no leverage. So for a leverage-undeclared strategy the two paths diverge whenever default_leverage != 1.0.

The mis-scaling is real: the backfill leverage feeds _kernel_open_paper_trade (scanner.py:5595-5596) -> _sizing.position_units(leverage=...) (5454-5457), stamping a wrong `units` and `signal_data.sizing.leverage` (5486-5489).

PnL impact correctly characterized as cosmetic: for a faithful (non-late) backfill, _kernel_close_recorded overrides pnl_pct/net_pnl_pct/pnl/pnl_usd with the kernel net (scanner.py:5541-5551), where pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net (5511) — independent of stored units/leverage. So recorded PnL and paper equity are not corrupted; only stored size/leverage metadata on backfilled trades is wrong.

Reachability is conditional on three things: backfill triggers (open+close within one scan gap — reachable on catch-up scans), strategy declares no leverage, and operator default_leverage != 1.0 (shipped default is 1.0 per backtest.py:7609, so the default config shows NO divergence). All plausible but not the out-of-box case. This is paper-only (_kernel_close_paper_trade). The finding self-rates low and is honest about the PnL override; the code defect is undeniable and the impact is correctly sized. Confirmed at low severity.

### `SCANAPPLY-4` — sizing_equity captured once per scan; a same-scan close->open sizes/stamps off pre-close equity (compounding lag)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** scanapply  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:6044, 6142-6143, 5471`
- **Claim:** `sizing_equity` is computed once at the top of the scan and reused for every faithful `open` in that scan. When a `close` (which realizes PnL) and an `open` are applied in the SAME scan (a same-direction re-entry, ordered close-then-open), the open is sized off, and stamps `kernel_equity_at_entry` from, the PRE-close equity, so its later pnl_usd does not reflect the just-realized compounding.
- **Impact:** The paper dollar-equity curve lags the backtest's compounding by one trade whenever a close and open coincide in a scan. pnl_pct (and therefore percentage returns/gate metrics) is unaffected; impact is bounded and self-corrects on later scans.
- **Suggested fix:** Re-read `_get_paper_strategy_equity(strat_id)` immediately before each faithful `open` (as the backfill path already does), so an open applied after a close in the same scan sizes off post-close equity.
- **Evidence:** `sizing_equity = _get_paper_strategy_equity(strat_id)` captured before the action loop (scanner.py:6044); the open applier is called with that same value: `open_applier(strat_id, strat, a, sizing_equity=sizing_equity, ...)` (scanner.py:6142-6143); it is frozen into the trade as `"kernel_equity_at_entry": round(float(sizing_equity), 4)` (scanner.py:5471), and the close uses that stamp for dollars: `pnl_usd = round(float(equity_at_entry) * pnl_pct_net, 4)` (scanner.py:5511).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All cited code verified literally. (1) scanner.py:6044 captures sizing_equity = _get_paper_strategy_equity(strat_id) ONCE, before the action loop that begins at 6131 (paper branch; the live branch at 6041 reads real equity). (2) Every open action passes that loop-invariant value: open_applier(..., sizing_equity=sizing_equity, ...) at 6142-6143, with no per-open re-read. (3) Inside _kernel_open_paper_trade it is both frozen as "kernel_equity_at_entry": round(float(sizing_equity), 4) (5471) and used to size units via _sizing.position_units(equity=float(sizing_equity), ...) (5454-5457). (4) The close path _kernel_close_recorded computes pnl_usd = round(float(equity_at_entry) * pnl_pct_net, 4) (5511) from that frozen stamp, while pnl_pct_net (5509) comes straight from the kernel trade and is independent of equity. Reachability holds: paper_reconcile.reconcile returns closes + backfills + opens + refreshes + orphan_closes (line 226), with the explicit design comment (224-225) that closes precede opens so a same-direction re-entry after an exit isn't mistaken for still-open. The opens loop (170-208) emits an open for a new entry_time even when the prior same-direction recorded open was just matched by the close loop (id(r_dir) is already in matched, so adopt is skipped; r is None for the new entry_time -> opens.append), so a close+same-direction-open in one scan is a real path (notably across multi-bar / downtime gaps). _get_paper_strategy_equity (589-616) = initial_capital + SUM(pnl_usd of CLOSED trades), and the close writes pnl_usd + sets status CLOSED (5544-5550 / close_trade_record), so a post-close re-read would reflect the realized PnL — but the open uses the pre-close snapshot. The asymmetry is confirmed: the backfill branch re-reads equity at 5588 (sizing_equity = _get_paper_strategy_equity(strat_id)) while the faithful open does not. Impact is exactly as described: dollar pnl_usd / equity curve lags compounding by one trade in the coincident-close+open case; pnl_pct and gate metrics (which run off pnl_pct, not pnl_usd) are unaffected; error is second-order and bounded, with later scans re-anchoring to actual book equity. No later line negates this. Low severity is appropriate: display-only dollar lag, no money lost, no state corruption.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The mechanical chain is exactly as described and verified against live code. scanner.py:6044 captures `sizing_equity = _get_paper_strategy_equity(strat_id)` once, before the action loop (the non-live `else` branch). scanner.py:6142-6143 passes that same value to every `open` action via `open_applier(..., sizing_equity=sizing_equity, ...)`. scanner.py:5471 freezes it as `kernel_equity_at_entry`, and scanner.py:5510-5511 computes close dollars as `equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net`. The reconciler orders `closes + backfills + opens + ...` (paper_reconcile.py:226) and the scanner applies them in that order (loop at scanner.py:6131), so a close realizes PnL into the DB before the open runs. Crucially, `_get_paper_strategy_equity` (scanner.py:604-615) derives equity from `SUM(pnl_usd) WHERE status='CLOSED'`, and `_kernel_close_recorded` commits `pnl_usd` (lines 5511 + 5543) before opens execute — so a re-read WOULD reflect the just-closed PnL, but the loop never re-reads. The finding's claimed asymmetry is also accurate: the backfill branch re-reads equity at scanner.py:5588, while faithful opens do not.

Reachability: a same-direction close→open within one scan is genuinely reachable. The kernel re-runs full history each scan and returns all closed_trades + current open_positions; after any scanner downtime/gap (explicitly supported by the backfill design) or a re-entry spanning scans, one reconcile yields both a close (finalizing the recorded open) and a new same-direction open (different entry_time, r is None → paper_reconcile.py:198).

Impact is correctly sized and self-limiting: this is PAPER-ONLY (live sizes off `_get_real_account_equity()` at scanner.py:6041 and books PnL from real fills, so no real money is mis-sized). Only the dollar curve lags by one trade's compounding (a second-order error ≈ realized_pnl × affected_trade_pnl_pct); pnl_pct and the percentage-based gate metrics are unaffected, and the lag does not accumulate across trades. Low severity is appropriate — it neither silently loses real money nor corrupts position state; it is a minor paper-equity-curve cosmetic lag against backtest compounding.

### `SCANAPPLY-5` — Adopted (drifted/legacy) orphan closes off fallback $10k equity and ignores its real entry price

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** scanapply  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5510, 5538-5552, 5624-5625`
- **Claim:** When the reconciler ADOPTS a drifted/legacy orphan, the refresh stamps `kernel_entry_time` but NOT `kernel_equity_at_entry`. On the later faithful close, pnl_usd is computed off the `_PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL` (10000) fallback and the kernel's historical entry, ignoring the orphan's real recorded entry_price/equity.
- **Impact:** An adopted orphan's realized dollar PnL is scaled by 10000 rather than the strategy's actual paper equity, and its real entry economics are discarded — a bounded equity drift for adopted positions.
- **Suggested fix:** When adopting an orphan, also stamp `kernel_equity_at_entry` with the current `_get_paper_strategy_equity(strat_id)` so the later close compounds off the correct base.
- **Evidence:** Fallback when the stamp is absent: `equity_at_entry = _coerce_positive_float(sd.get("kernel_equity_at_entry")) or _PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL` (scanner.py:5510). Adopt refresh stamps only the entry key: `if (action.recorded or {}).get("_orphan") and action.entry_time: updates["kernel_entry_time"] = str(action.entry_time)` (scanner.py:5624-5625) — no equity stamp. The faithful close then overrides PnL purely from the kernel net, not the orphan's row entry (scanner.py:5538-5552).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The defect is real and reachable as described. (1) An orphan is surfaced ONLY in the elif-is_open branch (scanner.py:5376-5391), i.e. precisely when the recorded OPEN trade has NO kernel_entry_time; trades with kernel_entry_time take the if-kref branch (5369) and never carry _orphan. (2) kernel_equity_at_entry is written at exactly two sites — paper open (5471) and live open (5867) — both ALWAYS paired with kernel_entry_time (5468/5866). Therefore an orphan, lacking kernel_entry_time, can never carry kernel_equity_at_entry. (3) On adoption the reconciler emits a refresh (paper_reconcile.py:184-187, applied at scanner.py:6146-6147), and _kernel_refresh_paper_trade stamps ONLY kernel_entry_time: `if (action.recorded or {}).get("_orphan") and action.entry_time: updates["kernel_entry_time"] = str(action.entry_time)` (5624-5625). _update_trade_signal_data merges (3042), so kernel_equity_at_entry stays absent. (4) On the later faithful close, scanner.py:5510 reads `equity_at_entry = _coerce_positive_float(sd.get("kernel_equity_at_entry")) or _PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL`; _coerce_positive_float(None) returns None (87-92) so it falls back to 10_000.0 (586), and pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net (5511) is written via the faithful-override branch (5538-5552), discarding the orphan's real entry economics. This corrupts pnl_usd, which feeds _get_paper_strategy_equity (SUM(pnl_usd), line 604), producing a bounded equity drift (error factor actual_equity/10000). Reachability check: adoption only fires when the kernel HOLDS that direction; if flat, the orphan is converge-closed instead (paper_reconcile.py:216-222 / scanner.py:5630) via close_trade_record, which does NOT use the 10000 fallback — so the two branches are mutually exclusive and the adopt-then-faithful-close path is genuinely reachable. Live is unaffected (close uses _kernel_close_live_trade with real fills). Severity low is appropriate: paper-only, edge-case (legacy/drift orphan held by the kernel then faithfully closed), and the error is bounded by actual_equity/10000 rather than unbounded.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Mechanics verified at every cited line. (1) scanner.py:5510-5511: _kernel_close_recorded computes equity_at_entry = _coerce_positive_float(sd.get("kernel_equity_at_entry")) or _PAPER_SANDBOX_INITIAL_CAPITAL (=10000.0, defined 586), then pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net. (2) scanner.py:5624-5625: the adopt branch in _kernel_refresh_paper_trade stamps ONLY updates["kernel_entry_time"] when recorded._orphan is set — no equity stamp; _update_trade_signal_data (3020) is a pure merge, so nothing backfills it. (3) A repo-wide grep shows kernel_equity_at_entry is written only at the faithful open paths (5471 paper open, 5867 live open) and read at 5510 — never on adopt/refresh. So an adopted orphan reaches close with the key absent → 10000 fallback. (4) scanner.py:5538-5552: the faithful-close branch overrides pnl_pct/pnl_usd from the kernel net (pnl_pct_net = trade.get('pnl_pct'), computed off the kernel's HISTORICAL entry), discarding the orphan's recorded entry_price. A true orphan is an OPEN trade lacking kernel_entry_time (5376-5391, skipping only manual source), and the reconciler has a dedicated adopt-orphan branch (paper_reconcile.py:184-187), confirming orphans are an expected production scenario; sources include legacy pre-kernel opens and the wired lab_regime_dispatch path (lab_intent_dispatch.py:306; router at api.py:671), neither marked manual so neither is filtered. REACHABILITY/IMPACT: correctly scoped PAPER-ONLY — the close applier is gated (scanner.py:6094: _kernel_close_live_trade for live, _kernel_close_paper_trade otherwise), so live never hits _kernel_close_recorded and no real money is mispaid. Error is bounded: paper equity = 10000 + realized PnL (5615), so using 10000 mis-scales pnl_usd by the strategy's accumulated drift from 10000, compounding into future paper sizing and the displayed paper stats that drive promotion decisions. Low severity is appropriate and unchanged: paper-only, no direct real-money loss, bounded magnitude, requires an uncommon orphan condition.

### `RECON-3` — recorded_open_by_dir keeps only the FIRST open per direction; a second same-direction open is invisible to both adopt and orphan_close

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** recon  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:143-144 (setdefault), 216-222 (orphan loop); forven/scanner.py:6081 (blank-asset escapes filter)`
- **Claim:** recorded_open_by_dir is built with setdefault, so only one open per direction is ever considered for adopt OR orphan-close. A second same-direction OPEN (e.g. a blank-asset row that escapes the scanner cross-asset filter, or a stuck backfill open) is never adopted, refreshed, or converge-closed — it is orphaned forever.
- **Impact:** A duplicate/blank-asset open lingers indefinitely in the paper book, never closed by the kernel and never converged. Display/equity drift; low likelihood (needs a blank-asset or duplicate open to exist).
- **Suggested fix:** Collect ALL open recorded rows per direction (list, not setdefault) and converge-close every same-direction open the kernel cannot match, not just the first.
- **Evidence:** `recorded_open_by_dir.setdefault(str(r.get("direction") or "long").strip().lower(), r)` (paper_reconcile.py:144); the orphan loop iterates only this map: `for direction, r in recorded_open_by_dir.items():` (paper_reconcile.py:216). The cross-asset filter requires a non-empty asset, so a blank-asset open is NOT held out: `if _rec.get("status") == "open" and _rec_asset and _strat_asset_u and ...` (scanner.py:6081). The unique index is per (strategy, ASSET, direction) (migrations.py:344-345), so a blank-asset open and a real-asset open of the same direction can coexist.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All five cited code claims are literally true. paper_reconcile.py:144 builds recorded_open_by_dir via setdefault, retaining only the first OPEN per direction. The adopt path (line 184, recorded_open_by_dir.get(direction)) and the orphan-close loop (line 216, iterating recorded_open_by_dir.items()) both see only that single winner, so a second same-direction open is invisible to adopt and orphan_close. The close/refresh paths use recorded_by_key (lines 157,174) keyed by (direction,entry_time), so a non-kernel orphan with no matching kernel entry is never closed there either. scanner.py:6081 requires non-empty _rec_asset, so a blank-asset open ("" -> falsy) is NOT held out as cross-asset and is passed into same_asset_recorded (6084) -> reconcile. migrations.py:343-345 keys the unique OPEN index on (strategy, asset, direction), so an asset="" open and a real-asset open of the same direction are distinct and can coexist. Tracing: with _kernel_recorded_trades ordering opened_at DESC (scanner.py:5361), if the legit real-asset open is iterated first it wins setdefault and the blank-asset duplicate is absent from the orphan map, so it is never converge-closed and lingers — exactly as claimed. The reconciler's own comment (lines 179-183) relies on a "<=1 open per direction" invariant that the cross-asset filter does not enforce for blank-asset rows, a genuine gap. Severity stays low: reachability is narrow because the kernel open path guards not-asset (scanner.py:5451), trades.asset is NOT NULL (db.py:736), and manual non-kernel opens are filtered before reconcile (scanner.py:5382); the trigger needs a non-kernel, non-manual OPEN inserted with blank asset. The secondary "stuck backfill open" example is inaccurate (backfills record CLOSED rows, line 125), but the blank-asset example holds and impact is display/equity drift only.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code mechanism fully verified. paper_reconcile.py:144 builds recorded_open_by_dir via setdefault (keeps only the first open per direction); the adopt path reads recorded_open_by_dir.get(direction) at line 184 and the orphan loop iterates only recorded_open_by_dir.items() at line 216. A second same-direction open with no exact (direction, entry_time) kernel match (e.g. an orphan row built at scanner.py:5384 whose entry_time is sd.entry_time/opened_at, never the kernel's bar timestamp) is therefore never adopted, refreshed, matched, or orphan-closed — it lingers indefinitely. The scanner cross-asset filter at scanner.py:6081 requires _rec_asset truthy, so a blank/empty-asset open is NOT held out and DOES reach reconcile (falls into same_asset_recorded). The unique index (migrations.py:344-345) is per (strategy, asset, direction) WHERE status='OPEN'; in SQLite '' and 'ETH' are distinct asset values, so a blank-asset open and a real-asset same-direction open can coexist, breaking the reconciler's explicit '≤1 open per direction' assumption (comment at lines 182-183). The defect is on the always-on reconcile path (paper and live), not behind a feature flag. REACHABILITY caveat: the trigger requires a blank-asset OPEN to exist, and I found no live writer that creates one — the kernel paper open guards `not asset` (scanner.py:5451), the kernel live open guards `not asset` (scanner.py:5851), all inserts go through _open_trade_db, and the schema is `asset TEXT NOT NULL` (db.py:736). The 'stuck backfill open' alternative in the evidence is inaccurate, since backfills produce CLOSED records, not opens. So in practice the precondition needs legacy/corrupted data, consistent with the finding's own 'low likelihood'. Impact when triggered is paper-only phantom that never converges (display/equity drift). The defect and its escape mechanism are real and correctly located; severity LOW already reflects the low reachability, so unchanged.

### `RECON-4` — Paper open applier does not catch idx_trades_unique_open IntegrityError; a failed backfill-close strands a stale open and drops the live kernel open

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** recon  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5491 (_kernel_open_paper_trade), 5595-5604 (backfill open-then-close), 6154 (action loop catch); contrast 5873-5875 (live catches it)`
- **Claim:** Unlike the live applier, _kernel_open_paper_trade does not catch the unique-open IntegrityError. The backfill path opens a trade then closes it; if that close throws, the stale backfill row stays OPEN, and the subsequent same-direction open/backfill raises an uncaught IntegrityError that the action loop merely logs — so the kernel's CURRENT open is never recorded while a stale backfill open is held.
- **Impact:** On a (rare) backfill-close failure during outage recovery, the paper book holds a stale opened-but-not-closed round-trip and misses the strategy's current open until manual intervention. Bounded by close-path DB writes rarely failing.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap _open_trade_db in _kernel_open_paper_trade in the same try/except sqlite3.IntegrityError -> return None guard used by the live path, and make the backfill open+close atomic (single transaction) so a partial backfill cannot strand an open row.
- **Evidence:** Paper open has no try/except around the insert: `trade_id = _open_trade_db(strat_id, asset, direction, entry_price, units, ...)` (scanner.py:5491). Live counterpart guards it: `try: trade_id = _open_trade_db(...) except sqlite3.IntegrityError: return None  # duplicate-open guard` (scanner.py:5873-5875). Backfill opens then closes within one applier: `_kernel_open_paper_trade(...)` then `_kernel_close_recorded(...)` (scanner.py:5595-5604); the action loop only catches at the outer level: `except Exception as exc: log.error(...)` (scanner.py:6154).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All load-bearing code claims verified against live source. (1) forven/scanner.py:5491-5495 — _kernel_open_paper_trade calls trade_id = _open_trade_db(...) with NO try/except, so a unique-open IntegrityError propagates. (2) forven/scanner.py:5872-5875 — the live counterpart _kernel_open_live_trade DOES wrap the same call in `try: ... except sqlite3.IntegrityError: return None  # duplicate-open guard`; the asymmetry is exactly as claimed. (3) forven/scanner.py:3830-3832 — _open_trade_db deliberately re-raises only the genuine duplicate-OPEN IntegrityError (`if \"idx_trades_unique_open\" in str(exc): raise`), and the partial unique index is real (forven/migrations.py:344-346, ON trades(key_expr, asset, direction) WHERE status='OPEN'), so the insert can raise. (4) forven/scanner.py:5595-5604 — the backfill path opens via _kernel_open_paper_trade then closes via _kernel_close_recorded in a non-transactional sequence; _kernel_close_recorded performs DB writes (close_trade_record / raw UPDATEs at 5513-5552) that can throw, stranding the just-inserted OPEN row. (5) forven/scanner.py:6131-6155 — the action loop only catches at the outer level (`except Exception as exc: log.error(...)`, line 6154). Reachability holds: within one scan, apply order closes+backfills+opens (paper_reconcile.py:226) means a failed backfill-close leaves a stale same-strategy/asset/direction OPEN row, and the following open insert trips idx_trades_unique_open uncaught — the current open goes unrecorded. One nuance: the finding's 'until manual intervention' is slightly overstated — on the next scan the kernel still surfaces the backfilled trade in res.closed_trades, so the reconciler re-matches the stale OPEN row by (direction, entry_time) and emits a close (paper_reconcile.py:157-163) applied before opens, so a TRANSIENT DB failure self-heals next cycle (a single missed-open window); only a persistent close failure needs intervention. That bounds the impact but does not refute the defect, and it matches the finding's own caveat. Severity 'low' is appropriate: requires a rare close-path DB write failure during backfill, and is largely self-correcting.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All code-level claims verified against live code. (1) _kernel_open_paper_trade's insert is bare: scanner.py:5491-5495 calls _open_trade_db(...) with no try/except; the try/except at 5496-5499 wraps only register(). The live counterpart guards it: scanner.py:5872-5875 (try _open_trade_db ... except sqlite3.IntegrityError: return None). _open_trade_db re-raises the unique-open error (scanner.py:3830-3832) and the unique index is (COALESCE(strategy_id,strategy),asset,direction) WHERE status='OPEN' (migrations.py:343-346), so a stale same-direction OPEN collides. The action loop only catches/logs at the outer level (scanner.py:6154). The path is the production default (paper_kernel_execution=True, scanner.py:5220-5222).

(2) Non-atomicity confirmed by re-reading 5595-5604 plus the call chain. get_db() (db.py:430) opens a fresh connection per call and commits on clean block exit (db.py:448-449). _kernel_open_paper_trade -> _open_trade_db commits the OPEN row inside its own with get_db() and returns from inside that block (scanner.py:3805/3829 -> commit at db.py:449), so the OPEN is durable BEFORE the close runs. _kernel_recorded_trades (scanner.py:5358) is a separate read connection, and _kernel_close_recorded uses further independent with get_db() writes (scanner.py:5513, 5514 close_trade_record, 5541). There is NO shared transaction and no get_db_immediate()/BEGIN IMMEDIATE wrapping open+close. So the backfill open+close is two-plus independent transactions, and any throw (or the row-is-None early return at 5602-5603) after the committed OPEN strands a status='OPEN' row. The finding's atomicity premise holds and the suggested 'single transaction' fix addresses a real gap.

Impact correction: the headline 'misses the strategy's current open until manual intervention' is overstated. The reconciler returns closes+backfills+opens (paper_reconcile.py:226); on the next scan the stranded OPEN row (surfaced by _kernel_recorded_trades, scanner.py:5368-5375) matches the kernel's finalized backfill by (direction,entry_time) -> a CLOSE action (paper_reconcile.py:157-163), applied before opens, freeing the unique slot so the current open inserts cleanly. So with the realistic trigger (transient SQLite lock clearing by next scan) it self-heals; it only stays stuck under a sustained DB outage where the backfill kc scrolls out of window while the open is still held (orphan_close blocked by direction in kernel_open_dirs, paper_reconcile.py:217).

Net: genuine code defect (missing duplicate-open guard the live path has + non-atomic backfill open/close), reachable on the default paper path, but paper-only (no real money), requires a rare transient DB-write failure at a precise point, and self-heals on the next successful scan. That matches the existing 'low' (defensive) severity.</parameter>
</invoke>


### `LATE-3` — Late hop-in can exceed its sized 1% risk: a kernel SIGNAL/time exit on a LATER bar pre-empts an EARLIER re-anchored-stop breach

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** late  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5217, 5577-5579, 6131-6170`
- **Claim:** _kernel_handle_late_entry_exits claims the trade exits at 'the re-anchored stop OR a strategy exit, whichever comes first' (docstring), but the implementation can violate that ordering. The reconciler's close path defers ONLY price exits (_KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS = stop/tp/trailing); a SIGNAL or time-stop exit is NOT deferred and is applied by the action loop BEFORE the monitor runs. So if the kernel's signal/time exit lands on a bar later than the bar where the hop-in's tighter re-anchored stop was breached, the reconciler closes at the (later) signal price and the monitor — which only runs on still-open trades — never enforces the earlier re-anchored stop. The trade then realizes more loss than the 1% it was sized for.
- **Impact:** Currently latent — late_entry_enabled is hard-coded False (scanner.py:6069) so no NEW late trades are created — but any pre-existing late_entry=True open trade, or re-enabling the feature, exposes a >1% realized loss versus the sized risk.
- **Suggested fix:** Before applying a non-deferred kernel exit to a late_entry trade, run the re-anchored-stop check over the bars up to the kernel exit and take whichever breach is chronologically first.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:5217 `_KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS = frozenset({'stop_loss','take_profit','trailing_stop'})`; 5577-5579 `_has_reanchor = ...; if _has_reanchor and str(trade.get('exit_reason') or '') in _KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS: return None` (only price exits deferred); apply order 6144-6145 (`close`/`backfill` -> close_applier) runs before 6170 (`out.extend(_kernel_handle_late_entry_exits(...))`).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the described ordering violation. (1) scanner.py:5217 `_KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS = frozenset({"stop_loss","take_profit","trailing_stop"})` — and the kernel's own exit-reason strings include "signal" (execution_kernel.py:212,302) and "time_stop" (execution_kernel.py:203), NEITHER of which is in that set. (2) In `_kernel_close_paper_trade` (scanner.py:5560-5580) a late_entry trade only defers (return None) when `_has_reanchor and exit_reason in _KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS` (5577-5579); a "signal"/"time_stop" exit on a bar after opened_at (so the 5566-5568 backwards-guard doesn't fire) falls through to `_kernel_close_recorded` at 5580 and closes the trade at the kernel exit price. (3) The action loop applies close/backfill via close_applier at scanner.py:6144-6145 BEFORE `_kernel_handle_late_entry_exits` runs at 6170. (4) `_get_open_trades` (scanner.py:3529) selects only status='OPEN', so the late-entry monitor skips a trade already closed earlier in the same scan — the re-anchored stop is never enforced. (5) For late closes, PnL is recomputed from the hop-in entry to the kernel exit price (5530-5536), so exiting at the later signal bar's price instead of the earlier re-anchored stop can realize >1% loss, violating the docstring guarantee (5738-5740) of "the re-anchored stop OR a strategy exit, whichever comes first." Reachability is latent/narrow, matching the LOW rating: it requires a pre-existing late_entry=True open row (or re-enabling the hard-disabled feature at scanner.py:6069) AND a single scan that processes both the breach bar and a later signal/time-stop bar (i.e., a multi-bar downtime gap — exactly the backfill-window tolerance documented at 5256-5258). In steady-state one-bar-per-scan operation the monitor wins, but the gap case genuinely breaks the ordering. Severity low is appropriate (latent money-loss, not currently armed for new trades).
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code traces out exactly as claimed. (1) scanner.py:5217 `_KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS = frozenset({"stop_loss","take_profit","trailing_stop"})`; scanner.py:5577-5579 `_has_reanchor = sd.get("stop_loss_price") is not None or sd.get("take_profit_price") is not None; if _has_reanchor and str(trade.get("exit_reason") or "") in _KERNEL_PRICE_EXIT_REASONS: return None` — only PRICE exits are deferred. A `signal`/time-stop exit is not in the set, so `_kernel_close_paper_trade` falls through to `_kernel_close_recorded` (5580) and closes the late trade at the kernel's historical exit price. (2) scanner.py:6131-6155 dispatches close/backfill actions via `close_applier` BEFORE `_kernel_handle_late_entry_exits` runs at 6170. (3) The monitor iterates `for trade in _get_open_trades(strat_id)` (5753), so once the reconciler-close has marked the trade closed, the monitor never enforces the earlier re-anchored stop. (4) `_kernel_close_recorded` for a late trade uses `exit_price = float(trade.get("exit_price"))` (5508) and computes PnL off the hop-in entry (5533-5536), so if the signal/time exit price is worse than the re-anchored stop the realized loss exceeds the 1% sizing. The docstring promise "exits at the re-anchored stop OR a strategy exit, whichever comes first" (5739) is genuinely violable. The pre-emption requires a single scan to cover both the re-anchored-stop breach bar T' and a later kernel signal/time exit bar T (the downtime/catch-up case, or the same-bar T'=T coincidence); in steady per-bar operation the open-only monitor catches the breach in its own scan before the later signal exists, so the window is narrow but real. REACHABILITY: scanner.py:6069 hard-codes `late_entry_enabled = False` and passes `late_entry=False` into reconcile (6087), so paper_reconcile.py:199-207 never emits a NEW late hop-in; the defect is reachable only via a residual pre-existing `signal_data.late_entry=True` open row (the monitor at 5753 and the defer guard at 5577 still process such rows) or a code change to re-arm the feature. The whole late path is paper-only (`if not is_live:` at 6161; docstring 5740). No real money is at risk and the error direction makes the paper trade look WORSE (more loss) than reality, so it cannot over-promote a bad strategy. The defect is real and accurately described including its latent/paper-only reachability; severity low is correct.

### `LATE-4` — Re-anchored-stop monitor silently swallows all exceptions in the hop-timestamp comparison — fail-open on a money-protective control with no log

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** late  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5764-5771`
- **Claim:** The monitor builds the bars-since-hop mask inside a bare `try/except Exception: continue`. If the candle index ever drifts to tz-naive or a RangeIndex (e.g. a future enrichment branch that resets the index), `idx > hop_ts` (hop_ts is tz-aware) raises and is silently swallowed per-trade, so the re-anchored stop is NEVER enforced and nothing is logged. The protective stop becomes display-only and the late trade rides to the kernel's far historical stop (or a signal exit), the precise loss this monitor exists to prevent.
- **Impact:** Currently benign (verified the candle index is tz-aware UTC DatetimeIndex and the monitor shares the kernel's df) and late-disabled, but it is a fail-open on a risk control with zero observability if the index assumption ever breaks.
- **Suggested fix:** Log a warning (not a silent continue) when the comparison fails, and/or normalize the index tz defensively (localize naive idx to UTC) so the stop is enforced rather than silently skipped.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:5765 `try: hop_ts = pd.Timestamp(hop_raw)` ... 5769 `mask = (idx > hop_ts).to_numpy() if hasattr(idx > hop_ts, 'to_numpy') else (idx > hop_ts)` / 5770 `except Exception: continue`.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified at forven/scanner.py:5764-5771. The hop-timestamp comparison and bars-since-hop mask are built inside a bare `try:`/`except Exception: continue` (5765 try, 5766 hop_ts=pd.Timestamp(hop_raw), 5769 mask=(idx > hop_ts)..., 5770-5771 except: continue). The except body is literally only `continue` — no log of any level — so on a raised comparison the trade is skipped and the re-anchored stop/target is never enforced that scan, leaving the late hop-in to ride to the kernel's far historical stop (the exact loss the monitor exists to prevent, per its own docstring at 5722-5740). The outer caller at 6169-6172 wraps the call in log.error, but the inner per-trade except swallows the error first, so the per-trade failure produces zero observability — the 'no log' claim holds. Reachability of the money-losing path is conditional (requires idx to become tz-naive/RangeIndex); I independently confirmed the candle index is currently tz-aware UTC (forven/dataeng/* consistently uses pd.to_datetime(..., utc=True)/tz_localize('UTC')), and hop_ts is force-localized to UTC at 5767-5768, so today the comparison succeeds and the except is not hit. The finding is honest about this ('Currently benign... fail-open if the index assumption ever breaks') and rates it low accordingly. The structural defect (silent fail-open with no observability on a risk control) is unconditionally present and matches the code exactly; impact is not overstated. One harmless discrepancy: the evidence quote omits the tz_localize at 5767-5768, which only strengthens the mechanism (tz-aware hop_ts vs a hypothetical tz-naive idx would definitely raise). Confirmed as a low-severity defensive/observability defect; severity unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code matches the finding exactly at forven/scanner.py:5765-5771. The mask is built inside a bare `try: ... except Exception: continue` with NO log. hop_ts is forced tz-aware (`tz_localize("UTC")`, line 5768), so a tz-naive/RangeIndex `idx` would make `idx > hop_ts` raise TypeError and be silently swallowed per-trade. The inner `continue` swallows it before the outer handler at 6171-6172 (`log.error(...)`) can fire, so the "fail-open with zero observability" claim is accurate: if the monitor skips a trade, the re-anchored stop is never enforced and the trade only exits via the reconciler on the kernel's HISTORICAL geometry/signal exit — structurally matching the stated impact.

On REACHABILITY/IMPACT the actual money loss is doubly non-reachable today, exactly as the finding itself concedes: (1) the candle index is currently tz-aware UTC, so the comparison does not raise; and (2) the late-entry feature is HARD-OFF — `late_entry_enabled = False` at scanner.py:6069, explicitly commented "Hard-off (not operator-gateable)" — so the reconciler (called with `late_entry=late_entry_enabled` at 6087) creates no new late_entry trades, and the monitor loop body (gated on `sd.get("late_entry")` at 5755) only ever fires for legacy persisted late trades. It is also paper-only (`if not is_live`, line 6161); late hop-ins never occur on the live path.

This is therefore a genuine but inert defensive/observability gap, not an active money-losing bug. The code claim is fully verifiable and true, and the finding correctly rates it `low` (the audit rubric defines low = defensive) and honestly labels it "currently benign." Confirmed at the stated severity; the hard-disabled feature plus tz-aware index mean it does not warrant escalation.

### `LIVE-7` — Live sizing can use a stale cached equity: daemon never clears account_equity on a failed/zero fetch and the reader ignores its sync timestamp

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** live  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:505-571; forven/daemon.py:414-417`
- **Claim:** _get_real_account_equity reads daemon_state.account_equity (then risk_state derivations) and returns None only when NO snapshot exists; it does not check account_equity_synced_at for staleness. The daemon only overwrites state['account_equity'] when the freshly fetched value is > 0, so a failed/zero exchange fetch leaves the PRIOR (possibly hours-old) value in place. Thus live_equity_unavailable can be False and a live OPEN can be sized off a stale equity rather than failing closed.
- **Impact:** Sizing off a stale equity snapshot mildly mis-sizes a live position. Largely mitigated in true live mode because can_open's Rule 0c re-fetches account value with require_connection=True and fails closed if unreachable; on testnet (default blast radius) it is fake money. Hence low.
- **Suggested fix:** Have _get_real_account_equity reject a daemon_state.account_equity whose account_equity_synced_at is older than a small TTL (return None -> fail closed), so a stale snapshot does not silently size a real order.
- **Evidence:** daemon: `account_equity = float(normalized.get("accountValue", 0) or 0); if account_equity > 0: state["account_equity"] = account_equity` (414-416) — never reset on failure; `state["account_equity_synced_at"] = ...` is written but _get_real_account_equity never reads it. Reader: `eq = _coerce_positive_float(daemon_state.get("account_equity")); if eq is not None: return eq` (536-538) with no age guard; manage_positions_via_kernel: `live_equity_unavailable = sizing_equity is None or sizing_equity <= 0` (6042).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the defect. daemon.py:414-417 (_persist_exchange_account_snapshot) only overwrites state["account_equity"] when account_equity > 0; on a zero/failed fetch the prior value persists, and the second writer at daemon.py:1461-1462 is identically gated (only writes when float(equity) > 0). Nothing ever clears account_equity on failure. state["account_equity_synced_at"] is written at daemon.py:417 but the reader never consumes it. scanner.py:536-538 (_get_real_account_equity) returns _coerce_positive_float(daemon_state.get("account_equity")) with NO age/synced_at guard; its fallback chain (risk_state last_equity/hwm, daily_risk start_equity) means it returns None (fail-closed) only when no snapshot exists at all — so a stale positive snapshot is returned. scanner.py:6041-6042 confirms sizing_equity = _get_real_account_equity() and live_equity_unavailable = sizing_equity is None or sizing_equity <= 0, so a stale-but-positive equity yields live_equity_unavailable=False and the live OPEN proceeds, sized off the stale value. The Rule 0c mitigation is real (risk.py:553-612): in mode=="live" it re-fetches with require_connection=True and fails closed (return False) on exception (607-612) and blocks at margin_ratio>=0.80 — but it only verifies margin ratio, it does NOT feed the freshly fetched acct_val back into sizing, so mild mis-sizing off the stale daemon snapshot persists when the exchange is reachable at can_open time but the daemon's cached equity is stale. Severity low is justified: error is proportional to staleness on a ~1% risk-per-trade size (trivial absolute dollars), gross over-leverage is bounded by Rule 0c, and the default network is testnet (fake money). The suggested fix (TTL on account_equity_synced_at in the reader, or better: size off the acct_val Rule 0c already fetched) is sound.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All three mechanical claims verified against live code. (1) forven/scanner.py:533-538 reads daemon_state['account_equity'] and returns the first positive value with NO staleness/age check; a grep for account_equity_synced_at across scanner.py returns zero hits, confirming the reader never consults the timestamp the daemon writes. It returns None only when no positive snapshot exists at all (line 571). (2) forven/daemon.py:414-416 writes back only when account_equity > 0 (`if account_equity > 0: state['account_equity'] = ...`), so a zero/failed fetch leaves the prior value; and a fully-failed fetch hits the early return at 411-412, never touching account_equity. (3) forven/scanner.py:6040-6042 sizes the live open off sizing_equity = _get_real_account_equity() (live_equity_unavailable only trips on None/<=0), and scanner.py:5859 in _kernel_open_live_trade computes position_units(equity=float(sizing_equity), ...) — so a stale-but-positive snapshot mis-sizes a real order.

Mitigation/impact framing is accurate: can_open Rule 0c (exchange/risk.py:553-612) runs only when get_execution_mode()=='live', re-fetches with require_connection=True (line 563/571), and on any fetch exception returns False with a fail-closed reason (607-612) — so the exchange-unreachable case is blocked. But that fresh acct_val is used ONLY for the margin-ratio/daily-halt check, never for sizing, so a genuine residual remains: when the exchange is reachable at open time yet the daemon's cached equity has gone stale, the live position is sized off the stale snapshot (mis-size bounded by equity drift — mild).

Reachability for real money is narrow: config.py:199 defaults execution_mode to 'paper', config.py:193-194 hard-locks beta builds to paper, and live requires a deliberate out-of-band FORVEN_EXECUTION_MODE/config edit; on the default path resolve_configured_testnet()==True (testnet/fake money). The daemon's periodic fetch uses require_connection=(mode in {live,mainnet}) (daemon.py:814-816), so the zero-fetch-leaves-prior-value branch chiefly affects testnet. Defect is real and reachable as described, the cited mitigation is correctly characterized, and LOW severity is well-justified.

### `HL-4` — Bracket SL/TP are placed as independent (non-OCO) trigger orders; exchange will not auto-cancel the sibling when one fills

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** hl  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1346-1398 (market_order order list), 1401 (`exchange.bulk_orders, orders` — no grouping arg)`
- **Claim:** market_order/limit_order submit the SL and TP as two separate trigger orders in one bulk_orders call without an OCO grouping (`grouping`/`normalTpsl` is never passed). The `tpsl: sl/tp` field alone does not create an exchange-side OCO link, so when one leg triggers, the other remains resting reduce-only.
- **Impact:** After a stop or TP fills on the exchange, the sibling stays on the book as a stale reduce-only trigger. Cleanup relies entirely on the scanner/reconcile retiring it by oid; the unique-open index prevents a same-asset reopen before cleanup, so the practical money risk is small, but a stale reduce-only trigger that survives into a future position could clip it. Worth confirming retire/reconcile always cancels both legs.
- **Suggested fix:** Submit the bracket with HL OCO grouping (normalTpsl/positionTpsl) so the exchange cancels the sibling automatically, or guarantee both oids are always cancelled together on any close path.
- **Evidence:** orders.append({... 'order_type': {'trigger': {'triggerPx': sl_px, 'isMarket': True, 'tpsl': 'sl'}}, 'reduce_only': True}) and the tp leg (1378-1398); submit is `_submit('place_order', hl_trade_breaker, exchange.bulk_orders, orders)` (1401) with only the orders list — no grouping parameter.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally matches the claim. In forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py, market_order builds the orders list (entry at 1346-1353; SL trigger appended 1378-1385; TP trigger 1390-1398) and submits via `_submit("place_order", hl_trade_breaker, exchange.bulk_orders, orders)` at line 1401 with ONLY the orders list. limit_order is identical (SL 1516-1524, TP 1528-1536, submit 1539). Each trigger leg uses `order_type: {trigger: {triggerPx, isMarket: True, tpsl: 'sl'|'tp'}}` with `reduce_only: True`. I resolved the installed SDK signature live: `Exchange.bulk_orders(self, order_requests, builder=None, grouping=Literal['na']|'normalTpsl'|'positionTpsl'|... = 'na')`. Because the code never passes `grouping`, the bracket is submitted with grouping='na' — independent orders, NOT an exchange-side OCO. A codebase-wide grep for grouping/normalTpsl/positionTpsl returns zero call-sites (only unrelated 'grouping token' comments), so no path anywhere uses OCO grouping. The claim's mechanism is correct: the `tpsl` field marks leg semantics but does not create the OCO link (that requires grouping='normalTpsl'/'positionTpsl'), so when one leg fills the sibling stays resting. Impact is accurately stated as small and severity 'low' is correct: both legs are reduce_only=True, so a stale sibling can only reduce/clip a position, never open a naked one; cleanup exists via _cancel_reduce_only_orders_for_asset (forven/api_domains/trading.py:887-914), which cancels ALL reduce-only orders for the asset by oid on close (covering both legs), and the unique-open index gates same-asset reopen before cleanup. Confirmed as a real but low-severity defect; the auditor's own 'worth confirming retire/reconcile cancels both legs' caveat checks out.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code claim fully verified. forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1401 and :1539 call exchange.bulk_orders(orders) with no grouping argument; the HL SDK signature is bulk_orders(self, order_requests, builder=None, grouping='na'), so grouping defaults to 'na' = no exchange OCO. The SL leg (1378-1385 / 1516-1524) and TP leg (1388-1398 / 1526-1536) carry only order_type.trigger.tpsl='sl'/'tp', which classifies the trigger but does not OCO-link it. A codebase-wide grep for grouping|normalTpsl|positionTpsl finds zero HL uses. So when one leg fills, the exchange leaves the sibling resting reduce-only — exactly as claimed.

Reachable in live: scanner.py:3335-3369 (_execute_direct 'open') mandates a stop (raise at 3337) and passes take_profit_price when present (3367-3368), so a strategy with a target submits both reduce-only triggers as a non-OCO pair; live kernel execution is the default.

Impact correctly sized LOW because compensating cleanup is real and verified: _trade_stop_oids (scanner.py:3655-3673) returns BOTH the stop and TP oids and _retire_trade_protection_orders (3629-3652) cancels them (fallback: cancel-all-reduce-only-for-asset). This runs on the signal/execution close (scanner.py:1291-1296, 4143-4147), the stale-reconcile path (trading.py:419-426 / _cancel_reduce_only_orders_for_asset 887-914), and force-close (962-963). The orphan is reduce_only=True so it cannot open a new position; money risk requires both a cleanup failure and a same-asset reopen in the window, which the unique-open index guards. The finding's claim, reachability, and LOW severity (with its own caveat that self-managed cleanup compensates) all hold against the live code.

### `HL-5` — cancel_all_orders reads open_orders without the breaker/transient-retry wrapper, so a transient read failure aborts the whole flatten

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** hl  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1814 (`orders = info.open_orders(address)`)`
- **Claim:** cancel_all_orders fetches open orders via a raw info.open_orders call (not _with_breaker), so a transient 502/504/timeout there raises and prevents any cancellation, even though get_open_orders elsewhere is breaker+retry wrapped.
- **Impact:** During an operator flatten/cancel-all, a single transient gateway blip on the orders read aborts the entire cancel sweep instead of degrading gracefully. Recoverable on retry; low severity.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the open_orders read in _with_breaker (or reuse get_open_orders) so the read is retried on transient upstream errors like every other account read.
- **Evidence:** `exchange, info, address = _exchange_for_trading(...); orders = info.open_orders(address); results = []; for order in orders: ...` (1813-1816) — the read is unguarded, unlike get_open_orders which uses `_with_breaker('account', hl_account_breaker, info.open_orders, address)` (2017).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1814 in cancel_all_orders does `orders = info.open_orders(address)` as a RAW call: _exchange_for_trading (line 1024) only builds exchange/info/address + agent-auth, it does not wrap the read, and there is no try/except around line 1814. So a transient 502/504/timeout on that read propagates out before the `for order in orders` loop (1816), cancelling nothing — exactly as claimed. By contrast get_open_orders (line 2017) routes the identical underlying call through `_with_breaker("account", hl_account_breaker, info.open_orders, address)`, and _with_breaker (line 637, docstring 640-647) provides bounded retry on TRANSIENT upstream failures (504/502/503, timeouts). This asymmetry is real. Reachable: the execution-trader `cancel_orders` agent tool (forven/agents/tools_exchange.py:662) calls cancel_all_orders without its own try/except, so a transient read error surfaces as a failed sweep. Severity low is correct: the failure is fully recoverable on retry with no double-cancel, lost position, or state corruption; and note this cancels resting ORDERS (not positions — position flatten is close_position at line 1830), so the impact wording 'flatten' is slightly loose but the core defect (no transient-retry on the read, aborting the cancel sweep) holds.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code confirmed at forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1814: cancel_all_orders does `orders = info.open_orders(address)` as a raw, unguarded call, whereas get_open_orders at line 2017 uses `_with_breaker("account", hl_account_breaker, info.open_orders, address)`. _with_breaker (lines 637-677) genuinely adds a bounded transient retry for 502/503/504/timeouts (retry_transient is True for non-price breakers), so the raw read at 1814 lacks that protection. A transient upstream error on the open_orders read raises before the cancel loop begins, aborting the entire cancel sweep — exactly as claimed. Reachable in production via the agent `cancel_orders` tool (forven/agents/tools_exchange.py:662, registered runner.py:759, permission execution-trader); the propagated exception surfaces as a tool failure. Two reachability qualifiers that keep this LOW and do not refute it: (1) the agent caller hardcodes testnet=True; (2) the automated kill-switch/emergency flatten in forven/exchange/risk.py (~2960) uses close_position plus breaker-wrapped get_open_orders / _cancel_reduce_only_orders_for_asset, NOT cancel_all_orders — so the "flatten" framing slightly overstates reach, but the "operator cancel-all" framing is accurate. The defect is real, the path is reachable, and the impact (transient blip aborts the cancel-all, recoverable on retry) is correctly sized as low. Severity unchanged.

### `RISK-2` — Manual PAPER open bypasses the risk gate (no can_open / is_trading_allowed)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** risk  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:490-533 (open_manual_position, paper branch)`
- **Claim:** The manual paper-open branch records a trade directly via _open_trade_db_safe with no can_open() or is_trading_allowed() check, so it opens even under operator STOP / kill-switch / daily-halt.
- **Impact:** Operator STOP and the kill-switch/daily-halt do not prevent a hand-opened paper position. Paper-only (no real money), and it is an explicit operator action, so lower severity, but it still lets paper-validation data accrue during a halt.
- **Suggested fix:** Call is_trading_allowed() at the top of open_manual_position before either branch so a manual paper open is also blocked while the system is stopped/halted.
- **Evidence:** paper_control.py:527-531 `trade_id = _open_trade_db_safe(strategy_id=..., direction=norm_dir, entry=mid, size=float(resolved_size), risk_pct=..., execution_type="paper", ...)` with no preceding is_trading_allowed/can_open in the paper branch (490-533). Only the live branch (556) gates. Same root cause as RISK-1 but operator-initiated.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. In forven/api_domains/paper_control.py, open_manual_position (lines 450-533) reaches _open_trade_db_safe at lines 527-531 with execution_type="paper" without ever calling is_trading_allowed() or can_open(). The paper branch (490-533) contains only a duplicate-position check (line 461) plus sizing/protective-level validation — no risk gate. grep confirms is_trading_allowed never appears in this file, and _open_trade_db_safe (646-664) only delegates to scanner._open_trade_db (enforces the unique-open one-per-asset index, not the halt). The live branch is asymmetric: _live_open calls risk_mod.can_open at line 556, which at risk.py:535 (Rule 0) invokes is_trading_allowed() — checking operator pause/system stop, startup recovery, kill-switch, and daily-loss-halt (risk.py:3287-3313) — and raises 409 if blocked. The automatic scanner path also gates for paper (is_trading_allowed at scanner.py:971; can_open at scanner.py:1035, scoped by execution_type), so this is genuinely a manual-path-only gap: a hand-opened paper position opens even under operator STOP / kill-switch / daily-loss-halt. The router dependency require_operator_access (paper.py:8) is authentication, not a risk-state gate, so it does not negate the issue. Severity low is appropriate: paper-only (no real money), explicit operator action, and the only harm is paper-validation data accruing during a halt. Evidence, line refs, and impact in the finding are all accurate.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. The paper branch of open_manual_position (forven/api_domains/paper_control.py:490-533) goes directly to _open_trade_db_safe(... execution_type="paper" ...) at lines 527-531 with no is_trading_allowed()/can_open() call. _open_trade_db_safe (paper_control.py:646-664) only catches the one-per-asset unique-index conflict and otherwise calls the scanner's _open_trade_db unconditionally — no halt gate. By contrast the LIVE branch gates: _live_open calls risk_mod.can_open at paper_control.py:556, and can_open runs is_trading_allowed() at risk.py:535 (Rule 0). is_trading_allowed() (risk.py:3287-3313) returns False on operator pause, startup recovery, kill-switch, and daily-loss-halt. The automatic scanner paper path also gates via _guard_open_trade_execution_intent -> is_trading_allowed() at scanner.py:971. So the manual paper open is the only open path that does NOT honor operator STOP/kill-switch/daily-halt. Reachability confirmed: it is reachable in production via POST /api/paper/sessions/{session_id}/open-position (routers/paper.py:123-133); the router's only dependency, require_operator_access (paper.py:8), is an auth/access guard, not a trading-halt gate (the "operator-guarded" comment at paper.py:109 refers to access control). Impact is correctly sized: paper-only (execution_type="paper"), no real exchange order and no real money, and it is an explicit operator action, so the only consequence is paper-validation data accruing during a halt plus an inconsistency with the live/auto paths. Low severity is accurate.

### `RISK-4` — Stricter mainnet risk limits are dead code; live mode always uses the looser testnet limits

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** risk  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:50-56 (_MAINNET_LIMITS), 88-89 (_get_risk_limits); forven/config.py:182-199 (get_execution_mode)`
- **Claim:** _get_risk_limits selects _MAINNET_LIMITS only when get_execution_mode()=='mainnet', but get_execution_mode() can only ever return 'paper' or 'live', so _MAINNET_LIMITS never applies and live trading runs on the looser _TESTNET_LIMITS.
- **Impact:** If a user forces real live/mainnet out-of-band (FORVEN_EXECUTION_MODE/edited config, the scenario this whole audit targets), the default risk caps are 2x looser than the author intended for real money. User settings overrides still apply, but the built-in mainnet safety floor is inert. Low because mainnet is gated/unsupported and overridable via settings, but it is a silent fail-loose.
- **Suggested fix:** Drive _get_risk_limits off the real network/mainnet flag (e.g. resolve_configured_testnet / FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET) rather than an execution-mode string that can never equal 'mainnet', or remove _MAINNET_LIMITS and document that testnet limits are authoritative.
- **Evidence:** risk.py:88-89 `mode = str(cfg.get_execution_mode() or "paper").strip().lower(); base_limits = dict(_MAINNET_LIMITS) if mode == "mainnet" else dict(_TESTNET_LIMITS)`. config.py:196 only accepts `mode in ("paper", "live")` from env and cfg defaults to 'paper' (199) — 'mainnet' is never produced. So base_limits is always _TESTNET_LIMITS. The intended mainnet caps (risk.py:50-56: max_drawdown 0.05, daily_loss 0.03, max_risk_per_trade 0.01) are unreachable; live defaults to the testnet caps (0.10 / 0.05 / 0.02).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The money-relevant core of this finding holds: in LIVE mode the stricter mainnet caps never bind. risk.py:88-89 selects _MAINNET_LIMITS only when the execution-mode STRING equals "mainnet", and the normal real-money path sets mode="live", not "mainnet". config.py:195-197 confirms the env override only ever yields "paper" or "live" (FORVEN_EXECUTION_MODE="mainnet" fails the `mode in ("paper","live")` check and falls through). The repo's own test test_risk_module.py:36-39 (test_live_uses_testnet_limits) pins this behavior: mode=="live" -> limits == _TESTNET_LIMITS (max_drawdown 0.10, daily_loss 0.05, max_risk_per_trade 0.02), i.e. 2x looser than the _MAINNET_LIMITS floor (0.05/0.03/0.01) the author defined. Crucially, the actual mainnet-vs-testnet NETWORK is decided independently by resolve_configured_testnet / FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET (hyperliquid.py:432-437), so a real mainnet live deployment via mode="live" trades real funds while applying the looser testnet floor — a genuine silent fail-loose, and the suggested fix (key the tier off the network flag, not the mode string) is the correct remedy.

One inaccuracy in the finding's stated mechanism: it claims _MAINNET_LIMITS is "dead code"/"unreachable" because get_execution_mode() "can only ever return 'paper' or 'live'". That is NOT strictly true — config.py:199 returns `cfg.get("execution_mode", "paper")` verbatim with no whitelist, so a hand-edited config.json with execution_mode="mainnet" makes get_execution_mode() return "mainnet" and _get_risk_limits() correctly applies the tighter _MAINNET_LIMITS. test_risk_module.py:41-47 explicitly exercises that path, and many call sites (trading.py:583, daemon.py:816, notification_policy.py:75) handle a "mainnet" mode. So _MAINNET_LIMITS is reachable, just via a config value the mode="live" path never produces. The defect is real and reachable as the title's second clause describes (live always uses testnet limits), even though the "dead code/never applies" framing is overstated.

Severity low is appropriate/unchanged: impact only materializes when a user (1) forces mode="live" out-of-band, (2) deliberately enables mainnet via FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET, and (3) relies on default caps (user settings overrides at risk.py:100-145 still apply on top). Result is a 2x-looser default safety net, not direct money loss or state corruption — a defensive fail-loose behind multiple intentional guard bypasses.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The finding's actionable conclusion is correct, though its "dead code" mechanism is partly wrong.

CONFIRMED part: The canonical live path runs on the looser _TESTNET_LIMITS. risk.py:89 selects _MAINNET_LIMITS only for mode=="mainnet"; the supported way to enable live trading is mode=="live" (the only env value besides "paper" accepted at config.py:196, and the value can_open's fail-closed margin guard keys on at risk.py:553). When mode=="live", risk.py:89 returns _TESTNET_LIMITS, so the author-intended stricter floor (max_drawdown 0.05, daily_loss 0.03 at risk.py:53-54) never applies to real live trading; live instead uses 0.10/0.05 (risk.py:46-47). These two caps are real and active on the live path: they gate the kill-switch and daily halt via is_trading_allowed (consumed at risk.py:2914 `drawdown_pct >= max_drawdown` and risk.py:2931 daily halt), independent of enforce_risk_caps. So live drawdown protection is 2x looser than intended.

CORRECTION to the finding's evidence: the claim that get_execution_mode() "can only ever return 'paper' or 'live'" and that _MAINNET_LIMITS is therefore "dead/unreachable" is FALSE. config.py:199 (`return cfg.get("execution_mode", "paper")`) returns the raw config.json value, so a hand-edited config execution_mode="mainnet" makes get_execution_mode() return "mainnet", which other modules treat as live-routing (daemon.py:816, trading.py:103/583, hyperliquid.py:755). In that case _MAINNET_LIMITS IS selected (risk.py:89) — but that same "mainnet" value bypasses can_open's Rule 0c live margin fail-closed guard (risk.py:553 checks mode=="live", not "mainnet"). So the stricter limits are reachable, just never on the canonical "live" path, and the only mode that activates them also disables a money-protecting guard.

REACHABILITY/IMPACT (lens): Only matters when live/mainnet is forced out-of-band — default is "paper" (config.py:199), set_execution_mode refuses anything but paper (config.py:216-221), and beta builds hard-lock paper (config.py:193). On the live scanner path, enforce_risk_caps=False (scanner.py:5855) skips max_risk_per_trade (Rule 0b, risk.py:541) and portfolio_budget (Rule 3, risk.py:692), so the testnet-vs-mainnet difference for those two values is moot; the practical fail-loose is limited to max_drawdown/daily_loss_limit, and all are user-overridable via settings (risk.py:103-143). A genuine but bounded, gated, default-off silent fail-loose. severity low is appropriate (unchanged).

### `RISK-5` — can_open margin gate (Rule 0c) only fails closed on a fetch EXCEPTION, not on a zero/garbage accountValue

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** risk  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:571-612`
- **Claim:** When the live account fetch SUCCEEDS but returns accountValue<=0 (or the key is absent), the `if acct_val > 0:` guard skips both the 80% margin check and the M9 daily-halt recompute and lets the open proceed; only an exception in the fetch fails closed.
- **Impact:** A degraded exchange response that returns a structurally-valid payload with accountValue 0 would skip the margin guard rather than blocking. In practice an empty/zero account cannot fill a sized order and live sizing fails closed elsewhere (scanner.py:4308), so real exposure is limited; flagged as defensive hardening.
- **Suggested fix:** Treat acct_val<=0 from a successful fetch as unverifiable in live mode and fail closed (return False) instead of falling through.
- **Evidence:** risk.py:574-576 `acct_val = acc.get("accountValue", 0); margin_used = acc.get("totalMarginUsed", 0); if acct_val > 0:` — the entire margin/daily-halt block is inside this branch. The fail-closed path only covers the except at 607-612 `return False, 0.0, ("Cannot verify exchange margin (account fetch failed) ...")`. A successful fetch yielding accountValue 0 falls through to open.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-truth verified against live code. risk.py:574 `acct_val = acc.get("accountValue", 0)` defaults to 0 when the key is absent; risk.py:576 `if acct_val > 0:` wraps BOTH the 80% margin check (578-579) and the M9 daily-halt recompute (599-606). The only fail-closed `return False` (607-612) is inside the `except`, so it fires only on a fetch EXCEPTION. A successful fetch yielding acct_val<=0 makes the `if` False, skips both checks, and falls through to line 614+ with no early return — the open proceeds. Reachability confirmed: get_account_value (hyperliquid.py:1962-1993) parses a degraded-but-structurally-valid user_state (e.g., empty marginSummary) into perp_value=0.0 (line 1989) and returns accountValue 0.0 without raising, so a zero payload genuinely reaches and bypasses the guard. Impact is correctly bounded: live sizing reads a SEPARATE source (_get_real_account_equity via scanner.py:4307-4323) and fails closed at scanner.py:4308 when equity is None/<=0, and Hyperliquid enforces real margin on the order while the M9 halt is recomputed on the next daemon tick. There is a narrow window (valid cached daemon snapshot + transient degraded can_open fetch) where the soft margin gate and at-open halt recompute are silently skipped, but it does not directly lose money or corrupt state. Defect is real and reachable as described; low severity (defensive hardening) is appropriate — unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code-level defect verified at forven/exchange/risk.py:574-612. Line 574 `acct_val = acc.get("accountValue", 0)` then line 576 `if acct_val > 0:` wraps BOTH the 80% margin check (578-579) and the M9 daily-halt recompute (599-606). The only fail-closed `return False` is in the `except` at 607-612 (fetch exception). A successful fetch returning accountValue<=0 skips the entire block and falls through to line 614, allowing the open — exactly as claimed. Reachability confirmed and it is a LIVE-money path: line 553 `if mode == "live":` gates the block (not paper).
