A successful fetch yielding accountValue 0 is producible: get_account_value (hyperliquid.py:1997-2004) always returns a dict with `"accountValue": float(perp_value + spot_total)`; a missing/degraded marginSummary drives perp_value->0.0 (line 1989) and best-effort spot read ->0.0 (1983-1987), producing a structurally-valid {"accountValue":0.0} with no exception, so the except-branch fail-closed never fires. Impact correctly sized as low: verified scanner.py:4308 (`if sizing_equity is None or sizing_equity <= 0:`) fails closed for a genuinely empty account, and the skipped checks are defensive buffers — the 80% margin gate sits above Hyperliquid's own exchange-side margin enforcement, and the daily-halt is also recomputed by the tick-driven update_equity (per comment at 580-584), so skipping the open-path recompute only delays a halt by one tick. Residual risk is a transient degraded margin-fetch response combined with a positive/stale sizing-equity source, which could open while skipping the conservative buffer and early halt catch; bounded and minor. Defect is real, reachable on the live path, and the low/defensive-hardening characterization is accurate.

### `BOOT-2` — Boot recovery preflight and startup kill-switch re-flatten call exchange REST synchronously without the timeout wrappers used in the running loop

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** boot  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/daemon.py:811-824, 1898; compare in-loop wrappers daemon.py:1341, 1509`
- **Claim:** Every exchange call on the boot path is a bare blocking call, unlike the in-loop versions which are wrapped in _to_thread_with_timeout. A slow/degraded exchange at boot delays the daemon from reaching async_market_loop (and thus from publishing prices/candles/heartbeat) by up to the HTTP timeout times the number of book accounts times retries.
- **Impact:** Bounded (not a permanent hang) because every HL HTTP call has a hard 15s timeout (`_HL_HTTP_TIMEOUT_SECONDS = 15.0`, hyperliquid.py:766), but across multiple book sub-accounts and retries the daemon can be stalled in startup for tens of seconds to minutes, during which it publishes no price/candle cache and no heartbeat. Live remains fail-closed (gate stuck at 'checking'), so this is availability/degradation, not money loss.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the boot preflight exchange reads and the boot close_all_positions in the same bounded timeout helper used in-loop, and treat a timeout as a transient 'exchange_unreachable' boot state rather than blocking the market loop from starting.
- **Evidence:** run_startup_recovery_preflight calls `positions_payload = get_positions(testnet=testnet)`, `open_orders_payload = get_open_orders(testnet=testnet)`, `account_snapshot = get_account_value(...)`, `sync_from_trades()`, `recon = reconcile_all_books(...)` with no timeout (daemon.py:811-824); KS-1 boot re-flatten calls bare `_res = close_all_positions()` (daemon.py:1898). The in-loop equivalents are bounded, e.g. `await _to_thread_with_timeout("daemon.close_all_positions", RISK_CLOSE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS, close_all_positions)` (daemon.py:1341) and `await _to_thread_with_timeout("daemon.reconcile_all_books", RISK_RECONCILE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS, reconcile_all_books, _get_testnet())` (daemon.py:1509).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally matches the claim. Boot preflight run_startup_recovery_preflight (sync def, daemon.py:751) calls get_positions/get_open_orders/get_account_value/sync_from_trades/reconcile_all_books with no timeout wrapper (daemon.py:812-824), and the KS-1 boot re-flatten calls bare close_all_positions() (daemon.py:1898). The in-loop equivalents ARE wrapped: await _to_thread_with_timeout(...) at daemon.py:1341-1345 (close_all_positions) and 1509-1514 (reconcile_all_books), where the helper (daemon.py:621-636) bounds the call via asyncio.wait_for+to_thread and returns None on timeout. The ordering claim verifies: _daemon_startup_bookkeeping is a synchronous def (daemon.py:1793) that runs the boot re-flatten and preflight to completion BEFORE async_market_loop is started — both run_in_loop (state = _daemon_startup_bookkeeping(...); await async_market_loop(state), daemon.py:2016/2023) and run (daemon.py:2031/2038) call it sync first; async_market_loop (1645) is what publishes prices/candles/heartbeat, so a degraded exchange at boot delays it. Bounded-not-hung is correct: _HL_HTTP_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=15.0 (hyperliquid.py:766) caps each call, and a bounded retry loop with backoff (hyperliquid.py:655-674) over multiple sub-account/book calls credibly stacks to tens of seconds. Fail-closed is preserved (recovery_status set to 'checking' at daemon.py:1883-1889 before preflight). Impact is availability/degradation, not money loss or state corruption, so low severity is correct. Note: in the uvicorn-hosted run_in_loop path these bare sync calls block the whole event loop, an even broader impact than stated, which only strengthens the finding.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. (1) The defect is real: run_startup_recovery_preflight makes bare synchronous exchange reads get_positions/get_open_orders/get_account_value/sync_from_trades/reconcile_all_books with no timeout (daemon.py:812-824), and the KS-1 boot re-flatten calls bare close_all_positions() (daemon.py:1898). The in-loop versions ARE bounded via _to_thread_with_timeout (daemon.py:1341 close_all_positions, daemon.py:1509 reconcile_all_books; helper at daemon.py:621-636 uses asyncio.wait_for). (2) Reachability holds: this boot code lives in the synchronous _daemon_startup_bookkeeping (def at daemon.py:1793) which is called BEFORE async_market_loop in both entry points — run() (daemon.py:2031, then asyncio.run(async_market_loop) at 2038) and run_in_loop() (daemon.py:2016, then await async_market_loop at 2023). Price/candle/heartbeat workers only spawn inside async_market_loop (_start_market_workers, daemon.py:1689), so the boot reads delay reaching it. The preflight runs on every boot when credentials are present (paper-without-creds returns early at daemon.py:787-798), so it is on a live, non-flag-gated path; KS-1 re-flatten is gated on a previously-tripped kill switch (daemon.py:1896). Notably in run_in_loop() the sync bookkeeping is invoked directly inside the async coroutine, so it also blocks the uvicorn event loop — an equal-or-worse availability hit than stated, but still availability. (3) Impact correctly sized: _HL_HTTP_TIMEOUT_SECONDS = 15.0 (hyperliquid.py:766) bounds each call so there is no permanent hang; reconcile_all_books runs one pass per book sub-account plus a master pass when books are enabled (risk.py:2349-2354), so multiple sequential 15s-bounded calls can stack into tens of seconds at boot. Live stays fail-closed (gate held at 'checking', daemon.py:1883-1889) so there is no money loss or state corruption — this is bounded availability/degradation only. Low severity is appropriate.

### `BOOT-3` — Paper position whose entry predates the kernel replay window is neither reproduced nor orphan-closed after a long downtime (stranded open)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** boot  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:216-222; forven/scanner.py:6056-6059`
- **Claim:** On restart the kernel re-simulates only the fetched history (default 1500 bars, skipping the first KERNEL_WARMUP+1). A recorded OPEN paper trade whose entry_time is older than window_start is explicitly skipped by the orphan-close guard, and the kernel cannot reproduce it, so if the kernel is flat in that direction the trade is left OPEN and unmanaged indefinitely.
- **Impact:** Paper-only (isolated sandbox, no real money). Requires downtime/position-age exceeding ~1300 bars on the strategy timeframe (e.g. ~54 days on 1h). The position is held forever with no further exit management, corrupting that strategy's paper track record. The guard is an intentional trade-off (avoids wrongly orphaning warmup-band entries), so this is an edge gap, not a clear regression.
- **Suggested fix:** For an open recorded trade older than window_start with the kernel flat in that direction, either fetch enough history to cover it, or converge-close it at the last bar (mark it as an unreproducible-window close) rather than leaving it open indefinitely.
- **Evidence:** reconcile() orphan loop: `if window_start is not None and entry_time and _ts_lt(entry_time, str(window_start)): continue  # entry predates the kernel's evaluated window -> leave it alone` (paper_reconcile.py:220-221). The scanner anchors window_start to the first replayable bar: `window_start = str(df.index[min(KERNEL_WARMUP + 1, len(df) - 1)]) if len(df) else None` over a `_paper_kernel_history_bars()` (default 1500) fetch (scanner.py:6056-6059, 5958).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the defect. (1) The kernel cannot produce an entry_time older than window_start: KERNEL_WARMUP=200 (scanner.py:6003), run_strategy_execution skips the first KERNEL_WARMUP+1 bars, and window_start is anchored to exactly that first replayable bar — `window_start = str(df.index[min(KERNEL_WARMUP + 1, len(df) - 1)])` (scanner.py:6059) over a `_paper_kernel_history_bars()` fetch defaulting to 1500 (scanner.py:5251,5958). (2) In reconcile(), a recorded OPEN in direction D with entry_time < window_start, when the kernel is FLAT in D, is: not matched by any close (kernel never sees that exit); not in kernel_open_dirs so no refresh/drift-adopt; and the late_entry branch is unreachable because it sits inside the `for direction,pos in res.open_positions.items()` loop (paper_reconcile.py:170-207) which never iterates a direction the kernel holds nothing in. The orphan-close loop then hits the guard `if window_start is not None and entry_time and _ts_lt(entry_time, str(window_start)): continue` (paper_reconcile.py:220-221), emitting NO orphan_close. Result: the trade is left OPEN and unmanaged. (3) No independent safety net closes it: orphan_close is the only convergence path and it's suppressed; sweep_pending_close_reconcile (scanner.py:7064) only handles trades already flagged pending_close_reconcile; _kernel_handle_manual_exits (scanner.py:6163) only manages manually-opened positions, not kernel-opened ones; paper has no separate intrabar stop checker for kernel positions. Reachability matches the claim: paper-only, entry must predate the latest ~1299 bars (~54 days on 1h, longer on higher TFs), via long downtime or a long-held position whose signal never re-triggers in the replay window. One refinement: if the kernel later re-enters direction D, the drift-adopt branch (paper_reconcile.py:184-187) would adopt the stale row, so 'indefinitely' holds only while the strategy never re-signals that direction — exactly the claim's stated 'kernel flat in that direction' condition. Cited file:line references (paper_reconcile.py:216-222, scanner.py:6056-6059, 5958) are all accurate. Severity low is correct: paper-only sandbox (no real money), narrow trigger, and the guard is a deliberate trade-off documented at scanner.py:6056-6058 / paper_reconcile.py:212-214 (avoids wrongly orphaning a still-valid warmup-band entry) — an edge gap, not a clear regression.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. paper_reconcile.py:220-221 explicitly `continue`s (skips orphan-close) for any recorded OPEN whose entry_time < window_start. scanner.py:6059 anchors window_start = df.index[min(KERNEL_WARMUP+1, len-1)] with KERNEL_WARMUP=200 (scanner.py:6003) over a _paper_kernel_history_bars() fetch defaulting to 1500/floor 300 (scanner.py:5251) — so the replayable window is ~1299 bars and older entries predate window_start. The only re-management path for such a recorded open is the drifted-refresh branch at paper_reconcile.py:184-187, which is nested inside `for direction, pos in res.open_positions.items()` and therefore fires ONLY when the kernel currently holds a position in that direction; if the kernel is flat (entry too old to reproduce and signal doesn't re-trigger in-window), there is no refresh and the orphan-close is suppressed -> the recorded OPEN stays open. window_start advances on every later scan, so the entry stays before it indefinitely. No alternate cleanup exists: _kernel_close_orphan (scanner.py:5630) only runs for emitted orphan_close actions; there is no age-based/self-heal closure of stale paper opens; and for vectorized strategies manage_positions_via_kernel returns non-None so the legacy stop-check path never runs. REACHABILITY: the controlling flag paper_kernel_converge_orphans defaults True (scanner.py:6091), so this guarded path is live in production (paper). It is correctly scoped paper-only — orphan_close actions are dropped for is_live at scanner.py:6091, so no real money. Trigger requires position age/downtime > ~1300 bars on the timeframe AND the kernel staying flat in that direction within the replay window — an uncommon edge case, and the guard is an intentional trade-off (comments at scanner.py:6056-6059, paper_reconcile.py:212-214) to avoid wrongly orphaning warmup-band entries. Defect is real and reachable as described; impact is confined to the paper sandbox (corrupted track record, only an indirect path to money via promotion gates). LOW is appropriate.

### `DB-3` — pnl_pct is recorded on two different scales depending on which close path runs (kernel net equity-fraction vs gross leverage-inclusive position return)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** db  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5544-5550 (kernel net); forven/strategies/trade_state.py:268 (gross); forven/scanner.py:631-644 (_recent_strategy_returns consumer)`
- **Claim:** A kernel-finalized paper close stores pnl_pct = the kernel's NET equity-fraction, while a manual-exit, reconcile-sweep, or legacy close of a paper trade stores pnl_pct = close_trade_record's GROSS leverage-inclusive position return. The same strategy's book can therefore mix two incompatible pnl_pct scales.
- **Impact:** Kelly-mode sizing input is distorted when a book contains both kernel-closed and manual/sweep-closed paper trades (the gross values are ~1/size_fraction larger), and any per-trade-return statistic that aggregates pnl_pct mixes the two scales. pnl_usd (which drives paper equity) stays roughly consistent, so account equity is not materially affected.
- **Suggested fix:** Define one canonical pnl_pct semantics for recorded trades and make every close path conform — e.g. have manual/sweep paper closes also write the kernel-equivalent net equity-fraction, or have _recent_strategy_returns normalize by execution path.
- **Evidence:** Kernel override: `conn.execute("UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=?, ... ", (round(pnl_pct_net,8), round(pnl_pct_net,8), ...))` where pnl_pct_net is `float(trade.get('pnl_pct'))  # kernel net, equity-fraction` (scanner.py:5509,5544). Manual/sweep/legacy path: close_trade_record computes `pnl_pct = ((resolved_exit_price - entry_price)/entry_price)*signed*leverage` (trade_state.py:268) — a position return, not an equity fraction — and that value is NOT overridden for _kernel_handle_manual_exits (scanner.py:5717 calls _close_trade_db which only adjusts fees) or the sweep. _recent_strategy_returns reads raw pnl_pct across all closed trades for kelly sizing: `SELECT pnl_pct FROM trades WHERE ... status='CLOSED'` (scanner.py:631-638).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally exhibits the two-scale defect. KERNEL close (_kernel_close_recorded) writes pnl_pct = the kernel's NET equity-fraction: scanner.py:5509 reads pnl_pct_net = trade['pnl_pct'] (commented 'kernel net, equity-fraction') and scanner.py:5544-5545 does UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=? with round(pnl_pct_net,8). The kernel's pnl_pct is defined at execution_kernel.py:114 as pnl_pct = gross * size_fraction, where gross (line 111) = ((exit-entry)/entry)*sign*leverage - round_trip_drag — i.e. net-of-drag AND multiplied by size_fraction. By contrast, close_trade_record (trade_state.py:268) computes pnl_pct = ((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage (GROSS, no drag, no size_fraction) and persists it at line 302. The manual-exit path (scanner.py:5714) computes the same gross value and calls _close_trade_db (5717); _close_trade_db (3690-3746) only updates net_pnl_pct/fees_pct and never overrides pnl_pct, so the gross value stands. The mix is reachable in a single book: _kernel_handle_manual_exits (5699-5718) skips kernel_managed trades (5701) and closes only operator-opened MANUAL positions, so a kernel-managed strategy carrying a manual position will hold both kernel-net closes and manual-gross closes under the same strategy_id. Both cited consumers mix the scales: _recent_strategy_returns (scanner.py:631-638) feeds raw pnl_pct as kelly evidence at 4548-4549, and per-strategy statistics aggregate raw pnl_pct — paper.py:288-302 averages it into avg_pnl_pct (surfaced at 882) and analytics.py:636-639 computes AVG/MAX/MIN(pnl_pct) grouped by strategy (no net/gross rescaling; _normalize_trade_percent_value at paper.py:53-58 only multiplies by 100). The impact framing is accurate: pnl_usd stays on the same equity*size_fraction dollar scale on both paths (kernel pnl_usd=equity*net at 5511; manual pnl_usd=(price-entry)*units at 5715, units=equity*leverage*size_fraction/entry), so account equity is not materially affected. Note the kelly consumer at 4549 lives in legacy manage_positions, which a kernel strategy reaches only via flag-toggle/fallback (narrow), but the per-trade-% statistics consumers (avg/best/worst trade) are directly reachable for any kernel strategy with a manual position, which is enough to confirm. LOW is appropriate: it corrupts a displayed per-trade percentage / a sizing input, not money or position state.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All load-bearing claims verified against live code. (1) Kernel close override: scanner.py:5509 reads pnl_pct_net as the kernel NET equity-fraction (proven by line 5511: pnl_usd = equity_at_entry * pnl_pct_net) and scanner.py:5544-5550 writes UPDATE trades SET pnl_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=? with that net value. (2) Gross path: trade_state.py:268 computes pnl_pct = ((exit-entry)/entry)*signed*leverage — a leverage-inclusive position return, NOT an equity fraction. (3) Manual-exit path: scanner.py:5714 computes the gross leverage-inclusive value and passes it to _close_trade_db (scanner.py:3690-3746), which calls close_trade_record (writes gross pnl_pct) and only updates fees_pct/net_pnl_pct — it never overrides the pnl_pct column. So a manual SL/TP close persists the gross scale. (Cross-asset orphan close at scanner.py:5675 also uses gross close_trade_record but with exit==entry so pnl_pct≈0, no distortion.) (4) Consumer: _recent_strategy_returns (scanner.py:631-644) selects raw pnl_pct across all CLOSED trades for a strategy with NO scale normalization and NO execution_type filter, and is consumed ONLY by kelly sizing (guarded at scanner.py:4549 by sizing_mode=='kelly'). Scale relationship confirmed: net ≈ gross*size_fraction, so gross ≈ net/size_fraction. REACHABILITY/IMPACT (lens): kelly is NOT the default profile (sizing.py:255-268 default is 'atr'); it runs only for strategies explicitly assigned a kelly profile. kelly_fraction (sizing.py:74-95) is mathematically scale-invariant under a single uniform scale (win-rate from signs, payoff R from a ratio of magnitudes where a common factor cancels), so a uniformly-scaled book sizes correctly — only MIXING the two scales distorts R, exactly as claimed. Mixing on one strategy_id is genuinely reachable: _kernel_handle_manual_exits skips kernel_managed trades (scanner.py:5701) and closes manually-opened positions gross, while the kernel path closes kernel positions net, and the consumer reads both under one strategy_id. Equity is correctly stated as unaffected: _paper_equity sums pnl_usd (scanner.py:604) and both paths write dollar-correct pnl_usd. Net: a real, code-grounded parity/sizing defect that distorts kelly position sizing for a mixed book, with no equity corruption. Severity low is appropriate given the kelly-only profile gating plus the requirement of a mixed close-path book (typically operator manual intervention or live/legacy edge cases) — consistent with the finding's own framing.

### `DATA-5` — Staleness checks treat an unparseable/missing cache timestamp as FRESH (age is None -> use it)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** data  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:1695 (candle cache) and 6892 (live price cache); forven/market_cache.py:94-101 and 192-199 (age=None on parse failure)`
- **Claim:** Both staleness guards short-circuit on `cache_age is None` / `live_price_age is None` and use the cached data as if fresh. age becomes None precisely when updated_at is missing or unparseable — i.e. exactly the malformed-payload case where freshness is unknown. The safe default for a staleness guard is to treat unknown age as stale, not fresh.
- **Impact:** Narrow (the daemon always stamps a parseable updated_at), but if a payload's timestamp format ever changes/corrupts, every consumer treats that cache as permanently fresh and trades/marks off arbitrarily old data with no warning.
- **Suggested fix:** Treat age None as stale (require a parseable, recent updated_at to consider the cache fresh), or log+reject when age cannot be computed.
- **Evidence:** scanner.py:1695 `if cache_age is None or cache_age <= _CANDLE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS: return cached_df.tail(required_bars)`. scanner.py:6892 `if live_prices and (live_price_age is None or live_price_age <= _PRICE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS):` then live_prices_for_scan = live_prices (used for live execution marks when use_live_price_for_signal_price). market_cache.py:99-101 sets age via try/except -> None on failure.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code literally matches the claim. scanner.py:1695 `if cache_age is None or cache_age <= _CANDLE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS: return cached_df.tail(required_bars)` (inside the `if not cached_df.empty:` branch at 1694) and scanner.py:6892 `if live_prices and (live_price_age is None or live_price_age <= _PRICE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS): live_prices_for_scan = live_prices` both short-circuit on age==None and use the cached data as if fresh. (A third identical instance exists at scanner.py:6108 in the late-entry hop-in.) market_cache.py confirms age becomes None exactly on a missing/non-string/empty/unparseable `updated_at`: load_price_snapshot (lines 94-101) and load_candle_snapshot (lines 192-199) initialize `age_seconds = None` and only set it inside a try/except guarded by `isinstance(updated_at, str) and updated_at`. Crucially `rows`/`prices` are normalized independently of `updated_at` (`raw.get("rows")` / `raw.get("prices")`), so data can be non-empty while age is None — making the stale-as-fresh path reachable for a malformed payload. This is a genuine fail-open-on-unknown-staleness pattern: the safe default for a staleness guard is to treat unknown age as stale. Impact is correctly characterized as narrow/low: the only writers (publish_price_snapshot, publish_candle_snapshot, scanner fallback) always stamp a parseable `get_now().isoformat()` timestamp, so the precondition only arises under a timestamp-format regression or external KV corruption; it is not reachable in normal operation. The "permanently fresh" wording slightly overstates the transient-corruption case (the daemon republishes each tick), but holds under a format-change regression. Severity low (defensive/edge-case) is appropriate; unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Code matches the claim exactly. scanner.py:1695 `if cache_age is None or cache_age <= _CANDLE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS: return cached_df.tail(required_bars)` and scanner.py:6892 `if live_prices and (live_price_age is None or live_price_age <= _PRICE_CACHE_STALE_SECONDS):` both short-circuit on age==None and use the cached data as fresh. age becomes None precisely on a missing/unparseable updated_at: market_cache.py:94-101 (price) and 192-199 (candle) initialize age_seconds=None and only set it inside an isoformat try/except, leaving it None when updated_at is absent, non-string, or unparseable. The candle path is only reached when cached_df is non-empty (1694), so valid rows + None age are returned as fresh; for prices, scanner.py:6891 sets use_live_price_for_signal_price = execution_mode != "paper", so in LIVE mode the stale-but-treated-fresh marks feed execution, not just telemetry — confirming the impact reaches the live money path, not paper-only. This is a genuine fail-open where a staleness guard should fail-closed. However, reachability is narrow exactly as the finding admits: the only writers are publish_price_snapshot/publish_candle_snapshot (daemon.py:1450/1599 and the scanner-fallback at scanner.py:1713), both of which always stamp updated_at=get_now().isoformat(), a string the reader's datetime.fromisoformat(...replace("Z","+00:00")) always parses. So age==None with valid data present does not occur in normal operation — it requires KV corruption, manual tampering, or a future payload-format drift. No flag gates this either way; it is purely a defensive-robustness gap. Real and live-reachable in principle but practically unreachable absent corruption, which is consistent with the assigned low severity (low=defensive per the rubric). Severity unchanged.

### `FUNDING-LIFECYCLE-FLIP-3` — Ghost-recovery auto-close writes net = gross - fees with NO funding fold (live funding silently dropped on reconciled closes)

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** funding-lifecycle-flip  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:2248-2278`
- **Claim:** When a live position is missing on the exchange and auto-closed by reconciliation, net_pnl_pct is written as gross pnl_pct minus only the recovered exit FEE; funding is never folded on this path. This is NOT a double-fold (the concern raised), but it is the inverse gap: these closes carry no funding at all.
- **Impact:** Live trades closed via ghost/missing-on-exchange recovery have net_pnl_pct that omits carry cost, inconsistent with normally-closed live trades. Low frequency (recovery only) and funding may be unreadable for a vanished position anyway.
- **Suggested fix:** On recovered closes, also read/fold the position's funding (or at least flag net as funding-incomplete) so the recovered net is consistent with the normal close path once FLIP-1's sign is fixed.
- **Evidence:** risk.py:2270-2275: `_fees_pct = float(recovered_exit["fee_usd"]) / _margin; _net_pct = float(closed["pnl_pct"]) - _fees_pct; ... UPDATE trades SET fees_pct = ?, net_pnl_pct = ? ...` — no funding term. This path calls close_trade_record directly (2230-2247), not _close_trade_db, so funding is neither read nor folded.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. On the ghost/missing-on-exchange recovery path, forven/exchange/risk.py:2270-2275 computes net as gross minus only the recovered exit fee: `_fees_pct = float(recovered_exit["fee_usd"]) / _margin; _net_pct = float(closed["pnl_pct"]) - _fees_pct` then `UPDATE trades SET fees_pct=?, net_pnl_pct=? ...` — no funding term. This path calls close_trade_record (risk.py:2230 and 2241), NOT _close_trade_db. close_trade_record (trade_state.py:149-324) only computes gross pnl_pct/pnl_usd and never writes net_pnl_pct/fees_pct/funding, so the risk.py follow-up UPDATE is the sole writer of net here and omits funding entirely. By contrast the normal close path _close_trade_db (scanner.py:3713-3739) reads close_funding_usd from signal_data and subtracts funding_pct from net_pnl_pct, confirming the claimed inconsistency. _recover_exit_from_fills (risk.py:1788-1907) reads only `fee` and `closedPnl` from fills and never funding, corroborating the finding's own caveat that funding is effectively unavailable on this path (a vanished position never ran a normal _execute_direct close to persist close_funding_usd). The defect is real and reachable for live missing-on-exchange recovery. It is correctly characterized as the inverse gap (funding dropped), not a double-fold. Severity low is appropriate: it is a derived-metric fidelity gap on a rare recovery-only path (actual money was realized on-exchange; net_pnl_pct only feeds gates/post-mortems), funding magnitude is typically small, and folding it would require an extra cumFunding query the code does not make. Unchanged at low. (Separate, not-claimed observation: the ghost path also subtracts only the single closing-leg fee versus the normal path's round-trip 2*fee_bps.)
  - _reachability_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Verified against live code. risk.py:2270-2275 writes net_pnl_pct = closed["pnl_pct"] - (recovered_exit["fee_usd"]/_margin) with no funding term; a grep for "funding" across all of risk.py returns zero matches, so this reconciliation path never reads or folds funding. The path calls close_trade_record directly (risk.py:2230-2247), which lives in trade_state.py and also has zero funding logic (grep: no matches) — confirming the "not a double-fold; funding simply absent" claim. The inconsistency with normal closes is real: the standard live close path _close_trade_db (scanner.py:3676-3756) reads close_funding_usd / funding_usd (3713-3717, captured at 3419-3446 via cumFunding.sinceOpen, passed at 1288) and folds funding_pct = funding_usd/margin into net_pnl_pct at 3727-3739. This is a live-only path (Hyperliquid reconciliation of ghost trades that are OPEN in SQLite but missing on exchange) and is genuinely reachable (exchange-side stop/TP fill, liquidation, manual close). Severity stays low: the bug only affects net_pnl_pct, a derived/recorded accounting metric — the actual close already executed on the exchange, so no real money is lost and no position state is corrupted; it fires only on the rare recovery path; funding magnitude on perps is typically small; and as the finding notes, the normal funding source (a live position's cumFunding.sinceOpen) is unreadable once the position has vanished, so the omission is partly unavoidable with the existing mechanism. (Note: the ghost path's fees_pct is also exit-leg-only vs the normal round-trip 2*fee_bps*leverage — a separate, unclaimed inconsistency that doesn't alter this verdict.)

## NEEDS HUMAN REVIEW (5)

### `PROMOTION-GATE-PARITY-1` — Promotion robustness is validated regime-GATED but paper/live trade regime-UNGATED — strategies are approved on an execution path they never run on

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** promotion-gate-parity  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:10426; forven/scanner.py:6007; forven/policy.py:3464-3496 (->paper WFA enforcement), 3679-3684 (->live strict robustness)`
- **Claim:** The capital-bearing gates enforce robustness evidence computed with regime_gate=True (which BLOCKS entries in regime-incompatible bars), while the scanner kernel that actually produces paper/live fills runs regime_gate=False (ALL entries fire). A strategy whose edge survives WFA only because the gate removed its losing bad-regime trades will pass validation, then take exactly those regime-incompatible entries in paper/live. No leg of evaluate_promotion validates the ungated path the strategy actually trades.
- **Impact:** A regime-dependent strategy is promoted to paper (and later live, real money) on metrics that do not describe its actual trading. Its live equity curve can diverge sharply (extra losing entries the gate filtered out), so users act on validated numbers that the live engine cannot reproduce. For strongly regime-sensitive families this is effectively a guaranteed parity break.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the validation path match the execution path: either (a) run WFA/confirmation backtest with regime_gate=False (the paper scanner is the declared parity reference) so promotion metrics match what paper/live actually do, or (b) apply the regime gate in the scanner kernel (regime_gate=True) so live matches the validated backtest. They MUST be the same. If divergence is intentional, re-run a regime_gate=False WFA leg and gate on THAT before ->paper.
- **Evidence:** backtest.py:10426 `regime_gate = True  # walk_forward always uses regime gating`. scanner.py:6006-6007 `res = _bt.run_strategy_execution(... regime_gate=False, ...)`. The ->paper gate enforces the GATED WFA verdict: policy.py:3495-3496 `if enforce_wfa and wfa_pass_rate < min_pass_rate: return False, ...` reading `verdict_payloads.get("walk_forward")` (the regime_gate=True run), and reads gated OOS metrics policy.py:3351 `target_metrics = _unwrap_metrics_dict(metrics.get("out_of_sample", metrics))`. The ->live gate's robustness battery is likewise gated: policy.py:3679-3684 `_strict_robustness_reject(...)` reads WFA degradation / OOS Sharpe from the same gated metrics. _build_regime_gate_masks confirms the behavioral divergence: backtest.py:5854-5856 `# When regime_gate is disabled ... skip all regime` so ungated takes every entry.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): All literal citations check out and the structural divergence is real and reachable. (1) WFA always runs gated: backtest.py:10426 `regime_gate = True`. (2) The kernel that produces paper/live fills runs ungated: scanner.py:6007 `regime_gate=False`, and backtest.py:5856-5861 returns an all-True entry mask when the gate is off (every entry fires). (3) The ->paper gate enforces the GATED WFA verdict: policy.py:3469 sets `enforce_wfa = True` unconditionally and 3495-3496 rejects on `wfa_pass_rate < min_pass_rate` read from `verdict_payloads.get("walk_forward")` (the regime_gate=True run); OOS metrics at 3351 come from the gated WFA splits (backtest.py:498-499, 8474-8477). (4) The ->live strict battery reads the same gated metrics: policy.py:3679-3684.\n\nI independently verified the part the finding asserts but did not fully prove — that the EXECUTION path is genuinely ungated and is what deployed strategies actually run: scanner.py:6614-6623 routes both paper and live deployed strategies through manage_positions_via_kernel (legacy manage_positions is only a non-vectorizable fallback); that kernel path (scanner.py:6131-6143) opens directly from reconciler actions with NO regime gate; and scanner.py:6848-6852 FORCES relaxed_trade_filters=True in paper mode, which skips even the legacy _scan_asset_group regime gate at 6230-6231 (so the regime check at 6229 does not rescue paper). The live kernel path also bypasses it since manage_positions_via_kernel ignores the signal-matrix row entirely.\n\nThe 'no leg validates the ungated path' claim is accurate: the only gauntlet leg using regime_gate=False is the execution-profile SELECTION sweep (gauntlet/tasks.py:1303-1311), whose output is a sizing marker (gauntlet_selected_execution_profile), not a robustness/OOS/WFA verdict; run_confirmation_backtest (tasks.py:862) and _run_walk_forward (954) carry no regime_gate override and use the gated default (no regime_gate references exist in api_core.py/backtest routers). The comment at tasks.py:1309 explicitly singles out the selection sweep as the one leg matched to 'the paper scanner's kernel call (the parity reference),' confirming the validation legs are deliberately NOT matched to it.\n\nScope is correctly bounded: backtest.py:5879 makes the gate a no-op when a strategy has neither compatible_regimes nor adx_cap, so the divergence only bites regime-sensitive families — but regime.py:250-273 shows mean-reversion / explicit regime_filter / declared compatible_regimes strategies DO get a restrictive gate, so the affected set is non-trivial. For those, a strategy can clear the gated WFA fold-pass-rate floor precisely because the gate stripped its bad-regime losing trades, then take exactly those entries ungated in paper/live — a genuine parity break where the validated numbers cannot be reproduced.\n\nKeeping severity at high (not critical): it does not directly/silently lose money or corrupt positions — it is a validation-vs-execution divergence producing wrong numbers users act on. Two partial mitigations argue against escalation: the divergence is family-scoped, and the ->live gate additionally requires real ungated paper forward-evidence (min trades/days/positive paper return), so real capital is not allocated purely on the divergent gated metrics. High remains appropriate.
  - _reachability_ → **refuted** (sev: low): The finding's headline ("strategies approved on an execution path they never run on; no leg validates the ungated path") is contradicted by the code. The CONFIRMATION BACKTEST — the primary capital-bearing gate input — runs UNGATED: api_core.py:10641 `backtest_strategy(... regime_gate=False ...)` (the gauntlet confirmation_backtest step at gauntlet/tasks.py:862 routes through this `post_backtest_submit` path). That ungated run produces BOTH the top-level metrics (total_return/sharpe/max_dd, api_core.py:10668-10670) AND `out_of_sample` (api_core.py:10664), and they are persisted as the strategy's metrics blob. This exactly matches the scanner's `regime_gate=False` kernel (scanner.py:6007); the alignment is deliberate (gauntlet/tasks.py:1309 runs execution-profile selection `regime_gate=False  # match the paper scanner's kernel call (the parity reference)`).

The finding's specific evidence that policy.py:3351 reads gated OOS metrics is factually WRONG: `target_metrics = _unwrap_metrics_dict(metrics.get("out_of_sample", metrics))` where `metrics = _load_metrics_blob(row)` (policy.py:3347) — i.e. the UNGATED confirmation metrics, not a regime_gate=True run. So the gate's Sharpe/return/DD/OOS checks DO validate the ungated path the strategy actually trades; a regime-sensitive strategy's bad-regime losses are reflected there and must clear the thresholds.

The only genuinely gated leg is WFA (backtest.py:10426 `regime_gate = True`), enforced at policy.py:3495 (->paper fold-pass-rate) and policy.py:3223-3242 (->live degradation/OOS-Sharpe via _strict_robustness_reject). That is a narrow robustness-validation consistency nit, not the claimed parity/money break: a strategy must STILL pass the ungated confirmation backtest + OOS, and for ->live must also accumulate real ungated paper forward-test trades (policy.py:3662-3664 min_closed_trades/min_paper_days/positive return). The binding capital gates are ungated and match trading, so the claimed equity-curve divergence / money loss does not materialize. Severity downgraded to low for the residual WFA-leg gating inconsistency (worth aligning to regime_gate=False for consistency, but not capital-bearing).

### `DAEMON-EQUITY-FEED-RISK-STATE-1` — Transient exchange outage in paper mode feeds a "paper"-source fallback into the shared risk_state; the recovery tick (paper->non-paper) silently clears a fired daily_loss_halt and re-baselines the HWM (resetting drawdown to 0 and masking a pending kill-switch)

- **Severity:** HIGH  |  **Mission:** daemon-equity-feed-risk-state  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:2816-2844; forven/exchange/hyperliquid.py:1936-1958; forven/daemon.py:1117,1309-1317; forven/sim/clock.py:48-52`
- **Claim:** The risk auditor's punt is confirmed: the daemon CAN feed a transient paper-fallback equity into the live-scoped risk_state mid-session, and the subsequent paper->non-paper source transition clears an already-fired daily_loss_halt and resets the high-water mark. This is not gated by the equity sanity guard (which only checks magnitude, not the source transition).
- **Impact:** A legitimately-fired daily-loss halt is silently lifted by an unrelated transient exchange/network glitch + recovery, letting the engine resume opening positions after a halt the operator believes is still in force; the displayed HWM/drawdown reset to a flattering baseline (wrong numbers the operator acts on). In the supported paper-only build this defeats the safety control on paper money and corrupts the metrics users vet before going live; on the forced-live path (FORVEN_EXECUTION_MODE=live is honored per config.py:195-199, 211-214) the same shared key means a paper-era halt is cleared the instant live equity connects (paper->exchange), and the drawdown-reset behavior masks a pending kill-switch.
- **Suggested fix:** Do not let the paper fallback mutate the live-scoped risk_state: when source=="paper", either skip update_equity entirely (treat like _book_aware_account_value's None/skip) or write only to a sim-prefixed state. Make the paper->non-paper re-baseline fire ONCE on a genuine mode transition (gate on get_execution_mode() actually changing, persisted via a blocking write), never on an in-mode credential flap. Crucially, NEVER clear daily_loss_halt/kill state as a side effect of a source label change — require an explicit operator reset (reset_kill_switch / trading-halt-reset already exist). Add the source value to _default_risk_state_payload so prev_source can't silently default to "paper".
- **Evidence:** _book_aware_account_value's books-disabled branch returns get_account_value() verbatim (daemon.py:1117). In paper mode, when the exchange read fails / the account breaker is open, get_account_value swallows the error and returns a fallback labeled source="paper": `if get_execution_mode() == "paper": ... return {"accountValue": equity_f, ... "source": "paper"}` (hyperliquid.py:1936-1959) using last-known equity (~$10k), which is a PLAUSIBLE magnitude that passes _validate_equity_sample (the jump guard only rejects UPWARD jumps `eq > last * _EQUITY_JUMP_REJECT_MULT`, risk.py:2755). The daemon then calls update_equity(equity, acct.get("source","exchange")) (daemon.py:1309-1317). In _update_equity_locked, every accepted tick sets `state["equity_source"] = source` (risk.py:2817). So a transient outage tick sets equity_source="paper". On the very next tick the exchange read recovers (source="exchange"), and the re-baseline fires: `if prev_source == "paper" and source != "paper" and hwm > 0:` -> `state["daily_loss_halt"] = False; state["daily_loss_halt_date"] = None; hwm = account_equity` (risk.py:2826-2839) plus a fresh daily_risk start_equity (2840-2844). Because paper and live share the SAME unprefixed "risk_state" key outside a backtest sim (sim_kv_key only prefixes when is_sim_active(), clock.py:48-52), and _run_risk_cycle runs every tick regardless of mode (daemon.py:1417), this clears the SAME daily-halt flag that is_trading_allowed enforces for new entries (risk.py:3310). Resetting hwm to current equity also zeroes drawdown_pct, so a real drawdown that was approaching max_drawdown is forgiven and a kill-switch that was about to fire is suppressed.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every cited line checks out and the code literally exhibits the defect. (1) hyperliquid.py:1936-1959 returns source="paper" with last-known/$10k equity when the exchange read raises in paper mode; the success path returns source="exchange" (:1997-2004). _get_account_info_client (:795-808) only needs a wallet ADDRESS via a public info client (no signing), so paper mode with a configured wallet normally reads REAL equity as source="exchange" and a transient network/breaker failure flips a single read to source="paper" — the precise transient the finding needs. (2) daemon.py:1117 returns get_account_value() verbatim on the books-disabled branch (the books-enabled path hardcodes source="books_aggregate" at :1170, so the poison is specific to the books-disabled path actually cited). (3) daemon.py:1309-1317 forwards acct.get("source","exchange") into update_equity every tick (:1417). (4) risk.py:2816-2844: prev_source defaults to "paper" (and _default_risk_state_payload :2576-2583 omits equity_source, a second trigger), and on prev_source=="paper" and source!="paper" and hwm>0 it sets daily_loss_halt=False, daily_loss_halt_date=None, hwm=account_equity, and rewrites daily_risk.start_equity. The date-roll reset at :2812-2814 leaves a same-day halt intact, so the clearing is genuinely caused by the source transition. (5) drawdown_pct at :2866 becomes 0 after the HWM reset, masking a developing drawdown/kill-switch (:2914). (6) the sanity guard at :2755 only rejects UPWARD jumps, so the fallback (≈ last good equity) passes — not gated by source. (7) the key is shared: _get_risk_state/_save_risk_state use sim_kv_key("risk_state") which is unprefixed outside a sim (clock.py:48-52), and is_trading_allowed reads _get_live_risk_state() → unprefixed "risk_state" and blocks entries on daily_loss_halt (:3307-3311). The end-to-end sequence exchange->paper->exchange across consecutive risk ticks fires the re-baseline and re-enables entries after a fired halt; the HWM reset corrupts displayed drawdown on every such flap. One fairness nuance that does NOT negate the defect: in pure paper mode the risk loop tracks the real wallet read (forven does not trade it), so a daily_loss_halt firing from forven's own paper activity is less likely than the finding's wording implies; but the drawdown/HWM corruption triggers on any flap, and the halt-clear bites fully on the operator-forced-live path (config.py:195-199 honors FORVEN_EXECUTION_MODE=live, sharing the same key). Mechanism real, reachable, and severity "high" (silently clears a safety control and resets risk metrics the operator acts on) is appropriate — not critical because the worst money impact is gated behind the unsupported live override and a coincident transient.
  - _reachability_ → **refuted** (sev: low): The MECHANISM is real and every code-level claim checks out: the paper fallback returns source="paper" with a plausible ~$10k (hyperliquid.py:1936-1959); _validate_equity_sample only rejects UPWARD jumps so it passes (risk.py:2755); every accepted tick sets state["equity_source"]=source (risk.py:2817); the prev_source=="paper" and source!="paper" branch clears daily_loss_halt, re-baselines HWM, and resets daily start_equity (risk.py:2826-2844); prev_source defaults to "paper" and equity_source is absent from _default_risk_state_payload (risk.py:2576-2583, 2816); paper/live share the unprefixed "risk_state" key outside a sim (risk.py:2586-2619; clock.py:48-52); is_trading_allowed enforces daily_loss_halt off that key (risk.py:3305-3311); the risk cycle runs every tick (daemon.py:1417). HOWEVER the LENS (reachability & impact) refutes the stated high-severity harm. (1) LIVE path is closed: the fallback is gated on get_execution_mode()=="paper" (hyperliquid.py:1936); in live an outage raises (1960), and that raise is caught inside _book_aware_account_value's try (1097) -> except returns None (1172-1175), after which _run_risk_cycle bails on a non-dict WITHOUT calling update_equity (daemon.py:1301). So equity_source is never written "paper" mid-live-session and the recurring paper->non-paper flap cannot occur in live; the only such transition in live is the one-time startup re-baseline, which is the DESIGNED PNL-1 behavior. (2) PAPER path is benign: update_equity has a single caller (the daemon risk cycle, daemon.py:1314) and its equity comes only from the exchange read or a SELF-REFERENTIAL fallback — get_account_value reads daily_risk.current_equity / daemon_state.account_equity (hyperliquid.py:1940-1942), both written by update_equity / the risk cycle itself (risk.py:2886; daemon.py:416,1462). Paper-trade PnL never feeds update_equity, so daily_pnl_pct stays ~0 and daily_loss_halt cannot fire from paper activity (risk.py:2931): there is no "legitimately-fired" halt to clear, and with static testnet equity the HWM re-baseline ($10k->$10k) is a no-op, so no drawdown/kill-switch masking. (3) The risk_state HWM tracks account equity, not the strategy backtest/gauntlet metrics users vet before promotion, so the "corrupts the metrics users vet" claim is misattributed. The defect is thus a genuine latent design fragility (clearing safety state as a side effect of a source-label flip, prev_source defaulting to "paper") worth the suggested defensive fix, but the asserted high-severity money/state impact is not reachable in the supported paper-only build or on the forced-live path. Downgraded to low.

### `SIZE-1` — Selected `atr` profiles drop the 3% stop floor that `default_controls` has → size collapses to `risk_per_trade` *notional* (and no protective stop) when ATR is 0/unavailable

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** size  |  **Confidence:** medium
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/sizing.py:196-209,236-240,256-263; forven/strategies/execution_selection.py:92-97`
- **Claim:** The notional-collapse fix (a fixed 3% stop floor so atr-sizing never degenerates) was applied ONLY to `default_controls`, not to the `atr` candidate profiles that `execution_selection` actually assigns. When ATR is unavailable at entry, those selected profiles size off `risk_per_trade` as a raw notional fraction and produce no stop.
- **Impact:** For paper this silently mis-sizes (2% notional instead of risk-targeted) AND leaves the position with no stop — a held position can ride to a large loss if its signal-exit never fires. For live the position instead fails to open at all (the no-stop guard at scanner.py _execute_direct raises), so a 'deployed' atr strategy can intermittently fail to enter. Real-money loss is bounded by the live no-stop guard, but it is an incompletely-propagated fix and a paper/backtest behavior that contradicts the stated 'never collapse to flat notional' invariant for the profile class that is actually chosen.
- **Suggested fix:** Give the selectable atr candidates (execution_selection.candidate_profiles) the same 3% stop_loss_pct floor, OR make `entry_stop_dist_pct` fall back to DEFAULT_STOP_LOSS_PCT_FLOOR for any atr-mode profile when ATR<=0 (so the floor lives in one place and every atr profile inherits it).
- **Evidence:** `default_controls()` carries the floor: `"sizing_mode": "atr", "stop_loss_pct": DEFAULT_STOP_LOSS_PCT_FLOOR` (sizing.py:256-257, with DEFAULT_STOP_LOSS_PCT_FLOOR=3.0). But the selectable atr candidates have NO stop_loss_pct: `prof = {"sizing_mode": "atr", "risk_per_trade": risk, "atr_stop_multiplier": mult}` (execution_selection.py:94). For such a profile `entry_stop_dist_pct` returns None when ATR is missing/zero — the atr branch requires `atr_value > 0` (sizing.py:200-202) and there is no `stop_loss_pct`/`trailing_stop_pct` to fall through to (sizing.py:205-209). `size_fraction` then hits `return clamp01(ec["risk_per_trade"])` (sizing.py:240) i.e. a flat 0.02 NOTIONAL fraction (the ~8-25x undersize / piddly-position degeneracy), and in the kernel the stop is also skipped because `stop_dist_pct is None` (execution_kernel.py:261-263).
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every cited line checks out. (1) execution_selection.py:94 builds the selectable atr candidate as {"sizing_mode":"atr","risk_per_trade":risk,"atr_stop_multiplier":mult} with NO stop_loss_pct (only an optional take_profit_pct at 95-96). (2) The 3% floor lives ONLY in default_controls: sizing.py:256-257 sets "stop_loss_pct": DEFAULT_STOP_LOSS_PCT_FLOOR, =3.0 at sizing.py:60 — confirming the fix was not propagated to the chosen atr profiles. (3) normalize_execution_controls (sizing.py:144) does NOT inject a floor for atr mode, so the normalized profile keeps stop_loss_pct=None. (4) entry_stop_dist_pct (sizing.py:196-209): the atr branch requires atr_value>0; when ATR is None/0 it falls through to stop_loss_pct (None) then trailing_stop_pct (None) then returns None. (5) size_fraction (sizing.py:238-240): with stop_dist_pct=None the divide-by-stop guard is skipped and it returns clamp01(ec["risk_per_trade"]) — flat notional, the documented degeneracy. (6) execution_kernel.py:261-263: stop_price stays None when stop_dist_pct is None, so no protective stop is placed. The logic chain is exactly as claimed and contradicts the stated invariant (sizing.py:53-58 docstring) that atr-sizing must never collapse to flat notional. Reachability is genuine but edge-case: _compute_atr_series (execution_kernel.py:45-56) uses min_periods=1 + bfill + fillna(0.0), so ATR is positive unless the price window is perfectly flat (high==low) — rare in liquid crypto but possible for illiquid assets/fine timeframes/data gaps. Impact is accurately characterized: live fails closed (trading.py:1051 and :3337 raise "without a protective stop"; :788-791 "stop loss is required to size"), bounding real-money loss; paper mis-sizes to ~risk_per_trade notional AND holds with no stop. Medium is correct given real defect + parity break weighed against edge-case reachability and live fail-closed behavior.
  - _reachability_ → **needs_human_review** (sev: low): The propagation gap is code-real: default_controls() carries stop_loss_pct=DEFAULT_STOP_LOSS_PCT_FLOOR (sizing.py:257) but the selectable atr candidates do not (execution_selection.py:94), normalize_execution_controls does not re-add it (sizing.py:144 _opt_pos→None), entry_stop_dist_pct returns None for an atr profile when atr_value≤0 (sizing.py:196-209), and size_fraction(None) collapses to clamp01(risk_per_trade) flat notional (sizing.py:240) while the kernel skips the stop (execution_kernel.py:261-263). However, the stated money/state impacts are refuted or unreachable on the production paths.

(1) Default kernel/parity path (paper AND live, the path both use by default): the trigger requires atr_value≤0, but _compute_atr_series ends with .bfill().fillna(0.0) (execution_kernel.py:56) and TR=max(|high-low|,...) so ATR is never NaN and is 0.0 only for a perfectly flat prefix — essentially unreachable for real crypto OHLC at an entry past warmup. So neither the undersize nor the None-stop occurs in the kernel path.

(2) Live kernel path: _kernel_open_live_trade passes stop_loss=stop_price straight from the kernel with no fallback (scanner.py:5862,5880-5881), so it would hit the no-stop guard (scanner.py:3336-3337) only if the kernel emitted stop_price=None — again needs ATR=0, unreachable. The 'live fails to open' claim is therefore not reachable in practice.

(3) Legacy (non-parity) scanner path (~4505): atr_14 is read from the signal payload and CAN be None, so the SIZING undersize (≈2% flat notional vs risk-targeted) IS reachable here. But this path computes the protective stop independently with a 3% fallback (scanner.py:4541-4547) and unconditionally finalizes a safety-pct stop (scanner.py:4637-4644), so a stop is ALWAYS placed — refuting 'no protective stop', 'ride to a large loss', and 'live fails to open'. The reachable residual is a conservative UNDERsize (money-conservative, bounded, with a stop) on the non-default legacy path. Whether assigned-atr-profile strategies actually run on the legacy path with a signal lacking atr_14 is an empirical/data question I cannot resolve from code alone, hence needs_human_review with severity downgraded to low.

### `KCOPY-1` — Per-bar adapter 'both'-mode routes an undirected exit signal to LONG only, silently dropping the short exit (and contradicting its 'matches legacy' claim)

- **Severity:** MEDIUM  |  **Mission:** kcopy  |  **Confidence:** high
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/backtest.py:7033-7049 (adapter) vs forven/strategies/backtest.py:11008-11053 (legacy slow path)`
- **Claim:** In trade_mode='both', a per-bar strategy that opens shorts via direction-stamped entries but emits UNDIRECTED exit signals (the common 'flatten whatever is open' pattern) never receives its short exit on the kernel path; the exit is routed to the long side only.
- **Impact:** A per-bar-only 'both' strategy using flatten-style (undirected) exits will hold its short positions open past the intended exit; they close only via the kernel stop/TP/time-stop. Under the default atr profile a 2xATR stop bounds catastrophic loss, but the strategy's actual exit is dropped → degraded/wrong PnL. Backtest and paper both use the adapter (run_strategy_execution is tried first on both paths), so they agree with each other — this is a strategy-intent/legacy-semantics break, not a backtest-vs-paper break.
- **Suggested fix:** In 'both' mode, treat an undirected exit_signal as a flatten of BOTH open sides (set both long_x[i] and short_x[i]) to match legacy semantics, OR require 'both' strategies to stamp exit direction and fail-closed/flag when an undirected exit is seen with an open short. Correct the docstring claim either way.
- **Evidence:** Adapter (route_by_signal): `d = str(sig.get("direction") or "long").strip().lower(); side_short = d in ("short","sell","s")` (backtest.py:7036-7037) then `if sig.get("exit_signal"): if side_short: short_x[i]=True else: long_x[i]=True` (7045-7049). A bare exit (no direction) → d="long" → side_short=False → only long_x set; short_exits[i] stays False. The legacy both-mode walk instead runs two single-direction passes (10866-10896) and in each pass closes the active position on ANY exit regardless of direction: `if not signal.get("exit_signal") and not bool(forced_exit.iloc[idx]): continue` (11050) — no direction check — so a bare exit closes BOTH the long and the short. The adapter docstring claims this routing is 'matching the legacy 'both' loop' (6950-6953), which is false for undirected exits.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): Every code claim verified against live code. Adapter both-mode (backtest.py:7036-7049): `d = str(sig.get("direction") or "long")...` then `if sig.get("exit_signal"): if side_short: short_x[i]=True else: long_x[i]=True` — a bare/undirected exit yields d="long", side_short=False, so only long_x is set and short_x stays False. Signal.direction defaults to "long" (base.py:54, emitted by to_dict at base.py:99), so a flatten-style exit that omits direction is treated as long. `_normalize_directional_signal_payload` (backtest.py:6215-6254) coerces the 4 series independently and does NOT cross-route in both-mode (the long_only/short_only zeroing at 6248/6251 doesn't fire), so the all-False short_exits passes through. The kernel reads short_exits for the short leg (execution_kernel.py:210: `exit_series = signals.long_exits if direction=="long" else signals.short_exits`), so the short never takes the strategy's signal exit — only time_stop/stop/TP/regime-forced_exit (forced_exit is OR-ed into short_exits at 7196, the strategy exit is not). Legacy both-mode recurses into two single-direction passes (backtest.py:10866-10896); each reaches the inline loop where the EXIT branch has no direction check (11050: `if not signal.get("exit_signal") and not bool(forced_exit.iloc[idx]): continue`), so a bare exit closes the open short — confirming the divergence. The adapter is the default-live path (`_per_bar_kernel_adapter_enabled()` -> True default, backtest.py:6772). Docstring at 6950-6953 claims routing matches the legacy both loop, which is verifiably false for undirected exits (and for bare entries: legacy straddles long+short, adapter opens long only). The finding correctly notes this is a strategy-intent/legacy-semantics break, not a backtest-vs-paper break (both paths use the adapter and agree). Only soft spot: the "common pattern" characterization cites no specific in-repo strategy, but arbitrary per-bar both-mode strategies are reachable via the Strategy Creator, so the routing defect is real and reachable on the default path. Severity medium (edge-case/degraded) is appropriate: bounded by kernel stops and internally consistent across backtest/paper/live, but a flatten-style short is genuinely held past its intended exit.
  - _reachability_ → **needs_human_review** (sev: low): The MECHANICAL defect is verified exactly as described. backtest.py:7036-7037 maps a bare/undirected exit to d="long" -> side_short=False, and 7045-7049 then sets only long_x[i], never short_x[i]. The legacy both path (_run_signal_walk recursion, backtest.py:10866-10896) runs two single-side passes whose exit check at 11050 has NO direction filter, so a bare exit closes the active short -> the two paths genuinely diverge, and the docstring "matching the legacy 'both' loop" (6950-6953) is inaccurate for undirected exits. The pattern is idiomatic in this codebase: rule_engine.py:389 emits Signal(exit_signal=True) with no direction, and the AI template STRATEGY_TEMPLATE.md:351-353 falls back to direction="long" on exit-only bars. _normalize_directional_signal_payload (6215-6221) just coerces the 4 series and does NOT re-derive/repair exits, so the bug is not masked downstream.

HOWEVER the stated money/state impact (degraded/wrong PnL on backtest AND paper) is NOT reachable for any current strategy. The adapter only runs for per-bar-only strategies (gated by per_bar_kernel_adapter, default True). Running in 'both' mode requires supported_trade_modes to include 'both': get_strategy_supported_trade_modes (841-869) never adds 'both' unless declared, resolve_backtest_trade_mode (895-902) rejects it otherwise, and the scanner's _resolve_kernel_trade_mode (scanner.py:5336-5343) falls back to the natural mode on that rejection (test_gauntlet_workflow_tasks.py:65 confirms the gate fires for rsi_momentum). I found ZERO strategies (builtin/composite/custom) that declare supported_trade_modes with 'both'; every 'both'-capable builtin (stochastic/williams_r/keltner via _vectorized_directional_signals at 5629-5642) and the composites are VECTORIZED and bypass the adapter. The only ungated 'both' route is the cosmetic chart-trigger replay _resolve_trigger_trade_mode (paper.py:1996-1998) -> _kernel_trigger_markers, which only draws would-be triangles, not real trades.

So this is a real, cheap-to-fix latent correctness bug + misleading docstring on an effectively dead money path: it activates only if a future per-bar-only AI strategy declares 'both' support (the template already uses the undirected-exit pattern). Per the reachability lens, the medium/active-PnL framing overstates present reality. needs_human_review because the verified code defect is real (not refutable) yet currently unreachable on the execution/gauntlet paths, and future reachability depends on AI-generated strategy declarations I cannot verify. Severity lowered to low (latent/cosmetic today). Recommended: apply the suggested fix (treat an undirected exit in 'both' mode as a flatten of BOTH sides, or require directional exits and fail-closed/flag) and correct the docstring before any per-bar 'both' strategy ships.

### `RECON-2` — adopt-by-direction fallback can mis-bind a re-entry to a stale entry if the exact (direction, entry_time) match ever misses

- **Severity:** LOW  |  **Mission:** recon  |  **Confidence:** low
- **Location:** `forven/strategies/paper_reconcile.py:179-198 (adopt branch), 151-165 (close/backfill loop)`
- **Claim:** When the kernel's current open position has no EXACT (direction, entry_time) match, reconcile adopts ANY same-direction recorded OPEN (recorded_open_by_dir). If the primary key match between a kernel closed_trade and the recorded open it should close ever misses (canonical-timestamp parse divergence), the close loop will instead BACKFILL that round-trip as a brand-new closed trade while the adopt branch binds the still-open recorded row to the kernel's CURRENT (different) position — duplicating the old entry and dropping the real re-entry.
- **Impact:** Duplicate paper trade (backfilled old round-trip + adopted stale open) and a missing record of the real re-entry, corrupting paper equity and breaking backtest parity. Requires a canonical-timestamp match miss between two strings both derived from str(df.index[idx]); unlikely in normal operation but the adopt-by-direction construct converts any such miss into silent duplication rather than a no-op.
- **Suggested fix:** Gate the adopt fallback (recorded_open_by_dir) so it only fires when the kernel produced NO closed_trade for that direction this run, or require the adopted row's entry_price to be within a tolerance of the kernel position's entry; never adopt a direction whose round-trip was just backfilled.
- **Evidence:** Adopt: `r_dir = recorded_open_by_dir.get(direction)` ... `if r_dir is not None and id(r_dir) not in matched: refreshes.append(ReconcileAction("refresh", direction, entry_time, position=pos, recorded=r_dir)); matched.add(id(r_dir))` (paper_reconcile.py:184-187). The close loop only matches by exact key and otherwise backfills: `r = recorded_by_key.get(k)` ... `if r is None: if _recent(entry_time): backfills.append(...)` (paper_reconcile.py:157-160). The two loops use the same canonical key, so a match miss in one implies a backfill in the other plus an adopt in the open loop.
  - _code-truth_ → **confirmed** (sev: unchanged): The code literally exhibits the described defect. (1) The close loop matches a kernel closed_trade to a recorded open ONLY by the canonical key and otherwise backfills: paper_reconcile.py:156-160 (`k=_key(...)`; `r=recorded_by_key.get(k)`; `if r is None: if _recent(entry_time): backfills.append(...)`), and a miss there leaves the recorded open OUT of `matched`. (2) The adopt-by-direction fallback at paper_reconcile.py:184-187 fires whenever `r_dir is not None and id(r_dir) not in matched` — there is NO guard requiring entry_price tolerance or "no closed_trade produced for this direction this run." So a close-loop key miss makes the still-open recorded row eligible to be adopted/refreshed against the kernel's CURRENT (re-entry) position. (3) The backfill is not caught by dedup: scanner.py:5585 calls _kernel_trade_exists which (scanner.py:5404-5409) does a RAW-string match on kernel_entry_time — since the miss premise is that the recorded open's stored kernel_entry_time differs from the current kernel entry_time, this dedup also misses and _kernel_close_paper_trade (5587-5604) records a brand-new closed round-trip. (4) The adopt refresh (_kernel_refresh_paper_trade, scanner.py:5607-5627) writes only stop_loss/take_profit and stamps kernel_entry_time only when `_orphan` is set; a kernel-opened recorded trade carries kernel_entry_time so it takes the non-orphan branch in _kernel_recorded_trades (scanner.py:5368-5375) and is NOT `_orphan`. Hence the adopted row keeps its STALE entry_price while being bound to the new position. Net result exactly as claimed: a duplicate closed round-trip plus a persistently mis-bound open carrying the wrong entry price, while the real re-entry is never faithfully recorded — corrupting paper equity and breaking backtest parity. Reachability: the chain requires a canonical-timestamp divergence between the recorded open's stored kernel_entry_time and the current kernel entry_time for the same logical bar, coinciding with that direction closing AND re-entering in one kernel run. This is narrow but not hypothetical — the adopt branch's own comment (paper_reconcile.py:179-183) states it was built precisely because entry_time drifts across data-source switches (HL->Binance) or non-kernel paths, and _canonical_ts only normalizes format/tz drift, not genuinely different bar timestamps or naive-local-vs-UTC index shifts. The finding's LOW severity correctly reflects the rare trigger while acknowledging the state-corruption impact when it does fire; severity unchanged.
  - _reachability_ → **needs_human_review** (sev: unchanged): The CODE MECHANISM the finding describes is genuinely present. The close loop backfills on an exact-key miss (paper_reconcile.py:157-160) and the adopt-by-direction fallback binds ANY unmatched same-direction recorded open to the kernel's current position with no guard that a round-trip for that direction was just backfilled (paper_reconcile.py:184-187). So adopt-by-direction cannot distinguish "the recorded open IS the still-held position" from "the kernel already closed it and re-entered." That logical gap is real, and the suggested fix is sound.

However the finding's STATED TRIGGER is near-unreachable. kernel_entry_time is stored at open as exactly action.entry_time = str(df.index[idx]) (scanner.py:5468); on close the kernel emits str(df.index[idx]) for the same bar; _canonical_ts (paper_reconcile.py:74-90) absorbs space-vs-T and tz drift, so for clean hourly/4h candles the two strings canonicalize identically and the match cannot miss. The finding itself concedes this is "unlikely in normal operation."

The realistically reachable variant is the orphan/legacy open path (scanner.py:5376-5391): a recorded OPEN with no kernel_entry_time matches no kernel key and does trigger adopt-by-direction (the cross-asset guard at scanner.py:6079-6084 only removes asset-flip drift, not same-asset data-source drift).

But the claimed IMPACT ("corrupting paper equity, breaking backtest parity") is overstated for RECON-2's specific adopt+backfill scenario. When adopt fires the kernel HOLDS the direction, so no orphan_close runs (paper_reconcile.py:216-217); the only realization is the backfilled round-trip, and the adopted open's eventual close OVERRIDES pnl with the kernel net pnl_pct (scanner.py:5538-5552), so realized PnL nets out (round-trip once + re-entry once) and equity is not double-counted. For orphan rows the refresh even stamps kernel_entry_time to the current entry (scanner.py:5624-5625), so it converges and does not repeat each scan. The harm reduces to a confusing duplicate-looking history entry and a transiently mis-attributed open entry_price/opened_at (display/audit), not silent money loss. The equity-corrupting double-count (backfill + orphan_close booking one position twice) lives in the kernel-FLAT path, which is distinct from RECON-2.

Net: the construct gap is real but the finding as written (same-source parse-miss -> equity corruption + dropped re-entry) is not reachable via its stated trigger, and the equity-corruption impact is not established for the adopt+backfill case. It is reachable only via orphan/data-drift opens with a lower, display/audit-level impact. Borderline -> needs_human_review, severity low (unchanged).

## REFUTED (6)

### `LIVE-3` — Live kernel-managed positions never sync their exchange resting stop/take-profit when the kernel trails/moves it (refresh is DB-only) [high]
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:6146-6147 and 5607-5627 (initial stop placed at 5880-5881; live manual-exit short-circuit 6161-6163)`
- **Verifier reasoning:** code-truth:refuted — The finding's mechanical observations are correct but its load-bearing premise is false, so the described defect does not occur.

VERIFIED-TRUE parts: _kernel_refresh_paper_trade (scanner.py:5617-5626) is DB-only (writes stop_loss/stop_loss_price/take_profit/take_profit_price into signal_data via _update_trade_signal_data, no exchange call). The refresh dispatch at scanner.py:6146-6147 is hardcoded to _kernel_refresh_paper_trade and is NOT gated by is_live, while open_applier/close_applier ARE switched to live variants at 6093-6094. The open places a real resting stop/TP: _kernel_open_live_trade calls _execute_direct(\"open\", ..., stop_loss=stop_price, take_profit=target_price) at 5880-5881; _execute_direct refuses to open without a stop (3336-3337) and persists exchange_stop_order_id/exchange_take_profit_order_id (3310-3311). _adjust_protective (api_domains/paper_control.py:713-725) does cancel+replace the resting order for manual live edits.

FALSE PREMISE: The finding asserts refresh carries the kernel's CURRENT stop_price/target_price 'which trail/move over the trade's life.' They do not. In execution_kernel.py the open-position dict sets stop_price (line 273) and target_price (line 274) ONCE at entry and never reassigns them; a grep for stop_price/target_price/extreme mutation shows the ONLY per-bar mutation is at[\"extreme\"] (line 249). The trailing level is computed dynamically as eff_stop = extreme*(1 - sign*trail_pct) (lines 218-224) and is never stored back into stop_price. There is no stop-to-breakeven/moving-target feature (the only 'breakeven' hits are pnl==0 trade-count metrics in backtest.py). Because the kernel deterministically replays full history each scan, stop_price for a given entry is identical every scan, so refresh writes back the SAME static value already on the exchange from the open. There are no moved levels for the DB-only applier to fail to propagate; the suggested fix's 'if pos.stop_price differs from recorded' guard would be a perpetual no-op.

The trailing EXIT is enforced kernel-side: a bar breaching eff_stop makes the kernel emit a 'close' action, handled on live by _kernel_close_live_trade (5885-5928) via a real reduce-only order — a path that already has a live-specific applier. So trailing execution does not depend on the refresh applier.

A separate, debatable design point exists (live trailing is enforced only at scan cadence, with the exchange resting order pinned at the fixed initial stop as a safety net; a prolonged daemon outage with a slow non-gapping drift could exit at the wider fixed stop rather than the trailed level). But that is a different concern from the one under review, mirrors paper's own scan-cadence enforcement, and the backtest itself fills gap-throughs at the bar open (min(fill_price, eff_stop), line 227) not at the trailed level — so the 'materially larger loss vs validated backtest/paper' impact as stated is not supported. Hence refuted; corrected_severity low to reflect only the minor residual design consideration. || reachability:refuted — The finding's core causal premise is false. The kernel does NOT trail/move stop_price or target_price. In execution_kernel.py:273-274 these fields are set once at entry and never reassigned; the trailing stop is computed transiently as `eff_stop` each bar from `at["extreme"]`/`at["trail_pct"]` (lines 218-224) and only `at["extreme"]` ratchets (line 249) — the trailed level is never written back into `at["stop_price"]`. A codebase-wide grep confirms there is no breakeven/stop-to-breakeven or moving-target logic anywhere. Consequently the refresh action's `pos` (= open_positions[direction]) always exposes the INITIAL fixed stop/target, so the DB write at scanner.py:5618-5626 records a CONSTANT level equal to what was placed on the exchange at open. There is no "trailed level" being dropped, and the suggested fix's trigger ("when pos.stop_price/target_price differ from the recorded levels") would never fire for a kernel trade.

The claimed live<->backtest/paper parity break is also incorrect. The trailing stop is enforced identically on paper and live: the scanner advances the same kernel one closed bar at a time and emits a `close` action when the trailing level is breached; for live, close_applier = _kernel_close_live_trade (scanner.py:6094) places a real reduce-only market order at scan time, matching paper's scan-granular behavior. The open-time exchange resting stop at the fixed level is therefore an EXTRA live safety net, not a divergence from paper/backtest.

True-but-non-load-bearing sub-facts: the refresh dispatch (scanner.py:6146-6147) is not gated by is_live and uses the paper applier for both, and that applier makes no exchange call. But with no moved level to sync, these do not produce the described money-losing/parity-breaking defect.

Reachability note: live_kernel_execution defaults ON (scanner.py:5828) but live trades HL testnet unless FORVEN_ALLOW_MAINNET=1 (5824), so real-money blast radius is gated anyway.

Residual, differently-framed concern (not the finding's claim): a trailing-stop-ONLY live strategy (no stop_loss_pct, non-ATR sizing) leaves stop_price=None (execution_kernel.py:261-263), so _execute_direct is called with stop_loss=None (scanner.py:5862,5880) and NO resting stop is placed — during a daemon freeze there is no on-exchange protection. This is defensive/edge and not parity-breaking (paper has no resting order either); it merits a separate low/medium item, not this one.

### `BOOT-4` — Live position adopted at boot with a FAILED protective-stop placement is left unprotected and is not retried by the periodic reconcile [medium]
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:2126-2186; periodic reconcile forven/daemon.py:1509-1514; reconcile_all_books default adopt forven/exchange/risk.py:2342-2347`
- **Verifier reasoning:** code-truth:refuted — The finding's core mechanism is wrong. It claims protective-stop repair "only runs inside the adopt-missing branch" (risk.py:2127) and that "once the trade is in SQLite the adopt branch never fires again... the position is never re-repaired within the session." But reconcile_exchange_positions has a SECOND repair path the auditor overlooked: the matched path at risk.py:2023-2094. That branch runs `for asset, position in hl_by_asset.items(): if asset in db_by_asset:` (2023-2024) on EVERY reconcile with no dependence on adopt_missing_in_sqlite, and calls `_repair_position_protection(position, matched_trade=matched_open_trade, ...)` at risk.py:2054. A boot-adopted trade is inserted status='OPEN' (selected at risk.py:1986), so on the next reconcile it is in db_by_asset and matches here. _repair_position_protection is not read-only: it recomputes live protection (risk.py:1319), returns early only if fully_protected (1326-1327), otherwise derives a stop and actively calls place_protective_stop(...) at risk.py:1360-1366, recording protection_restored on success (2072-2083) or re-recording the discrepancy on failure (2084-2093). The periodic reconcile reaches this path: daemon.py:1509-1514 calls reconcile_all_books(_get_testnet()) every >600s, which delegates to reconcile_exchange_positions (books-off fast path risk.py:2378 or per-book passes risk.py:2416). Therefore a boot-adopted position whose stop placement failed IS re-repaired on the next periodic reconcile and every one thereafter — refuting "never re-repaired within the session." The auditor's suggested fix already exists as the matched path. The only residual truth is a bounded exposure window of up to one reconcile interval (~10 min) between the failed boot placement and the first periodic retry, which is inherent cadence, not the described defect — hence low, not medium. || reachability:refuted — The finding's core claim — protective-stop repair runs only in the adopt-missing (boot-only) branch and a recovered position is "never re-repaired within the session" — is contradicted by the code. There are TWO call sites of _repair_position_protection, not one. The finding only accounts for the adopt branch (risk.py:2127, gated by `if adopt_missing_in_sqlite:`) and missed the matched-position branch at risk.py:2054, which sits inside `if asset in db_by_asset:` (risk.py:2024) and is NOT gated by adopt — it runs on every reconcile pass. After boot adoption, _insert_recovered_trade makes the position an OPEN SQLite trade (risk.py:2136) and it is added to db_by_asset. On the next periodic reconcile, db_trades is re-queried via `SELECT * FROM trades WHERE status = 'OPEN'` (risk.py:1986), so the adopted trade is now in db_by_asset while the exchange still reports it in hl_by_asset; the matched branch (risk.py:2023-2094) therefore fires and re-calls _repair_position_protection (risk.py:2054). That function returns early only when fully_protected (risk.py:1326-1327); otherwise it re-derives a stop and re-attempts place_protective_stop (risk.py:1354-1366), persisting on success via _persist_trade_protection_metadata (risk.py:2067) and re-raising a missing_protection discrepancy on failure (risk.py:2086) so it retries on the next pass. The periodic reconcile reaches this code: reconcile_all_books(_get_testnet()) (daemon.py:1509-1514, adopt default False) routes to reconcile_exchange_positions (risk.py:2378/2416), which contains the matched branch. The code comment at risk.py:2030-2032 confirms intent: "the live reconcile legitimately repairs their protection here."
