The finding's own suggested fix (a periodic-reconcile-driven repair sweep for OPEN trades whose protection != protected) is already implemented by this matched branch. The only residual is a bounded transient: between the failed boot placement and the next periodic reconcile (<=600s per daemon.py:1481) the position is unprotected, but the recovery gate blocks new entries during that window — far short of the permanent unprotected state claimed. Hence refuted; residual risk is at most low.

### `RESTART-3` — Live trail-only kernel positions place NO resting exchange stop; during a daemon restart/freeze they are fully unprotected (trailing/time-stop/signal exits are bot-enforced only) [high]
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:5862, forven/scanner.py:5880-5881, forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:261-277, forven/strategies/execution_kernel.py:218-231`
- **Verifier reasoning:** code-truth:refuted — The finding's described mechanics up to the _execute_direct call are accurate: for a trail-only strategy the kernel leaves stop_price=None (execution_kernel.py:261-263; trailing level computed in-loop at 218-231/275, never written to stop_price), the reconciler passes the kernel position through as action.position (paper_reconcile.py:198/207), and _kernel_open_live_trade reads stop_price=pos.get("stop_price")=None (scanner.py:5862) then calls _execute_direct("open", ..., stop_loss=stop_price=None, ...) (scanner.py:5880-5881). HOWEVER, the auditor overlooked the fail-closed guard at the top of _execute_direct's open branch: scanner.py:3336-3337 — `if stop_loss is None and not is_sim_active(): raise ValueError(f"refusing to open {trade_id} without a protective stop")`. is_sim_active() (forven/sim/clock.py:44-46) reads a ContextVar set only during deterministic simulation/replay; on the real live daemon path it is False, so in live a stop_loss=None open RAISES before market_order(...) is ever called. The exception is caught and logged at the caller's try/except (scanner.py:6154). Therefore a trail-only live kernel position is NOT placed on the exchange with no resting stop — the open is refused entirely (fail-CLOSED). The finding's impact ("a trail-only live position is open with zero downside protection during a restart/freeze → unbounded real-money loss") cannot occur because such a position can never be opened via this path. The claim that this is "a fail-open where it must fail-closed" is the inverse of the actual behavior. Note one genuine but out-of-scope residual: _open_trade_db (5873) and register (5877) execute before the guard raises, so a refused open leaves a phantom DB open-row + risk slot with no real exchange position — a bookkeeping inconsistency, and the opposite of an unprotected real-money position, not the defect this finding describes. Refuted; downgraded from high since the money-loss/unprotected-position scenario does not exist. || reachability:refuted — The kernel-level mechanism is real but the impact is refuted by a fail-CLOSED guard the finding omitted. Confirmed pieces: (1) execution_kernel.py:261-263 leaves stop_price=None for a trail-only profile (no stop_loss_pct, sizing_mode!='atr') because the condition `ec["stop_loss_pct"] is not None or ec["sizing_mode"]=="atr"` is False even when stop_dist_pct is non-None; trail_pct/extreme are carried instead (lines 219-224, 275). (2) scanner.py:5862/5880-5881 passes that stop_price through as `_execute_direct("open", ..., stop_loss=stop_price=None, ...)`. (3) live_kernel_execution defaults True (scanner.py:5828), so the path is reachable.

REFUTATION: _execute_direct does NOT place a stopless order. scanner.py:3336-3337 — `if action == "open": if stop_loss is None and not is_sim_active(): raise ValueError("refusing to open {trade_id} without a protective stop")`. is_sim_active() defaults False (sim/clock.py:10) and is only True inside an isolated simulation context, never in production live/testnet. The raise occurs BEFORE market_order() at line 3369, so no exchange order is ever placed. The queued-intent path guards identically (scanner.py:1050-1051: "trade execution requires a protective stop"). Therefore a trail-only position can never open on the exchange, and every live position that DOES exist necessarily passed this guard and carries a resting stop_loss_price (line 3361). The finding's premise of a "fully unprotected" live position riding to an unbounded loss during a daemon outage cannot occur, and its "fail-open where it must fail-closed" framing is exactly inverted — the code fails closed.

Residual (different, lower-impact issue, NOT RESTART-3): _kernel_open_live_trade inserts the DB record (scanner.py:5873) and calls register() (5877) before _execute_direct raises, so a trail-only live open would orphan a DB "open" row with no exchange exposure and propagate the ValueError. That is a phantom-DB / "trail-only strategies silently can't trade live" defect with no adverse-price money risk — not the unbounded-loss unprotected-position scenario claimed. Downgrading from high to low to flag that residual; the headline defect is refuted.

### `DATA-4` — Source-divergence promotion gate reads raw settings (so it's silently OFF until a settings save) and is fail-open even when on — the Binance-vs-HyperLiquid divergence rarely actually blocks [medium]
- **Location:** `forven/policy.py:1867-1875 and 1978 (reads kv_get('forven:settings') raw); 1877/1900-1911 (fail-open); forven/dataeng/settings.py:52-66 (default enabled=True); forven/api_core.py:2228 (defaults only merged in _load_settings_payload)`
- **Verifier reasoning:** code-truth:refuted — The literal code reading is accurate: evaluate_promotion reads the RAW kv blob (policy.py:1978 `general_settings = kv_get("forven:settings")`) and passes it to _evaluate_source_divergence_gate (policy.py:2027); the gate only locates source_reconciliation if data_engine_settings is present in that raw dict (policy.py:1868-1873), else cfg={} and `not cfg.get("enabled")` returns True/"source reconciliation disabled" (policy.py:1874-1875). Fail-open branches (policy.py:1900-1911, 1920-1923, 1926-1927) are as described.

However, the finding's PRIMARY impact — "silently OFF until a settings save" — is wrong. The raw forven:settings blob is materialized with the merged defaults at API startup with NO operator save: api_core.py:209 runs seed_default_research_settings() inside _on_startup; that function (api_core.py:2263-2273) sets `payload = _load_settings_payload()` which injects data_engine_settings via _merge_data_engine_settings_payload (api_core.py:2228, source_reconciliation enabled=True). On a fresh install raw={}, so research_settings differs from defaults -> should_persist=True -> _save_settings_payload(payload) writes the FULL payload (line 2271 only overrides research_settings; data_engine_settings remains). api.py:408 runs `await _on_startup()` BEFORE spawning the headless brain loop (api.py:447-450) that drives promotions and the in-process daemon (api.py:467-483); the Tauri shell launches `python -m forven.api` (comment api.py:467-471). So evaluate_promotion runs in the same API process against the shared DB AFTER the seed, and kv_get("forven:settings") at policy.py:1978 returns a dict that DOES contain data_engine_settings.source_reconciliation.enabled=True. The gate is therefore enabled-by-default after first boot, not disabled-until-operator-save.

The finding's second half (fail-open when enabled: block_when_missing defaults False so missing/stale/unparseable readings ALLOW) is literally true per code, but it is the explicitly documented, intended posture (policy.py:1862-1865; dataeng/settings.py:47-66) and the finding itself calls it "fail-open by design" — that is a risk-appetite choice, not a defect. A narrow residual exists (an upgraded install whose stored research_settings happen to exactly equal current defaults could keep should_persist=False and leave the raw blob without data_engine_settings, disabling the gate), but that is an edge case, not the medium-severity mechanism claimed, and any UI settings save (_apply_settings_section -> _load_settings_payload, api_core.py:2346) also materializes it. Refuting the headline; residual is low. || reachability:refuted — The gate DOES read the raw blob (policy.py:1978 `general_settings = kv_get("forven:settings")`, passed unmodified to the gate at policy.py:2027; policy.py:1869 reads `general_settings.get("data_engine_settings")`), so that code fact is true. But the finding's load-bearing premise — "on any install the raw blob has no data_engine_settings key, so cfg={} and the gate returns 'disabled' despite enabled=True" — is refuted by both the code and the live DB.

(1) Startup seeding materializes the key. api_core.py:209 calls seed_default_research_settings() (api_core.py:2263-2273): it sets `payload = _load_settings_payload()` (line 2265), which at api_core.py:2228 merges data_engine_settings defaults (source_reconciliation.enabled=True), and on first run (should_persist=True, since research_settings is None != default) writes the FULL payload back to the raw blob via _save_settings_payload (line 2272). So after the API runs once the raw blob carries data_engine_settings — the gate is NOT silently disabled-by-default on a fresh install.

(2) Live DB evidence on this install: kv key forven:settings HAS data_engine_settings, with source_reconciliation = {"enabled": false, "max_divergence_pct": 2.0, "block_when_missing": false, "staleness_hours": 24, "min_overlap_bars": 20}. So cfg is NOT {} (the finding's scenario does not occur here), and the gate is off because enabled is persisted as false — not because of a raw-vs-merged read defect.

(3) The suggested fix would not help. merge_data_engine_settings_payload (dataeng/settings.py:79-99) preserves the persisted value (_merge_nested returns current when not None), so reading via load_data_engine_settings() would also yield enabled=False on this install. The persisted False (stale old-default or operator setting) is what disables the gate, and merging cannot override it.

(4) The precompute job is scheduled (scheduler.py:3120-3128, every 4h) and reads merged settings (source_reconciliation.py:58), so the data half works; the fail-open-when-missing behavior (policy.py:1877/1900-1906) is real but explicitly by-design (docstring 1862-1865, settings.py:47-59) and is moot when the gate is disabled anyway.

Residual (downgraded to low): a narrow window remains where an install's blob has data_engine_settings but lacks the source_reconciliation sub-key (persisted by an old version) — then the raw read gives cfg={} while merged would give enabled=True. That is a legitimate but minor defensive inconsistency, not the medium "silently OFF by default, fix=read merged" impact claimed; the startup seed materializes the sub-key for fresh installs and this install already has it.

### `LIVE-EXCHANGE-RECONCILE-5` — reconcile_exchange_positions reads-decides-acts (ghost-close, adoption INSERT) without _POSITION_LOCK, racing the scheduler's concurrent open/close path [medium]
- **Location:** `forven/exchange/risk.py:1985-2201; contrast forven/exchange/risk.py:525, 733, 762`
- **Verifier reasoning:** code-truth:refuted — The lock-absence is literally true (reconcile_exchange_positions opens `with get_db() as conn:` at risk.py:1985 with no _POSITION_LOCK, while can_open/register/release hold it at 525/733/762), and all cited mitigations are real (only_if_open guard trade_state.py:173, reduce_only=True hyperliquid.py:1882, idx_trades_unique_open migrations.py:344). BUT the finding's harmful IMPACT is not reachable because its mechanism is inverted. The claim is "a just-placed exchange open whose SQLite insert has NOT yet landed is seen by reconcile as missing_in_sqlite / duplicate-adopt." The actual open ordering is SQLite-insert-FIRST, exchange-order-SECOND in BOTH live paths: kernel path inserts the OPEN trades row via _open_trade_db (scanner.py:5873) then places the order via _execute_direct (5880); legacy path does _open_trade_db (4722) then _open_via_execution (4753), with the comment at 4734-4735 explicitly stating "the INSERT raised BEFORE any exchange call." _open_trade_db (3805-3829) commits a status='OPEN' row and returns the trade_id that the exchange call then needs, so the insert structurally precedes the order. Therefore there is NO window where the exchange holds an engine-opened position that SQLite lacks; reconcile can never see such a position as missing_in_sqlite or adopt it via this race, so the claimed entry-blocking discrepancies and startup duplicate-adoption do not occur. Additionally the suggested fix is misdirected: reconcile reads the `trades` table (risk.py:1986), which _open_trade_db writes WITHOUT _POSITION_LOCK; the lock only guards portfolio_positions (register/release), so acquiring it in reconcile would not serialize against the trades-table insert. A genuinely orphaned exchange position (exchange has it, SQLite doesn't) only arises from real recovery scenarios (manual trades, prior-run divergence), which adoption is designed for. Note for a human follow-up (separate from this finding): the REVERSE window — SQLite OPEN row present while the exchange order is still in-flight — could in principle let an unlocked reconcile ghost-close a freshly-opened live trade; there is pending_open_reconcile handling for failed opens, but that is a differently-shaped concern and is NOT what this finding claims. || reachability:refuted — The structural facts are correct but the causal mechanism is inverted, so the claimed defect is not reachable. CONFIRMED: reconcile_exchange_positions (risk.py:1924) does its read-decide-act under a plain `with get_db()` (risk.py:1985) with no _POSITION_LOCK, while can_open/register/release do hold it (risk.py:525/733/762); close_trade_record's only_if_open guard (trade_state.py:173) and close_position's reduce_only=True (hyperliquid.py:1882) are accurate. REFUTED: the finding's window — "a just-placed exchange open whose SQLite insert has not yet landed is seen as missing_in_sqlite" — cannot occur because every live open path commits the SQLite OPEN row BEFORE placing the exchange order. (a) Kernel/legacy path: _open_trade_db (scanner.py:4722, INSERT ... 'OPEN' at 3822) → register (4748) → _open_via_execution which sends the order (4753). (b) _kernel_open_live_trade: _open_trade_db (5873) → register (5877) → _execute_direct("open") (5880). (c) execute_trade_intent requires the trade row to already exist (1167-1168) before _execute_direct (1188). get_db() commits on context exit (db.py:449), so by the time the order reaches Hyperliquid the OPEN row is durably visible to the reconcile's separate connection. A concurrent reconcile therefore always finds the asset in db_by_asset and takes the matched-protection branch (risk.py:2023-2094) — never missing_in_sqlite (2198) and never adoption (2095). The adoption-failure narrative is backwards too: the real insert lands first; an adoption insert would hit idx_trades_unique_open and is caught/skipped as duplicate_open_recovery_skipped (risk.py:2146-2156), not stranded. At startup (adopt=True) the scanner is gated OFF during the preflight (recovery_active/checking, daemon.py:1883-1889; the separate scanner thread reads this KV and keeps entries blocked per the comment at 1858), removing the concurrent-open window entirely. Finally, _POSITION_LOCK guards portfolio_positions, not the trades table (the trades table is serialized by idx_trades_unique_open on insert and only_if_open on close), so the suggested fix targets the wrong lock. Residual (not the claimed defect, hence low): a window of the OPPOSITE shape exists — the OPEN row is committed before the exchange shows the fill, so an interleaving reconcile could treat an in-flight live open as a ghost — but the finding explicitly disclaims the close/ghost direction, the periodic reconcile only runs every 600s (daemon.py:1481), and any ghost close is itself bounded by only_if_open + reduce_only. Verdict: refuted; downgrade to low.

### `FUNDING-LIFECYCLE-FLIP-1` — Live funding fold sign is INVERTED vs HyperLiquid's actual cumFunding convention (and vs the backtest) — every live trade's carry cost is flipped [critical]
- **Location:** `forven/scanner.py:3415-3418, 3432, 3686-3688, 3724-3739`
- **Verifier reasoning:** code-truth:refuted — The finding's central empirical premise is false. It correctly establishes that Hyperliquid's userFunding ledger uses positive usdc = funding RECEIVED, but then ASSUMES cumFunding.sinceOpen (read at scanner.py:3429-3432 from clearinghouseState assetPositions) "shares this sign." Live HL API data (using the finding's own address 0x010461c14e146ac35fe42271bdc1134ee31c703a) proves the two endpoints use OPPOSITE conventions. Decisive natural experiment, coin ME: a recently-opened LONG whose entire funding history fits the query window has userFunding ledger sum = +490.14 (received; funding was predominantly negative so the long receives) but cumFunding.sinceOpen = -490.32 — same flow, magnitudes matching to 0.04%, opposite sign. Therefore cumFunding.sinceOpen = -(net usdc received), i.e. positive sinceOpen = funding PAID (a cost) — exactly what the code comment at scanner.py:3416-3417 states. Multiple other window-representative coins (MINA short paying → sinceOpen +455; kNEIRO long receiving → sinceOpen -523; TRUMP short paying → sinceOpen +948; kBONK short receiving → sinceOpen -926) all confirm positive=paid. The finding's only cumFunding "corroboration" (BNB long sinceOpen=+1043.59 claimed as receiving) is wrong: live data shows BNB funding was predominantly POSITIVE (142 vs 38 ticks) and its ledger sum is -78.98 (PAID), so the positive sinceOpen correctly reflects a cost. Consequently scanner.py:3738-3739 (funding_pct = funding_usd/margin; net_pnl_pct -= funding_pct) is CORRECT: a received-funding position has negative cumFunding.sinceOpen, so net -= negative RAISES net — matching the backtest's signed funding PnL at backtest.py:6332 (funding_pnl = -sign*funding_sum*... then pnl_pct += funding_pnl). No sign inversion, no 2x error, no parity break, and funding-harvest strategies are NOT mis-scored. The claimed critical money/state defect does not exist. (Note: a separate, unclaimed question of margin-vs-notional normalization between the live margin-fraction fold and the backtest's leverage-inclusive funding_pnl could merit its own review, but that is not what this finding alleges and does not involve a sign flip.) Verdict: refuted; severity downgraded to low as there is no real defect. || reachability:refuted — REFUTED by exact, reproducible live HL data. The finding's claim hinges entirely on one external fact: the sign convention of HL's cumFunding.sinceOpen. I verified it directly against api.hyperliquid.xyz (public info endpoint) using the finding's own address (0x010461...703a).

Step 1 — ledger convention (the finding got this right): 6/6 per-event userFunding deltas confirm received=positive usdc, paid=negative (e.g. BTC long, fundingRate −3.25e-6 → long receives → usdc +0.134; DYDX long, fundingRate +1.25e-5 → long pays → usdc −0.446).

Step 2 — the decisive cumFunding reconciliation: PURR is LONG (szi=+208573); its last size-change was 3 funding-hours ago. The ledger usdc deltas since that change sum to EXACTLY −0.66909 (long paying positive funding → negative usdc). HL's cumFunding.sinceChange for PURR = EXACTLY +0.66909. Equal magnitude, OPPOSITE sign ⇒ cumFunding = −(ledger sum). Hence positive cumFunding = funding PAID = a cost — precisely the convention the code comment (scanner.py:3416-3417) states and the code applies: funding_pct = funding_usd/margin; net_pnl_pct -= funding_pct (scanner.py:3738-3739). The finding conflated the userFunding LEDGER usdc field (received=+) with the cumFunding field (paid=+, its negation); they are opposite-signed. Its cumFunding "corroborations" (BNB/AVAX snapshots) are non-probative — a single hourly funding-rate sign cannot reveal the sign of a cumulative integral over the whole hold — and live data even contradicts the cited BNB case (BNB funding is currently +1.25e-5, long PAYING, with sinceOpen +1043.59, i.e. positive=paid, matching the code).

Parity also holds: backtest (backtest.py:6332, funding_pnl = -sign*funding_sum*… then pnl_pct += funding_pnl) reduces pnl when a long pays; live subtracts positive(=paid) cumFunding from net. Both charge paid funding as a cost and credit received funding (negative sinceOpen → net -= negative → net rises). No sign inversion, no backtest/live parity break, no 2x error.

Reachability note: the path IS live-reachable (scanner.py:3410-3446 close action → get_positions cumFunding read → fold in _close_trade_db) and feeds net_pnl_pct/track record/gate — but since the math is correct, there is no money/state impact. The 'critical' severity and the claimed defect do not exist. Tests at tests/test_direction_books.py:525-572 only assert the subtraction mechanics, which are correct given the verified convention. Set to low to reflect no real risk (refuted).

## Completeness-critic notes

Coverage of the in-process money/state math (kernel core, sizing, PnL conventions, reconciler matching, scanner apply, restart replay, freeze/boot lifecycle, persistence transactions, data freshness) is genuinely thorough — I did not re-issue mandates there. The 6 gaps above are all SEAMS between auditor mandates or whole components nobody held, and every one was either explicitly punted by a prior auditor ('for another auditor', 'could not verify') or named in the prompt's unsimulated-scenario list. All anchors were confirmed against live code in this session: books.py exists with the routing helpers but no audit; risk.py reconcile_exchange_positions/reconcile_all_books/_insert_recovered_trade/get_user_fills(closedPnl) recovery exists and was only edge-touched; policy.py promotion gates read COALESCE(net_pnl_pct,pnl_pct) over mixed-scale paper rows; daemon.py:1298-1314 feeds acct.get('source') (incl. 'books_aggregate'/paper fallback) into update_equity; scanner.py run_scan has NO lock (grep for scan_lock/in_progress returned nothing) while two production scan entry points exist; and the live funding fold at scanner.py:3415-3446 rests on an unverified cumFunding.sinceOpen sign assumption. Ranking by money/state blast radius: (1) live-exchange-reconcile and (4) daemon-equity-feed-risk-state are the two highest — both are fail-safe backstops/safety controls whose failure is silent and unbounded. (6) funding-lifecycle-flip is a direct per-trade money-sign risk. (2) direction-books and (3) promotion-gate-parity are systemic correctness gaps for any books-enabled / promote-to-live deployment. (5) concurrent-scan-race is the classic production race the prompt explicitly asked about. Recommend assigning reconcile and equity-feed first.
